haue vpon v wrought without cauſe thinge nought daye ſayeth yet late trowe ſo newe yet date freſhe remembred mynde vnto blode ſo ye kinde ſuppoſe foryetfulneſſe may put away mortal heuyneſſe harmes olde whych aye renewe agayne mynde ſaye certayne trowe playnly thought yet grene ne dyeth nought haue ſlaine olde progenitours whylom ſo noble werreours cytye brent brought vnto ruyne robbed falſly rauyne tourned wilderneſſe grece caryed rycheſſe father ſlayne hyght lamedon without cauſe iuſte occaſyon raught frō golde treaſour ſemeth foule errour might ryght amendes well chalenge eke deſyre fully aduenge afore goddes full high offence onely reaſon conſcience paſſyng theyr mortall crueltee one thinge moſt greueth vngoodly agaynſt gentylleſſe without regarde worthineſſe byrth ne royall blode ſo fayre eke ſo good meane ſyſter called exyon ala theyr confuſyon diſuſe kepe like degre day day ſuch diſhoneſtee thrugh honour name lorn cōſiderīg nought ſtock ſhe born blinde take hede aduert roote kindred ſurquidrye ſo indurate ſyth ſhe borne ſo highe eſtate ytreated like ye may ſe may coniecte thoſe lowe degre gouerned paſſing diſhoneſtly ye may thinke demen truely wyues maydens companie eke allye yhaunted vſed theyr luſte grekes haue better truſte ne ſpare nother blode age thus liue torment ſeruage without routhe mercy pitee toucheth well ſemeth equite ryght ye ought echone ful might wronges ye offended ſeke waye might amended worke one aſſent ſins procede like entent theyr malyce curſed crueltee one auenged herte wil thought one accord ne varye nought force doubled pouſte right reaſon good equite requyre vengeaunce yt doth ye wrōge though ſo differre longe truſte alſo goddes rightwiſeneſſe ſhall helpe harmes redreſſe fauour v innocence chaſtice wrought offence ¶alſo ye knowe citye ſtronge mighty great ſuertye toures high walled werre alſo fer ſhineth ſonne ſterre none like reken may force therto peregall ye knowe alſo ſhall eft founde cheualrye habounde except armes olde aſſayed yet dreade neuer diſmayed haue plenty alſo vytayle frendſhyp eke ne v fayle theyr might v ſuccour wherfore reade without ſoiour ſet vpon theim ſith well able time nowe ſemeth couenable manhode byd make delaye venge wronge hap ſo euer maye differring oft drawen domage worke time double auauntage purpoſe lacketh neuer dele manhod aſſured wel holde haſty rakell worken wilfully werre alſo ſtant auenture aye mart doubtous eure reade firſt grekes ſende wyt harmes amende without ſtryfe werre debate may ſayne fortunate yf contrarye reaſon condiſcende concluſyon graunte aſkyng equite righte haue cauſe preue might proceden rygour ſhall aſſaye fyrſt meaſure fer ryght reaſon eke requere diſdeyne yf lyſt quarell deuoyde wylfulneſſe yrooted vppon good ſykerneſſe great offence demaunde amendes fyrſt pacience god fortune hope wyll aſſent ende ſhulde ſame repent better peace haue redreſſe gyn werre without auiſeneſſe therfore let v wofull auenture paciently aye ſuffre endure porte humble playne tyll v anſwere ſend ayene though ſo myne entencion meaued iuſte occaſyon irous ſort proceadyng vengeaunce wyll put remembraunce letten ſlyde foryetfulneſſe wronges voyde heauineſſe toward grekes axe wyll exiona reſtore v againe whiche moſt dere ſtynte hatred debate werre ſurplus mortall eure ſhall deſſymule prudently endure harmes olde forth pacience ye accorde vnto ſentence saye vpon ye full auyſed yf ſonde deſpiſed lyſte reaſon obeye may iuſtly ſeke nother waye haue redreſſe saue purpoſe ſenden anthenore whiche man diſcrete well auyſee ſpecially mater treatee wyſe eloquent ye well knowe paſſyngly prudent whan kyng tolde tale anone counſeyle conſent echone anthenor iourney vndertake haſt gan ready make without abode wyll one denye take hym embaſſadrye full well auiſed diſcrecion toke went informacion poynt poynt great charge hym caſte ſtande large without errour coulde good theffecte full playnly vnderſtode euery thyng prynted thought went hath forgat ryght nought worde caſte fayle ſhyppe goth began ſayle ſhort tyme companye aryued vp theſalye citie called monoſyus fortune kynge pelleus ſame tyme anthenor anone vnto kynge right way gone guydo hath conceiued pryme face right beningly receyued whan knewe cauſe comyng bad haſt without tarying anthenor fell viſage shortly ſaye theffecte meſſage troian knight aſtoned neuer adel full demure auyſed well haſty rakle ſayne abydyng loke face playne pelleus manly chere sayde effecte right thus ye ſhall ¶the worthy kyng called pryamus wyſe ſo noble ſo manly famous knighthod paſſyng excellent hath fyrſt goodly wyſe ſeyt troye royall chiefe eitie full entent meſſage ſhall ſaye wordes playne ſo ye diſdayne paciently gyue audience remembryng fyrſt aduertence harmes full longe ago wronges ye wrought alſo full cruelly eke troye lande progenitours iniuryes deſtruction cauſeles without occaſyon ye ſhewed haue cruelty mercyles deſtroyed citie slayne father named lamedowne cytie brent beat adowne nother lefte paleys houſe toure lad awaye rycheſſe treaſour nother ſpared reherſe ſlaughter woman childe man might none ſwerde aſtert yet one thynge yt moſt hathe herte ſyſter called exyon hold kept kinge thelamon diſhoneſtly agayne gentrye great diſhonour great vyllanye kindred lyke ye may ſe treated cheriſhed like degre wherfore ſyth ye ſo wyſe knight ye ought aduert haue ſyght ſuch thinges iuſt affection conſydre diſcrecion gentilneſſe equite ſuch wronges might amended wherfore pryam great auiſeneſſe fully buſyneſſe herte deſyreth peace reſte sendeth beſeching beſte ye wil buſy diligence make hym litell recompence may haue reſtytucion knightly mediacion ſyſter withouten longer ſpace remenaunt wyll let pace strife werre onely eſchewe deſireth fully ſewe peace quyete hole affection purſue meaſure reaſon finallye lyke ye may ſe occaſyon werre fle conſyder holdē ſo ſage fine fully meſſage ¶whan pelleus hym playnly vnderſtode ſodayne yre hert waxed woode cheare loke fell furyous rancoure right melancolyus ne might attempre appeaſe haſty fyre gan herte ſeaſe anone full diſpytous wiſe gan pryamus threten deſpiſe malyce ſet ſond nought al meanes yt anthenor hath ſought gan alſo troian knight manace bad haſte auoyde place vpon peryll fall might anone went ſyght haſte meynee without abode taken haue ſee gan ſaylen theſalye theyr waye ſo faſt gan theim hye ſhorte tyme aryued vp salerne mighty ſtrong citye fortune royall towne anthenor fonde king thelamowne paleys hath waye nome firſt finde come accepted vnto preſence beningly without offence exyone preſent tyde auenture ſtanding ſyde reuerence womanheade anthenor toke better hede albe cuſtome kyng thelamon hye deſpyte indignacion euerye troyan could eſpye ſpecially enuye rancour onely bytter rage hert might neuer yet aſwage al pacience anthenor hath giuen audience anone ful ſobre wiſe tayle gan ſhall deuiſe ¶syr quod ſupporte grace ye graunt oportune ſpace declare cauſe cominge reherſe without tarying matter hole brefely ſentence make kouthe magnificence signifying without diſpleſaunce priamus hath gouernaūce troye towne hath vnto ſent faythfull meaning clene entent beſechyng firſt goodlyheade wronges forgotten eke deade ye onely hygh nobleſſe equite gentilneſſe ye reſtore exyona agayne ye hold ſpeake wordꝭ playn ſothe like eſtate wherfore prayeth ſtinten debate euery harme put memorye knightly honour owne glorye ſende home make delyueraunce goodly withouten varyaunce ye haue holde ſo many longe dayes ne tarieth ſetteth delayes ne let founden ſlouthe ſothfaſtly great routhe recorde ye haue abuſed may trouthe goodly excuſed ſhall lett lightly ouerſlyde ye beningly liſt prouyde ſende home like haue ſayde lo charge layde without abiding certayne goodly anſwere ye ſende agayne ¶whan thelamon herkened tayle haſty yre gan wexen pale fyery collor hath made ſo woode face aualed blode within herte gan frete bite wyth loke aſkoye tourned vp whyte hye diſdayne face diſpytous pale ſmilyng laughter furyous gan rake fearful mortall fyre fretinge hate brent deſyre ſhortly made concluſyon anthenor put ilke obiection ſayde frende euer thou wonder greatly meruayle auenture ſodaine newe thinge vnprudently meueth nowe thy kinge vnto make ſuch ſonde thou foole whā ſo thou toke hōd eyther vnhappy elles infortunate bring proude embaſſete wyl nothing haue loke thou ſay ſo ne aqueynted lyte nothing platly delyte ſhort wordes thou liſt heare hym ought prayer ne haue delyght ioye ne feſte thinge wherof maketh requeſte wote well whyle go troye ſelfe mo reforme thinge amys offence ſhortly thus certaine thing wrought lamedowne manhod wonnē ye towne ſlewe kyng helde knightly wiſe meting felde euerye man might ſe ieoparde firſt enter cytye graunted memorye onely ſigne mine hygh victorye withouten contradiction grekes haue poſſeſſion moſt entere exiona nowe thou claymeſt well ſyker thyne aſking vayne truſte right well certayne thou getteſt one worde yf may ſhal firſt made full greate affray leue liue euer grutche agaynſt ſtriue ſittyng leue ſo whilom ſo great gat ſpending blode ſo wrothe therwith wood kepe ſhall founde ſo many mortall wounde troye towne thenſe wan good fayth fer forthe ſhall lightly fro handes pace ſhe alone ſo ſtandeth grace beaute ſemelyheade bounte godlyheade ſhal reaſon ſhortly fine ſothe moſt feminine euer ſawe without dreade porte conning womanheade hath alone exiſtence ſouereynte perfect excellence priamus ought thou cā ſayne lyue getteth agayne bye many deadly wounde ſharpe ſwerdes ſquare ſperes groūde ſhal firſt reyſed ſuch ſtrife ſhall coſt many mannes lyfe ſhe agayne reſtored take forſothe yu getteſt liſt may wel beginne ſupoſe ſhall litell winne none otherwiſe haue tolde woteſt yu great foole holde put thy ſelfe ſo ferre ieopartye execute embaſſadrye manly grekes ſo boldly offende beware therfore ſende vpon thy ſelfe rancoure pride go thy waye yf thou abide longer ſothly ſyght thou woteſt ye pryſe yt haue hyght thou ſcapeſt liefe lothe anthenor anone ſhyp goth forth ſayleth hym liſt delaye towarde yle called achaye whan taken hath lande ryuayle auenture fonde worthy kynges pollux caſtor ryght anone troyan anthenor without abode courte fare vnto meſſage declare together preſent right thus ſayd ſentement ¶the noble kynge troye citee hath vnto ſent wyll beſechyng full lowe maner ſhe voucheſafe vnto prayer equitie condeſcende goodly helpe certeine wrong mende touchyng ſyſter called exion may haue reſtitucion agayne diſcrete aduyſe ſyth ye ſo manly ſo wyſe lykely oppynion ye good medyacion may eaſely agayne reſtored cheryſhe peace vnitee wherfore prayeth wt herte entere goodly wyſe done deuere holde byn ſo knyghtly ſo ſage wyll playnly ſurpluſage wronges olde put ſuſpence deſyreth knyghtly hygh prudence ſtynte warre nouryſhe peace nother rakle rekles euell auyſed workes caſte afore ſhall fall thynges future aduertynge ferre ſeeth peryll werre wyll hym conforme vnto peace reſte conceyueth beſte euery man vnite ſewe prudently alſo eſchewe debate hole full occaſion lo fyne entencion commyt vnto iugement ¶this caſtor yre inpacient haſtineſſe ne might abyde cruell herte ſo ſwolen pride brake anone right deſpiteous face ſayde frende knowe treſpace euer grekes vnto thy kynge axe amendes wonder thynge v neuer dyd none offence saue made maner recompence wronge wrought lamedon whiche fyſte ſought occaſyon agaynſt grekes vngoodly wyſe cauſed v vpon hym tho ryſe one manly hym ſette due ryght quyte dette lyke deſerte haue playnly ſerued nothīg wrought hath deſerued axe amendes gynneth late coueyte mortall hate vtter malys enmyte outher peace accorde vnite effecte hereafter ſhall fele ſo dare hereafter v deale bargayne ſhall full dere ben abought frendeſhyp ſothly ſet nouhgt ouermore ſpeake lykely ſemeth vnto pryamus loued lyte thincke value myte whan ſent forth meſſage thou folye dyddeſt great outrage take ſo hyghe peryllous thynge vnto grekes bryngen ſuche tydynge throughe thy lyfe put inpartye counſayle faſte thou hye▪ ſyght leſt thou repente ¶and anthenor forth ſhyp went wynde gan ſayle anone towarde yle called pylon haſt whan dyd aryue ſhope hym forth court blyue duke neſtor maner thynge houſholde helde royall kinge anthenor full ſad auyſee tofore neſtor ſyttyng ſee whan admytted ſayne tale tolde full openly playne poynt poynt ye herde afore vayne reherſe alway concluded hath one ye haue herde touchyng exion ¶but duke neſtor face nothyng red hewe aſſhes dead fret collor ſo inwardly blode eche extremitee withdrawen downe alowe vnto herte yre ſo ſore made hym ſmerte gan quake euery ioynt vayne hande vnneth may reſtreyne melancolye venged lyke lyon ſo wood wroth fer hym ſelfe ſo alyenate inwardly rancour paſſyonate loke reſerued furious ſyghte tho rule hym ſelfe vnneth myghte felte anger ſo great aduerſytie ſyth amyddes crueltie ſodeyne haſte one brake euen thus anthenor ſpake ¶o thou quod al thy wordes whyte ſuppoſe thou wotteſt full lyte tofore thou haſte thy tale tolde meruayle howe thou arte ſo bolde thus preſume myne eares offende pryam ſo proudely pretende maner tytle thy kynges name worthy grekes put blame vniuſtly foule hardyneſſe requere haue redreſſe iniuryes wrought lamedon boldely affyrmyng falſe preſumpcion vpon grekes wronkes outragious whiche myne eres ſo odyous fretyng eke ſo bytyng ſo kene lyſte may ſuſteyne hearyng ſo hatefull ſowne ner honour hye renowne refrayned ſhulde cruell wyſe execute full haſtely iuſtyce rygour mortall law beſtes wylde fyrſte drawe thervpon thy fayned tale diſmembre peces ſmale deſpyte pryamus thy kynge teache bryng tydyng preſumptuouſly tale newe lorde hym better knewe thus ſhuldeſt thou haue thy preſūpcion thy laſt mede fynall guerdon without mercy lyke haue behyght haſt bego ſyght vtterly doth great offence vnto myne eye haue preſence diſdeine cauſeth myne vnreſte ¶than anthenor thought beſt holſom longer abyde caſte wyſely rancour pryde beſte beare fayre ſhyppe gan anone repayire haſte poſſybilitee without abode taken hath ſea gan ſayle homeward faſte drawe ſodeynly boylen gan wawe ſeas ryſe cloudes blacke appere wynde wake wonder gaſtfull alſo heauen dredfull fyre bryght leuen thonder ſmote ſo gan tēpeſt driue toppe maſt aſunder gynneth ryue alofte poynt drowne fell wether gan ſo theim frowne naught awayte death euen poynt yeldyng vp brethe ne ſawe none remedy styll amonge gan clepe crye vnto goddes auowes make deuoutly vndertake eche growen age eſcape go pylgremage lyke rytes paynym wyſe goddes ſacrifyſe ſubſtaunce myght ſodeinly wether derke nyght newe lyght grace gan adawe ſea ware calme ſmothē gan ye wawe happe amonge euerychone tempeſt periſhed one tofore troye within lyttell ſpace aryued euerychone grace eſchaped ſafe euery ioypardye bothe anthenor companye temple toke ryght way prayer full longe laye many another alſo ſake thankyng goddes yt lyſten ſo ſlake euery peryll tempeſt ſea vnto kynge goeth lordes full royall paleys dongyon pryncipall sat abode full ſolempnelye heare reporte embaſſadrye knyght hath hym fall hath tolde kynge tofore lordes anthenor hath fyrſt made mencion tofore kynge iuſte relacion exployt ordre wyſe howe vncurteouſly receyued kynge pelleus thretes wordes deſpyteous ſuffred kyng thelamon ferſe cruell wood lyon afterwarde gan alſo complayne deſpyte bretherne tawyne rebuke great dread neſtor howe happed ſpede lyfe myght vnneth eſcape tolde gan ende make iourney eke repayre wherby pryam fully diſpayre outher force yet aduenture ſyſter neuer might recure conceyueth aduertence cleare reporte experte euydence aye theim beninge vngoodly ayen malinge ſheweth ſelfe moſt debonayre ayeneward fond thē moſt cōtrayre frowardly euer theim quite shewing ſygnes ſet lyte frendſhyp ought could aduerte wherof ful ſorowfull herte conſtrayned ryght nede tho compelled iuſtly procede haue redreſſe onely rygoure profered peace myght haue fauour admitted tytle rightwyſeneſſe hygh deſpite haſty wylfulneſſe euery meane meaſoure vayne saue onely werre engendred diſdayne began cauſed olde hatrede gan anone ſuch broyle brede newe enuy within kynge breſte priamus without areſte inly irous rancour fret diſdayne ſo ſore ground whet ſo muſt leſe wyn vpon grekes wyll werre begyn therin ieoparde manly knight lyfe deathe bycauſe ryght caſt hym firſt nauye ſende haſt grece fomen offende like knight force haunte knightly wiſe caſt daunt pompe grekes ſturdineſſe fynally theyr pride oppreſſe ¶but ſaye priam infelycitye newe trouble hap deſtiny aboue hateful influence deſcended vnware violence meue ye thus thou canſt liue peace ſodayne ſorte fortune graceleſe chaunce vnhappy without auiſeneſſe wilfull luſt fonde hardineſſe haue put thy ſoule tranquilitye make werye thy proſperitye ſauoureſt yu bitter thē ſwete canſt lyue peace quiete thou art trauayled wilfull mocions ouer mayſtred thy paſſions lacke reaſon hyghe prudence derked blinde prouydence full barayne caſt afore ſe harmes folowyng thine aduerſitye thou ſlowe wiſely conſydre want ſyght made thus ſlydre myſt errour falſly forueye pathes wronge right weye voyde reaſon wylful haſtyneſſe thy guyde thy mayſtreſſe diſcrecion ſo prudēt ſo ſadde auyſely ſhould haue lad trace ſenſualitee though ful ſelde mannes power ſufferaunce ſelfe refrayne whan ſodayne yre doth herte ſtrayne thou ſhuldeſt afore better haue caſt thi chaūce wrought counſayle put balaunce thy ſykerneſſe ala diddeſt thou ſo haue ſymuled ſome dele wo caſt thy chaunge wel afore prime haue forgotten wronges olde time thought afore thine aduertence oft falleth experyence while men moſt theyr buſyneſſe vengeably olde wronges redreſſe double harme beware fall agayne newe ſnare domages forgotten cleane falſe reporte rumour freſhe grene renewed ſwyfte fame fleeth fer hurt lordes name namely whan ſo purpoſe wende head forſee ende pryde ſodayne heate voyde ſelfe quyete aduertyng worke auyſely prouerbe teacheth comonly ſtande ſure enhaſte hym meue yf ſhall greue walketh ſurely playne ſtumble vayne onleſſe ſo lyſte folye neclygent put hym wylfully auenture hym ſelfe reche eſchewe peryll holde wreche ſothly pryam thou recheleſe commytte thy quyete peace dredfully durynge date cruell fortune fykell fate whoſe maner cuſtome comonly whan man truſteth moſt ſuredly goddeſſe blynde full vnſtable ſhe hym moſte deceyuable hym abate royall ſtalle ſodeynly doth make hym downe falle tryp throwe backe gayne ſtriueth ſhal haue lytle tacke ſo ſlyely gylefull ſnare ſhe make man welfare pantre fraude englewed whā leaſt weneth remewed therfore man may hope affyaunce fortune rule ſo full varyance ne lete wyght eaſe iuparte ne recke ſhe game departe tourne chaunce outher well wo ſelde one ſhe doth game go ye may ſee example pryamus foly ſo deſyrous worke head folow ſo wylle troubled calme tranquille boke hereafter ſhalbe founde hym citie platly confounde vtterly confuſyon afterwarde longe ſucceſſyon ſhalbe red ſtory fable remembred dytees delytable pleaſaunce ſhall ſample beware lere haſty luſt raſhe voluntee gyn thyng wherin ſuretee dependeth aye ſtryfe werre debate ſuch play vnwarely cometh check mate harme ydone late amende whoſe fyne ofte wende ſtory ye ſhall ſee lette pryam alwaye myrrour haſty errour tymes correcte anone poyntill wyll directe maner trace rude ſtory remnaunt conclude worthy kyng euer one ſentence aye fyred feruence hath breuettes letter ſente lordes holde parlement cōmaunded al haſt may come anone aſſygned daye euery warde party towne aſſemble noble ilyowne chiefe reigne echone hym preſent noble kyng anone tofore theim ſhortly wyll declareth thus began ¶syres quod bycauſe ye ſo wyſe nedeth longe proceſſe deuyſe reherſe comynge cauſe tell ſhortly clauſe meane maketh delaye ye wotte day sent grece counſayle knyght myne anthenor call haue recured exiona agayne whoſe meſſage tho vayne grekes full vncurteyſly receyued diſpyteouſly threte rebuked poynt haue dead vnneth myght eſcape head put hym ſuch hygh offence blame muche redoundeth alder ſhame day day muſt encreaſe ordeyne ſome remedy therfore meaſure haue offred haue v werre ſtryfe yprofred hyghe deſpyte rancour heate malys cruelly v threate wold peace thē purchace wronges done felly v manace ye harmes yt haue v wrought purpoſe playnly thought redreſſe amendes make vtterly werre v awake whoſe ioye fully encreaſe greuaunce wolde god repentaunce contryte herte ſtynten myſchiefe lykely fall eke grefe outher parte myght ouer ſlyde ala rancour pryde ſwole new threaten god defende halfe deale ſore infortune euer ſhulde fall purpoſe euery v ſyth haue deuyſed thus v muſt reſyſte wyll malicious myght god neceſſitie deffence wyll none beſte holde vnto entent worke one aſſent purpoſe ſoneſt ſhall achieue diſcorde may quarell preue parte hertes one victorye may way gone chiefe conqueſt peace vnitie ryght diſcorde aduerſytie wherfore read wyll harte lette v ſet grekes ſmerte ſothfaſtly ſo ye lyſte ſe dare affyrme farre ſtronger grekes vpon euery parte haue armes parfytly arte accoūted knighthod crop roote plenty haue horſemen foote arrayed well eueryche degree therwith alſo ſtronge citie withſtonde fomon euerichone counſayling ſyth ordayne anone fyrſt taſſemble holy nauye ſtuffe ſtrongly wt chiualrye grece haſtely ſende proude grekes manly offende iuſte cauſe tytle ryght theim werre force might townes bren fyeldes waſte herte vnfayned alſo v enhaſte quite deſerued haue read ſhall none ſaue cruellyf theim vengeaunee ne hath eare ne let greuaunce though tofore fortune victours ſlewe father progenitours vnhap fyrſte put downe remounteth ofte hyghe renowne charge duble varyance werre ſtryfe aye balaunce day aſſured wele ſee morowe caſt downe whele victor ofte lykewyſe aduenture vanquiſhed diſcomfyture hym afore victorie vp ſyth downe armes ſtant glory martes chaunce man may aſſure cometh ſo muſt take eure gery mar ſudden influence gyue man whylom excellence wynne pryſe lyke conquerour ſodaynly falleth ſomer floure honour make fade whan aſpectes glade man lyſteth wrythe olde renowne goth away blythe floode ebbe foloweth aye men deſerue prayſe daye though day phebus mery ſhyne morow may bemes downe decline thickneſſe miſtes trouble ryght ſo mar chaunces double vp downe low alofte fortune whiche chaungeth ofte lyſt whele make man aſſende vnwarely downe agayne deſcende stounde mele honour auaunce aſweigh throwe miſchaunce fauour ſet vp full hye erſt auale twyngling eye playe vnſtable tourneth ball whyle one goeth vp hath fall reyſeth one doth another loute euery man whan cometh aboute muſt take tourne playe requireth experte fraudes lereth shall hir ſugre fynde gall ymeynt hony aye bitter ſpreynt peace werre honour fame dignity renowne ſhame lykyng lyſt graunt therfore man hap muche auaunte ¶for though grekes whylom lofte may happe hereafter full vnſofte wherfore echone ſhewe worthyneſſe ſo named ſtrength hardineſſe fortune playnly commytte lette feare manly hertes flytte ſtonde hole meanyng playne therupon let ſe ye wyll ſayne one voyce gan reyſe ſentence hyghely preyſe one herte manly gan expreſſe wil one deſpende goodes rycheſſe bodyes put ieopardye one wolde tho denye graunt thanketh echone gaue leue lyſt gone diſſolued hath parlement euery man waye went repayred manſiowne kynge alone lefte ilyowne sole hym ſelfe inwardly muſynge purpoſe myght brynge ſoth nothyng elles thought therupon fyne thus wrought kyng pryamus makyng thus mone tolde chambre alone many wayes caſtyng vp downe perfourme concluſyowne fulfyll fyne entent fyrſte prudently hath ſent ſonnes come hym haſte well borne baſte taſſemble yfeare purpoſe lyke ye ſhall haue counſaile nedeful purueaunce againſt grekes maken ordenaunce fyrſt ſelfe alone pryuely ordre eueryche ſet dewe ſee lyke age degree hector fyrſt floure chyualrye repayred home panonye moſt acceptable euery wyghtes grace nexte father taken hath place ¶and whan pryam leyſer eſpye ſyghes ſore caſtyng vp eye echone ſyttyng enuyron gan declare hertes mocyon firſt might ought wil expowne ſalt teares gan hym ſelfe drowne inly wo outragyous wepyng ſobbyng furyous vnneth myght word breake vnto diſtreſſe ſpeake openly inwarde meanyng ſhewe tyll laſt wordes fewe gan abrade pyteous fare euen thus ſentence gynnyng declare ¶my dere ſonnes ſo louyng ſo kynde ſuppoſe ye haue mynde remembre diſcretly aduerte eke imprente full freſhly herte grekes agayne ryght lawe cruell ſwerde mundred haue ſlawe auncetours whylom hyghe renowne deſtroyed brent beate downe fyrſt troye walles olde vngoodly alſo withholde myne owne ſyſter called exion full great ſhame confuſyon hyghe repryfe worthyneſſe ſemeth kyndeneſſe nature ye ought agreued inwardly herte ſore amened ſuffer hyndring name treated alder ſhame ala nyl ye beſyneſſe highe deſpyte knyghtly redreſſe tauenge vpon crueltie recure fynde iniquitie sith ye ſo myghty ſo ſtronge certes ſemeth ye byden longe day day ye ſo differre knyghtly wyſe gyn werre force myght manly aſſaye pure ſory ye lyſte delaye confyrmen vnto deſyre hate bren hoote fyre vpon lyke ye may ſee frettynge yre auenged lyke deſert quyten mede ye ala lyſten take hede whyle renowne doth ſo freſhly ſhyne vnto luſte hertes declyne conſyderyng lyke well kouthe ſelfe tender youth foſtred brought forth echone fro thilke daye firſt ye coud gone tenderly could might thynge inward ſyght ye ſhuld aduert alway newe newe nature ſorowes rewe remedye mine aduerſytee whych toucheth alſo wel sith ye wote ſore doth greue ye ſhulden ſhape myne harmes releue ſodeinly thus gan mourne towardes hector gan face tourne ſayd hector truſte ioye mine heyre alſo like reygne troy daye ſucceſſoure named art ſouerayne floure worthyneſſe manhod well al thy brother knighthod doſt excelle armes lyke conquerour called ſtock worſhyp honour hertely praye though thou ſytteſt ſtyll wyllinge nowe purpoſe fulfyll execute deſyre ſo fynally mo full fayth bryng thinge take nothinge doubte chefetayne alſo gouernour purpoſe vtterly ſocour thine hande iourney committe hooly herte ſo thou ne flytte confourme good auyſement vp perfourme fine mine entent reaſon beſt ſyt whych art ſo prudent ſo ful wyt strong deliuer flouryng eke youthe ye fame ye world kouthe yonge yeares olde diſcreciowne eurous loue paſſyng renowne vnto whoſe thy brother ſhall obeye ſtande lyue deye cōdeſcēde accomplyſhe requeſt thou feleſt anſwere leſte ¶and whē kinge hath ſhewed ſētēce demure cheare humble reuerence worthy hector example gentrie ſoft ſpeche teacheth curteſye anſwere gaue ſobre countenaunce effecte ſubſtaunce ¶mine owne lorde father dere beningly ſo ye liſt heare force great might eke ſumme nature ryght euerye thinge kinde doth conſtrain bondes large chayne ſytting ſhe doth enſpyre ende euery man deſyre wronges done haue amendement lawe ryght conuenient namely ſuch nobylytye kinde hath endewed ſet high degre ſuch great reprefe ſhame wronge vnto theyr name eche treſpaſſe muſt conſydered iuſtly meaſured qualyty hym offended alſo parſon wrong werre conteck debate greater grefe high eſtate ſuffer harme caſe auenture wronge vniuſtly endure iniuryes compaſſed malyce offence diſcrete aduyſe theim famous manhod well renoumed borne gentyl blode ſuch one holde wretch wherfore muſt greatly charge retch onely knighthod worſhyp eke wronges done mendes ſeke ſtate conſydered high nobleſſe plyte ſtand worthyneſſe whan beaſtes reaſon rude blinde deſyre ſame iuſt inſtinct kinde ¶and parte truſteth certayne ye haue ſonne woulde half ſo fayne vpon grekes auenged trouthe ſay faythfully yre theim bren doth glede thurſt blode mede ryght eldeſt age amonge ſonnes ſo moſt wt rage fret within iuſtly knighthode right hand ſhed grekes blode ſhalle fele peraunter wene whan time cometh ſothe ſhalbe ſene ¶but firſte rede wiſely minde caſt afore leue behinde ye begyn diſcretly aduert prudently conſydre herte onely gynnynge ende yt middes way wil wēd fine fortune theim lede ye thus amiſſe ye may ſpede counſayle mine opinion worthy lytell diſcrecion haue pryſe caſt courſe thinges ordre ceryouſly waye trace wo delyte though ginninge haue appetite yet ende playnly fable may thīg fall cōmēdable worthe ginninge fortunate cauſeth ſtrife great debate wherfore ſothe begynninges dread mē well knowe fine ſhall ſuccede ginninge grace well fortuned whan ende middes lyke contuned wele ne may conteme well better rather abſteine put doubt ſtandeth ſuerte ſo doth hath aduerſitee humble eſtate royall herte pray let offende bolde ſay mocion good fayth none entencion nothing meue offence onely magnificence procede heade wilfully ne haſt meue foly gyn thing wil ſhende lacke ye ſe tofore ende take hede aduertence conſydre good prouidence grekes haue theyr ſubiection europe affryke many region ful large wide knighthod moſt famous rycheſſe wonder plenteous right renoumed alſo worthineſſe ſupporte dare wel expreſſe ful peryllous theim diſpleaſe diſturbe yf quyet nowe parturbe ſtandeth fully peace drede though aſſye helpe v nede loked euery parte aryght egal vnto grekes might ¶and though alſo mine aunte exion agayne right holde thelamon good redempcion put v vnto deſtruction rede bye halfe ſo deare many v perhappes ſyttē mo might ſake death vnderfonge ende make wiſedome lyke ſemeth may happe alſo ſhe ſhorte time fatall courſe ſhall fine whē attropos thredde two ſhal twine wonne ſhe go enmite thought ſorowe wo slaughter men death confuſyō wherfore reade without diſcencion without wo endure put ſelfe auenture holde beſt worke wyſe doubtles cowardiſe ſaye high preſence forcauſe holde prudence fortune knowen ſo ful doubilneſſe syth ſure put ſykerneſſe thus ſome effect worde hector helde hym ſtyll whan yt hector ful high prudēce cōcluded hath fine ſētence ful demurely kept lippes cloſe therwithall paris vp aroſe gan tale thus afore kinge lorde quod ſo lykinge highneſſe taken hede ſemeth ſhuld litell dread knightly wiſe vndertake vpon grekes werre make one theyr pride confounde sith ſo paſſingly habounde chiualry within towne haue plenty poſſeſſyowne eche thinge may werre auayle stuffe ſelfe royall apparayle longeth aſſautes marciall ſpeciall helpe ſuccour many region v worke theyr deſtruction pompe pryde manly abate grekes malyce amate al herte ſo ſtoute ſemeth ſhortlye nede doubte parte diſmayed wherfore reade let delayed ſhyppes fyrſt ready make ſelfe wyl fully vndertake liking pleſaunce empryſe hooly gouernaunce aſſure put certayne exyona recure agayne fourme ſhall wrought haue waye deuiſed thought likely hereafter done vnto declare anone firſt haue caſt ſtrōg myghty hand rauyſhe ſome lady land high eſtate make taryinge mightely troye brynge maugre might concluſyon ye may haue reſtitucion chaunge ye deſyre ſo therupon ſhall longe ado behete grekes ſtronge ſhall tale prolonge wil ſayne excluding euerye doubte aduiſe ſhal well brought firſt ſhal purpoſe fine goddes haue thrugh power diuine shewed reuelacion therupon auiſyon late agone laye ſlepe vnto ſo ye take kepe ye may fayle deſpayre haue recure ſo fayre ye haue ſo much care ¶and maner hoole wyl declare dreame magnificence ſo ye lyſteth giue credence tale ſhal dwelle ceryouſly ordre tell trouthe fable fayne lorde moſt ſouerayne ¶firſt ye remembre minde daye laſt inde aduyſe commaundement matter entent ſpecially cheirte knowen betwene whych toke vpō tho charge within bondes land large ¶the ſame time deſyre ſpede titan beames rede geminy droue chayre golde toward crabbe take holde named paleys diane bent moone wex wane halowed ſonnes ſtacion nigh middes moneth iuyn ſeaſon early morowe whan phebus auoiding nightes ſorow doth pirrous wayne vp drawe aurora eſtward doth adawe water teares rounde ſiluer dewe cauſeth habounde vpon herbes floures ſoote ful kindly noryſhyng crop roote ¶vp roſe bed anone ful deſyrous huntinge gone pricked herte luſty freſhe pleſaunce loue ſome dewe obſeruaunce diana daye magnifie called lady venerye reuerendly rite obſerue citherea tho ſerue feres hertes releue caſt v fully til drewe eue within foreſt playe v diſporte pleſauntly v recomforte longeth loue luſtyneſſe thilke day venus goddeſſe yſacred full great excellence great honour dewe reuerence done vnto one fryday aduenture fall whan gā haſte v woodes grene hope day ſome game ſene great labour riding fro til full many bucke doo ſtrengthe ſlayne might thē fynde herte ychaſed hoūdes hinde downes dale lowe till phebus high vpon dayes bowe amid arke meredien beames ful hote ſhene▪ moſt buſy vpon chaſe befell wonder diuerſe caſe fortune happed ſodeynly ſeuered companye sole ſelfe amonge holtes hore finde game deſyrous euermore ware thicke thyn ful great harte ſawe afore ryn downe launde vale grene ſothe ne might ſuſtene ſwift nigh hym nere though hym ſewe pricked courſere nigh ye death many ſundry ſhawe ſyght ſo fer withdrawe al euer ſewe myght anone loſt hym ſyght wood dabare name ſo faynt gan wexen game mine horſe whych tho ryde fomyng full whyte vpon euery ſyde flankes blode diſtayned purſute ſo ſore conſtrayned ſporres ſharpe dyed redd harte ſo prycked ſtede vp downe ful buſy thought laboure auayled right nought tyll laſt amonge bowes glade aduenture caught pleſaunt ſhade ful ſmothe playn luſty ſene ſoft veluet yonge grene fro horſe alight faſt bowe aloft reyne caſt faynte mate weryneſſe layde downe vpon gras vpon bryncke ſhortly telle beſyde ryuer criſtall welle water reherſe like quicke ſiluer ſtreames ran whych grauell bryght ſtone golde agayne ſonne ſhone ¶where ryght anone weryneſſe ſodayne ſlepe gan ſo oppreſſe ſyth tyme firſt borne neuer aſleped ſo toforne lay heard wonder ſweuen thought high downe heauē wynged god wonderful cheare mercuryus appeare ſome dele firſt aferde gyrde croked ſwerde brought alſo hande ſlepy yerde plyaunt wande ſerpent goyng enuyrowne fete alſo lowe adowne ſemed alſo ſtode cocke singing houres trewe clocke mouth god mercurye pypes ſet ſonge wonder merye whych ſwete ſugred hermonye made mine eares ſuch melodye ſemed tho mine aduyſe rauyſhed paradiſe thus god dyuerſe likneſſe wonderfull expreſſe shewed ſelfe apparence like deſcryued fulgence boke methologies reherſed many poeſyes many likeneſſe like ye may ſe take moralitee longe yerde right lyne whiche ſyde wrongly may decline signifyeth prudent gouernaunce diſcrete folke yt theyr purueyaūce caſt peryll befall pypes loude ſhall muſyke entuned trewe betokeneth eke many luſty hewe ſugred dytees great excellence rethoryke eloquence god ſoueraigne patrowne cocke ſwete luſty ſowne iuſtly kepeth houres night vtterly aduiſe inward ſight ſuch voyde waker diligence theyr court ſtouthe necligence ſworde croketh ſo againe forged ymade vayne reuoke right weye wrongly trouthe forueye ſerpent whiche tolde wrincled ye may beholde vpon yerde goeth signefyeth falſhode wood wrothe lieth wayte many ſleyghty weye ginnes trouthe werrey god eloquence kinge brought eke comminge citherea theſe louers ſerue iuno pallas called minerue venus liege delite head flikered douues white loke beninge eyen debonayre aye circuling ſnowy winges fayre declare ſothly ſentence douues innocence theim loue yt trouth meane yt theyr groūde ſhuld honeſte cleane ytokned clerely witneſſe without ſoyling vnclenneſſe freſhneſſe roſes redde ſomer ſo luſtyly doth ſprede wynter theyr coloure fade signifieth hertye thoughtes glade yonge folkes ben amerous feruent hope inly deſyrous whan loue gynneth theyr hertes floure till longe proceſſe maketh theim loure wynter vnweldy age luſt palled dulled rage febleneſſe ſomer gone folkes knowe wott well mo one therfore venus fleteth ſee ſhewe trouble aduerſytee loue ſtormye lawe whych byſet many ſturdye wawe nowe calme rough ſo taketh hede hope aſſayled aye ſodeyne dreade next venus pallas behelde ſpere bryghte ſhelde raynbowe rounde head colour grene blewe rede tofore diſcryue growyng grene freſhe olyue therupon browes fowle braunches ſawe ſyt like owle firſt ſhilde pallas goddeſſe signifyed expreſſe vertue force manly high diffēce agayne vyces maken reſiſtence ſpere ſharpe kene ygrounde iuſt rygour forged confound theim falſe put abacke mercy ſhall medle wt ye wrack ſhafte ſothe ſhauen full playne leſt mercyles right ne wrought vain werre make falſe releaſe oliue betokeneth peace owle alſo ſo odious ſonges ſyngeth feaſtes funerall declaring playnly fine euery glorye onely death hath memorye raynbowe grene read perſe signifyeth chaunges ful diuerſe oft falleth werre battayle winne ſodeynly fayle ſtable blew chaūging grene pallas playe alwaye meynt wt tene alder laſt nowe haue minde nimphes iuno came behinde whyche cuſtome fulgencius ſo telles abydeth floudes depe welles iuno theiſe poetes fayne mayden fruyte barayne pecock freſhe quene yſacred fethers ſhene splayed abrode large ſayle argus eyen emprinted tayle ¶the water ronninge ryuer floud labour men haue good great trouble beſyneſſe day nyght ſuffer rycheſſe ſo euer theſe floudes rowe let beware aye flowe nature ryght courſes dewe folowing ye moone muſt ebbe ēſewe moſt dread aye vpon full leſt fortune freſhe fethers pull ryche folkes ſhine golde ſhene sith ſhe chaūche lady quene ¶and argus eyen ſet aye behinde nygardes hertes yt oft ſythes blinde aduert goodes ende like ebbe ſodeynly wil wende whyche nothinge conſydre ſight fayre luſty fethers bright pecock vnwarely fall awaye right ſo ryches ſhortly daye theyr mayſter ſodeynly forſake saying adewe then theyr leue take iuno barayne fruyte right ſo naked bare deſtitute theſe gredy hertes couetous gather ſo deſyrous nothing haue ſuffyſaunce fret dred thē putteth ī ſuch miſchaūce imagening world wil fayle theyr feare agayne ye wynd ſayle till one muſt departe fro thus good aye fine wo namely theim ſo pinche ſpare dread clerkes declare fruite good ſpende large ſo euer ſet lytell charge frely parteth treaſour commune diſcretely ſeeth time opportune hath ioye put good mewe herte fredome liſt ſewe gentylneſſe taketh hede therto ¶and wyſe pallas iuno freſhe venus adowne deſcended like haue ſhortly comprehended vnder guyding mercurius whych vnto began tale thus ¶parys quod lyft vp thine eyen ſee lo theſe goddeſſes nombre thre whych heauen wyth theyr eyen clere dyuerſly vnto appere feaſt wherof tell ſhall goddes aboue celeſtyall iupyter helde owne borde none abſent ſaue onely diſcorde deſpyte ſhe preſent auenged ſet entent wyttes many wayes ſought tyll laſt euen thus ſhe wrought olde poet lyke yt tolde toke appel rounde pure golde greke letter grauen vp downe whych ſayd thus concluſyowne without ſtrife let gyue anon vnto fayreſt theim euerychone diſcorde lady goddeſſe ſhe conteke mayſtreſſe hath appel paſſyng delyte brought feaſt malyce deſpyte caſt downe among theim borde deynous chere ſpeaking worde waye faſt gan hye ſodeynly ſo inly great enuye courte appel hath broughte great werre ſuch conteck wrought hertes theſe ilke thre longe may ſtaunched amonge theim ſelfe ſo gan diſdayne whiche beaute moſt ſeueraygne whych theym hath moſt tytle right cōquere burned apple bryght firſt gan thus beaute ſtryue rancour almoſt theyr hertes ryue wite ryght ſhuld firſt poſſede ¶lo yet enuye reygneth womanhede one fayrer holde eche woman kinde would haue ſome parte priſe aboue eche eſtate ſothe eche theim owne aduiſe hath ioye beaute haue priſe none ſo foule doth myrrour prye ſhene fayre owne eye like foole ſelfe doth quite aumber yelowe cheſeth white goundy eye deceyued ſoone colour cheſeth moone ſome colour fyre made fine ſome encreaſed ſpices wyth wine oyntementes confection night falſe illuſyons appeare wonder freſhe fayre loke full derke day light ayre prefe early morowe ſuch nede beaute borowe nature hath ſelfe diſpoſed therfore faſting box vncloſed make thy choſe ſo byddeth ouide whan euery drugge pot ſet ſyde leſt haply thou ſentence deceyued lightly falſe apparence dayes ſuch craft ful ryfe wiſe firſt began ſtryfe betwixt iuno venus pallas decended ſodayn caſe one aſſent touchyng theyr beaute dome therof committed vnto ſpeake called art parys holdē arte ful prudent right wyſe wel auyſed thy dome ſhal fyne ne may fro decline muſt obeyen one aſſent without ſtrife thy iudgement hercke firſt thou procede eche theim ſhall thy mede conſydre ryght take good hede therto thou appel graunt vnto iuno ſhall gyue plenty richeſſe hyghe renowne fame eke worthyneſſe habundaunce golde treaſour reyſe ſo hyghe honour thou alone ſhalte excelle thy guerdon lyke telle ¶and yf pallas goddeſſe prudence lyſt fyne conclude thy ſentence ſhe may lady appell thy mede ſhe ſhall aſſure wyt eke ſapyence thou ſhalte hooly haue excellence wyſedome diſcrecion diſcerne clereneſſe reaſon alſo fer phebus caſt may lyght ſhall prudent knyght worlde ſyth fyrſt began iuſt reporte manly man thy name none equipollent ¶and venus true clene entent lyſte graunt concluſyon appell haue poſſeſſyon freſhe goddeſſe ſyt ſo hyghe aboue shall enſue haue vnto thy loue fayreſt lady tofore worlde hereafter ſhalbe bore grece thou ſhall knightly wynne aduiſed thou begynne iuſtly deme thynge ſpare ¶and anone gan loke vp ſtare greatly aſtoned beſt tyll laſte ſpake mercurye ſayde certayne ne wolde gyue dome naked myght haue fully lybertee eueriche aduiſedly ſee well conſider euery circumſtaunce fayreſt vnto pleaſaunce goodlyeſt ſpeake womanhede wolde dome procede ¶and anone ye haue herde ſeye deſyre mekely gan obeye haſte buſy cure diſpoyle clothing veſture lyche ſtatute dome bonde point wolde withſtonde myght haue full inſpection fourme ſhape eche proporſyon diſcerne remembre vyſedly ordre euery membre erſt iudge ryght ¶but whan yt thus ſyght gaue venus appell right anone bycauſe ſhe fayreſt eche one moſt excellyng ſothly beatie moſte womanly goodly ſee tho demed playnly ſyght ſtremes eyen bryght yleche glade egall lyght like yt ſterre yt ſheweth towardes ye night whiche called heſperus ſo ſhene venus ſelfe freſhe luſty queene whiche anone heauenly empereſſe dome harty hyghe gladneſſe appell ſhe hooly hath glorye wonne thus iuſtly victory reioyſed tell ſhe feares beautie dyd excell ſhe haſt trewe affection concluded hath fully guerdon full demurely lowe lofte mercury ſobre wordes ſofte deuoyde doubleneſſe ſlouthe lyke beheſt holde wyll trouth ſodaynly without iniurye diſapered god mercurye streyght heauen ryght waye toke anone ſlepe woke ¶wherof lord moſt loue drede ye aduerte wiſely taketh hede beheſt affyrmed certayne vnto aſſured vayne goodly venus lyke haue tolde wherfore rede ye herte bolde ſende ſtronge mighty hande without abode grekes lande fourme haue ſayde thus hope ye ſhall well apayde whan haue ſpede wenus hath hight home retourne lady bryght ſhall ye beſt lyſte ſpeake vayne exchaunge ſyſter wyn agayne thelomon withholden hath yore lo ſay touchyng theffect hooly myne aduyſe tho ſatte hym downe parys hym ſelfe full well aquytt ſaye pryam ala thy wytt neclygence taken kepe thy truſte ſette dremes ſlepe full thynne forſothe thy diſcrecion take grounde falſe illuſyon procede lyke fantaſye vpon ſweuen meint flattery ala reaſon tho nothynge thy guyde pallas wrongly ſette ſyde receyued dewe reuerence iuno eke ſapience good lokynge debonayre treaſour heſtes fayre refuſed ala wylfulneſſe ſhe loue goddeſſe eke alſo vulcanus wyfe whoſe ſeruyce euer werre ſtrife preferred appell poſſede againe ryght paris toke none hede saue vnto luſte ſette aſyde trouth ala yt ful great routh myghty ryche noble towne troye brought full confuſyowne knyghthode hath forſake prudence golde choyſe ytake woman holde hym therto roote wo ſtory ceriouſly ſhall tell dreames longer dwell write forth deiphobus thirde ſonne priamus tale began open audience kynge ſhortly ſentence lyſte trouthe ſpare euen thus gan fantaſye declare ¶my lorde quod euery wyght aduerte ſhulde caſte ſyght future thynge peryll doubte ſerche wel within eke without poynt poynt alwaye reaſō caſte doubtes tournen vp ſo downe ſhulde wyght purpoſe wende matter make ende eyther preſume manhode thought caſteth doutes achieueth lite nought plowman alway caſt aforne many graynes fielde corne shalbe deuoured foules rauynous doth ſowe fieldes plenteous ſhulde neuer vale playne cowardſhyp throwe abrode grayne let ſuche drede layde aſyde holde folye longer abyde yt parys brother make hym ſtronge ſhyppes venge wronge vpon grekes payne might preue ſhortly knight reaſon ye conſyder may man iuſtly may ſaye nay parys hath counſayled wele trouth fer fele errour purpoſe contrary wherfore let hym longer tarye holde waye ſtronge nauye auenge ſhamefull velanye grekes haue done ſo ye lyſt take hede alder dayes v kynred eke fynall execucion recure touchyng exion demeyne ſuch diſhoneſt wyſe agaynſt ryght title iuſtyce wherof thinke giueth hert wounde ſhame ſo newly doth rebounde vpon v ally wherfore beſt eſpye parys take maye voyage ſuche freſhe luſty age manly wende grekes lande force myghtye hande maunger grekes proude moſt elate rauiſhe ſome lady eſtate thā ye may knighthod brother ye lyſte chaunge moſt redy ſhort concluſyon ſe reſtytution exyon ſo parys wende counſayle ſhortly thus end▪ ¶and faſte full diſcrete ſage helenus fourth ſonne age roſe ſeate humble reuerence praying father graunte hym aundience may ſay preſence openly ſhalbe fall moſt ſecrete thynges ſoberlye thus tale began cleane entent trewe affection ¶my lorde quod ſupportacion grace wherin moſt truſt let none offence vnto luſte diſpleaſe yf ſo conceyte declare ſyth meane decetie neuer yet fayled ſentence fyll efte experyence lyke tolde partie pryuye treate eke generall without meanynge doubleneſſe folowed dyd expreſſe remembryng ye ſhall fynde trewe yf god wyll ſhall new spare ſay lyke conceyue dede fraude deceyue declaryng fyrſt trewe entention ſhall folowe concluſion ¶that yf parys grece wende truſteth well wyll v ſhende goddes ſo reuelacion haue made playne demonſtration eke knowe aſtronomye neuer yet prophecye deceyued ſhulde fall none lyſte counſayle call taught thyng ſhall betyde wherfore praye rancour pryde enuye wrought olde hatred take vengeaunce ye procede aduyſe lyke ye purpoſe ſaye playnly ylyſt gloſe ye ſhall repente ſo ye parys ſende grece whiche god defende wytte full well concluſyon shall fully tourne deſtruction fynally vnto ruyne lyke gan afore deuyne fyne folowe ſhall subuercyon towne wall houſe paleys citie al goth nought ye get forme ſemeth ought ynough ſuffyſe haue ſayd ſyth ye wyſe yf ye aduerten ſawe doubte ye wyll withdrawe hande tyme domage aſſayleth conſtraynte rage better betymes abſteyne purpoſe whiche yet grene hede thus haſtely aſſente thynge ſhal echone repente plenerly ſhall nothynge ſocoure ſhal folowe deſpyteful death without excepciowne one abydynge towne fyrſt ſelfe playnly endite shall vengeaunce grekes byte fury mortall tene wyfe fayre hecuba queene shall lede lyfe grekes crueltie ſorowe wo captiuitie lyeges ſworde ſhall pace cruell death withouten grace innocentes merciles ſhall blede aduyſe ye procede wylfulneſſe werre make folyly thus vndertake parturbe quyete reſt ſhal retourne nothyng beſt ruyne v miſchyefe fall counſayle afore ye prouyde letteth wylfulneſſe ſette aſyde specially whan death tolde muſt fyne ye purpoſe holde lo without wordes mo grece ſo parys go ¶and wyſe whan helenus playnly ſayde guydo telleth v tryſte heuy pale deadly face agayne reſorteth ſyttynge place whoſe ſentence aſtoned euerychone sat ſylence ſtylle ſtone powerles hertes efte reſume ſpeake worde man dare preſume preſe kept lyppes cloſe laſte troylous vp aroſe yonge freſhe couragyous alſo aye deſyrous haue armes manly longeth knight whan chere ful glad light sawe father brethern euerychone inly troubled thus ſpake anone ¶oh noble worthy ſyttyng enuiron hyghe prudence great diſcrecion manfull alſo hyghe courage ſodein fere hath brought ī rage new trouble cropen breſt ſentence coward prieſt syth echone ye ſhall euer fynde deſyre veryly kynde lyue luſt voyde awaye trauayle deadly hate battayle wyt fynally applye ſewe luſt lyue glottony fyll ſtomake reſtore mawe reſte eaſe euermore drawe ſewe inwarde appetite ioye delyte eatyng drynkyng couetyſe ſtudye fully deuyſe may folow luſt without ryght nought elles ſetten ſtore ala ſhame ye ſo diſmayde ſytte mate aſtoned afrayde wordes hym helenus fearefull drede lyttle mouſe quaketh ſpeake fyght moreouer agayne ſkylle ryght preiudice goddes taketh hym ſay ſhall fall thynge future ſpecyfye yf ſpirite prophecye graunted hym alone ſpeciall though connyng perygall goddes hauynge preſcience ſhewe afore ſapyence ſhall betyde outher euyll good let let wyght ſo woodd hath wyt gyue therto credence man crafte ſcyence mortall hath connyng deuyne fortune courſe fate termyne suche cauſes hyd conceled ſecree reſerued goddes priuitee men may dyuyne folye take hede lye wherfore rede mattere one al lorde moſt dere exclude drede may diſturbe herte let nothyng perturbe highe courage helenus hath tolde yf herte bolde manhod wold helpe venge wronge let hym go hyde temple ſtronge kepe cloſe contemplation wake praye deuocion without ſocour dayes nyghtes ſuffer ſuche luſty knyghtes haunte youth grene luſtyneſſe manly armes preue hardineſſe may haue better acqueintaūce tyme comyng vengeaunce enmyes cruell foen ſith cōmaunde yt parys may forth gone execute fyne entent afore purpoſed parlement vpon grekes offention perfourme payne talyon wronges olde whiche yet fame reherſed vnto alderſhame world ye wote lece therwithall troylous helde peace ſodeynly preſent began one holly one aſſent troylus counſayle greatly preyſe manhode heauen reyſe freſhe courage hygh proweſſe feruent zeale hardineſſe one herte greatly commende ryght anone made ende pryamus whan done vpon tyme houre none mete goeth within great ilyon ſonnes ſyttyng enuyron mete called hath parys deiphobus alſo full wyſe ſecretely bad ſhulden go ſame day lordes mo panonye haſte maye make ready agayne certayne day wyth araye worthy cheualrye maye get companye towardes grece ſaylen haſtely kynge ſodeynly next day made counſayle call euen thus ſayde afore ¶oh noble lyeges beynge nowe preſent purpoſe ſaye myne entent without abode ye lyſte thyncke vnwyſte grekes pryde tyrrannye malys olde compaſſed enuye many wyſe haue agayne v wrought whiche ſo grene foryet nought day day encreaſynge euer mo remembraunce renewed wo whan recorde caſten vp downe greues exiowne ſeruytude amonge doth ſoiourne whiche ofte day cauſeth mourne hath herte almoſt aſonder ryue conſyder ſe lyue whoſe crueltee haue dere bought albeit haue meanes ſought haue reſte without whan grece ſent anthenore peaſably ſyſter recure paciently ſurplus endure nought toke hede offred goodlyhede herde lacke gentilneſſe recorde whiche doubleth diſtreſſe ¶wherfore muſt teacheth ſurgerye ſharpe irous ſeken remedye cutte away roote rounde dead fleſhe feſtred wounde whiche wyll voyde wt oynetmentes ſofte albe applyed full ofte right ſo muſt attempte dureſſe get recure whan fayreneſſe may none haue wherfore aduyſe purpoſe haſt ſende paryſe forth grece ſome lady wyn bringe home ſhal within strongly kepe mauger ſayth nay tyll ſee ſome agreable day fayne lyke myne opinion haue exchaunge exion ſyſter namely loue ſo may fayle ſhal thus goddes v fauourable counſayle alſo acceptable echone whan thynge toucheeh comonte wyttye men affyrmed comon ought confyrmed thyng touchyng ſhuld fyrſt appreued euerychone achieued wherfore caſte aduiſe plainly worke forthwith withall noble pryam ſodeynly peaſe amonges preaſe whan whyſhte alder ſyghte knyght vp roſe percheus highte ſonne great euforbyus de tranſformatis ſayth ouidius fayneth whylom ſoule pithagoras hooly tranſſumed ſo wryte ouyde touchyng wyll longer byde tell forth percheus afore kynge whiche gan tale thus ¶my lyege lorde vnto hygh nobleſſe diſpleaſe worthyneſſe though preſence maieſtye ſhall ſaye acquyte towardes fayth trouthe ſothfaſtly may ſlouthe touchyng honour without dread zeale fayth bren doth glede harmes byd ye beware doubtleſſe affyrme well dare ſo ye ſtande firſte aduyſe ye purpoſe ſenden forth paryſe doubte ſhall rewe god well wote olde newe father called enforbius diſcrete wyſe ryght vertuous knowyng afore euery thynge preſcyence wyttynge tell playnly philoſophye heauenly ſawe eye na thyng might ſo ſecretely hyd hym ne yet pryuytee ne knewe wyt ſo ſage laſte whan age hundred yere locke grey hore well bethincke complayned ſore wepte alſo pitie tenderly fully affyrmyng parys vtterly wente grece rauyſhe hym wyfe ſhulde inſue ſuche mortall ſtryfe vpon v ſothly citie shulde ſcindred aſſhes tourned ſhulde nothyng v ſocour grekes ſworde ſhulde cruelly deuoure hye lowe playnly ſpare none wherfore praye amonge euerychone tell haue ye deſpyte wronge venge putteth reſpyte rancour olde reade ye lete tranquyll quyete haſtyneſſe ye ſubmytte fortune lyſte ſo falſely flytte trouble auncient enmyte newe ſterynge felycitie ye iourney thus aſſente ye euerychone full ſore ſhall repente yf ye wyll algates thether ſende parys ſtede let ſome wende leſt voyage ſpede loe counſayle fully rede sayde vnder ſupporte grace ¶and ſodaynly gan echone chace penthens loude agayne hym crye repreuynge hym prophecye father confuſyon ¶but oh ala reuolucion ioye wo felicitee thing tofore ordeyned muſt nedely ſtate thynges wt fate ſo englewed ſhall fall may eſchewed whiche cauſed taſſent one al haſt parys ſhulde gone vnhappely wt hap enuolued ¶and thus concluding counſaile diſſolued caſuelly loe befell ryght aduyſe vnto eres ran caſſandra ſhe great afraye ſodayne wo gan cryen welaway ¶alas quod ſhe ala wyll ye ſhall parys grece go worde ſhe braſte wepe full piteouſly inwarde ſyghes depe gan wayle ſowne payne furyouſly noyſe complayne wofull rage many pyteus ſowne made mortall lamentatiowne deade ſhe might withholde heare torne fyſtes folde ſayde ala hundred ſyth ah ſtormy fortune lyſt thou kythe thy cruell force oure aduerſytie vpon v eke citie mortall yre gery violence ſword vengeaunce worſe thā peſtilēce ¶oh troye troye gylte ala haſt thou done thy treſpas euerſed tourned nought wylde fyre thy ſynne dere abought ah pryam kynge vncely thy chaunce haſt thou gylte outher greuaunce thy goddes wyrched vnryght prouoke ſhewe cruell might vpon thy bloud ala haſt thou oh mother myne oh hecuba alſo maner cryme importable offence haſt thou cōmyt haue ſuch recompence daye abyde oh noble worthy quene thy ſonnes ſuche vengeaunce ſene oh wofull deth cruell horryble ala ye credible counſayle ſuche harmes eſchewe mortall purpoſe fully remewe go ordeyned thought hart hath ſo cōſtrained vnneth may wo endure father wofull creature helde ſtreight way falleth plat groūd wepyng water drownde chekes ſo gan teares rayne ſhe myght conſtraint paine vpon hym ſhe gan clyppen crye beſechynge hym ſhape remedye pyteous voyce ſhe yt knewe ful wele matter playnly euerydele ſhall befall full mynde ſodeyne harmes ſhal inſue behynde clamour vayne ſhall fall ſome clerkes ſayne ne may well men eſchewed eke fortune great aduerſytie haſty ire furyous wood aye vnkynde vnto troyan bloud cauſeleſſe agaynſt ſore agreued rancour ſodaynly amened blind awaite catche traūce vyolence vnhappy chaunce hath wt ſweyght tourned whele vnſtable ſhe enuyous mutable haſten troyens theyr confuſyon wylfulneſſe vndiſcretion agaynſt grekes quarell make therupon haue counſayle take haue achieued ye herde deuyſe without aſſent moſt wyſe yf ſo diffynycyon hector herde concluded reaſon matter helenus counſayle take percheus aduerted wyſely ſentence without faynyng gyuen full credence caſſandra neuer lyſt lye aduyſe harde prophecye poynt poynt caſte aforne ſuch miſchief tho lorne floured yet theyr felycitie without domage aduerſytie fortune fortholde courſe alway whoſe wyll abydeth ſo ſayth ye nay ſhe cauſed voyage forhead playne blandiſhing vyſage ſugre ſhad venim roote bytter taſte ſhewing ſoote wrynckled double like horned ſnayle fayth face fraud ay tayle haſte troyans accorde one parys ſhuld grece gone ye haue herde ſayne herupon caſt theim ordayne ¶how priam king ſent paris deiphobus others worthy troy grece aduenge rauiſhinge ſyſter exion returne rauyſhed faire heleine wife menelaus brought troye ca xiii time approched whē ye ſon ſhene golden wayne whyrleth vp atwene cleare ſterres hyades ſo read haue theyr ſcyte bulles head pleyades ſeuenth ſterre ſo bryght whych ſyxe appearen ſyght ſeuenth draweth aſyde couertly doth beames hide whylom ſhe hath done great offence vnto v cauſeth abſence ſhe dare ſhewe ſtremes cleare ſyſtren openly appeare whelom ſhe god mortall ſyn committed cryminall noyſed kouth thrughout ye heuē ſhe alone amonge ſiſtrē ſeuen shroudeth v ſhamefeſtly chere ¶and titan zodiak ſphere atwene theſe ſterres taken ſee bul ſixtenth degre vpon time ioly grene maye flora hewes gaye hath euery playne medowe hil vale floures quicke nothing pale ouer ſpred clad lyuery newe braūches bloſme diuerſe luſty hewe byd v fully glad lyght aſſuraunce fruit haue hight agayne autumpne ſo liſt thē ſhake vine ripeth euery grape thus ſeaſon moſt luſty diſporte embraſeth hertes newe recomforte onely hope kinde dewe holſom fruite ſhall bloſmes ſewe whan time cometh reuolucion thus may ye luſty freſhe ſeaſon whan byrdes ſynge theyr hermonye ſame time pannonye repeyred deiphobus parys theim brought choſen deuyſe thre thouſande knightes redy gone theim grece ſhippes many one ful vitayled may theim nede theſe ſhippes nomber rede two twenty like wryte guydo without ado kinge commaundeth vnto eneas anthenor polydamas al haſte theim redy make parys knyghtly vndertake ye haue herde iourney acheue time whan toke theyr leue pryamus ſhorte concluſyon sheweth effect entencion ſpecially theyr deuer done recure ſyſter exione ye haue herde tofore tell ſhuld matter dwell whan ready without ſoioure parys firſt lord gouernour voyage made pryamus brother called deiphobus theyr leue haue take longed deutye ſhip right manfully without abode gan theym ſelues dreſſe name venus goddeſſe mighty ioue taken theyr iourney anker hoiſt forth large ſea gan ſaile haue winde wil water calme blandiſhing ſtill without trouble boyſtous wawe coſtes ginnen faſt drawe grekes lande nothing ne theim let fortune theyr courſe met grekiſhe ſhyp mine auctour telleth thus whych king menelaus towarde pyram famous ſtronge citie viſite duke high degre neſtor hight menelaus brother eke vnto king famous wiſe worthy great agamenon greateſt name reputacion amonges grekes worthineſſe menelay ſtorye beareth wytneſſe huſbande quene heleyne ſhe ſyſter brother tweyne caſtor pollux whych tolde hand ſo worthy knightes hold time like degre stryneſter theyr moſt cheif citye helde houſholde ſolempne royall loue tho ſo ſpeciall wyll herte accordinge dede atwixe theim two brotherhede none could lyue alone eke mayde hermyone yonge doughter quene heleyne fayreneſſe moſt inly ſouereyne moſt paſſyngly excellyng beaute ¶and thus troians ſayling ſea towarde grece amonge wawes wete auenture theim happed mete kinge menelaus ſayling theyr ſyde none theim liſt pryde enquere paſſen forthe ſwyft luſty paſe none theym could knowe aye wynde peaſebly gan blowe troian flete cauſyng whyle approche noble yle called cithera daye hauen haſte may anker caſt boūd theyr ſhippes ſtrōge theim liſt tarye longe take lande ful many luſty man araying theim freſhly ¶now yle paſſyng excellence temple great reuerence buylded olde foundacion honoured moſt region throughout land fer nere feaſt day aye yere yere like fil reuolucion repeyringe thither great deuocion honour onely venus goddeſſe grekes al theyr buſineſſe honoured moſt euery maner age giftes brynging pilgremage great offryng ſacrafiſe vſed theyr paynem wiſe ¶for phane knele wake herte contryte theyr prayer make ſtatue gaue euery queſtyon perfect anſwere ful ſolucion ceremony venus loute euery thinge wherof doubt hadden ful declaracion thus grekes vpon citheron halowe feaſt riche great araye rytes dewe fer forthe may hope fully better thryue ¶and fortune aryue vp land aduenture caſe ſame tyme feaſt halowed many greke coming fro euery coſte temple go pilgramage theyr vowes acquite place reliques viſyte parys eſpye choſen hath companye worthieſt cheſe may temple toke right way ful wel beſene knightly wiſe honour ſacrafiſe ful humble grekes liche many ouche many iewel riche golde ſyluer ſtones riche perre ſpendeth like degre quit manly oblacions ful deuoutly oryſons demeneth ioye ſe ¶now parys paſſing great beaute amonges euer alyue none might wt ſtriue troian greke ſpeake ſemeliheade wonder freſhe luſty reade porte full lyke gentil knighte whoſe perſon haue ſight gan preaſe nigh fere royally bare gere preaſe high eſtate loowe knight deſyren knowe men aſken buſyly whenſe came cauſe coming enquyring one one prudently kept theym euerychone nothing openly eſpyed theyr anſwer ſo ſelues guyde euery thing kept ſecree eueriche theim ſo auiſee albe ſome openly declare ne liſt ſpare tolde playnly cauſe cominge howe pryam ſtronge mighty kinge father moſt royall renowne came alſo exiowne thus eche theim gan rowne pryme face whan came towne therupon ymagynatyfe sore muſyng much inquiſitife eche ſuſpection deminge therof lyke theyr opynyon ratheſt nothinge ne knewe folkes done thinges newe whyles matter treate ſondry wiſe among theyr wordes greate ſaying theim gan anone atteyne eares quene heleyne nigh beſide regyon ſhe herde relacion reporte come bytwene fayre heleyne freſhe luſty quene anone ſhe ſothe vnderſtode without delay abode caſteth ſolempnytye freſhe folke phrigia ſe wel god wote entention ſe parys deuocion vnder colour holy pylgramage temple ſhe taketh voyage great meyne royal apparayle parys ſe ſhe wyll fayle ¶but oh ala luſty newe fyre herte hath nowe enflawmed deſyre go vigiles ſpectacles none holyneſſe heare myracles hath meued ſhal befall maner woman drawe thether platly conclude ſure multytude ygathered lybertye ſee may finde oportunitye theyr deſyre ful narowe awayte couertly theyr eyen baite place ſet theyr pleſaunce pryuely haue dalyaunce ſome ſygne caſting eye token ſhewing hert drye touche hādes ſtole amonge preſe arme fote catche vp theyr leſe lyſt free bonde nature holde honde ayen whoſe ſleyght auaileth wyt myght theim liſt yt wronge ryght aye achieue ſo ſayth yea nay agayne whoſe luſt defend man may ¶thus guydo aye curſed falſe delyte ſpeak thē harme hath caught appetite throughout boke woman ſay yll tranſlate agayne wll hath aye ioye theyr honour ramuerſe ryght ſorye muſt reherſe fel wordes booke yfounde woman ſo mikle bounde echone ſo goodly ſo kynde dare theim ſay finde guydoes write throughout troy booke redde feare herte quoke veryly wyttes gan fayle whan therof muſt maken reherſaile like decrete guydo wyte ye ſhall heare anone chit quene heleyne cauſe ſhe went herte deuoute offryng preſente temple venus goddeſſe thus word word ſayth expreſſe ¶o mortal harme moſt dread fraude ycaſt ſleyght womanhead euery wo ginning crop roote agaynſt whych helpe may bote whan luſt hath dryue theyr herte nayle aye deadly venim ſeweth tayle man hath power reſtreyne recorde take quene heleyne inly brent ala deſyres newe luſt dele thoſe ſtraungers ſhe knewe nat ne neuer ſawe beforne wher ala ful many mē lorne cruel death embraſed cheyne without pyty ſaye thou quene heleyne ghoſt ſpyryte ala hath meued sole fro thy lorde ſuch royaltye thy houſe go among preaſe yu wery liue home peace wenteſt ſtraungers ſe taking hede vnto thine honeſtye thou ſhuldeſt haue kept thy cloſet ſecretly haue paſſed ſo folyly abſence thy lorde ala thou wilful rakel caſe ſe afore ſhuld ſewe al ſone thou drawē mewe coulde kepe home tho thy boūdꝭ thou wēteſt hare among ye houndes caught wilfulneſſe thy deſyre coudeſt compeſſe though thy luſt lyſt refrayne many woman hath caught trayne goyng ſuch halowes ſeke ſyt theim better home kepe cloſe theyr chaumber fle occaſyowne neuer ſhyp ſhuld peryl drowne ryue rocke tempeſt rente caribdis dreached yſhent go wrake wether yll kept hauen ſtyll wil occaſyons eſchewe dread peryll ſewe muſt nedely neceſſytie beware endure aduerſytie fote fro trappes ſpare let take hede fall ſnare harme ydone late compleyne whylom noble quene heleyne ſelfe kept home ſecrete cloſe ne ſo wicke loſe reported yet grene freſhe newe whoſe chaūce vnhappi eche mā ought rew cauſe ſuch deſtruction many worthy confuſyon huſband many mo grekes ſyde thoſe troye alſo ſtorye ye ſhall reade ¶and ſo quene faſt ſhe may ſpede temple hath way ynome full royally whan ſhe come ful deuoutly within citheron made vnto venus oblacion preſence ſyght many one many iewell many ryche ſtone ¶and whē paris thing eſpied temple anone hath hyed ful thriftely haſt myght wher forthwith ſyght goodly fayre freſhe quene cupides darte whet ſo kene ware hath marked ſo aſtoned niſt much meruayleth ſemelineſſe womanhead porte fayrneſſe neuer erſt ne wende nature coud ought haue made ſo fayre creature aungellyke ſhe beaute feminine ſo goodly ſe ſothly dempte liklyneſſe beaute ſome goddeſſe ſo herte aye aſſure ſhe ne mortall creature heauenly fayre ſo celeſtyall thought ſhe partye eft conſydereth auyſely feature ordre curyouſly aye reaſon euery thinge good inſpection golden heare like ſonne ſtreames freſhe phebus bright beames goodly heade fleſhly face full replete beaute grace ylike enewed quickenes coloure roſe lyly floure egally nother wite none exceſſe much lite within cerclynge eyen bryght paradiſe compaſſed ſyght eche hert ye beaute gā perce certaynly ſo ſhall reherce ſhape fourme feature guydo doth ordre ceryouſly head foote clearly deuyſe want englyſhe therto may ſuffyſe wil tunge nothing like want alſo floures rethorike ſewe flouryſhyng peynture diſcryue ſo fayre creature ſo coloures feble feynte nother ennewe wel depaynte eke acqueynted muſe nine therfore excuſe echone neclygence defaute onely eloquence remit guydo ſe deſcriueth ordre beaute take preſumpciowne ¶but wil tell parys vp downe gothe temple eye caſt towardes heleyne gan preſen faſt brent hoote loues fyre enflawmed greatly deſyre oft chaungeth coūtenaunce cheare euer neygheth nere nere ydarted eyen tweyne likewyſe freſhe quene heleyne hote ſhe brent herte priuely albe man outward could eſpye thought ſhe neuer erſt fore men euer yet bore se none ſo fayre like pleaſaunce loke harte ſuffyſaunce temple ſhe taketh hede nought compaſſeth caſteth thought ſhe may catche ſome oportunitye ſpeake lybertye hooly buſyneſſe ſhe felt ſo inly great diſtreſſe oft ſhe chaūgeth coūtenaūce hewe venus hath theim marked ſo newe brondes fyred feruence enflawmed ſodayne influence egally brought rage ſaue eye atwene meſſage eche ſo fyxe haue caſt theyr ſight conceyue wyſt anone right within theim ſelfe theyr herte ment nere euer parys wente ſeke fully get occaſyon might ful relacion theyr hertes conceyte declare ſecretly ſo befell parys nigheth nye place quene heleyne stode ſee atwene thē tweyne broke al ſum theyr whole hert gaue yſſue theyr inward ſmerte done leſt eſpyed whan people moſt occupyed temple ſtare gaſe maſe kept theim cloſe worde aſterte man treaſō myght aduert theim twayne ne would mene laſt parys quene concluded haue wyth ſhorte auyſement fully fine theyr entent ſet time betwyx theim certayne whan appoynten mete agayne leſt men theim ſuſpection made ende without ſermō ſyth departe albe lothe ſoberly anone parys gothe temple breſt euery parte fully gyrt loues fiery darte ſhippes helde right way anone al haſt may whan aſſembled chiualrye one al companye fewe wordes ſhortly tofore theim tale thus began lordinges quod ſhortly expreſſe cauſe kouthe youre worthineſſe father grece v ſent ye knowe chief entent recure ſiſter exion handes mighty thelamon thinge ought eſpye impoſſible ſhortly mine eye waie fer ſe ſo great ſtrong countre allyes aboute euery ſide herte ſo inly full pride yelde vp hath diſdayne therof treate vayne therfore beſt deuiſe sith power may ſuffiſe werrey regiowne egall might renowne lacke men holde felde may win ſpere wt ſhelde tencountre multitude wherfore beſt conclude ſith fortune hath v hither brought goddes haue eke v wrought graciouſly make v londe venus temple faſt ſtronde whiche aboundeth ful great richeſſe grekes offringe vnto goddeſſe londe ſea fro many ſundry porte men woman hyther haue reſort place worſhyp venus wife kinge menelaus preſent ful riche wel beſeyne manhod might atteyne rauiſhe temple ſpoyle theyr treaſour cheſen coyle chefe iewels chargen ſomers wyth golde ſyluer wyth pryſoners maugre theim ſhyppes brynge ſame night without tarying may fayle euer ſaythe nay ye aſſenten worthye pray wherfore haſte ye redy make euery man anone harnes take arme hym well beſt aray aſſente without delaye theyr ſhyppes bydē till night whē phebus chaire wtdrawē light vnder wawes ſterres appeare heauen theyr ſtreames cleare moone time aryſe ſhope theim forth ful thrifty wiſe manly troians armed ſtele bryghte temple holding theyr waye aryght caſten longer tarye proudly enter ſanctuarye chappel called citheron without reuerence deuocion done venus oratorye cleane theyr memorye honour dread obſeruaunce fynally theyr attendaunce myn auctour ſothly diffine ryght nought onely rauyne token came theyr hande rycheſſe treaſour lande golde ſyluer ſtones riche iewelles releques ſacred holy eke veſſels without abode ſacrary yfeare theyr ſhippes carye wonder thynke good kil ſley theim withſtode likewyſe pytie ſe theim blede grekes ſhip lede lyued captyuytie ful many yeare troye citye ¶and while goth parys heleyne embraſeth armes tweyne full humble great reuerence found maner reſyſtence ſat ſhe ſo womanly ther parys ſhe yolde vtterly herte hap yolde came therfore yelde ſhe leſſe feare ſtryue woman ſholde anone gentilneſſe wolde comforteth beſt may led forthe without delaye vnto ſhyppes full buſyly ſet wardes kepe honeſtly temple retourneth agayne ſpoyle robbe make playne temple withe walles wyde ¶nowe ſtode caſtell faſt beſyde yſtuffed well grekiſhe souldeours whych awoke wyth noyſe pylours ſame nyght gan make ſhoute therwithall anone yſſue oute armed ſtele temple reſkewe manfully theim ſewe ſo befell whan togyther mette wyth ſperes ſharpe ſwerdes kene whet ¶they ran togither theſe tygres wilde like wood lion theſe bore vnmilde fayninge foūd theyr fyght albe felde departed ryght troians doubled nomber vtterly grekes encoumbre miſchefe made theim faſt flee purſute ful cruelly theym flee without mercy caſtell gate reſcuſe came late ſkermyſhe fine deathe nowe thei yeldē vp ye breath mightely troians theim aſſayle withſtāde might theim auaile manhod felde haue wonne ryght cruelly begonne haſty wyſe ranſacke caſtell ſhyppe broughten euerydell treaſour golde may win morowe ſalen begyn stuffed good grekyſhe ſea towarde coſtes troye citye ſea calme fully theyr tempeſt ſtormes ill cleare alſo bryght heauen ſpace almoſt dayes ſeuen caſtel called tenedowne aryued ſixe mile towne glad light land wente finde parys ſente meſſāger ſtreyght vnto kinge enfourmeth home cominge theyr exployt tolde theim euery dele pryamus lyketh wonder wele ſo manly haue borne made publyſhe towne theſe tydynges new great ſolempnitie hygh lowe cytie ioye moſte eke leſte remembraunce halowe holde feſte thanke goddes full humble wyſe obſeruaunces ſacrafyce aulters great deuocion whyle tenedon holdeth ſoiourne quene heleyne whiche hap gan rewfully complain vnkouth life dwellen ſtraungers diſconſolate amonge pryſoners ferre ſequeſtred away countrey ſolytarye captiuitie wepeth cryeth pyteous chere wawes vpboyled eyen clere wherof ſtremes chekes rayne conſtraynt inwarde peyne full often ſythes ſonge wel away ſobbing voice ſhe ſo fer awaye departed menelaus whoſe abſence rage furyous hateth lyfe curſeth eke fortune wo ſhe euer doth contune without ſoiourne alway brethern pollux caſtor loue doughter dere pale grene ſhe wexeth chere whylom freſher ſene lyilye ſtalke grene ala chaunged roſen hewe aye elyche wo encreaſeth newe lyke woman ſhe beholde aye ſhe wepte ſhe water wolde ¶till laſte heauyneſſe parys came gentylneſſe recomforte appeſe rage beſyeth hym ſorowes aſwage sayeng ala may mene ye one oh goodly freſhe quene lyſt thus ſelfe ſorowynge diffygure wonder greatly ye may endure moche water cauſeles thus ſhede weping haue dewed ſo wede like conduite ſtreames ran downe penitaunt contriciowne ye diſraye ala ye ſo let fare let ouer go wepynge thought heauineſſe lady diſtreſſe make ende greuaunce eaſe comforte pleaſaunce men may truſte well ye ſhall haue foly ſorowe thus raue lette paſſen ouer theſe ſharpe ſhoures trouth ye youres lyſte ſhal haue ſuffyſaunce ferforth haboundaunce haue ye amonge grekes enſure nothyng feare ſhall holde haue hyght trouthe true knyght worde dede herte entire ſhe anone dolefull chere ſhe myght forſobbyng tho ſuffyce anſwered agayne full lowly wyſe ¶i wote quod ſhe lothe lefe syth caught take miſchiefe vnto wyll may ſeye ſo bounde muſt obeye vnder daunger may flee holde diſtrayned captiuitee ¶ye wot alſo nature dreade ne longeth vnto womanhead ſtraunge ſoyle ſtryue rebell namely quarell shall haue fauour ſuſteyned yf ye lyſte haue pitee myne goodlyhead ye may god deſerue thanke mede wyll rewarde iuſtly geue tho comforte care wo ¶now lady myne quod parys maye lyke deuyſe ſhall truſteth ryght wele trouthe ferre feele thyng may pleaſaunce ye ſhall haue habundaunce enſure heſte fallyble agaſte fully credible wordes heſtes euerychone therwithall ladde ryght anone place royall apparayle comforte wolde auayle ſecretely betwene two parys fyrſte without spake vnto ſayde lady dere fayne ſpeake herte entyer hope ye ſhall hereafter fynde wherfore praye enprenteth mynde ſaye remembraunce ſaye ſyth ye purueyaunce ben goddes brought therto fortune eke ſo dare affyrme playnly fyrſte diſpoſed haue worſte good ſo ye muſt take wherfore reade ſuffer ouer ſhake heauyneſſe loketh ye glad lyght countrey though ye owne lande faythfully tunderſtande ye ſhall haue moche habundaunce euery parte full ſuffyſaunce ſemeth pleaſaunt one thyng dare well auaunt countrey ſhalbe founde euery thyng plenteouſly habounde ful grekes yonder though ye ben farre ſonder lande called achaye cauſe whye ye ſhoulde diſmay syth ye worſhyp reuerence honour greater excellence ſhalbe cheriſhed ye afore ye playne ye haue forbore owne lord left ſole ye maken al wo dole ye ſhall haſte ſette better eaſe certaynly ſo diſpleaſe offende vnto womanhead ſtede hym purpoſe dread wedde trewe man loue ſerue euer without faynyng lyues ende lowly kynde dylygent eke laborous whylom menelaus euery thynge luſtes obeye haue trouthe tyll tyme deye ¶and though wordes plain loue god haue diſdeyne requeſt grutche leaſt ſtocke royall deſcended come hygh bloud menelay byrth good loue farre trewe erſt chaunge newe ¶wherfore leue thus playne wepe let ſome comforte boſome crepe wo appeaſe worth haw lette ſome myrth herte adawe beſeche womanhead wordes ye lyſt take hede ¶alas quod ſhe myght befall haue ylefte frendes one ſtraunge lande al alone ſhuld thā ſtil complaine one haue cauſe god wote pley yet chekes kepe drey ſalte teares ala wyll none ende myne aduerſyte good fayth agaynſt kynde ſodaynly tabandon mynde thilke thyng eyther ioye ſmerte worlde ſytteth nexte herte ala ſo ſore deſtrayned ſyth goddes haue ordeyned better chaunce hope vnto muſt take gre humbly accepte alſo ſonde weake power withſtonde wherfore ſhal agayne wyll ſtriue al wo herte fele ryue conſent lowly admytte thylke thynge fro whiche may flytte maugre wyll neceſſytie fully obey ye lyſt wil helpe although ſayed nay thus ſhe playneth al euer ſhe may little little ſorowe aſwage ſhulde ſhe aye lyue wo rage leſe ſelfe ſo tender creature herte ſtele ne myght endure aye woman maner kynde ſorowe make ende tyll leyſure wepte haue full laſte whan gynnen dull make ſorowe happeth faſte grace ſoone ouer caſte lyghtly catche comforte ſmerte ſo tender yt men may conuerte fro wo ioye thought diſſeuer ſtorme may laſte euer clerkes wyſe bookes lyſte diſcerne thynge vyolente may nothyng eterne ſtormes phebus bryghter ſo comforte counſayle parys adawed olde ſorowe euen lyke glade morowe veray kynde ſeweth dercke nyght proceſſe herte wexeth lyght wepyng dryed well lyke ſtorye ſhall anone v tell howe parys receyued troye retourne maryage heleyne capitulo xiiii vvhan ſo ye quene called heleine adawed drery peyne wawes heauy cheare chekes gonnen clere parys herte freſhe amerous haſte hath ſente kyng pryamus horſe men apparayle clothes golde full noble entayle made heleyne wrought none ryche perle many ſondry ſtones agayne commyng troye towne parys tenedowne shappeth lede troye pryamus mette waye full royally faſte myght hye many lorde companye full many lady freſhe well beſeyne many mayde ryde agayne fyrſt eſtates communers nowe parys pryſoners set order tweyne tweyne rode next quene heleyne deiphobus vpon ſyde knyghtes enuyron dyd ryde nexte hym rode worthy eneas troyan called pollydamus meane ſuynge eche degree gentylmanly ioye ſee eche kepyng certayne ſpace forth ryden ſofte pace tyll kyng mette ſodaynly receyued hath full ſolempnely beſte coulde goodly toke rayne hande quene heleyne conueyed forth citie great preyſe abode ſee ſondry folke ſhoued faſte croude ſhyrle trumpettes yreyſed loude vp ſkye goth blyſfull ſowne whan people entreth towne many nother dyuers inſtrumente tofore gate went ſondry wyſe made melodye heauenly armonye muſycke touched vpon ſtrynge corde euen one iuſtly accorde wolde herte rauyſhe ioye whan entred troye amydde palayſe pryamus alight anone faſte euer myghte chambre ryche well beſey quene heleyne haſte dothe conuey cōmaundyng eft herte wyll thought offycers fayle nought thynge ſhe bethyncke ſpyces parted anone ye wyne drinke kyng toke leue tyll ſupper ſhe whyles chaungeth attyre ¶but ioye towne euery place men went vp downe rude ſothly wryte muche herte troyans delyte ſafe ſounde retourned parys wende haue ben ioye paradyſe ſo well ſped iourne hath one loſte meyne wherof herte glad lyghte haſte nexte nyght wryte guydo without tarying longe erely morowe larke ſonge pallas temple myne auctor ſayth aſſured othe eke fayth bond wedlocke heleine euermore laſte atwixte tweyne knotte knitte ſacrament thus done fully thaſſent firſt kyng alſo thaduyſe citie fauour paryſe ſo feaſt great ſolempnitee continued muche royaltee weddyng myrthe ſolace towne eyght dayes ſpace ſhulde wryte reuell ye daunces freſhe aray countenaunces ſcole touch lokes amerous priue grutche yt ialous great iuſtes bourdes tornaye amydde paleſtre many ſundry playe dyuers courſes eke euery feſte large plente done moſt leſte ſtraunge meates maner ſeruyce haue none englyſhe deuyce paſſe ouer ¶but whan weddyng came vnto ye ere caſſandra fyrſte dyd eſpye thouſande ſythe ala ſhe gan crye pyteous wo vntreſſed heeres ſayde thus albe ſpreynte teeres wretched troye errynge caſe within thy ſelfe ſuffer treſpaſe conſente vnto ſuche folye ſuſteynyng foule auouterye parys ſhulde taken vnto wyfe quene heleyne whoſe huſband alyue oh wofull troye cruell thy fate beware almoſt late tyme come thou ſhalte deſtroyed many father ſhall ſonne ſee hole morne ſhalbe ſlayne eue amyddes fyelde wyll ſore greue many wyfe ſhall carefully bewepe ſe huſband large woundes depe gryde body pale colde grene ala ſhall ye ſorowe mowe ſuſteyne ¶ah wretched mother ſhall ye endure ſe child cruell aduenture afore ſlayne withouten remedye wyll helpe though ye clepe crye ¶ah mother myne heccuba quene ſhalt thou byde ye ſharpe ſtoundes kene thy worthy ſonnes ſe afore ſlawe fyelde cruelte ydrawe ¶ah blynde people death yu takeſt hede nylte thou worke rede caſe prudent wyſe take awaye heleyne fro paris right requireth withouten lorde iuſtely reſtore ¶what trowen ye thefte cruel dede shall paſſe thus nay nay withouten drede ſword vengeaūce ſhal ful ſharply byte offence ſhall beare wyte paleys houſe ſe within throwe toures hye layde erthe alowe ala ala ſaye heleyne vnhappy woman cauſer payne harde vnſely alſo graceleſe vnwealfull woman diſturbler peace thou haſt v brought miſchefe kyndled bronde burne v yfeare ala thou arte grounde roote many drery feaſt funerall ſhall beholde amonge v towne wiſe caſſandra vp downe aboute ran ſubarde ſtrete crieth one euer ſhe mete full ofte ſyth ala welaway tyll pryamus bycauſe affray noyſe ſhe tho make without abode anone doth take bounde faſt fetred pryſon without mercy remyſſyon toke hede ſadde trouthe wordes routhe ſhet vp bondes great ſtronge without pitie ſhe abyde longe thus pryſon whyle let morne grekes wyll agayne retourne thunhappy tyme ſame whyle falſe
