fortune frendly gan ſmyle vpon troyans bad mery highly gan goddes hery wenyng ioye haue aſſured weale nothyng aduerting tournyng ye whele laſteth ſtable throwe whē men moſt truſt ſhe make mowe tourne forhead face wrythe suche ioye ſhe hath doubleneſſe kythe wrappe clereneſſe vnder cloude agaīſt whoſe might ther mai mā hī ſhroud whē moſt ſhe flattereth thē ſhe leſt triſte ioye troyans lyttell wyſte ſhe hath mente confuciowne whyle aboute towne wende grekes haue gotten full recure domages haue ſure thilke pray ye paris thē wonne wycked fame rumour yronne ſwift wingꝭ al yt haue wroughte menelay fydynges ybrought whyles abode neſtor pirrha firſte temple cithera ſpoyled robberye golde treaſoure tyrrannye vpon men troyans execute aſſaylyng ſuite grekes made cruelly ne ſpared vtterly man woman came waye ne toke ladde praye theyr ſhyppes alſo fyght afore caſtell nyght ¶and alder laſte heareth wyfe loued derely lyfe tenderly god wote thouſande folde herte waxed colde ſtone therto pale hewe hertye wo ſo inly gan renewe fyrſt whan harde name ſowne without anone fell ſowne ne myght endure ſtande til duke neſtor toke hym hande hym adawed deadely ſwowe ala quod haue loſt howe lyues luſte hertes ſuffyſaunce ah death come make greuaūce fully ende thy cruell darte wounded euery parte herte alſo korne euery veyne wyfe myne owne heleine deforced fro welaway farewell ioye farewell olde playe haue ſtraungers poſſeſſyon whiche wyll full confuſyon ala cheryſhe trete fayre heleyne ſo ſwete ye gone penſyfneſſe ſleath may wayte death amyd wo menelay ſhope hym go reygne lyttell beſyde axeth horſe ſaid wolde ryde sole complaine yt felte greue whyle neſtor wyll leue go hym conſolacion frendly ryght hauynge compaſſion hym comforte full myght leading many worthy knyght reygne menelaus ¶than fyrſt ſtory telleth v ſent kyng agamenon caſtor come anone pollux myght ſo comen three ſaw brother ī ſuch miſchief brought almoſt murdred owne thought without abode wyſe agamenon gyue hoope conſolacion dyd labour diligence entere sayinge hym ye ſhall ¶oh brother mine wo heuineſſe deadly ſorowe thus inly may oppreſſe knightly hert trouble manhead furiouſly ywys nede though ryght required vtterly ſorowe hadden cauſe yet ſemeth iuſte prouidence ye ſlyly ſhulde dyſſymule offence sith eche wyſe man aduerſytie shulde fame chere kepen ſecree inwarde wo bynt hym diſtreſſe manly force ratheſt compeſſe ſpyryte ire melancolye people myght eſpye doctryne prudent whan man furye rent fayne chere tyll tyme ſe leyſure vengeaunce kyndell may fyre ſorowe ſhewed ſhall fayne ſo taketh hede doth thynges twayne cauſeth frendes ſyghe ſore enemyes reioyſe thy frende herte ſorye nature thyne enemye glad thy myſaduenture wherfore herte whā wo doth moſt haboūde faineth gladneſſe thyne enemye confound ſhew chere thou roughteſt nought moſt greuous thy thought yu haſt moſte matter complayne make good face glad porte ye faine teares though thou diſtylle rende thy ſelfe thou woldeſt ſpylle helpeth ledge thy greuaunce honour nother purſuite vengeaunce ſorowe makynge mowe execute though laſt ay ther cometh therof frute men ſay diſſimule wronge ſlyghe herte ſtronge peaſyble ſmerte token hath manly herte wepe woman rage whiche contrary hygh courage word weping auenge paine meanes worſhyp attayne let v ſworde wordes fyght tunge appeſe māhod preue might worde winde water wepe though tempeſt fluddes depe two encreaſe euer mo may augment wo foon therof dole heauy chere encreaſe ioye wherfore brother whyle acoye cruel tourment byndeth ſo ſore prouerbe hath ſayd full yore proweſſe manly knyght proued moſt miſchyefe myght aſſured aduerſitee strongly ſuſteyne wo cowardly courage ſubmytte euery peryll honour flytte diſpeyre hope alway wele haue truſte trewe ſtele tacheue aye take hande fynally vnderſtande hym ſelfe hath good fantaſye ſet vpon put inpartye befall happe happe may takyng chaunce tourneth play fyne ſuche gladly victorye fayle ſelde palme glorye tyme ſpeke wordes fewe oh brother myne manhode ſhewe plucke vp herte make ſtronge venge damage wronge ſhall echyone helpe lay hande kynges duke lordes lande atones buſyneſſe behyght harmes redreſſe deſpyte euer v lette ſhall v lodge tentes ſette euen fyelde afore troye towne beſeage deſtructiowne albe therof ſet daye brother firſt haſte may let maken letter without ſermon lordes region matter touchynge vyllanye come gyther ſhape remedye theffect ſayne ¶and thus releaſed ſomwhat payne menelays cōfort brother whan ſawe myght none tale kynge made ende thrugh ye lande letter ſende fyrſt kynne allye come helpe hym curteſye ¶and fyrſt menelaus came achylles patroclus alder nexte ſtronge dyomede many another helpe nede echone open parlement accorded full aſſente gouerned agamenon lyſt ordayne diſcrecion voyage made hym gouernour hooſte chieftaine emperour amonge full vnitee vpon troyans auenged bee purpoſe neuer remewe fyrſt fynde parys ſewe voyage toke ye worthy brethern tweine pollux caſtor recure heleyne yet neuertheles ſome bokes lyſten tell theſe kynges longer wolde dwell alder faſte parys agone toke ſhyppe folowed hym anone many worthy company doubtleſſe yf olde bokes lye ſayled dayes three troyewarde large ſee tempeſt roſe wyndes dyd awake heauen derke cloudes blake haue day tourned nyght bryght phebus mirked light fyry lenen ſtroke thonder smote maſte ſhyuerde ſonder ſo derke lyghte myght adawe ſea gan ſwell many ſturdy wawe roſe hyghte large mounte fell downe ſwapped frounte euen ſhyppe plunged full lowe vp downe forcaſt ouerthrow ſhyppes tempeſt fro fomy water grene whyte blo feruent boylyng pytche blacke ſtorme wynd al goeth wracke hydouſly blaſtes theim dryue euery borde gan ryue peryſhed ſcaped man atones reherſe dead drowned tempeſt ſodaynly ſcaped none ſay certaynly except brethern ſuch bookes tel one heauen lowe hel lordes made tabyde eternally ¶and ſome fayne theyr poeſy goddes haue theim defyed like heauen yſtellifyed theyr ſhyppes ware ygo wrake made ſterres zodyake ſygne tranſfourmed vtterly whych clerkes called gemyny whych ſygne conſtellation mercury houſe manſyon kinde femell maſculyne whych egle alſo dolphyne haue theyr aryſyng reuolucion tayle alſo aboue dragon exaltate thyrd degree gemyny whych ſygne hathe moſt pouſte hande armes man oute doubte like lucina halt courſe aboute wyſe brether twayne heauen rapt theſe poetes fayne tempeſt ye get wiſe grekes ſea ende made ful wylfully erneſt firſt came vnhappely theim echone ginning theyr wo finall chaunce brether two ¶how ye grekes aſſembled aduēged yt troians rauiſhing helein ca xv bvt aſmuche dare frigius boke whilom curyous fourme troiens grekes deſcriue lyke ſawe auctour lyue ſhape fourme complexiowne partye theym troy towne grekes good auiſement time trewſe amonge theim wēt seyng maner theyr gouernaunce porte theyr chere wt euery circūſtaūce namely tho high degre forgate one looſe qualyte condicions alſo theyr ſtature deſcryue dare cure grekiſhe tunge beginning heleyne like tofore ye haue herd ſeyne beaute ſemelyneſſe ſeryouſly guido doth expreſſe saue ſayd lytell ſpace ſtrype endlong face whych wryte became wonder wele embelyſhing beaute euerydele like dare maketh deſripcion ¶and firſt ſayeth king agamenon good ſhape high ſtature might laboure beſt endure vnpacient lyue quyet armes ſo egall ſo mete coloure whyte good proporcion flemytek complexion diſcrete hardy wonder vertuous ſpeche ryght facundious coud wel euery thinge demene ¶but menelay ſtature meane proporcioned atwix ſhorte longe worthy armes delyuer ryght ſtronge courage hert vygorous semely alſo aye deſyrous lyue werre rather peace ¶and furthermore ſpeake achilles ryght fayre great ſemelyneſſe aborne heyr criſpyng thickneſſe eyen glawke large ſtepe great ſhuldred brode wt breſt ful ſquare mete endure armes fel coragious loke wonder amerous high ſtature large giftes eke ſtrength greke ſpend ſet lytel charge herte ſo plenteous large felde paſſyng chyualrous ¶and tell forth tantalus ſanguine hewe hauing much reed diuerſe eyed aye meuing head huge making alſo great ſtrengthe wel anſweryng hys brede lengthe hatinge ſtriue ſawe nede ryght trewe worde alſo reade neuer quarel wolde take hande fyght might vnderſtande fully grounded vpon ryght wolde quyte hym like knyght ¶cilcus ayax right corpulent well cladde ſet al entent ryche aray ful curyous although body corſyous armes great wt ſhoulders ſquare brode almoſt horſe lode hygh ſtature boyſtous pres ſpeche rude rechles ful many worde ydel hym aſterte coward herte ¶an ayax thelamonyous alſo dyſcrete vertuous wonder fayre ſemely beholde whoſe heyr black vpward ay gā folde compas wiſe rounde ſphere muſyke none pere hauing voyce full melodye right well entuned hermonye inuentife counterfete inſtrumentes aſwell ſmal grete ſundry wiſe longing muſyke yet good practike armes eke noble knyght man orped hardyer fight deſyrous haue vyctorye deuoyde pompe hatyng vaynglorye ydle laude ſpent blowe vayne ¶of vlyxes ſhall alſo ſayne ſo noble worthy dayes ful wyles ſleyghty aſſayes meaning double deceyuable forge leyſyng alſo wonder able face playn coud make toughe mery worded ſelde loughe counſayling diſcret ryght prudent tyme moſt eloquent holpe grekes often theyr nede ¶and ſpeake worthy diomede full wel compact growe well length ſturdy porte famous eke ſtrength large breſted ferſe alſo ſyght deceyuable euer hyght haſty teſtyf ſmyte reckles medlyng aye ſelde peace ſeruauntes ful inpacient baraytous ſo euer went lytel worthe diſpoſycion lecherous eke complexion loue oft ſyth parte brenning within cupydes fyery darte ſpechles ful ofte felt ſore ¶what ſhal ſayne eke duke neſtore longe ſtature wel compact wythall corbe ſhoulders middell ſmall handes ſtrong armes large roūde counſalyng prudent wyſe yfounde whoſe wordes ſugred wyth pleaſaunce vpon frende hauing aye remembraunce trouthe ne coud fayne anger might refrayne ſo fret wyth melancolye man myght yre modefye albe laſte lytell ſpace could ſuffer anone would pace lightly came lyghtly went awaye ¶and protheſalyus yt freſhe araye wonder ſemely great beaute trowe fayrer might man ſe good ſtature delyuer ful lyght man ſwyfter ſpeake myght makyng paſſyng ſtronge ferſe courage lothe take wronge ¶and tell neptolomus making wonder corſyous whoſe heyr blacke ſhining doth geat eyen rounde brode therto great large breſted ryſyng backe ſpeche ſtamerd whan ſpacke cauſes could medle wele lawe ful depe fele luſt beſet plees ¶but tell pallamides king naulus ſonne withouten wene face fayre body longe lene manful hert hardy battayle deſyrous enemye aſſayle famylyer curteyſe therto right tretable al dedes inly worſhipable giuing large paſſing grete fame whoſe bounteful wide ſprange name many land ſtorye telleth thus ¶and next finde polydamus worthy greke great thyckneſſe wombe ſwolle enboſſed fatneſſe vnneth might ſelfe ſuſtene yet herte ful proude kene right ſurquidrous ful penſyfeneſſe ſelde glad ſo thought oppreſſe ¶but machaon like wryte guydo longe ſhort betwyx two ful proude ferſe deuoyde pacyence vengeable hym offence yet balde coote whoſe forhead euen roote heyr fallen waſted clene away ſelde neuer would ſlepe daye ¶and ouermore tellen cryſyde stumbleth pen longe ſhe dyed mayſter chauncer diligence deſcryue great excellence beaute ſo mayſterly take high folye wyſe adde therto wel wote anone haue ſothe thāke deſerue maye cauſe wrytyng ſo gay wryte muſt trouthe leue troye booke matter breue ouer paſſe go doth guydo ordre ceryouſly muſt offencion necligence preſumpcion ſet euen amiddes twayne great cauſe haue matter complayne attropos enuye tho brake thred made dye noble galfryde chefe poete brytayne among engliſhe yt cauſed firſt rayne golden droppes rethorike ſo fyne rude language onely tenlumine god praye ſoule haue whoſe helpe nede muſt craue ſeke boke left behinde goodly worde therin co finde ſet amonge croked line rude whych wryte ſymylitude rubye ſtant ſo royall renowne within ryng coper latowne ſtant making doubtles amonge bokes englyſhe pereles ful eaſy knowen ſo excellēt making equipolent halte ſo taketh hede medle makyng without drede whan would ſtyle counterfete may alday colour grinde bete tempre aſour vermilyon al holde preſumpcion foloweth therfore let fyrſt wil excuſe procede haue erſt begon fauour certayn con troye booke make ende left wyl agayne nowe wende vnto criſyde though ſuccour rethoryke haue floure hewes ryche ſtones yet perre al bare curyoſytye though crafty ſpeche enbroude ſleue yet al wil leue ay bolde bayarde blynde caſt peryl way finde right ſo wil ſtumble forth haed vnconning take better hede beaute diſcryue ſothe al tho alyue one ye fayreſt calchas doughter dere therto ſhap face cheare might fayrer creature high lowe meane ſtature ſonniſhe heyr like phebus ſphere boūde treſſe bryghter thā gold wyere downe backe lowe downe behinde thred golde ſhe would binde ful oft ſyth cuſtomaunce therto ſhe ſo much ſuffyſaunce kindes worke without ſaue browes ioyned yfere man coud lacke eſpyen furthermore ſpeake eyen ſo heauenly perſyng ſo clere herte ne might ſelfe ſtere agayne ſhyninge yt ne woūd wolde throughout breſt god wote make yold alſo ſhe al ſemelineſſe symple wyſe ful ſoberneſſe beſt nouryſhed eke might goodly ſpeche fulfylled pytye facundious therto right tretable ſayth guydo loue variable tender hert vnſtedfaſtneſſe accuſeth newfanglyneſſe ¶and dare doth reherſe amonges kyng perſe came grekes many worthy knight helpe euer myght whych kyng ſtature longe wonder fat wryte right ſtronge whoſe berd heyr redde flawme fire eyen ſtepe feruent deſyre haue ado ſterne cheare loke oft ſythes ſodayne yre quoke wertes plenty face ¶and thus dare ſhortly pace grekes wryteth fynde troians make mynde ceryouſly doth ſtyle dreſſe diſcryue ſhall expreſſe ¶the deſcryption priam ſonnes doughters ariuall ye grekes tofore temple diane goddeſſe ca xvi firſt ſayeth king pryamus cheare bening gracious ſtature hygh lymmes ſklendre lōg delytyng much muſyk ſonge ſpecially moſt deſyrous heare ſonges amerous ſemely man great hardineſſe ſpake lowe bookes v expreſſe deuoyde dread hating flatterye could gloſe lye trewe worde euery wyght playnly equite right mede liſt declyne loued early morowe dine time one worthyeſt kinges loued beſt worthy knightes al euer knewe manfull herte trewe coud cheriſhe man halfe ſo wele golde gyftes myght fele great fredome large eke withall ¶and ſonnes reken firſt byrth ſo bookes tell worthy hector knighthod ſprīg wel floure manhod ſtrength pereles sad diſcrete prudent neuertheles crop roote ground chyualrye cheare demure curteſye example therto ſoberneſſe myrour gentilneſſe time therto moſt renoumed reken goodlyhead moſt famous peace werre whoſe fame ſtretched nygh ferre eche parte ſo vertuous loued moſt gracious brawne bone compact meaſure wel brethed armes endure wel perfourmed proporciowne quicke ſo liuely moſt renowne huge made ſo well growen length wel complet haue great ſtrengthe▪ worlde ſhal fayne neuer none fully myght attayne prowes worthy knight prayſe herte well might therwithall ſo wyſe aduyſee lowlyeſt eke degre ryche pore wordes fewe vnto ſuche cheare could ſhewe preſence glad euery wight whan leyſur ſyght ſo bening towne enemyes like ferſe lyowne could ſhewe whan felde might man ſo reken labour halfe endure ſtorye doth v plyan aſſure neuer werye battayle faynt herte fomen aſſayle good finde beſt proweſſe vertue ſet reſt paſſingly neuer ſhall none bore mother ſo perygall manhod chiualrie paſſed yf bokes lye nature ne nothing wyte saue tunge let lite ſome auctours make mencion ſanguine complexion ¶and furthermore brother deiphobus like finde alſo helenus lyke pryam ſothly theim thre hard eſpye dyuerſyte ſhape fourme countenaunce saue age varyaunce father olde yonge lyght deiphobus worthy knight armes fame excellence helenus clergye ſcyence well expert toke lytell hede al werre knighthod manhede ¶but ſothly troylus ſhall diſcriue herte manlyer alyue likly armes endure well growen hight great ſtature yonge freſhe luſty hardy lyō deliuer ſtronge champyowne perygall manhode dede reade derryng noble worthy wight fulfyl longeth knight te ſecounde hector worthineſſe called high proweſſe duryng werre bare ſelfe ſo wele therto loue trewe ſtele secre wiſe ſtedfaſt courage moſt goodly alſo viſage might moſt beninge cheare without chaunge one herte entere alway faythfull iuſt ſtable perſeueraunt immutable vpon thing • one ſet herte doubilneſſe might dot peruert dedes ſo hole playne foon ſothe ſayne ſo ferſe might hym wtſtand whan helde blody ſworde hād vnto grekes death confuſyon troye ſhelde protection knighthod ſhortly accounte might māhod mā ſurmoūt world though mē wouldē ſeke reken troian nouther greke none ſo named famous hardineſſe bokes olde beare witneſſe except hector ne ſuch ¶and ſpeake brother meane parys moſt paſſing beaute worlde man might ſe ſothe ſemely knight reade title right fayrneſſe bare aye away floure locke yelowe like golde coloure ſhotyng moſt delyte hauyng hunting full great appetyte dare lyketh diſcriue beſt archer one time liue hand eke noble knight manly man delyuer good might werre preued wel ¶and reade troian eneas mine auctour lyſteth endyte wel breſted body lyte bare troye wonder great eſtate workes diſcrete temporate fame paſſyng eloquence wiſe counſayle great ſapyence moſt renōmed alſo lecture delyting muche bokes ſcripture euer glad porte cheare sterne loke perſyng eyen cleare amonge dwellyng towne ſpeake goodes poſſeſſyowne caſtelles toures great plentye finde ſothly none citye ne might attayne vnto rycheſſe alſo al worthyneſſe golde iewellꝭ paſſyng great treaſor ¶and felowe hyght dan̄ anthenor ſklender longe great dalyaūce circumſpect gouernaance welbeloued alſo pryamus wordes wonder copyous reſowning ay myrth playe bouerdyng long daye amonges feres companye dryely mā might eſpye ſobre countenaunce euery wight great pleſaunce heare talke whan glad albeit porte ſad yet ſpeche ful bouerdes ¶and ſon called pollidamas like father ſtature make ythewed well lacke perſone gentill right trewe wonder ſtronge pale alſo hewe yre ſtered ſodaynly albe wordes kept couertly heate paſſe would anone ¶and tell king mereone large breſted makyng beſt compacte moſt tall ſhape fourme men coulde fynde eke ſo well perfourmed vp kynde none lyke hym nye ne ferre locke yelow criſping heare styll porte gentill playe inly ſtronge maiſtryes aſſaye wonder curteyſe wyght rygorous wrought ariues dedes meruaylous boke hereafter ſhalbe ſene ¶nowe heccuba quene lyke ſtory ſtyle muſt enclyne whoſe lymmes rather dyd declyne ſhappe man womanhead ſayth guydo worke dede ſoth moſt womanly beſte aduyſed moſt prudently dedes could ſelfe gouerne man wyt myght wiſe diſcerne fynde better doubtles ſhe trewe example femynyte ſothe euery wyghte benynge porte gracious ſyghte pore alſo pyteous mercyable vnto nedy wonder cherytable wife hector doughter eke law lore ſemed muche drawe andromecha faythfull trewe wyfe good ſo iuſt whiche lyfe honeſte dyd aye moſt delyte longe ſhap breſtes fayre white ruddy chekes ennewed meaſure perſynge eyen angelyke fygure leke golde treſſes roſen lyppes red ylyche freſhe colour nothyng dead therto ſhe chere goodlyeſt riche pore ſpake alwaye beſt euery one aye helpyng ſhe might man heauy went ſyght ouer euery gentylman wolde euer ſhe gladly euer dyd dylygence get grace dyd offence vſage condicion ſo fylled compaſſyon woman myght lere ¶and caſſandra owne doughter dere ſtature wonder womanly colour whyte therwith ryght ſemely saue face ſondry place many wertes growyng ioye felycytee kepen virginite freelte woman haue kynde vertue morall ſhe put minde foly fleynge occaſyon aye ſtudy contemplacyon ſondry bookes ſhe wolde occupye moſt knowe aſtronomye ¶of prophecye ſpyryt alſo ſhe ſome men ſaye ſhe one three thilke woman cebyle bare name ye renowne floureth fame vnto daye yet full grene ¶and tell younge polycene deſcryue beautie vp downe ſoth foule preſumpciowne take ſo great thynge clymbe ſo hye paſſeth connyng syth nature hath forgynge mayde connyng vtterly aſſayed make fayre aboue eche creature ¶and ſayd proudely ſe nature whan lyſte enbellyſhe worke lyke phebus amonge cloudes derke paſſyng clere ſo comparyſon worke operacion right lyſte adourne make fayre painte floryſhe ſhall appayre colour ſo craftely diſpoſe lylye freſhe roſe ſo ennewe yt ſhall fade aye one wiſe made dere doughter ye know whō mene yonge freſhe fayre polycene aſkaunſe none crafte worke boſted vtterly nature ſelfe whan ſhe may wrought ſhe fully herte thought aboue maken excell beautie well therwithall ſhap ſtature ne lacke dare well aſſure god aboue gaue ſoueraintee thewes wolde ſhe ſhulde crop roote named womanhead fulſomneſſe goodlihead paſſyngly ydelneſſe preſume wordes expreſſe beaute vayne trauayle wel wote mine engliſhe would fayle ſuch matter talke felingely euer certayne therfore paſſe ſtreight wil go matter dare mo booke maketh menciowne theim grece troye towne ſpecial put mo minde ye haue herde ſaue ye ſhal finde ſtorye whan cometh therto theyr knighthod beſt hath laſting ſiege maner euerydell ryght anone ſharpe poyntell wil dreſſe ſtorye entreate werre tellen great time nigheth yore breme wynter troſtꝭ hore gan aſwage bitter colde whan apollo paſſed holde ſygne call aquarye fyſhe fer februarye yronne toward ariete ſeaſon feynte heate hylles high gan beames ſmyte makyng ſnowe fayre flake white water kyndely relente whych aboue valey wente nere floudes ſodayne thowe grene mede gan ouerflowe yſe gan ſ • oundmele deſtyll downe fro hight brokes fyll fomy ſtreames wawes ſmale broke bankes auale luſty vere yonge grene yrecomforted ſonne ſhene lytel litel hewes ſtyl amēdeth ayein ſphere titan vp aſcendeth whan marche approcheth braūches ouer gan blowe equinoctiall vere halowed ſeaſon amerous whan grekes proude couragious hole floure chiualrye aſſembled hooly theyr nauye hauen moſt fame athene tyme bare name ygathered aſſent echone towadre troye ſayle gone great nomber ſith world begā remembred maner man togyther one companye met yfeare ſo paſſyng nauye manly men ſo lyſt take hede ſtorye ye ſhall rede make deſcripcion ¶mine auctour telleth howe agamemnon worthi king hondred ſhippꝭ brought worthy knightes ſtuffed thē ought ¶and menelay lay moſt ye charge hath wt brought ſyxty ſhippes large land called sperten ¶and boece ful manly men came fifty ſhippes ye ſtory telleth thus prothenor achelaus ¶and land called sithemenye came ſyxty ſhippes companye duke hyght achalaphus whō eke freſhe deſyrous helmyus erle worthy knyght ¶and fyfty ſhippes enarmed fyght brought kyng epiſtrophus onely helpe king thedius ¶and thelamon ayax men call ful renowmed reken hath fifty ſhippes brought iourney salerne royall chefe citye earles duke many worthy knight eueryche theim ſtele armed bryght ¶and duke tenter amphiacus earle daryon noble theſeus ylke foure full worthy renowne voyage came thelamowne ¶and olde neſtor cruel hert thought pylon hath fyfty ſhippes brought ¶the kinge dyames yt full worthy eke kinge hight alſo thoas brought theim theyr companye hundred ſhippes knightlye guye ¶and thelamou ycalled pyleus armes fell • ſpytous brought lande ſo ferre sixe thyrty ſhippes werre ¶amphymacus kinge polibete thyrty ſhippes brought flete calcedoyne mereō kinge ydameus theyr ledinge foure ſcore ſhippes theym crete ¶and vlixes grekes dyd mete fyfty ſhyppes ſtuffed trace towardes troye proudly pace ¶duke mellens full manly men brought eke hym great ſhyppes ten moreouer duke prothecatus ¶and duke named protheſylaus hauen called athene brought fyfty ſhyppꝭ enarmed bright ſhene phylyarcha ſtronge myghtye yle ¶and machaon guydo doth compyle brother polydris alſo countrey trycionyco brought two twenty ſhippes finde ¶and phyces mynde achilles came fyfty full numbre ¶and rhodon troyans encombre came twenty ſhyppes wt kyng thelapolus ¶and duke hyght antipus lande heſyda men call whiche folke nyghe cherles ſayle croſſed agayne bryght heauen numbre came ſhyppes eke elleuen name full famous worthy duke called amphymacus ¶and polibethes ſtronge myghty kyng fyfty ſhyppes brought cōmynge richa noble regiowne kyng full worthy renowne latniſus duke eke rede ¶and fynde noble diomede ſhyppes great ſaye ſmall barge hath wt brought fro calidonye arge foureſcore numbre ſothly tale ¶and thelemus myghty euryale two manly men armes ſage dyomede came voyage ¶and polyphebus brought ſhippes ſeuen phyneus hardy kynge enleuen ¶and prothoylus ſpecifye brought fyfty ſhyppes vnto nauye fro demeneſa myghtye regyon ¶and carpenor made mencion brought fyfty eke capadye coūtrey great prouynce whiche king ¶tricorius beyſa lorde kynge brought two twenty eke cōmyng fynally ſhall lye full many ſhyppe nauye mo guydo maketh reherſayle towarde troye grekes ſayle homer diſcrypcion grekes ſhyppes maketh mencion shortly affyrmyng ye man neuer borne ſuch nombre ſhippes ſawe toforne countyng ſhyppes palamydes brought nombre encreaſe whan theſe lordes aforſayd euerychone kynges duke erles one aſſembled without wene afore hauen called athene famous kynge great agamenowne wyſe ſo worthy ſo hye renown prynce gouernour grekes hooſte anone dyd labour buſy cure waker dylygence hyghe aduyſe inwarde prouydence deliberate wiſely nede procede matter caſtyng vp downe reuoluynge hygh diſcreciowne may ſo begyn ende conclude well wylfulneſſe ne ſhende hooly purpoſe rakelneſſe ne none haſte without auyſeneſſe may afore ſo wyſely ſee fynally felicitye accomplyſhe may purpoſe certayne ¶and ſo king vpon large playne citie lyttle ſtronde lordes wyll nothyng wonde haue counſaile wyſe agamenon makyng anone conuocacyon ſuche great inſpeciall ſyttyng fyrſte ſee royall lordes eueryche ſee lyke hye lowe degree tumulte ſtynted ſcylence ye preſe gyne hym audyence whan anone full ſobre wyſe began tale ſhall deuyſe syres quod praye taketh hede ſo noble ſo renowmede wyſedome worthineſſe manhode eke hyghe proweſſe knyghthode reporte fame thrughout ye world reboūdeth name doubtleſſe floure chyualrye men may fynde companye ſawe euer manly men yfeare together met younge ſo freſhe couragyous alſo well beſene haue ſo lykely ſyth worlde began without raſkayle ſo many knyghtly man kynges duke many lorde wyll one accorde one herte aſſembled place yf fortune goddes grace behynde iourney repreue may fayle purpoſe achyeue deme hym playnly arage worſe wood durſte voyage wyſe perturbe preſume take agayne v outher aſſume myght hym malys exſcyte worthyneſſe neuer ſolyte v prouoke ire offence ne ſhulde mortall recompence aquyte mede lyeth myght aſſemble many worthy knyght amouges whiche hundred yet mo coulde cheſe able go manly force knyghtly ſuffyſaunce take hym vengeaunce vpon troyans hym ſelfe alone whyche gathred echone men ſuffycient execute ſumme entent accomblyſhe felicitee cauſe meane whiche aſſembled ben together hye lowe ¶and alſo vnknowe howe ſhamefully troyans haue v greued prouoked v wylfully ymeued ryſe agayne haue recure right wronges done force myght wherfore let v one aſſent wyll sette haue ryght ſkyll redreſſe fynde nowe complaine one harte buſy peyne vpon troyans werre make ſuppoſe ſhall ſo awake ſhall lerne thenſe wende remembre worldes ende hereafter ſhall dare take hande preſume grece lande bolde haue lyfe ſpace agayne grekes treſpace whoſe offence ſayth late within herte deadly brennyng hate feruent hete gredy yre fro day day ſo ſetteth v fyre reneweth conſtreynt peine inwardely yf ſhall fayne muſt reaſon ſo hygh greuaunce ſelfe enforce vengeaunce ryght requereth iuſte ſorowe compelleth v eue morowe troyans harmes bewreke ſtoppe tounges ſo ſpeake reprefe villanye muſt attones ſhapen remedye foen henſeforth may haue drede worſe v god forbed tyme commynge yf pacience lykely ſuffer importable offence paſſe forth take hede syth neuer yet grekes coulde reade man dyd reprefe name iuſtly might rebounde ſhame withouten quyte agayne thrugh manhode ſo openly playne man myght ſeyne ere wyſe reporte amyſſe ¶ne ſhall dyſſymule caſe chere oppreſſed dredfull face let ſlyde lyghtly ouer go great offence ſo late ydo might happly tourne v oures great reprefe ſucceſſours tune comming ſhamfully beſpoke grekes durſte worke vpon foon whiche may enſure ſythe one wyll refourme wronge therwithall ſo mighty ſo ſtronge coulde brede length ryght reherſe power ſtrength durſte euer worthyneſſe aſſayle ne ſhulde withouten fayle repente herte ende rewe saue troyans daye newe wylfulneſſe foly rage lande made voyage vnware v pray home wente whiche ſhall full haſtely repente treſpace great offencyowne ¶for worlde knoweth vp downe late gone grekes fewe vpon troyans power dyd ſhewe ſlewe kyng called lamedowne father pryam kyng towne cleane fordyd toures citye ſlewe vp commynaltye grekes ſworde yt liſt ſpare thoſe amonges v ſeruitude care compleine harme yt may recured may ſtande full aſſured agayne v holde chaumpartye haue ſo worthy companye lykely thouſande acheue foure fyue ſo lyghtly myght preue yet one thynge affyrme well dare cummyng troyans well ware labour diligence agaynſt v maken reſyſtence al myght knowe doute gather frendes countreys helpe ſtrength nede v withſtande ſo may ſpede ¶but fynally one thynge counſayle hauen ferther ſayle may fortunate one aſſent make ambaſſyat prudently wende delos haſte ſende whiche yle little beſyde diſcretely iourney prouyde may haue better hap grace apollo patron place haue maye ſpeade fynall anſwere great nede exployet ſhall fall ſo ye wyll aſſenten counſayle moſt eke leſte ¶and echone thought beſt condeſcende concluſyon without contradiction attones without drede preyſe counſeyle wiſe rede therupon diſtretly ought ſayth ſtory euen thus wroughte ¶how achilles patroclus ſent delos receiue anſwere god apollo ſhuld ſpede ayenſt ye troyans cap xvii tyme agamenon concluded fully reaſon ye haue herde ſentence fyned grekes herte full enclyned one voyce accorded plainly thus achilles alſo patroclus comon profyt ſyth ſage shall take ye charge meſſage appollo anſwere gone ſhyppe haſte anone ſayle forth large ſea towarde delos proſperitee aryued ycome lande whiche yle vnderſtande myne auctor ſayth without le hath ſcyte amonges cyclades men rockes haue ſo muche amyd ſee called heleſpontico whyche yle make deſcrypcion muſt awhyle make diſgreſſyon fro matter myne auctour doth yle iſodorus ſoth reherſeth playnly latona quene appollo fyrſt dyane ſhene ychilded hath iubyter lorde whan iuno ſuche diſcorde wryte ouyde lyttell whyle ſo befell lyttell yle temple whylom dedicate vnto appollo alſo conſecrate worſhyp olde foundacion honoured great deuocion bycauſe appollo beames cleare floud fyrſt dyd appere ſhewe horne rather ſoone eke dyane called moone whiche ſhewyng yle bereth name day ſo great fame onely apperyng ylke twayne delos greke ſayne ſhewyng apparence thus began great reuerence appollo fyrſt honor eke hym ydone ſo many greke ſyſter called dyane pale moone ſo waxe wane called paynems goddeſſe whylom wod huntereſſe lady ſonne brother yle hath lordſhyp none natiuitie shewed lyght fyrſt countrey whyche yle grekes alſo calle ortygya language bycauſe curlewes fyrſte yſeyne otygyas ſeyne curlewe grewe vnderſtande fyrſt ingendred lande ¶and appollo called eke tytan tyme ſo moche worſhyp wan longe afore made ſterre iubiter whan helde werre alſo ycalled phebus ſome ynamed phyteus phyton victorye hym ſl • great glorye great ſerpent erthe alowe arowes mighty bowe whiche conqueſte great god cupyde hadde enuye samuel loue saule byble tell temple large longe olde ſtatue pured golde full great hyghe huge weyght therin deuylles ſleyght ſpyryte vnclene falſe illuſyon gaue anſwere euery queſtyon ydoll dombe chylde ſought mali crueltye horryble holy wryte recordeth byble whiche purſuite perſecucion dyd appere tho auiſyon holly aungell ioſeph ſlepe bad hym ryſe alſo take kepe vnto chylde alſo marye go waye herode hym aſpye egypt great regyon lyke goſpell maketh mencyon ryght anone came lande none ydol yt vpright might ſtand ſhyuered vnto piece ſmall holy wrytte plainly tale recorded fyrſt eſaye lorde write tellen v alder fyrſt prometheus founde ydolles ſhortly conclude ſymulacrum cometh ſymylytude nothyng playnly lykeneſſe made man ymage expreſſe vnto whiche paynems guyſe falſe honour curſed make worſhypped ſake brent golde falſe effection ſette vp conſolacion amynde memoryall vnto whiche herte wyll • l ignoraunce fleſhely loue dyd honour god aboue temple moſt excellence made people reuerence ſayde heauen masdefyed man durſte denyed tyll ſoone lyttell whyle wycked ſpyryte folkes begyle ydoll entred abyde gaue anſwere vpon euery ſyde people lyſt demaunde agayne wyll cōmaunde obey fully folke aſſyrye whiche vnto god great iniurye makyng people ſuche errour fall ſome belus ſome bell call ſome balym ſome belphegore felle errour alway belzebub named alſo whiche name made theſe wordes two bel zebub thus ſyngnyfye bell god zebub flye belzebub togyther ſpecyfyes ioyned one great god flyes fayned falſe ydolatrye gan worlde worſhyp mawmentrye ¶for ſome saturne god goddes gan errour falſely call whylom myghty king crete gaue hym name planete heauen hath ſo large ſphere poetes fable lere ſapyence sawe diuine prouydence howe ſonne ſhulde hym deſcende ¶and iuno goddes wende ſhuld plainly fro reigne expell ſuffer hym lenger dwell kyngdome whan came age wherof saturne fyll ſuche rage wyll ſhape remedye therfore byddyng wyfe ye childe bore ſhe hym ſhulde brynge anone ſtede wherof ſhe brought ſtone ſaue childe ſhe dyd buſyneſſe saturne gredineſſe ſtone deuoureth melancolye saturne bookes lye ſonnes thre doughter mo ¶iubiter neptunus pluto iubiter greateſt name moſte renowmed worthyeſt fame amonge paynems veryfyed ſo hyghe haue hym magnifyed hym call god fyre eyre next saturne borne heyre ¶and next hym bookes rede god batayle myghty mar rede ¶and next appollo ſo clere ſhene bright dayes eye voyder nyght cheriſher fruite herbe floure corne whiche god lyke ſayd toforne delos worſhypped honoured ¶and venus often hath ſocoured many louer fayre luſty quene aledge woundes grene fyrſte hurte fyrye bronde ſhe goddeſſe many lande worlde hath demeyne faſt enbraced fyry cheyne meane lady called venus ¶and next ordre mercurius ſpeche hath moſt excellence rethoryke ſugred eloquence muſyke ſonge hermonye hath lordſhyp hole regalye ¶next moone wexe wane called lucyna alſo eke dyane delos hath mancyon lyke tofore maked mencyon full myght horned pale ſhe lady chaunge mutabilitie ſelde one halte tyme ſo fare borne clyme aye delyte thynges newe whoſe herte cladde many ſondry hewe diuers affection wyſe ſondry regyons mawmentrye venym ronne lyke clerkes well deuyſe konne ¶for fynde mauryens worſhyp iubam egypciens ¶honour yſis connyng whylom doughter inachus kynge taught thē firſt lond ere ſowe alſo letter reade knowe lecture ſette buſyneſſe whiche thyng call goddeſſe ¶and iubyter honoured crete whylom helde ſouerayne ſeate theim layde many dyuers charge egles beaten baner large lorde eyre land ſee royall kyngdome deuiding three ¶in higheſt ſelfe doth contune ¶and hoole ſea gaue vnto neptune laſt earth holde ſea royall ¶he gaue pluto god infernall alder laſt whan ſtellyfyed iubiter moſt magnyfyed theim crete aboute ouer made memoryall large tombe ſtatue high alofte honoured theyr rite ofte encens ſacryfyſe matter ferther deuyſe latines wyth theyr buſy diligence theyr rytes didden reuerence goddes yf credyble ycalled fawny inuiſyble haue dwelling wodes grene albe men theyr fygure may ſene ¶and romaynes deuyne moſt ī honour haue god quirine whych whylom bokes tellen v amonges theim called romulus bylte fyrſt walles towne herde came ſuch renowne manhod worthineſſe ſpere bokes ſayne expreſſe heade pytched grounde gan anone lyke founde flouryſhe floure budde myracle nature none obſtacle waxe grene freſhe blomes newe manhode men athenienſes hoole herte choſen haue ſerue goddeſſe great called minerue pallas eke criſtall ſhelde neptunus euen amyd felde helde champartye wyth woman ſyde men full ſurquedous pryde defendeth gyuing large depe whych thinge apollo toke good kepe whych dome reckles olyue tokeneth loue peaſe water trouble conteck werre ſtryfe gaue ſentence anone diffynitife pallas ſhould called minerue palme plainly reuerence ¶and pauye region worſhyp moſt quene citheron meane venus ful doubilneſſe afore ſomwhat expreſſe temple full ſolemplye ſet higheſt moſt rychly gold aſure ſtatue paint coloures may neuer faynte ſet vp higheſt ſee temple men may ſe ſhe ſtant naked wawy ſee enuyron goddeſſes thre aſſygned buſy attendaunce wayte obſeruaunce floures freſhe blewe rede whyte aboute delyte heade ſhe hath chaplet roſes rede ful pleſauntly yſet heade downe vnto foote ſondry gommes oyntementes ſoote ennoynte ſweter ſmell alofte theſe poetes tell dowues whyte fleing eke ſparowes beſyde cupyde arowes blynde ſone hurt dere loſeth ofte ſmyte wote muſt nedes bycauſe blynde thus honoured moſte mynde amonge people venus goddeſſe ¶and naxyens theyr buſineſſe ſerue bachus myghty god wyne whoſe lycour moſt precious fine recomforte hertes make glade refreſhe hewes fade face pale maketh wyttes ſharpe loſeth tunges make theym loude carpe cauſeth theim walke lybertee diſcure thynges ſecree without aduyſe diſcreſcion wyne hath domynacion ſecretneſſe may kept mewe ſome bachus ſerue ſewe amonge haue ſuch deuocion ſome voyde reaſon haſty wood without dreade ſome alſo ſo toty theyr heade voyde power myght haue foote ſtande vpryght yet iargaunt pye right pale cheared glaſye eye full reaſon til winde ſpent woman vynolent veryly beaſt vnreaſonable dome holde theim eke vnable accepted companye whan theyr tunge wadeth lye ne may bryng forth worde ¶and thus bachus ſtrōg mighty lord ful oft cauſeth folkes erre debate maken werre haſtyneſſe nede wherfore wyſedome men drede ſleyghty workyng fall ſnare feble braines meaſure ſpare vnwarely areſted take bachus make theim ſhake feuer worſe tercyen cuſtome cotydyen alterat bachus myghty iou affered tourning hous fordreynt drye lande hath loſt vſe foote hande ſtrawe playeth lyke ape deuoutly ginneth gape noddeth oft wyth iowſy heade heauy cappe leade condicion entre maye relegyon myghty bachus habylite whych lorde hath ſouereynte hony mylke therto bawme ſo ryche alſo lordſhyp hath high power diuine grape euery vyne theim nouryſhe influence honour reuerence reyſed moſt vnderſtande amonges vynters euery maner lande bycauſe theim ſo gracious ¶and lemnos worſhyp vulcanus god fyre iubyter ſmythe whych forgeth blacke ſtythe great thonder hydous horryble leuens whylom viſible weſt oryent gaſteth v dredful dent ſmotry ſmyth ſwarte vulcanus whylom herte ſo ialous toward venus wedded wife wherof roſe deadly mortall ſtrife whan mar gan firſt eſpye hygh malyce cruell falſe enuye ye ſhining phebus bemes bright lying abed mar owne knight herte brent glede making ſlaundre abrode ſprede gan theron falſly muſe god forbede man accuſe ſo lytell woman euer loue ſet hard diſſeuer though ſuch thing gentilneſſe paſſe ouer lyghtly beare none heuineſſe leſt thou woman odius yet ſmythe falſe vulcanus albe theim thus eſpyed amonge paynems yet defyed ſo falſly theim awoke haue ſet laſt boke amonge goddes falſe mawmentrye wyſe gan ydolatrye ye haue herde oppynyons people erryng theyr affection falſe trouthe ſerche teaching holy churche holy doctryne tradicions ſhal deſpyſe ſuch opynyons whych fende founde late whan aungelles heauen create prelacye prophete called eſaye wryteth ryght thus cedres grene paradyſe ſo fayre ſene planys fyrre heyght ſoth ſayne highnes might attayne tree ſo delycious paradyſe ſo precious nouther ſight ſemelineſſe egall fayrneſſe pryde ſurquidrye whan ſo ſayde god ſyt ſo hye wyll lyke alſo ſet ſee high north paſſyng degre caſt downe wyth legyons fayre heauenly manſyons ſodaynly pyt hel perpetually dwell ſayde whan fel ſo ferre fell thou ſo thou morowe ſterre middes ſtones bryght ſo perſyng fyery theyr lyght whilom thy great bryghtneſſe called lucifer whō chriſt ſayeth expreſſe goſpell ſawe fro heauen sathan deſcende lyke fyery leuene olde ſerpent ſo lowe yfall hebrues theyr tunge call ¶bemoth doth latin playne expreſſe beaſt rude full curſedneſſe vile ſerpent leuiathan ſydore well deſcryue whych kynde neuer conuerſaunt welles trouble hath moſt haunt amonges water large ſea ſayth dauid like ye may ſe pſalter making mencion ſnake monſtruous dragon ful venym hard grace whych ſea large great ſpace wyth foule adder hath manſyon vnto mankynde illuſyon whylom ſawe holy monke brādā ſayled forthe occyan thorowen deiect pyt horryble foule hydous credible abide tortuous ſerpent vnto daye playnly iudgement malyce enuyed ſo mankynde whych ginnes ſleightes find came father firſt paradyſe deceyue bet deuyſe couertly worme paſſage toke ſerpent lykneſſe ymage cheare loke countenaunce lyke mayde hath reſemblaunce woman recordeth bede deceytes rather ſpede meane face onely elles behynde ſo clerkes telles lyke ſerpent wombe backe tayle whan gan aſſaile towarde eue whan gan glyde fyrſt enquereth toke aſyde god forbad theim eten tree whych eate ſothly ſhulden like goddes knowing good yll right forthwith gan fulfyll fendes heſt theyr eyen vncloſed theyr gylt ſodaynly depoſed paradyſe wretchedneſſe lyue labour ſorowe diſtreſſe thus fende whan fyrſt toke fourme ſnake woman loke made tunge heade meue falſe engene mankinde greue doth theim trauayled wycked ſpyrytes vexed aſſayled meue theyr tunges falſly breake blaſphemy thinge yt ſpeake ſame ſerpent leuiathan continuing aye falſely gan curſed idolles dombe deafe blinde ful oft ſpeaketh ſpyrytes finde fendes dauid wryte certayne▪ goddes folkes ſo vaine honour rite ſuperſticious whilom apollo delphicus like tofore ye haue herd deuiſe ought inough ſuffiſe ¶and trowe cauſe myne auctour reherſeth grounde ginnyng idolatrye cauſe ought eſpye ſawe matter knowe ilyche well high lowe perauenture pleaſaunce hath grounde put remembraunce falſe goddes mawmentrye moſt theim poeſye ye ſtorye reſorteth ſoone agayne achilles ye haue herd ſaine patroclus haue waye ynome temple thyther ycome haue aunſwere theyr embaſſadrye great apollo whych may lye ye pryeſtes haue theyr counſaile take temple praie wake tyll may finde vnto theyr entente haue aunſwere time conuenient theyr purpoſe leyſure oportune ¶and one herte ſo longe contune praying faſtyng oblacions wyth ſacrifiſe ſundrye oryſons tofore god awayting alwaye faſt tyll theim anſwered laſt ſofte voyce ſayde achilles twye home grekes faſt thou hye thou hyther ſente ſaye thē ſothly ſūme entent shalbe fulfylled withouten wordes mo ſhall troye go abyde many ſtronge battayle laſt withouten fayle ten yeares daye win ſhall towne brynge playnly deſtructiowne wall toures fall ſhal ruyne al theyr purpoſe fyne kyng priamus hecuba wife theyr ſones mortall ſtryfe shall ſlayne brother brother fine may none ſhal none eſcape place ſuch grekes liketh vnto grace routhe mercy take ſome thus ende make aunſwere achilles glad light hert al myght thanketh apollo bleſfull eure ſodeynly ſorte aduenture ſelfe tyme befell wonder thynge troye pryamus kynge ſent byſſhop ſame caſe haue anſwere named calchas came fool without preſe ſame houre whyle achilles preſent man great ſcyence meane calchas experyence eſpecially calculacion ſorte alſo dyuinacion lerned aſtronomye whan tyme dyd eſpye haue anſwere moſt conuenient appollo lyke entent heretofore maked memorye entred oratorye doyng rytes obſeruaunces lyke cuſtome circumſtaunces beſely gan knele praye thinges deuoutly ſaye god crye call ful ſtronge apollo would tho prolonge sodaynly aunſwere gan attame ſayd calchas twies name right wel ware thou ne tourne agayne troye towne vayne finally lerne thinge ſhorte tyme ſhall deſtroyed ſothe whych may denyed wherfore wil thou alyed grekes achilles go theim anone ſo ſhall haue haue diſcloſed victorye honour may diſpoſed fatall ne may varye thou theim ſhalt neceſſarye counſeling yeuing rede right helping good ſpede worde roſe vp calchas achilles went eaſy pace whan came preſence great honour muche reuerence receiued like eſtate ſoone confederate swore togyther bonde aſſuraunce al one withouten varyaunce haſte togyther gone theyr ſhippes ſhope theym forth anone patroclus goyng theyr ſyde hale vp anker longer byde ſayle forthe calchas twayne toward grece theim nedeth complaine winde wawe till aryued athene ſtode vpon ſea large citye olde foundacion achilles kyng agamenon hath calchas brought alſo patroclus whan grekes ſtorye telleth v aſſembled together went tofore king calchas repreſent lordes longer dwell right anone achilles gan tell without abode delos mette tofore apollo aunſwer fette god hath playnly determyned grekes purpoſe ſhal fyned vpon troians bad calchas alſo wyſe troye go grekes abyde ſtyll tyll theyr purpoſe fynally fulfyll whiche thyng grekes glad chere calchas accepte herte full entere one confederate bonde one water londe without chaunge varyaunce othe made put remembraunce agayne fully hym aſſure cheryſhe hym whyle theyr lyfe may dure weale wo ſo made ende parte lodgyng wende till morne ſterry nyght aurora gladded wt light phebus beames grekes vp aryſe goddes many ſacryfyce honour may deuoutly holdyng feaſt daye rytes meynt loue drede remembraunce good ſpede anſwere ye goddes haue ſent agreable vnto entent patroclus achilles amonges preſe calchas come tofore agamenon lordes ſyttynge enuyron lyke eſtates eche place dewe humbly gan ſalewe vpon knee ſobre countenaunce prayed diſpleſaunce ſtynte whyle gyue hym audyence ryght anone made ſylence amonge calchas gan abrayde euen thus full ſobrely ſayd oh ſyres quod lordes dere kynges prince duke noble echone worthy famous eke ſo manly ſo vertuous whiche place preſent fyne chiefe entent cauſe alſo ye echone aſſembled troye gone power great ſtrength purpoſe longe drawe length differred forth day daye damage platly naye longe ye ſoiourne yle trowe ye pryam whyle hath eſpyes amonge pryuely wote wele ſaye faythfully knowe fyne gouernaunce whyles may make purueaunce hym defende ye ydell reſte ſemeth ſothly ye beſte abydyng ſuche delayes great harme may fal certayne nay preue thus playnly whyle yee enmyes graunte lybertee puruey may mighty hand enforce power withſtande fryendes allyaunce leyſour make ordinaunce foly ye ſo dyfferre syth ye ready make werre ennemyes euery circūſtraunce nothyng may quarell ſo auaunce haſty ſuite ſharper byte iron hoote tyme ſmyte abyde tyll colde wyl neither plye folde go ſette vpon one accorde ſhyppe anone within borde enhaſte tyme remewe might quarell purſue agaynſt haue treſpaſſed many dayes ſomer paſſed many monthes ronne ouerſlyde titan oft chare hath ryde eaſt weſt wawes depe ſtreames bathed whyles ye ſlepe ſpent tyme place thus whyle wynde called zephirus beningly enſpyred hath alofte attempre aier wether fayre ſoft calme ſea wawes ſtyll playne whyles ye waſte dayes vayne foon therto taken hede wil ſuppoſe drede bolde ſet lite truſte forſothe wyll quite trewlye like bounde thynke ye haue goddes founde toward bening fortunate honour ſaued high lowe eſtate ſo ſhall forthe ingratytude prouoke theim purpoſe delude wylfully ſlouthe good fortune wonder though contune towardes ſhewe theyr grace wherfore reade henſe pace ſhapeth longer lye whyle wether ſo fayre clere luſty ſomer abydeth hete wynter come wyth raynes wete ſeaſon ſo freſhe grene ſpeake herte platly mene exployt alder eaſe ſo angre pleaſe forth haſte ye ſhyppe wende tale ende ¶howe grekes nauye retourning athene diſtreſſed tempeſt toke caſtel ye troians called saranaba ca xviii one cōdeſcēded aduyſe haue wel cōmēded al haſte agamenon grete luſty time ſeaſon ſwete haſtyng grekes high lowe made ſoūde trumpe ſhipward blowe echone bidding obey theyr ſhippes go right weye without abode longer dwell ſhuld nomber tell theyr ſhippes ſyth ye haue herde afore nedeth reherſe ſe might auayle forthe dreſſe thē begā ſayle ſothe playnly wene great nauye neuer yet yſene worlde together met winde good yt let theyr waye fyrſt whan begon ſoone gan ſhene ſon clearneſſe chaunge bryght face dimme cloudes gan light enbrace ſodaynly full ougly wiſe heauen dercke wynde gan ryſe hydous thunder leuene clere smote maſt bryght fyere blacknes ſmoky reyne blindeth eyre nothyng may ſene wawes gan ryſe alofte theyr ſhippes fell nothyng ſofte plonge downe theyr toppes ſmyte theim thought wanted lyte haue dead ſelfe ſtounde tyll calchas hath craft yfounde cauſe oryſons charmes incantacions made ſodaynly tempeſt appeaſe wt craft done theim right great eaſe founde cauſe euerydele dyane lyked nothyng wele grekes durſten take hande ſo bolde parte ſtronde ſea maner wyſe maner ſacrifyce nouther offer tofore gothe thyng goddeſſe ſo wroth towarde grekes ſaylynge ſea echone wende haue drowned tyll laſte kyng agamenon hath counſayle information wyſe calchas made ſette vp londe yle faſte ſhyppes bonde aulydes little yle hyghte whiche fonde vnware ſyghte lyttle temple oratorye founded olde made memory great dyane anone wente full deuoutly offerynge preſent quemed oblacions lay longe oriſons rytes vſed lawe tell ſawe tempeſt gan adawe ſome bokes maken mencion touchyng thyng agamenon ouyde lyſt reherſen boke kyng owne doughter toke effygenya benynge face chere endelonge vpon aultere mayde layde diſpoyled wede tofore dyane maken blede fyne heauenly quene bloud innocent clene appeaſe myght quemen rage goddeſſe gracious viſage hath mercy meynt magnifycence ſuffer mayde ſo full innocence gyltleſſe temple ſlawe hath myracle away body drawe conſerued anoy ſmerte ſtede vnwarely caſte herte deth bokes maken mynde agamenon fyrſt gan grace fynde goddes modefye cruell ire cleren gan ſkye ſea waxe calme wether fayre▪ phebus eke glade eyre gan ſhewe newe beames caſte ſea kynge faſte vnto ſhyppe repayred agayne thrugh helpe clerkꝭ ſaine lady quene wayes paſſage goddeſſe called voyage ſentence opynyon worke calculacion gyn dome aſtronomy moſt magnifye tenth twelfe houſe ſhe ſaye moſte gracious beſt fortuned clere ſhade ſhe haue comeforte aſpectes glade planettes ſtandynge tho good ſtate meane ſuche planettes fortunate voyage iourney make ſuch tyme agamenon hath take happy waye ſhypped good houre taken hath ſea grekes wether agreable eolus hath maked acceptable wynde eyre hoole wyll nouther loude playnely ſtyll meane ſo mery made blowe attayne lyttell throwe certayne boundes troye citie vnto caſtell ſtode vpon ſea right wonder ſtrong though lite name whiche thoughe dare liſte wryte meane dare called frygius yet auctours reherſe ſothly thus saranaba ycalled rounde aboute diched well walled hyghe toures rounde ſquare wide vnder went ſea faſt beſyde hauen able ryuayle whiche playnely grekes wyl fayle power myghtely aryue maugre tho agayne ſtryue might well denied except eſpyed alone caſtell dwell whiche anone herde tell commynge proudely berde mete nothyng aferde iſſue downe vnto ſtronde purpoſe onely lette londe might wolde auayle grekes ſo proudely aſſayle ne myght defence endure wende haue aſſure demyng grekes plainly ſea weryed faynted haue longe ſaylinge parbraked forbroke wherfore caſt haue wroke ſodeinly ſette head put ſelfe aduenture drede rakelneſſe vnaduyſedly wherof ſelfe vnhappely befell grekes mette ſperes longe ſwerdes ſharpe whet eche manhode ſhewe cauſe troyans fewe yſſue dyd folyfye fyelde parted egally grekes innumerable mete troyans able tyme mighten ſuffyſe toke paſſyng hygh empryſe yet wold nothing wtdrawe tyll wounded yſlawe ouerlayne grekes vtterly bore downe cruelly mercyleſſe guydo doth reporte behoueth home agayne reſorte verye nede neceſſytee attones gan flee meane ſuche lefte alyue caſtell haſted full blyue ne myght longer holde fyelde agaynſt grekes ſpere ſhielde feble ſhortely conclude abyde ſo great multitude flee grekes great pace ne ceaſe ſewe chaſe full haſtyly caſtell gate entre cruell fate kyll ſlea hye lowe ſpare none ne lyſt wyght knowe none eſtate felly oppreſſe fonde golde eke rycheſſe vnto ſhyppe caryed anone caſtell ne lefte ſtone aboue tourned vp ſo downe wall toure chiefe dongeowne nothynge ſtode ſo vnder myne whan brought vnto ruyne grekes anone ſhyppes haſte one aſſent purpoſen faſte without abode one wyll herte fro hauen playnly dyuerte ſayle towarde tenedowne ſtronge caſtell whyche troye towne diſtaunce thenſe ſyxe myle ſtode ful treaſour rycheſſe good replenyſhed habundaunce theyr ordynaunce yſayled haue theyr iourney ſafe ſound fro ſea taken haue grounde theyr pleſaunce wonder agreable ſyght place delectable holſome eyre ſoyle fayre grene luſty playnes goodly ſene alſo haboundaunt vitayle replenyſhed may auayle oſteyng ſouldiours firſt land freſhe floures plenteous corne grayne wyne fruyt yt thynge laye baraine beaſtes foules paſſyngly plentee faſt adioyning ſee full habundaunt fyſhe fynde ſeaſon euery maner kynde whan yt caſtell grekes ſea londed ferre without abode arme went vpon theim make hidous ſhoute stuffyng caſtel wt meyne ſtrong behinde toke waye guydo fynde towarde foen knyghtly ſet vpon right forth grekes eke anone mette vpon fyde right ſurquidous inly full pryde clenly armed harneys ſtele freſhe arayed beſene ſo wele fielde thicke ſworme eche ſyde men may beholde ſeen spradde playne downe vnto ye ſtrond tyll laſte mette hande hande yoyne wt ſquare ſperes groūd hurtle yfere many bluddy wounde good day ſaluynge ſtrokes felle men hardeen rynge baſſenettes fieldes rounde cruelly fyre ſprange oute amonge tuftes brode bryght ſhene foyle golde fethers whyte grene eke breſtes perced many ſhelde courſers fledde abrode fyelde many layde mortal ſtounde full deadly pale lowe vpon grounde face gruf bluddy ſtreames wyde aldermoſt vpon grekes ſyde ſlaughter diſcomfyture▪ mightly troyans dyd endure till laſte ſo fewe multitude grekes thē hewe mo forty againſt one force abacke muſte gone nothyng lacke manhode dare ſeyne ſo many haue ouer layne longer may fyelde ſoiourne caſtel home agayne retourne full great haſte ſuche myght eſcape away aliue ſome rape drede death toke flyght horſe backe troye towne full ryght wonder though haſte faſte gate chace grekes laſte cruelly purſewe ſome myght remewe troye ſyde forweryed fyght grekes ſlewe full myght whō might atteine may raunſom mercy gayne none eſtate without excepciowne vnto tenedowne grekes went ſette aboute troyan none myght eſcape yt bulwerkes ywonne ſkale walle begoone made ſaute manfully ofte eke troyans ſtode lofte dryue enter ne myght caſte ſtone quarelles bright bowe turkey ſhote arbalaſters gonners ſtandyng corner alſo caſte wylde fyre yrous hate full hote deſyre lyke manly men ſelfe deffende aye grekes vp aſcende cruelly dryuen grounde tyll without ordynaūce haue foūde gynne deuyſed none gonne great caſte ſtones bent toures ryght lyne large ſowes lowe myne ſome vpon walle gone ſo thycke made lyme ſtone entre many wayes ſeke sette baſtyles hurdeys eke rounde aboute harde walle ſkalyng ladder ſawtes marcyall gan vp caſte hokes holde vp aſcende ſturdy grekes bolde tyll troyans creſtes caſte great ſtones whyle woulde laſte roller eke grekes oppreſſe wonder manly dyd buſyneſſe deffence made plonge low caſte quarell ſhote bowe olyettes neceſſytee put may none broke neckes ſhulder bone fell downe ſquare ſtones lyen dead pyteous pale hewe grekes aye gan ſaute renewe multytude troyans aſſayle withſtande gynnen fayle feble reſcuſe came none ſo force grekes gone ye walles haue thē broke troyans ſo cruelly wroke fynally lefte none alyue ſlea kylle blyue walles baners haue ſette yonge olde myght bette goth wracke vpon troye ſyde wyll longer byde treaſour golde ſo may fynde caſte heape together bynde make ſpoyle within haſte walles begyn pynacle toures alſo dungeowne brenne hewe bete downe ſoyle made euen playne great pray anone went againe ſhyppes glad lyght chere fyre flawmes clere caſtell conſumed ybrent auyſe ryght prudent manly man worthy agamenon let make anone conuocation grekes bad ſhulden bryng golde treaſour without taryinge pray wanne tenedowne preſence concluſyowne may make diſtribucion amonges without exception lyke deſert vnto pore ryche departeth euery man lyche moſte ſuche dyd beſt deſerue hym ſelfe lyſt nothyng reſerue hath leuer hertes good ſuche ſpente owne bloud manfully caſtell wynne largeſſe fyrſt begyn ne fayleth well ſpede helpe men whē hath nede loue foloweth fredome comenly ¶howe agamenon aſſembled counſayle noble grece determyned ſente vlyxes dyomede ambaſſade kynge pryam capi xix kyng let make crye al kinges lordes oſtie duke erles come euery coſte next morowe afore appere nyght ypaſſed phebus gan clere hemyſperye larke ſonge whan yt king amonge grekes ſtronge vpon playne ſee royall faſte moſte chife pryncipall lordes ſet degree king ſawe oportunitee made ſcilēce euery lyeges ſtandynge enuyron kyng chere ſad iocounde ſpeche full faucounde began tale ſobre countenaunce effect whiche ſubſtaunce syres quod full worthy degree verye ryght neceſſytee compelled hygh lowe myght lyke ye well knowe redreſſe thynge amys worlde reported force power myght worthyneſſe euery wyghtes ſyght moſt renowmed moſt worſhypable ydempt iudged moſte able people lyklyeſt ſtonde perfourme haue take hand euer grutcheth ſayth nay yet ſemeth paye thylke power moſte acceptable vnto goddes longeſt ſtondeth ſtable deuoyde ſurquidry pryde kouth vpon euery ſyde eche lande one many harmes greues haue befall rancour onely pryde wylfulneſſe inportable coulde expreſſe pryde done offence hygh goddes maken reſyſtence tho ſurquydous whiche vyce ſo contraryous ne may place abyde good fayth manhode pryde hath acqueyntaunce outher frendſhyp alyaunce proude man confederate herte hyghe lowe eſtate nedes muſt euer many neceſſytee lothſomeſt enmy contrayre nothyng may man ſo moche appayre pryde ſoth highe lowe degree wherfore rede playnely wee foule vyce herte arrace quarell may haue grace ſpecyally dedes conueyed euer fall ryghtwyſeneſſe voluntee trouth ſothfaſt guyde v derecte rightfull lyne ſhall quarell aye honour ſhyne contune full felycytee ¶and ferthermore knowen ye come done vengeaunce frendſhyppe alyaunce vpon pryam wronges done olde hym haue ofte tolde hereupon haue grounde ytake ſome maked wake manful hande caſtelles ſtronge beate downe ſtonde haue ſo longe take rycheſſe founde ſlewe men many bluddy woūde harmes mo done countre wote well enmytee vnto v great moche afore dare ſaye double yf auenged myght v echone anone ye ſhulde ſee great ire ſo cruell ſo huge execute without refuge yet ſoth wote haue eſpyed beynge though aſkyred yet dare ſaye vtterly well ware faſte ouermore wote well alſo harmes haue whiche yet freſhe grene ſtronge mighty ſuſteyne werre v anone wolde gynne yet citie whiche walled ſtronge toured rounde wenen fully doute meyne haue gathred theyr allyes ſhall wyn ſmale werre ſtryfe ſoth hath prerogatyfe aduauntage countre hym ſelfe deffendeth namely ſtuffed ſtronge frendes hym beſyde alyes doth abyde lyke rauen fether blacke within neſt often tyme make agayne faukon gentyll nature full harde diffence whyles hy may endure vanquyſſhed outrayed yet ſome whyle faukon delayed whyles rauen beſyde neſt doth flee within courte lybertee euery foule frowarde areſte daunted owne neſte yet theſe wordes ne ſaye wyſe putten fraye knyghtly hertes ſo manly ſo ſtable ſhulde doutable troyans fully ſhall confounde citie habounde playnly deſtroye albe ſtronge nowe amonge shall fynally conſumpt death thorowe grekes ſworde yelden vp breth ¶but cauſe without drede ſaye thus ye take hede pryde preſumpcion aduerte diſcrecion prudently reaſon nede haſte may brydell lede ſo ordeyne henſe wende laude prayſe ende may reported haue deuyſed many man hath aduiſed purſuite lacke prouidence ſe tofore aduertence ſhuld fall deth hath thē brought suche wylfull haſt good thought v fore examynacion well diſcuſſed reuolucion ¶of thynkyng ofte repente fyrſt remembre pryam ſent v late exyon yet holde kynge thelamon whiche v without aduiſement vndiſcretely denyed aſſent whiche hath v none aduauntage grounde rote full great damage wyſe purueyaunce made tho delyueraunce harmes great eſchewed parys ſo purſewed temple faire cythera buylded beſyde cirrea treaſour great alſo iewelles thenſe ladde troye great rycheſſe ſlaughte men heauineſſe yet made quene heleyne throughout grece great payne menelaye ben nowe vnwrought ſo foreſene thought wyſely tofore reſtored exyon harmes ne one enſewed v ſothfaſtneſſe ſpent labour ſo ydelneſſe treaſour good waſted ſo vayne come ſo ferre fetche agayne quene heleyne coſtes inportable withouten harmes eſchewable yet ne wote whether ioye aduerſytye thynge ſhall tourne syth ofte ſyth dependent doubte fatall thyng vnſyker vnſtable fro gynnynge often varyable ende ſene fortune tranſmewe gery courſe therfore eſchewe harmes poſſyble lykely fall counſayle amonge al vpon arryuaile trauayle eſchewe matter ſewe pryamus without ſende fyrſte agayne reſtore quene heleyne ryght reaſon harmes done eke parys treſpaſſe offencion iuſtely maken reſtytucion may worſhyp honour retourne home without labour aſſente requere axynge lyſte folyly wylfulneſſe refuſen worthyneſſe double aſſured ſyker grounde iuſte tytle troyans confounde thynges two ſhalbe vnder pyght fyrſt power borne vp ryght shall v fyght quarell dareyne balaunce euen weye atwixe v twayne fyne ſhalbe excuſed tofore haue wylfully refuſed iuſte profers made afore ſhalbe worlde therfore without ſpot treſpaſſe blame myſreporte hyndrynge name foly ſhall ynoted wylfull wodneſſe playnly shall ſtande free power vſe euery man ſhall v well excuſe though execucyon takynge vengeaunce offencyon men chylde eche ſecte age ſhall death holden paſſage ſworde without mercy pace one better grace bvt yet tofore counſayle taketh hede ye meaſure bede holde beſte moſte ſyckerneſſe worke good auiſeneſſe amonge ſelfe longer tarye whiche counſayle ſome contrary varyaunt opinyon saue moſt diſcrecion aſſented playnly ende choſen haue pryam ſende amonges ambaſſyat ſpede vlyxes wiſe worthy dyomede whiche anone gan ready make ſhope forth waye take towarde troye lyne ryght ſonne ſhone full ſhene bryghte holdyng courſe fyry ſphere mydday arke wonder bryght clere gylte eche hyll vale playne roche beames dyd approche walles gate towne go without noyſe ſowne▪ full well ſene porte ryght manfully waye ladde paleyes ſtreyght lyne nedeth aſyde declyne courte large wyde ſquare thei ful knightly wight wold ſpace vnto effecte manly procede charge without feare drede commyng tho refuſed tho dayes peraunter vſed haue conduite embaſſadrye cuſtome man denye ſuppoſe entre paſſage ſo come meſſage courte builded ſo royally come fyrſt meruayled greatly royall ſyght ſo huge ſtrength well complete brede length ne lyfe tofore sene none ſo fayre yet wonder paleyes together gone paued iaſper ſtone tree amyddes ſtode loke thought thē good muſyng artifyciall erecte ſette magyke naturall engyne workemen curyous ſubtyll craftes ſuperſticious worke nycromancye profounde caſtynge phyloſophye apparaunce ylluſyon outher crafte incantacion vp downe caſten mynde reaſon myghten fynde rote grounde wonder worke trouthe ſo derke wytte though longe trace pryuitee compare conceyue poſſyble eye vyſyble ſoth without fable mannes hande ſo palpable whiche ſtocke guydo tolde ſothfaſtneſſe pured golde whiche ſhone bryght ſomer ſonne enlumyne thinges donne body maſte ryght proporcyoned moſt goodly ſyght subſtanciall huge ſtrengthe twelue cubytes body length croppe rounde large brede compaſſe gan flouriſhe ſo ſprede playne aboute enuyrowne bowes ſhadowed vp downe ryche braunches leues fayre twayne twayne ioyned payre one golde another ſyluer ſhene meynt among wt ſtones whyte grene rede ſome ſapher hewed euery daye blomes renewed bloſſomes many ſundry ſuyte ſtones inde bare ſtede fruyte ſayth guido tell grekes longer dwell holde theyr waye many ſondry wente parfourme fyne entent tyll atteyne chamber pryncypall pryamus ſee royall lyke eſtate full kyngly wyſe sat aboute ful prudent ful wyſe lordes ſettes hym beſyde whan grekes ſurquedous pryde ſterne cheare frowarde coūtenaunce lytell remembraunce gentylneſſe curteſye guydo doth playnly ſpecifye enteryng taken haue theyr place thoppoſyte kynges face ſet theym downe without ſermon obeyſaunce ſalutacyon worſhyp honour reuerence done kyng excellence preiudyce gentylneſſe anone vlixes gan expreſſe cauſe theyr comyng kyng pryamus without abode ſaying euen thus forberyng preſence kynge meruayle haue wondrynge though honour dewe comynge ſalewe syth ne longeth ſothe thinketh rancoure hertye enmyte deadly hate ſalutacions fayned falſe affection ſhewe hertes ben fyre naturally man ſhall deſyre enmye helthe welfare platly lyſt ſpare shortly ſhewe fyne entent lyke hauen commaundement meſſage agamenowne noble kyng moſt worthy renowne whych v hath ſent ſeyne vnto quene heleyne rauyſhed grekes lande brought troy force mighty hād agaynſt ryght vyolence wherfore ſhortly without offence iuſtly axe without demaunde thou anone rightfully commaunde menelay ſhe ſent agayne axe vayne thou make reſtytucion wronges done regyon pylfres great ſlaught robberye paris done wylfull tiranye whych thy ſon ſuſteyned errour wronfully maynteyned wherfore come fully condeſcende without grutching wronges amende ſo thou mayſt beſt goddes queme lyke thou mayſt thy reaſon deme right requireth worke wyſe ſo thou deſpyſe execute haue tolde truſte right well leſſon thou ſhalt lere whych thou thine ſhall hereafter rewe without feyning thou ſhalt fynde trewe thou better ende make cruell vengeaunce ſhall take fynally ſhuld fayne force death quarell ſhall darayne vpon vpon thy bloud raunſomles golde good queſtionles reporte merciles riche ſtronge cyte shall downe bete ylayde ful lowe walle toures alſo ouerthrowe ſome beth well aduyſed axyng deſpyſed wyſely worke haue ſayde ſodaynly king priamus abrayde haſty yre ne might abyde grekes whan ſawe pryde great outrage preſumpcyon without abode delyberacyon vlyxes anone gan breake vnto euen thus ſpeake ¶i wonder greatly myn aduertence beyng aſtoned preſence vngoodly ye dare make demaunde lyke ye power commaundt conſtrayne byddyng obey feare durſt ſaye maner thinge ye axen contrayre ye requyre wherof ſothly herte amened threttes inwardly agreued aſtoned ſurely lyfe ye ſo hardy excyte vylaynouſly myn honour prouoke wordes worke truſteth right wele wyll paſſe boundes neuer dele rather ſhortly ende axyng ought condeſcende ¶for conſydre fyne entente ſyttyng conuenyent kynge graunte axing though yt stode myſchefe captiuite without recure vttraunce ybrought outrage playnly thought axe hym ye axe ſothly yet beleue ye accomplyſhyng may ſo much auayle ye haue ſayd platly ye ſhall fayle purpoſe ſaye god toforne mauger might though ye ſworn requeſt euery man ſyght wanteth grounde trouthe righte axe ſatyſfactyon ſelfe fyrſt occaſyon whan ye ſlewe father lamedowne lyeges brent eke towne many harmes ſoughte cauſeles tho ye wrought longe reherſe whych daye daye herte perce ſyſter eke called exiona regyon ye haue ladde away whych vnto worthineſſe ytreated lyke gentilneſſe ¶and ye would amendes haue wrongly whylom ſaue thynges peace ſtynt werre haue ſente grece ferre onely haue exyona agayne whych ſonde ye hadden diſdayne cruelly vngoodly wiſe meſſenger ye gan tho deſpyſe vnueth ne might eſcape awaye grece ye knowe naye ſo vngoodly cheare good fayth lyſt nowe heare requeſt gyuen audience axyng great offence leuer ſhortly deyen condeſcende ought ye requere wyl fully concluſyon knowen agamenon haue leuer doubtles fynally werre peace syth ye haue done ſo great treſpace trouthe ſelfe place cruelly anone ye ſhulden dye offyce embaſſadrye agaynſt death fully diffence ſo bolde withouten reuerence preſence ſo thret ſpeake truſte right wel ſhuld anone wreke wherfore haſte without wordes mo counſayle ye ago ſight voyde cyte thus ſtandeth while ſe herte may entre gladneſſe fret yre ſo holdeth diſtreſſe good fayth may ſuſtene inportune rage tene inwardly bindeth whyle diomedes tho began ſmyle ſayd anone thus vnto kinge ſo thou cominge thine herte haſt ſo mykle payne v beholde twayne art therwith ſo inly ſet fyre ſhalt thou neuer withouten yre thy life deuoyde wo syth thou haſt ſo many cruell fo grekes entred thy lande hundred thouſand almoſt thyn hande agayne whoſe might yu mayſt ye aſſure reſyſt playnly endure conſyder well ſtronge thou ſhalt wyt peraunter longe manly men ſo well arayed expert armes olde aſſayed diffence may agayne theim vayle wyte eke well thou mayſt fayle death ſworde theyr hande deye thyne ſeye though ſo proudly thou ſpeake thy tunge onely wreake afermeſt thou mayſt acheue better ſuch boſtyng wordes leue wyſe counſayle taketh better hede bvt haſte agayne diomede surquidous inly full pryde roſe vp ſome kynges ſyde ſwordes drawe wold haue fal al hewen among theim haſty yre brenning glede tyll pryamus gan taken hede roſe vp ſeyng diſeaſe manfully rage gan appeaſe theim diffending vpon death lyfe none theim hardy ſtryfe embaſſadoures harme greue though fole foly leue preſume ſpeake vnconningly wyſe man muſt ſuffer pacyently though happe offence foliſhe ſpeche lacke ſapyence wyſe man ne ought ſothe ſayne taken hede ſpeake agayne fole pertynent ſhewe foly right ſo conuenient wyſe ſothly ſuffraunce porte haue tolleraunce vnto foles belongeth kindely without aduyſe ſpeake folyly vndiſcretly mening fulfyll wyſe man heare ſtyll tyll ſe tyme haue pacience diſſimule aduertence rage foles laſt throwe tunge fole oft knowe leuer wel aſſure perſone domage endure ſuffer meſſengere court haue wronge great lite ſwerde rancoure may alway bite vengeaunce thyng nought oft falleth wronge wrought lytel exceſſe foloweth great reprefe haſte aye medled wyth myſchefe wherfore byd ye ſytte adowne wiſe preſumpciowne attempteth maner wyſe ſygne worde deſpyſe thembaſſadoures grekes ſente let theim frely declare theyr entente ye whyles kepe lippes cloſe ſodaynly eneas roſe whych next kinge helde ſee inwardly rancour fret ne myght ſelfe refrayne ſayd ſyr ſo ye diſdayne ſhall ſaye ſemeth wel according one hath ſayd amys rekly ſpoken vnaduiſed foly chaſtyſed maye example take wel ware ſuch noyſe crye make ſpecially open audience offende royall excellence ſothly yet wote well might gouerne playnly ſyght haſtineſſe without auiſement ſhulde commaundement death deſerue great offence trewly yet ne preſence twayne haue ſo yſpoke without abode ſhuld anone wroke worthy ryght well ſittyng whan fole preſence kinge bolde hardy preſumpcion take indiſcreſcion thinge reherſe concluding ſentence preiudyce magnificence taught better gouerne large tunge konne bet diſerne whan ſhal ſpeake whan peaſe ſuffer renne leſe doth ſpoke hath ſo large wherfore haſte counſayle charge without abode worde mo ſyghte anone ago beſt rede anone ful proudly diomede aſtoned ſterne loke eneas yre quoke anſwered agayne wordes fewe ſayd ſyr thy wordes doth well ſhewe ſo thou thou art ryght wiſe well king doth thyne aduyſe hath nye counſayle ne maye erre degre art ſo rightful thy iudgement wylfullneſſe without aduyſement cauſe lorde bondes pace would god ſome place myght fauoure fortune mete leyſure oportune lyke deſyre canſt ſo well endite olde fable thy labour quyte thanke thy gentyll chere ſo knightly thou haſt v ſhewed truſte well therto haue therof drede tho vlixes diomede gan interrupte wordes prudently ſayde full aduyſely beſt ſtynt ſtill know fully thy quod vlyxes full manly kynge go henſe without taryinge thy ſight agamenon make playne relacion thy aunſwere ordre horſe wenten ſodaynly ſhorte time ſo haſt way come ſaye kinge ſatte tentorye worde worde came memorye reherſe ſubſtaunce euery dele wherof grekes like nothing wele conceyuing full remedye reporte embaſſadrye saue onely vtterly procede theim ſhall gouerne nede agayne troians neceſſitee well wote may none aſſented wyl dede puruey theim faſt theim ſpede ſtorye ye ſhall fynde bvt fyrſt therof maken mynde muſt whyle eneas endyte myne auctour lyſt hym wryte whych ſothly bokes ſaye manly troian worthy eneas anchiſes ſone great worthineſſe whylom gete venus goddeſſe conqueroure many regyon whan troye brought deſtruction wente waye large ſee called tyrene ſaylyng forth goth many coſte many ſtreyght paſſage many daunger tyll cartage ryued thenſe gan ſayle conqueſt great ytale ſo rome hath waye take whoſe ſpring auctours mencion make came auguſtus ceſar emperour whilom ſo noble conquerour renowne daye doth ſhine enee emperour iuſtyne bokes called autentykes full playnly wryt therin rubrykes ceſar ſo ceſares named yet ryght ſo eneades enee name ſhoulden beare whych fro troye comen ſo fere vnto ytayle eneas haue tolde ceſar deſcended downe lyne ryght ful manly royall fyrſt rome ſceptre imperyall maugre theyr myght gouernaunce wyſedome ſet ordynaunce common thynges touchyng cytee procede enee hooly lyfe knyghthod ye lyſt reade ceryouſly ye may ſe ful autentyke ſtyle eneydos compyled vergyle albeit ſo noble clerke graue afore cōplete werke bokes olde maken mencion ¶how agamenon ſent achilles thelephus ilande meſſa vytayles ſlewe king ordeyned thelephus kynge ca xx bvt nowe agayne agamenon without wyll ſtyle retourne whych kyng ſoiourne matter delayes make haſte hath counſayle take lordes beyng preſent ſuch hath ſent one al earles duke kinges ¶and ſayd ſyres amonge thynges iourney neceſſarye counſayle longer tarye fyrſt make ordynaunce one aſſent prudent purueaunce alder fyrſt ſhape v vytayle without whych none hooſt may auayle parfourme iourney thryftely wherfore reade faſt lykyng pleſaunce yle ful habundaunce called meſſa ſende anone one worde aſſented euery chone choſen haue worthy achilles thelephus ſone hercules execute purpoſe fynally many worthy theyr company ychoſen hooſt anone achilles meſſa gone whych lande ryche plenteous reygned kynge worthy famous tentran hyght whych tranquylyte without werre aduerſyte holde sceptre royall ſete yle ſo pleaſaunte ſo mete albe ſome ſaye lytell yle kyngedome longeth cecyle hath name gyuen plente meſſane huge great cite full plenteous ſe lande whych kyngdome vnderſtande ſayde meſſena meſſes latin habundaūce fruyt corne wyne aryuayle playnes large wont ſtuffe charge merchaunt ſhyppes ſtraunge fer countre thyther ſayle large ſea fetche vitayle aye yeare yeare fro many coſte landes farre nere onely eſchaunge merchaundiſe eke alſo bokes deuyſe guido full playnly telleth v kyng called meſſanus countrey firſt meſſa toke name tyme great fame paſſyng ryche wonder plenteous dare frygyus boke maketh mencion ſhortly telleth concluſyon achilles thelephus alſo meſſena togither go thre thouſande grekes choſen moſt manly men amonges theyr route whych faſt gan londe kynge gan vnderſtonde theyr comyng deſcended downe worthy regiowne horſe foote ſtele armed bryght agaynſt grekes manfully fyght theim deuoyde playnly yf ſodaynly thus ſkermyſhe gan atwixe grekes mortall fone parte many one slayne hurte death ywounded neuer lykly therof ſounded ¶for treate theim atwene ſwerdꝭ ſharpe ſperes ſquare kene go ground euery man foo confounde labour dyd buſyneſſe though grekꝭ theyr worthineſſe theyr foen much londe ywon yet retyre begon meruayle none bycauſe theyr fone alwaye thre noumber agaynſt one time may none till achilles gan beholde ſe mortall ſlaughter vpon grekes ſyde tourning ye backe wt woundes large wide haſty rancour chaungen gan bloode yre furious woode whan behelde men leſe theyr lande wt ſwerd whiche helde hande made waye kylled bare downe felde like fierſe lyowne fared ſothe yt men ſlawe makyng foen backwarde withdrawe grekes ſo manly recomforte maugre theim made reſorte ¶and euer waye ſtode without mercy kylleth mode gayneth nought crueltee doubtles ne manhod paſſyng renowne worthyneſſe knighthod eke high proweſſe grekes daye fynallye vanquiſhed without remedye helpe recure achilles ſturdy wall gan ſerche ſheltrouns theyr rāges brake tofore whoſe face fomen go wrake ¶and alderlaſt whan gan eſpye tentran kyng chyualrye defende ſelfe lyke worthy knyght lyon bare fyght grekes ſo oppreſſe achilles cruell hardyneſſe ne would ceaſe purſewynge warde tyll came king manly force ſtoute full pryde makyng waye rounde euery ſyde agayne whoſe might nothyng might auayle ¶and tentran fyrſt auentayle raced hath rent male aſonder al hewe wonder conſydre daye cruelte al broke hath baſſenet wyth many cruell wounde myght ſmyt kyng grounde haſte maked hath let head rende baſſenet merciles vengeaunce harme gan heyght auaunce fully purpoſe ſhulde dead raunſomles gan amyn heade blody ſwerde deſpytous herte caſtyng playnly ſhulde aſterte ire ſo furyous ¶but fortune befell ryght thus thelephus yonge luſty knyght caſuelly therof ſyght achilles maner ful behelde ſtroke anone bare vp ſhelde gan achilles mekely preye haue pytye ſo deye syth laye wounded almoſt deathe brought poynt yelden vp ye breathe beſeching beningnyte manly routhe eke knightly pyte withdrawe hande grace graunt life lytell ſpace syth euery knyght ſhould gentilneſſe enmye ſpare whan diſtreſſe vttraunce brought ſpecyally whē mercy requireth humble voluntee ¶to achylles feruent yre rancoure ſet fyre aunſwered agayne lyſt ſo preye nolde pryde wyll obeye gyn werre nede highe diſdayne indignacion hauyng truſte preſumpcion manhod myght auaile agaynſt grekes holden battayle preuyd playnly ende otherwyſe ſhortly wende dyche iuſtely falle hath made malys v ¶where wyll entencion gaue vnto hym none occaſyon vpon ſyde platly fer nere miniſtred hym ſuch matere lande menten damage hym ſelfe grounde rage without offence done hym v ¶and efte agayne yonge thelephus humbly required hath hym achylle knyghtly routhe axyng fulfyll haue mercy hym caſe father kynge whylom quod thelephus bonde confederate whiche lyeth nowe diſconſolate expectant deadly face vpon houre whan goſte ſhall pace gyrte ala wt many mortal woūde ¶and bycauſe haue found afore tyme aſſured great kyndeneſſe manhode gentylneſſe boundes regiowne vnto highe renowne whylom caſually gan ryde shewed ſoth vpon euery ſyde full royal chere great humanite bounde duytee remembre haue mynde doubtles elles ſemeth vnkind wolde name foule twyte parte wolde acquite beſeche reſpyte lyfe achylles withouten ſtryfe delyuered hath ſtory telleth thus tentran frely vnto thelephus whether hym lyſte ſauen ſpylle hym wyll hath conſydered woundes grene ſo mortall ſothly ſo kene nede muſt dye gayne remedye auayle maye medecyne houre whē phebꝰ weſtward gan decline battayle brought ende whyle grekes ſhyppes wende meane whyle tentran payne woundes gan complain without ſtaunche ſo pyteouſly blede offycers faſte gan ſpede lytter made tho full royall toward paleys doūge owne pryncipall cary hym ſofte eaſyly ¶and prayer full benyngly thelephus alſo achylles conueyed hym among preſe tyll brought hym lyſt receyued lyke degree full royally kyng aye languyſſhyng drewe towarde endynge might longer drawen forth length wofull lyfe ſo weke ſtrengthe ſpirite muſt algates wende haſte cauſed ſende achylles thelephus whan came ſayd vnto thus ¶syres quod full worthy degree helth honour longe proſperitee vnto goodly aduenture whyle lyfe may dure ſpecyally oh thelephus whiche haſte ſo gracious gentilneſſe paynes ſtronge onely grace lyfe prolonge death ala may eſchewe ſworde parte remewe without recure knytte bytter bondes vpon brincke fall fatys hondes lyfe fully diſpeyre whiche body neuer myght haue heire daye ſucceſſyon gouerne lyttell regyon whiche lykely ſtande diſconſolate gouernaunce fully deſolate erſt wan full great trauayle day werre ſtronge bataile haue kept ye well knowe echone defended maner fone withouten loſſe yeres heretoforne recurlees yore lorne ne helpe eke ſocour hercules great conquerour whylom father thelephus ſtronge ſo mighty ſo chyualrous whoſe manhode whoſe hardineſſe knyghthode great worthyneſſe whiche daye day new memorye foen vyctorye daunted made ſo ferde rygoure ſharpe ſwerde fynally manlyhede cauſed reygne poſſede maugre might peace quyete ſeptre crowne royall ſeate none tyll dead hardy lyfte vp head agaynſt ſpeake wordes fewe wherby may fully declare ſhewe euydence little yle perteynent longeth cecyle hercules memoryall sette pillers conqueſt royall ryde gon tho ſo ferre columpna yet name beare hym called herculea though ſome ſaye hyght herracula name chaungyng corrupcion whiche lande whylom manſyon people wylde barbarye whiche kyngdome magnyfye frederyke ſothly ſecounde golde
