good paſſyngly habounde choſen emperour rome towne mighty gouernour whylom eke kyng cecyle whiche made reyſe large yle myghty toure hyghe thycke wall ſayth guydo memoryall put name longe remembraunce ſoyle pleaſaunce floures freſhe many ſondry hewe ſome bokes lande named newe ycalled vnderſtande fayreneſſe luſty newe lande tentran aye lyinge payne faſte gan houre attayne cruell death afore lordes made haſte thelephus call preſence mortall chere sayde openly men myghten ſonne quod ſyth nedely muſt pace worlde gayne may grace lyfe ſaue mannes myghte bycauſe equytye ryght compelled iuſtly ſentence declare clerely conſcyence tofore death herynge preſe ſaye thy father hercules wyſe worthy knyghtly man whylom lond conqueſt wan whiche onely godlyhead ſtocke manlyhead toke vnto cōmyſſyon gouernaunce regyon free wyll hole regally nolde ſelfe countrey occupye ſothly yet ryght laſſe loue ſyth ſhall paſſe full entent laſte wyll graunt ryght ſkylle heire iuſtly ſuccede longe honour therin thy lyfe lede makyng proteſtacion full token confyrmacion wyll fynall myne hearte fro whiche man may diuerte vpon ſyde vtterly declyne ¶for fyrſt wyll diſſent lyne together combyne one fro whiche thyng man may gone deſyre laſte langour thou playnly ſucceſſour fynally thus conclude deme vnto septer diademe delyuered euery circumſtaunce wyll aſſuraunce made write teſtament fyne concludynge laſte entent full piteouſly beſought thelephus moſt hertely manly routhe knyghtly gentilneſſe deuer buſyneſſe death like eſtate royall halowe holde feaſt funerall solemply exequies ſodeynly without wordes mo kyng tentran yeldeth vp goſte went waye note coſte deme ſuche myſtyhede whan perca broken threde rocke forth waye thelephus marbell graye curiouſly tombe made carue dead corp therin conſerue full rychely aboue graue epythaphe anone dyd graue honour playnly expreſſe knighthode worthyneſſe howe goſte deuorced letter ryche golde aboue enboced rounde aboute wonder curious tombe ſayden playnly thus lyeth tentran kyng doubtles whylom ſlayne cruell achylles ſcepter regallye hooly gaue whiche man may denye thelephus ſonne hercules whiche tombe reſteth nowe peace whan perfourmed euery thynge thelephus meſſa crowned kyng hyghe lowe one aſſent ſolempnely open parlement made fayth hym ydone homage lyke degree age hole herte beſt entent othe aſſured ſacrament trewe lyeges receyued kyng ¶than achylles without taryinge whan ſette peace gouernaunce without grutchinge varyaunce ſhyppes anone made carye euery thyng neceſſarye grekes corne fruite vitayle fleſhe fyſhe might auayle hoſteynge helpe nede downe ſea dyd lede fully veſſell ſtuffe lade thelephus made stylle boundes regyon abyde concluſion helpe diligence buſynes diſcrete prouydence agayne myſchyefe ſcarſytee whan nede myght ſocour albe lyke ſayth guydo achilles full fayne wolde haue go abode ſothly beſte bonde aſſured fully beheſte euery thynge grekes releue haſte achilles toke leue thelephus gan anone ſayle ſhyphes ſtuffed vitayle towarde grekes made menciowne ſhorte tyme tenedowne aryued taken hath grounde knyghtes likwiſe hole ſounde ¶and agamenon fyrſte hath made full relacion exployt lyke fall preſence lordes sittyng enuyron many worthy knyght ¶and fyrſte meſſa telleth fyght whan entred welcomyng ceryouſly tolde eke kynge tentran hyght playnly alſo achylles amydde fyelde hym ſlowe death hole entent fully ordeyned teſtament thelephus alſo heire tolde eke repayre vnto ſea eke vyttayle ¶and thelephus wyll fayle ſende may pleaſe whiche thynge grekes great eaſe brought herte lyke wonder well achilles tolde euerydell greatly preyſed hygh prouydence manhode ſapyence beynge bare ſo achylles ygo lodgynge lyttle beſyde knyghtes vpon hym abyde myrmydones full glade comynge hym receyued longeth kynge abode reſted hym whyle ¶but guydo declyneth ſtyle grekes troye towne muſt alſo make digreſſyowne myne auctour ſteppes ſewe lyke conuenient dewe matter ſyth guyde whyle grekes ſette aſyde wyll reherſe dare frygyus troye booke declareth vnto v ceriouſly maketh menciowne lordes came troye towne helpen manly defence agaynſt grekes maken reſyſtence ordynaunce many dyuers thynges came thē erles duke kinges dare playnly made mynde reade boke ye may yt fynde ¶and alder fyrſt reade specyally ſpeaketh kynges three full manly men alſo great fame reherſeth name kyndomes yet wryteth thus ¶the fyrſt theim called pandarus reade tapor ſeconde thirde andraſtrus lyke founde guydo lyſt ſpecyfye thre thouſande knyghtes companye manly men euerychone ¶and yle called coleſon lyke dare liſteth expreſſe came alſo excellent proweſſe ¶kynges foure whiche fyrſt hath wrytte ynamed carras ſeconde hyghte ymaſyus neſtor thirde iiii amphymacus fyue thouſande worthy knightes came manly fall vpon grekes helping towne fro ye prouince knowen great renowne called lycye came kyng glaucon brought ſonne sarpedon noble knight armes full famous allyed kyng pryamus thre thouſande yf ſhall fayne came knightꝭ wt theſe lordes twaine ¶and laryſſe ryche lande alſo fynde camen kynges two quite manly ought thouſand knightꝭ troye brought ¶and kyngdome named lycaowne euphemus kyng great renowne brought hym dare doth wytneſſe thouſande knyghtes great worthyneſſe fyue hundred dare telleth v came hupon epedus many knyghtes plate ſyluer bryght hym eke kyng yt remus hyght brought iii thouſande troye many myle tabaria large mightye yle duke foure chiualrye erles viii came companye hauynge armes great experyence bare without difference men ye fyelde chiefe golde eueryche ſhielde wherby kynge holy nauy amonge knowen mighten albe bore eke ſame alſo frō trace kynge pylex name fro thylke trace moſte excellent whiche plage oryent haueth ſcyte frō mighty kyng thouſande knightꝭ brought cominge myne auctor recordeth eke alſo hundred knightes troye go alchamus worthy duke famous came pilex guydo wryteth thus troyans helpe great nede fro pauonye ſothly reade came pretemeſſus noble werryour lorde lande kynge gouernour duke stupex alſo knyghtes thouſande ladde towarde troye region ſtorye maketh mencyon prouince ſtandeth moſt wilderneſſe woodes plenteous thickeneſſe wherin growe full many diuers tree moſt foreſt men may ſe buylde houſes fewe lande full diuerſly ſhewe many lykeneſſe queynte monſtruous beaſtes vnkouth ſyght merueylous stoundmele apparence illuſyon falſe exiſtence wonder gaſtfull playnly ſene dyuers goddes woodes grene apperen called satyrye bycornes eke fawny incubye cauſe often men falle rage lande people full ſauage hardy knyghtes furyous woode deſyrous aye ſheden bloude greatly experte ſpecyally ſhete darte ſpere peryllous mete caſte euen lyne ¶and yle named boetine great araye troye citee lyke fynde came duke three fyrſt called amphymus samus ſecounde thirde forcius ſayth dare liſteth lye twelue hundred knightes company ¶and fro brotyne made remembrance riche lande hath ſuch habundaunce ſpyces gummes fruites corne wine holſome rote ryndes ryche fyne wonder vnkouth precious alſo comen kinges two full knightly men armes deſyrous kynge boetes epriſtuis wt brought troye ferre thouſande knightes arayed werre ¶and fro lande called pafflagonye whiche ſeuered companye bookes ſaye hyſtoryall vnder plage oryentall sette ſo ferre made reherſayle fewe none lande trauayle come nere impoſſyble whiche lande called inuiſyble bycauſe onely remoſion yet yt ryche regyon golde ſyluer alſo ſtones habundaunte plentee none ſo full treaſour good hath ſcyte ryche floude ynamed tygre fer eufrates ſayth myne auctour called dare whiche lande ſtele armed clene thouſand knightes came phylomene worthy kyng whoſe ſhildes drede cuirboilye guydo read golde depainte fret ſtones ryche world trow nōe liche floudes choſen deuyſe whiche haue courſe paradyſe whiche kyng gyaunt ſtature makynge paſſyng meaſure stronge delyuer alſo fynde ¶and fro lande yt marcheth vpon inde kyng perſes came many knightly man alſo hande hym wan moche honour noble kyng menon eke brother called sygomon whiche lande ſubiectiowne duke erles knyghtes renowne thre thouſande brought plate ſhene ſperes rounde whet ful ſquare kene ethyope came noble route ¶and kyngdome alſo doute thereo dare called came kyngfull prudent full wyſe manly man named theſeus eke ſonne hyght archylogus thouſande knyghtes company theſeus full nyghe allye pryamus diſſent bloud kynges twayne paſſyng ryche good renowmed knighthode fame albe guydo reherſeth name yet ſtorye maketh mencion agreſta lyttle regyon thouſand knightꝭ brought vnto troy grekes pryde daunte acoye choſen pycked ye none ¶and land beyond amazones lyſſynya kyng epyſtrophus wyſe ſo worthy inly vertuous paſſyng counſayle diſcreciowne full worthy renowne preued alſo ſpeciall artes called lyberall lerned expert ryght notwithſtandyng worthy knyght werre peace manfull ryghte ſage albe ronne ferre age ſtorye maketh reherſayle thouſande knightꝭ cladde plate mayle troye towne fynde ladde hym guydo ſayth hadde wonder archer ſyght meruaylous fourme ſhap maner monſtruous lyke myne auctour reherſe fro nauell vpwarde man lower downe lyke horſe yſhaped thilke parte man maked ſkinne blacke rough bere couered fro colde paſſyng foule horrible ſyght whoſe eyen twain ſparkeling bright furneis reade leuene lyghtnyng falleth yt heauen dredefull loke reade fyre chere reade good archer bowe euen morowe vpon grekes wrought moche ſorowe gaſted many hydous loke ſterne many quoke whan hym ſawe ſo ougly horryble lothſome credible many one hath wounded death cauſed yelden vp breath grekes ſyde ye ſhall ¶and wyſe aſſembled byn yfere kynges duke erles renowne ſundry landes within troye towne byn ygathred come fro ſo ferre ſayth dare helpe werre numbre maketh mynde two thirtye thouſande fynde worthy knyghtes lordes eſtate ſyth worlde fourmed create ne ſene trowe one citee together aſſembled ſo hygh degree knightes ſo great multitude yet dare ſothly conclude boke maketh mynde came troye ſmaler inde nouther moſte famous renowne wt priam yborne troy towne ¶that fynally trewly ſought syth ye houre world wrought dare affyrme vnder phebus ſphere many worthy mette yfere manly men flouryng luſtyneſſe freſhe ſo yonge lyklyneſſe euery poynt ſhape arraye well ſothly naye lyſt conſyder vpon outher ſyde world men go ryde floure knighthode worthineſſe chyualrye hyghe proweſſe aſſembled without within fully aſſented werre ſo begyn ¶wherfore ye lyſters taketh good hede delyte boke reade fyrſt lyttle werre began light cauſe ſo many man hath loſte lyfe myſchyefe pyteouſly yet man beware therby almoſt nought ſtryfe begonne lyſte loke haue hereby nought wonne deth ala hard ſtound many knight caught dethes wounde without recure remedye ¶and woman ſhall lye gan ſtryfe pytie ſo great miſchyefe aduerſytie mortall ſlaughter euer ſhulde betyde better haue ſette aſyde suche quarelles dere ynough myte let thē paſſe yt vengeaunce byte wyſedome caſte afore ſe ſuche ſklaunders myght eſchewed venym gynneth rype though ye men horne blowe pype whan houſe fyred hete ſparke late treate cauſed wherfore gynnynge remedye put euery thynge euery wyght may deme reaſon ¶and grekes lay tenedon refreſhe reſte peace worthy kyng hyght pallamydes thirtye ſhyppes grekes lande stuffed wt knightꝭ ful worthy hande beſte choyſe regyon aryued vp tenedon wherof grekes whan ſyght reioyſynge ryght glad lyght hauynge regarde vnto worthyneſſe afore made heuyneſſe abſence ſo longe ſome grutched hym ſtronge ne kepte mouſter athene ſhewe clene ſpotte conſcyence full manfully open audyence lyke knyght gan ſelfe excuſe stoppyng tho theron lyſte muſe ¶of abſence ſhewyng cauſe ſykeneſſe ſodeyne malady cōſtrained preſence withdrawe ſawe ſyckneſſe hath law helde excuſed fully abſence ¶and moſt reuerence amonge grekes ſo wight ſecounde alſo full wyſe eke habounde golde good auyſe prudent ſo euer ſette entent knyghtly wiſely wolde aye well achieue ſoeuer gan nolde leue maugre foen maner wyſe tyll ſawe fyne empryſe moſt opinion amonge grekes reputacion beſought wolde counſayle auiſely forſe euery maner thyng aſſenteth vnto axynge benyngly great gentilneſſe grekes dyd theyr buſyneſſe procede withouten delaye enhaſte euer maye gyn ſyege differre nought ſundry way ſerched haue ſought wyttes tenedowne may remeue towardes troye towne hauen ſhippes ſome thought moſte commoditee beſt exployt nyght pryuely toward troye towne ſtode faſt proudely ſayle ſhyppes ſome ſayde great peryll might fall towarde night take ſea leſt derkeneſſe ennoſed bee paſſage knowynge waye wherof great harme fall maye thus diuers opynyon procedyng concluſyon effecte purpoſe ne helde ſtyl abyden lodged fyelde lyke entryked drede ¶tyll daye worthy dyomede grekes ſeynge cowardyſe euen thus counſayle gan deuyſe ¶syres quod preſent lyſte one aſſent goodly conſyder aduertyng prudently ſhall ſaye tofore openly whiche knighthode haue ſo noble name ſothly ſemeth oughtē haue gret ſhame whiche holde ſelfe ſo mighty ſo ſtronge lande ſoiourned haue ſo longe nigh yeare durſten wiſe remoue henſe cowardiſe haue nought elles certaynly foen graunted folyly euen luſt ſpace liberte make theim ſtronge oportunite v withſtande playnly hande ſo ye may well vnderſtande ¶for daye daye confuſiowne ſought way full wiſely vp downe get theim helpe meane ſpace theim enforced aboute euery place large cite barres pali walles maſcued agayn ſkalis truſteth theron made great ordinaunce gouernaunce haue eſpyed ſeyng drede haue herte manly procede purpoſe hold werre aye ſe differre catchen hardineſſe v reſyſte al buſineſſe alſo ſe truſt veryly afore hand manfully began knightly forth contynued iourney better fortuned ſodaynly ſtronge mighty hande vnauyſed lande without abode afore time ariued muſt depriued delayed fyrſt victorye honour palme high glory might ſothly ne ſlouthe complyſhed playne trouthe maugre v lande ariue ſtrōg defēce agayne v ſtriue put v ſtronde may win aye tarye begin ſothe liſt lye put ſelfe echone ieopardye ſhould ſayne fage ye trouthe tarying cowarde ſlouthe likely tourne v great ſorowe wherfore betimes next morowe counſayle ankers vp pulle matter longer dulle enarme ſhippes werre vpriſe morowe ſterre let v ordayne knightly apparayle thys hauen winde ſayle manly herte luſty freſhe courage courſe holdinge right paſſage towarde troye landen openlye euer fall truſte ſykerlye without ſcarmiſhe may ariue troye deſcende bliue like manly men mete v berde let v aferde dreade avoyde manhod ſet afore cowardiſe ne entre bore adaunt manhode herte worde grekes gan aduerte manly counſayle diomede effect procede dede vnto poynt nothinge wyll ſpare wiſe anone declare ¶how grekes lāded tofore troy ſtoutly fought ca xxi next morowe wonderly betime phebus roſe longe prime whan began full merily dawe grekes hooſt ſhipward ginnen drawe manly herte fully deuoyde drede onely comforte diomede alder firſt anone awake lordes wiſely gan counſayle take concluded amonge theim euerichone ſhippes ſhulde ye formeſt gone ſea ſhoulde theim guye ariue man theim aſpye deuiſed certayne marke night paſt ſinging larke grekes ben ſhipped without tarying high lowe rathe dawning ¶and firſt tofore hūdred ſhippes toure stuffed many worthy werrioure gan proudly ſayle charge theyr baners brode bright large diſplayed euery ſide departe fomy wawes wyde ſight whelmen vp ſo grene next theim werre enarmed clene ¶another hondred folowed faſt bare ſayles paſſing proudly ful many worthy knight armed mayle plate bryght foloweth hooly nauye trowe ſuch companie worthy knightes lordes degree neuer afore ſene vpon ſee eolus fortunate eke neptune made tho none debate wt winde trouble amōge ye ſterne wawes attempre wether ful mery thē dawes tide ſayled tight troye towne caught anone ſighte wherof herte full glad light whan troians firſt ſhippes ſe proudely ſayle litell ſtronde ſawe caſt thenn londe bode arme theim haſtely plate mayle iackes richly irous herte done anone toke horſe forth haſt gone gate made tariynge ne bide prince duke kinge lorde guyde theim gouerne haſt theim forth ſo many ſo yerne felde ſo great multitude amonges folkes rude manly men thriftely ſayne clenly armed large playne ye grekes gan theim firſt beholde great nomber made hertes cold none ſo manly theim amonge yonge ſo freſhe ſo hardy ſo ſtronge high eſtate low degre ne aſtoned ſe hardy troiās ſo proudly deſcend let grekes aſſende well wiſt ſeme vtterly none meane tariue onely death manly fight cowardly take theim flight conduyte playnly none ſharpe ſworde ſperes caſe tyll ſodaynly hardy fierſe kinge protheſalius gouerninge formeſt hundred ſhippes ladde gan haſt ire hadde win lande firſt would mete theim ſo great deſyre ſuch winde gan ſayle driue ſhippes whan ſhope ariue▪ vnwarely ſ 〈…〉 vpon londe getteys drye ſonde ſhippes ſhiuered aſonder ſome dreynt broke yon • er deuoured wawy ſee routhe pyte ſe greater parte tho gone wrake while ſome buſy take drye lande filth mudde ylade troians theim ful cruell ſlaughter made maugre might grekes ſo conſtrayned wt blud wawes yſtayned mortally ſothly beholde amonge ſonde pale dead colde grekes lye woūdes freſhe grene eyre withe ſhote arowes kene yſhadowed ye phebus beames bright vpon ſoyle derked light newe alway troians theim aſſayle grekes playnly ryuayle mortall ſo infortunate vnwelfull diſconſolate vndiſpoſed infelicitee trowe neuer erſt ſee ne came none hooſt harder londe grekes ne wolde wonde lyfe death manly aryue ſo befelle aduenture blyue ¶thre hundred ſhyppes ye next ſewe aduyſedly tyme dewe entred haſte faſte ſtryke ſayle ankers caſte ſtrongly enbatayled londyng leſt aſſayled wiſely fyrſt ſette arbalaſters gonners beſt archer pauyſers go aforne knightly land though troiās haddē ſworn contrary proudely lette yet fyerſly vp ſette grekiſhe ſhote made withdrawe many lande laye ſlawe maugre ſtrōde recure ſuche myght moſte manfully endure ſette afore tyll lande haue take attones ſuche aſſaute make vpon troyans tho began fyght protheſylaus ye noble worthy knighte wonder lyfely ryght paſſyng ſtronge grekes entred amonge hardy troians euery thē ſought armes meruayles thē wrought thilke daye worthineſſe many troyan brought diſtreſſe went felt full vnſofte whoſe manhod grekes alofte thilke daye knighthod grekes great aduerſite vanquiſhed fatall purueyaunce finally brought vnto vttraunce yout abacke playnly lye auayleth chiualrye worthineſſe fierſe courage might helpe auauntage syth vii thouſande grekes ado hundred thouſād troians tho meruayle might endure wiſe ſtronde recure ſo fewe holde felde theim ſelfe one thinge behelde full prudently whych tho gaue theim herte ſawe mighten aſterte ſcape life woulden fle backe nothing ſee fore hooſt ſo great huge waye refuge dye attones fight manfully wherfore caſt ſhope theim knightly like manly men liues rather ieoparte cowardly foen departe leſe grounde drenchen ſee thus longe would grekes defende theim aboue might albe many killed fight ſtreames red bloud ran ſonde large flode cruelly troians theim ſet ſpere ſwerd ful ſharpe ground whet routhe pyte thinke till almoſt droue theim brinke grekes miſchiefe diſtreſſe great anguiſhe paſſing werineſſe theim ſelfe defende mate full ywery ſhoulde haue peryſhed vtterly recureles ſothe euermore ne archelaus worthy prothenor ſhippes aryued vnto lande ſodayne happe theim ſtande yet full great aduerſyte ariue cruelte troians yet lande win grekes cruelly begin agayne foen ſtanden defence manly force great violence tho gan encreaſe blody werre newe ye ſoyle depeynted wt dewe firſt grene tourned red eche ſide ſo many one lay deade vpon grounde life depryued ¶but duke neſtor ſodaynly ariued knightes fell full irous herte right melancolious ſperes archiers aſide entred ſterne full pride ſworde grounde ſharpe kene ran yfere met vpon grene hoked arowes alway flewe amonge ſhaftes ſhiuer braſt tourne wronge tole ſteled well whet longe daye haue togither met ſlaughter newe alwaye began euery halfe many worthy man woundes large deſpytous ¶for prothenor king archelaus ſwerdes ſtiffe among renges kerue many troian made ſterue daye ſo paſſingly irous theim tauenge inly deſyrous neuer ſeaſing purſewing ¶and releue theim alagus kinge ylonded eke king attalus troians full enuious brenning ire fiery glede vpon theim olde hatrede knightes ſodeynly fall ire bitterer gall cruelly foen oppreſſe aſſent buſineſſe maugre theim backwarde reſorte amide felde reporte choyſe ſo cōſtreyned force manhode payned withdrawe confuſiowne haſt downe troye towne worthy knightes freſhly armed newe deuyſes many ſondry hewe without abode ſhortly conclude came downe ſo great multitude eche armes depaynte vpon ſhylde comming glittereth al felde armure ſonne bryght whan entred fight grekes metynge felly enuye ſette vpon fret melancolye ſuch herte courage ſuch furye mortall rage accorde none mene ſlaught death theym go betwene thrugh ſtroke axe dagger ſpere force compelled grekes theim retourne backwarde ſtronde whoſe reſcuſe anone came londe king vlixes hole nauye full knightly wyth chiualrye towardes troians enhaſteth anone one herte grekes gone theyr courage hooly reſume gan foen felly conſume vnto death domage reuenge wight may iuſtly theim chalenge manhode ſo well haue theim borne acquite harmes done beforne time like fierſe lyowne amonge troians ranging vp downe vlixes wente ſwerde honde killeth ſleeth knightly gan fonde thilke daye like man founde many mortal wounde vpon troians wrought wracke thē bering downe fote horſe backe ire ſtrokes ſo kene ¶at time worthy philomene lorde king pafflagonye whan behelde companye many troian vlixes ſlawe towardes anone gan drawe horſe backe ſpere rounde ſadyll bare grounde vlixes roſe vp anone right taking horſe lyke manly knight anone philomene hath ſayne toke eft ſpere rode agayne mightely ſuch violence fynally gayneth diffence ſmote euen ye ſhelde flewe aſonder felde plate without fayle ſpere head reſted mayle forged ſtele ful ſhene bright perce ſpere head hath might trewly made haberiowne wt ſtroke vlixes bore downe yet efte agayne haſteth vp anone ne ſtroke herme felt none raught ſpere ſharpe whet ygrounde philomene gaue ſuch wounde myght armes twayne yrous herte ſo great payne ſheld ye plate maile ſmote vp auentayle gorge ſtocke gan glyde horſe fell downe aſyde full peryllouſly pyght vpon head knightes wenyng ſothly dead toke vp layde ſhelde bare home haſt felde great daunger might wyn grekes lord twyn troians ſuppoſed ſykerly philomene withouten remedye dead aſtoned caſe daye ne befall phylomene grekes ſtronde outrayed arruing vp londe knighthod doubtles phylomene vlyxes vnhorſed hath mortall wounde knightly wyſe troians confounde wherof aſtoned euerychon ¶but thoas agamenon grekes hooſte lorde emperour aryued vnto theyr ſocoure knightes menelaus eke worthy thelamonious called ayax lande come leyſure haue theyr horſe nome grekes troians occupye sore fighting gan faſt hye towardes theim making delay fruſhe haſt may ran yfere ſperes bracke herte enuyous vpon horſe backe myght men worthy knyghtes ſe ſtedes eche flee ſtyffe ſwordes ſhaftes great rounde hedes ſquare pointes kene grounde myght men ſe furyous tene many knightes dead vpon grene moſt ſlaughter confuſyowne fell thilke time theim towne grekes ſo myghty ſo ſtronge felde contynueth longe ¶til protheſylay ſtronge mighty king daye ſkarmiſhe fighting full lyke knyght occupyed againe troians cruelte manhode onely worthineſſe aduenture weryneſſe refreſhe taken eyre abrethe making repeyre ſtronde aryue thought herte gan ryue cruel yre alſo pyte hath caught onely ſe men ſlayne endlonge ſtronde ſome theim comyng vp londe dreynt ſea amonge flodes depe whych thinge gan anone wepe full pyteouſly aſpyed whoſe wofull eyen might tho dryed conſtreynt ſat ſo nygh hert till laſt amonge paynes ſmerte cruell yre gan herte enbrace ſodaynly deſpytous face without abode thought vpon theyr death would auenged finally attones theim deye ſtede toke right weye towarde foen ful yrous rage line right holdeth paſſage swift grayhounde yt renneth leſe ſawe greateſt ye prefe preceth amiddes felde ſworde yt hande helde grounde kerue byte full mortally aboute gan ſmyte theſe troians might aſterte ne ryueth ſome vnto herte ſome woundeth ſothly death ſome made yelden vp breath ſome alſo vnhorſeth cruelly met daye vtterly horſe made alyght rode fled ſighte preſence death eſchewe ſtyll one gan theim ſewe chaſe lyke wood lyon thus playeth theim towne tyll perſeus etheopye kinge came cyte ſodaynly riding many knyght many lyuely man whoſe coming newe began freſhe ſkarmyſhe furyous wood many greke daye loſt blode fell aſſaute troians theim make amonge theim ethiopes blake manly bare thē fighting troians afore fere remounted newe aſſured yt helpe haue ye feld recured made theim leſe alſo much agayne tofore wonnen playne ſo hole ſo mightely kept theim togyther ſo auyſely gouerned theim glaue ſpere ſhelde grekes compelled felde maugre grutche neceſſyte ſtronde backwarde flee almoſt diſpayred mate comfortles kinge pallamides theyr reſcous came aryuayle luſty freſhe entreth battaile knightes hole maynee taking horſe tho faſt ſee proudly thenſe embuſhed one ſpere ſwerde yground none wiſe gouernement doinge haue ſo oppreſſed coming manly troians wonder ſe theim lye ſlayne yonder continueth til amonge preſe auenture pallamides brenning aye furious hete amid felde happeth mete worthy knight called sygamon brother kyng menon neuewe alſo guido doth reherſe manly man kinge perce grekes daye ſore oppreſſed knighthod expreſſed grekes worthineſſe oft ſithes brought great diſtreſſe ſame daye great encreaſe ¶but fortune ala pallamydes tolde hath fyelde mette ſpere ſquare ſharpe whette whan knighthod moſt pride rode hym ſmote ye ſide laſt deadly fatall wounde ſtede bare hym grounde playne bloud red pallamydes lefte pale dead amonges troye forth rode bare downe euer waye ſtode theim ſo furyous wood maugre troians tofore playne made reſorte walle agayne manly knightes alway faſt awayting ful ententifely redy honde euery great empriſe tho began noyle aryſe wofull clamour pyteous crye theim troye vtterly agayne grekes mighten ſuſtene mortall ſwerde ſo ſharpe kene noble worthy famous knyght pallamydes great myght longe daye hath yborne ſo agayne foen ſo knightly perſone high renowne chaſed hath almoſt towne troians echone manly made theim flee noyſe entred cite hydous crye mortall ſhoute ¶wherof amened hector yſſueth oute furyouſly haſt ſon mar knyght māly mā worthy yet worthieſt euer hardieſt phebus beames cleare amonge ſterres right ſo appeare excellyng ſtele armed bryght heauenly ſyght nigh terre worthineſſe lode ſterre whych whan entred felde like reade bare daye ſhelde fyelde pure golde thre lion ſtorye tolde whoſe coloure made mencion fynde diſcripcion paſſant reporte ryght borne breſt troian knyght ye ground rote high proweſſe floure accompted worthineſſe ſo manly without abode amonge knightes grekes rode lyke man cominge aſtoned gan thringe amonges thē killeth downe ſlethe met death afore ſwerd grekes go wrake wardes knightly force brake maugre theyr head ſeuered thē ſonder bare downe ridyng yonder caſually meteth waye ¶protheſylaus whych longe daye ſore fought agaynſt theim troye ſlewe tho comen waye hardy knyght worthy fierſe kinge whych troians euer purſewyng theim ſo hertely great enuye whych thinge whan hector gan eſpye knyghthod gan taken hede towardes tho turneth ſtede line right haſty ire rode ſwerde diſteyned al blode cloue head baſenet ſuch might ſtroke na let force mayle thicke plate fynally mortall fate ſwerd hector thrugh nerue bone vain worthy kynge parted hath twayne vtterly gayneth none armure agayne ſtroke hector endure kynge ſo full worthineſſe stronge mighty great hardineſſe receyued hath laſt fatall wounde lyeth dead parted grounde hector forth amonge grekes rideth whoſoeuer ſtroke ſo abydeth refute none diffence death many greke thus daye ſleyth whych theim tho waye ſtode ſharpe ſwerde batheth blode alſo ferre might ſe death ſwerde fle mortal vengeaunce vpō thē wrought many greke felowe ſought gan enquere might lyfe coulde neuer ſe none ſo knightly haue battayle playnly dempte ſuppoſayle hector noble warryour whiche knighthode bare away floure amonge euer yet borne na greke may ſtād aforne day gan ſo enchace ſtronde euen afore face ne durſte mortall ſtroke abyde euery ſyde grekes chaced wawy ſea wounded mate great aduerſyte reſt troyan knight anone lyke mar himſelfe home troye gone whoſe partynge grekes efte preſume manly agayne hertes reſume newe fomen aſſayle inparte wolde auayle lyfe death ſette outraunce fortune lyſt ſhe wold auaunce parte agayne recure fyelde thē enforce might ſpere ſhielde anone forthwith maken delay wynne agayne troyans maye viii tymes ſythen begonne felde haue day loſt wonne lyke fortune lyſte cure vp downe tourne eure whele went rounde right ſo day wan loſt groūd ſpecially moſt deſmayde whē hector came hath thē ſo outraide thrugh knighthod made hertꝭ ryue reſorte dyd aryue thus continued mauger myght fielde troyan knyght ¶tyll phebus chere gan weſtre downe repayred towne whiche grekes wrought afore full yll ¶but hardy cruell fyres achyll aryued knyghtes myrmydones men wonte calle whyche ſea taken haue playne whoſe cōmynge grekes haue agayne fyelde recured put ſelfe preſe helpe worthy achylles whiche ſo felly troyans fall vpon hath ſlayne full many one thre thouſande ſtele armed bryght hym brought redy fyght knyghtes echone full worthy renowne whiche achylles grekes champyowne haue mercileſſe crueltee slayne many troyan citie ſo feruent mortall ire enuyous hate deſyre newe newe ſhede bloud achylles thought dyd good ſworde ye troians bloud ſhede ſoyle ſe lye blede rowthleſſe melancolye hath ſo hote enuye without deth may quenche ſworde ful depe hath made drenth throughout day troyans bloud batheth floude whiche forged ywhette ſo knene many ryuer ſothly grene ran hurtes ſore knyghtes alway purſued afore hym flee harde walles troye cytee dolefully made pyteous crye whyle fynde ſtorye ¶the grekes hooſt hooly aryued lyke guydo deſcryued men armes ſuche multytude knightes ſhortly conclude ſhyppes newe landed troye aſtoned ſe abaſhed gan wexen ſodaynly gynneth fall euery halfe paſſyngly great preſe euer one hardy achilles ſworde made ſydes red laye bodyes dead wounded ſome entre gate knightly gan debate furyouſly fell cruell knyght chyldren ſlewe father ſyght beholde great pyte yet ſlaughter tho greater numbreleſſe towne perpetually confuſyowne lykely euer haue ouercome ¶if troylus ne reſcuſe come yenge freſhe luſty inly deſyrous come paris deiphobus many worthy partye ſocoure grekes tho ne myght endure agaynſt ſtanden deffence pryde maken reſyſtence worthy troylus ſo well yt time hym quytte ſoth greke hytte outher maymeth made hym deye wherfore deth fled weye fyerſe achylles companye nyght homewarde gan hym hye towarde grekes glorye honoure receyue hym lyke conquerour whiche tyme ſo happely mette ¶and troye haue gate ſhet made thē ſtrong throughout al ye towne ¶and tyme kyng agamenowne yſerched hath place couenable thought moſt agreable liklyhod moſt conuenient euery lorde pytchen tente fylde full large ſpace moſte competent lodgyng place dewe ſcyte ſette cite eche lorde ſigned ſhulde ¶and gan anone ordeyne manſyons pytched tentes pauyllyons ſuch might tentoryes haue ſtorme rayne ſelfe ſaue deuyſed habytacles tiguryes ſmalle receptacle ſhroude night alſo ſhyppes hadden moche ado might well haue horſe lande ordeyne ſhulden ſtande alſo buſye carye thynges neceſſarye nedefully vnto ſyege longe eke made tye ſhyppes ſtronge porte ankers haue caſte aſſent buſyed full faſte confyrme one entenciowne ſet ſyege tofore troye towne thervpon bounde aſſured faſte abyde whyle lyfe many laſte fynally without repentaunce prudently made ordynaunce beſt coulde longe nyght bete fyres brennen wonder light ſpace deuyded fro fyres ſette vp lyke theſe barrier rounde lodgyng paled fyelde compaſe acheue fyne purpoſe ſlyly wrought kept thē ſelfe aye cloſe ¶and kynge treaſon fall let make watche without tentes ſuche reſted afore mynſtrelles made ouermore ſayth guydo longe nyght kepe tydes tofore fyres bryght meryly ſowne inſtrumentes made reſte tentes afore wery fyghte ſea faynted might others eke made armure awayte wyſely agayne aduenture deceite founde vpon ſyde ¶and thus kyng knightly prouyde aduyce nothyng hym eſcape al night fynde dyd wake ¶tyll morowe rowes red phebus chare gonne ſprede thus eche thynge diſpoſed ought wyll procede tellen wrought ceryouſly without eke within ſupport thirde boke begyn thus endeth ſeconde boke thyrde boke ¶of firſt battaile wherin hector ſhewed hym ſelfe valyauncye tofore capitulo xxii wvhen aurora pale lyght vnder ye mantel mirke night curtyne hewes fade yſhrouded derke ſhade abaſhed rud dy defyne ſhe femynyne aſhamed durſte tho ſeyne bycauſe ſhe ſo longe bedde leyne freſhe phebus owne choſen knight whiche ſhe hydde ſothly ſyght tyll ſtede called flegonte enhaſted hym aboue oure orizonte appollo beames clere hath recomforted oppreſſed chere ſaye dawnynge tytan vp eaſt ryſinge hete atempre ryght ſofte hemiſphere glade lofte ¶the ſame houre troyan champiowne gouernour werres towne worthy hector whiche cite nexte pryam ſouereyntee towne guyde knightly excellence manhode ſapyence troyan knyghtes lorde eke cheuetaine whiche hath commaunded large playne hyghe lowe exceptynge none kynges prynces lordes euerychone ſame morowe mete yfere araye muſtre appere lyke name eſtate beſyde temple whylom conſecrate goddeſſe called dyane moſte honoured riche phane array haſte lyke deuyſe knyghtly man ¶and playne paſſynge fayre ſe ſette amydde troye cite smoth right faire full freſhe floures worthy noble werryours troye towne togyther aſſembled many beholde ſe famous knyghtes arme yt place ſome gan full ſtreyte lace doublettes made lynnen clothe certayne folde aboute hym goth ſome alſo dempte moſte ſureſte arme batayle areſte dyd fyrſt deſyres sabaton greues cuſſues voyders payre brech alder fyrſt mayle ſome eke ne wolde fayle haue mayle payre braſe therwithall cuſtome payre guſſettes pety coote garniſhed golde vp vnto throte paunce plate whiche ſelfe behynde ſhot cloſe theron fynde enuyron abordure ſmalle mayle ſome choſe newe entayle ſurmyd foe hole breſte plate arere dors behynde ſhet elles ſyde armes rynged wyde voyders fretted mayle cordes rounde freſhe entayle vambras wynges rerebras therto theron ſette beſaguys alſo vpon head baſenet ſtele within locked wonder wele craftye ſyght wrought viſer ſome wolde haue plate bauer breſt faſtned aforne canell pece eaſy borne gloues plate ſtele forged bryght ſome wold armed light thicke iackes couered ſatyne ſome wolde haue mayle wrought ful fine hawberion late wrought caſſade weight ouer lade hym ſelfe welde lyke lyfly man ſome wyll haue choſe geſeran boublet hawberyon ſome ſure gepon ouer polrynges rechinge knee ſleues eke ſo longe vambras may cured ner pryckynge palet plate couer ſome wyll haue alſo vyſer ſaue face onely aſer ſome wyll haue payre plate lyghte welde hym well whan ſhall fyght ſome wyll haue target ſpere ſome pauade body ſome targe made ſtronge laſte ſome wyll haue dartes caſte poilax headed fyne ſtele pycked ſquare laſte wele ſome ſwerde enemye mete ſome wyll haue bowe ſhete arblaſt ſtanden ſyde ¶and ſome foote ſome ryde array ſelfe fomen ſayle many one buſye nayle felowes harneys make ſtronge dreſſe ſette wronge poyntes taſſhyes maner thinge ſuche caſe longeth armynge haue connynge euery thynge telle vnto longe dwelle fayle ye mot haue excuſed ſuche crafte lyttle vſed ignoraunce doth pennelette order dewe termes ſette ofte chaūgeth ſuche harneys deuyſe ye therin expert wyſe diſdeyne ſpeake place armynge grace right lyſt correcte euerydell ¶and hector ſawe al well euery man armed arrayed worthy knight longer hath delayed aduyſedly wardes make prudently badde ſhulden take grounde haſte put certayne ſtande order endlonge playne man founde recheles ¶and gate called dardanydes without abode hector made vnſhette bad men ſhulde fette preſence done haſte ¶cyncynabor brother borne baſte vnto hym fyrſt euerychon ¶and lord named glaucon kynges ſonne lycye heire many baner auaunſed eyre theſe two hector gaue guarde gouernaunce fyrſt warde hath thouſande knyghtes ſette ſperes rounde ſwordes kene whette breſt full many ryche ſhyelde choſen fielde amonge beſte endure myght agayne grekes manly fyght vnto hector bad anone goddes name ſhulden gone gate ſothly rede ¶and leſt fyll miſchiefe nede aſſygned ſelfe place manly chere kynge trace wyſely hym awaytyng thouſande knyghtes haue ledyng wynge knyghtly abyde wayte hym vpon euery ſyde hym ſonne archylogus age man ryght vertuous fulfyll longeth knyght herte alſo myght ¶and next hector gan deuyſe next warde kyng fryſe time called zantipus vnto hym ſtronge deſyrous aſſygned wayte banere thre thouſand knightꝭ armed bryght clere whiche warde kyng alcanus alſo hector commaunded go byddyng mekely dyd obeye full knyghtly taken haue waye gate paſſyngly arrayed towarde grekes baners diſplayed penons vnrolled euerychone ¶and hector aſſygned hath anone noble yonge luſty freſhe free brother troylus ſo goodly ſe whiche knyghthode ſuffyſaunce thirde warde haue gouernaunce thre thouſand knightes yonge age flourynge force hardy courage suche cuſtome wont lede hector brotherhead full goodly ſpake ſayd partynge brother quod herte ſo louynge towardes kyndneſſe though haue party gret gladneſſe thy manhode ſo ferre kouthe knyghthode thy grene youthe yet doubtleſſe fantaſye ful ofte daye ſtande iupardye penſyfehead buſye drede whan remembre vpon thy manhead leſt thy courage vyolent thy lyfe neglygent thy ſelfe put ferre aduenture ſurquidrye ſo moche aſſure thy force knightly ſterte euery peryll thy manfull herte hauynge regarde ſuche mortall ſtryfe wylfulneſſe nouther death life aduertence thy ſauacyowne fortune turneth vp downe whele meuable hye lowe martes ire wynde doth blowe whiche cauſeth ful ofte ſyghe thincke wake whan ſhulde wynke reuoluynge aye thy haſty wylfulneſſe gentyll brother hardyneſſe thus ylke daye vpon euery ſyde praye ſo wyſely prouyde hate yre thy foe purſuynge excede ſettynge let prudence kepe mene wyſdome eke holde agayne reyne thy herte thy fyerſe courage fyred haue thy grene tendre age deuoyde drede eche peryll endure ennemyes thy myſauenture reioyce myne owne brother dere myghty mar praye herte entere thus euery day troyans grounde handes kepe ſounde lyke wolde dyd ¶to anone humilite manly wiſe yonge luſty knight worthy troylus herte freſhe light anſwered agayn ſayd glad cheare mine owne lorde brother deare god tofore fully ſhall obeye fullfyll lyſt ſeye vnto gentilneſſe decline none reckleſneſſe poynt commaundemente hole herte beſt entente ſhall take hede playnly none ye haue ſayd mine owne lord bother lothe offende greue wiſe lowly toke leue forth rode ſo lyke manly knyght beholde noble ſyght amonge men haueth hym ſo wele thre thouſande knightes armed ſtele enuyron rode troylus fyelde day beareth ſhielde paſſant golde thre lyon rychely champe aſure wrought full craftly gate yſſued anone ladde knyghtes euerychon grekes holdyng next waye ¶and hector haſteth euer may prudently wardes ordeyne noble worthy bretherne twayne kyng hupon andelius aſſygned ſtory telleth thus fourth warde guye wyſſe lande called laryſſe brethern two reigned longe hupon paſſyngly ſtronge ſtature lyke chaumpyowne ſaue hector troye towne none hym egall myght delyuer better knight foen paſſyng deſpytous whiche brother andelyus foure thouſande knyghtes hadde lede ſeuen thouſande ſothly rede lyke wryte guydo worthy hector aſſygned hath alſo one brothern called dimarchus noble knight armes ryght famous manhode paſſyng excellence hector taken haue lycence rode waye amonge preſe gate dardanides ¶the fyfte warde haue ledyng hector commytted kyng ceſoyne lorde prynce brother called pollidamas theſe cyſones hye ſtature might armes paſſyngly endure vpon full many man behelde kyng bare nothynge ſhyelde fyelde gules fynde ſygne guydo maketh minde forth rode full ſterne paſe noble kynge pollydamas whan hector lene take whiche euer one full buſye make ſyxth warde diligence kyng called pretemenſe full worthy werre peace ¶and duke hyght sterepes whyche alſo full worthy honde toke folke poenye lande gouerne fyelde day whiche people hath cuſtome aye without plate hawberion mayle ſwyfte horſe fomen aſſayle mighty bowes arrowes ſharpe groūd harneys mortally wounde folke hector eke alſo deyphobus aſſygned go fyelde guyde lede waye faſte gan theim ſpede paſſe dardanydes full diſcretely hector cheſe panyſers cladde mayle plate commaundyng yſſuyng gate archer fyelde gone many worthy well armed euerychone awayte lore folke ſpake tofore poenye hadden none armure prudent hector make ſure agreſt myghty regyowne hath choſen full worthy renowne beſt knightes euerychon ¶and kynges eſdras phylon aſſygned taken hede fotemen haue nede whiche phylon ordeyned full rychely rode chere yuery whyche wheles wrought full curious tree ycalled hebanus whiche tree groweth ferre inde blacke hewe alſo fynde korne tree wyll anone nature harde ſtone whan graue eyther rounde ſquare pure golde roued chare fret perle many ryche ſtones ſuche trowe none worlde ſhall fayne ladde mighty knightes twaine men armes within eke without armed ſtele rydyng rounde aboute theſe worthy kynges eſdras phylon hector hath called hym anone one brethern ſo falle guyde leder name pytagoras ¶and great troyon eneas tofore made mencion hector good deliberation ſeuenth warde aſſygned hath kepe vpon ſtedes luſty lepe ſuche vſed moche ryde full manly knightes haue ſyde whiche ewpheny vnto troye towne come ſo ferre regyowne ſuccour hector ſake hym leue take rode full proudely forth eneas gate wonder knightly paſe brode fyelde tyll haue atteyned ¶and whyle hector hath ordeyned lyke myne auctour reherſe eyght warde folke perce worthy knightes manly ryght wyſe whiche committed paryſe day tawayte buſyly hector tho full beningly spake ſaide thus departyng oh brother myne maner thynge whan thou arte paſſed dardanides daye ferre put preſe amonge grekes iupardye leſt thy toen miſchyefe eſpye haue olde newe date hertes full freſhe mortall hate fyre breſt hath ſo enbraſed harde araced wherfore brother loke thou euer wiſe ferre fro kepe nye miſauenture fall vpon ſo may ſuccoure daye mine owne brother deare parys full humble cheare anſwered ſayd euery thinge would obeye vnto bidding rode waye anone meyne felde cite ninth warde ordre dreſſe whych thought hym ſelfe lede whych put ſothly rede fiue thouſand knightꝭ borne troy towne worthyeſt greateſt renowne paſſyngly famous knighthode borne diſcent troians bloud ¶and brethern taketh wt hym ten suche knewe moſt manly men forayne ſtocke regallye lyne borne baſtardye hector great chyerte knyghthod could theim ſe whan knightly purueaunce wardes ſet gouernaunce lyke mar ſelfe faſt gan ſpede without abode take ſtede whych bokes called gallathe horſe hauyng ſoueraynte ferre men ryde coſte dare maketh ſo great boſte ſhape heyght alſo fayrneſſe ſtrengthe loke great ſwyftneſſe lyke horſe perfourmed oute wt wyer men might tourne lyke dare maketh menciowne whō hector rydeth troye towne armed came wonder well foote head full rychly euerydele ſhone bright ſon ſomers daye pryam helde ryght waye whan come kinge reherſeth ordre euery thynge hath done ordynaunce lowly ſayd ſo pleſaunce noble royall excellence haue choſen buſy dylygence thouſand knightes full ſuffyſaunce fyue hundred haue attendaunce perſone alway ye footman cyte ſhall awayte euer one wherfore lorde faſt gone lowly praye worthineſſe ſewe v good aduyſeneſſe towne alway eke ye togyther kepe knightes meyne beſeche full myght within boundes ſhall fight ye ſuffer none theim paſſe kepe ye hole ſelfe place atwyxe v ſtronge cyte haue nede ye maye aye ſe v releue kepyng aſyde ſpecially abyde moſt lyckly partye ſuſtene euer amonge ſhal men go betwene exployt trouthe reporte parte mar lyſt fielde ſorte power ilke daye fatall ye ſhal caſtell wall refuge ſaue v ſmerte ſpecially one thynge ye aduerte deceyt fraude treaſowne compaſſed behynde towne foen reckleſneſſe whyles hooly buſyneſſe agaynſt theim fielde fight wiſe therto haue ſyght nothynge tourne vnto domage engine worke ye ſage victorye maye conclude grekes fraude v delude engyne vnware vyolence hopyng alway none offence highnes haue ſayde worde pryamus abrayde beningely cheare countenaunce ſayde hector ſothfaſt ſuffyſaunce fynall truſte ſupportacion thy diſcreat diſpoſycion hooly put thou liſt ordaine next god ſhall fayne fayth hope ſikerneſſe welfare ſothfaſtneſſe committed hole thy hande gouernaunce playnly lande thou ordayneſt muſt nedes prayer make nowe goddes aboue celeſtyall preſerue partye eche myſchiefe aduerſyte thou mayſt home ayene cite repaire honour laude victorye praiſe renowne memorye thy name put remembraunce perpetually thine honour auaunce fare well mine owne ſonne deare hector tho full humble cheare leue toke forth rode anone amonge lordes knyghtes euerychone roote nobleſſe knyghthode groūd ſtrengthe hardyneſſe ſtocke therto inuincyble muche poſſyble nature myght graunt kynde touchyng manhode bokes fynde hadde ſoueraygne excellence gouernaunce medled prudence nought aſterte ſo wyſe ware ſhelde fynde bare vpon breſt troian champyon chyefe golde gowlys lyon depeynt therin baner bete ſelfe ſame ſo amydde ſtrete toke waye dardanydes beholde huge preſe noyſe trumpettes claryons baners vnrolled longe freſhe penons red whyte grene blewe blacke wyſe hector hath ytake felde wythout wt herte hole entente mar ſelfe tho preſente guydo maketh mynde rode warde lefte behinde manhode would abyde ſmote ſtede ſharply ſyde fell courage hath horſe ſo payned fyrſte warde hath atayned vale hylle tofore frounteres aſtoned fell cheares grekes platly aferde lyke knyght euen afore theyr berde gan preaſe theyr foo mortall ¶and whyle vpon troye wall ſondry place hygh toures freſhe beſene may floures ladyes aſcended towne fayre ſo yonge ſtandinge enuyrowne quene heleyne paſſyng fayre ſene kinges doughters goodly pollycene many whych womanheade herte full buſy dreade inly agaſte feare afrayde whan behelde fyelde diſplayde brode baners ſome tenderneſſe loue ſome kyndneſſe pale dreadfull theyr lordes ſome theyr face hyden eke feare bolde lyfte vp theyr ſyghte heholde armure cleare bryght glytterynge aye agayne ſonne ſhene theyr hertes tender myght ſuſtene theyr dreade thus lette theim dwel grekes forth ſhall tell yf ſo ye liſt abyde whyle muſt fordulled ſtyle agayne dyrect agamenon well maye make exclamacion ignoraunce ſtaunt ſo lyght cauſeth full cloudy ſyght makynge ſpeken werre lacke tearmes muſt nedely erre conningly wardes ſette cruell alecto buſy lette nyghtes doughter blynded derkneſſe crafte armes trouthe expreſſe ordre dewe felde deſcryue chauncer nowe ala alyue refourme rede lacke ſlower ſpede noble rethor excelle making dranke ſo welle vnder pernaſo muſes kepe hylle neuer yet might ſlepe vnneth ſlombre whych ala playne ſayne though wede pollymyte coloures forth wyll endyte cometh euen thought playnly write ye kinge hath wrought manly knight great agamenon lyke latyn maketh mencion ¶what trowen ye entente founde ſlowe neclygente grekes halfe wardes make nay nay ſo lyſt wake tyme ſothly ſlepe lyke kinge daye felde kepe neclygence myght herte fade daye fynde made syxe twenty wardes well deuyſed ſo prudently man might amende ordynaūce fyrſt gaue gouernaunce manfull noble patroclus wt ladde myn auctour telleth thus myrmydones ſo myghty ſo ſtronge folke achilles longe beſyde thylke meyne whych brought countre cominge ſiege troye rode forth theim waye ſyelde made delaye fell ſo ſame daye achilles kept tente ſyckneſſe daye ne wente lecheſſe made abſtene woundes freſhe grene caught daye tofore whych heale theyr akyng ſore counſayle kept ſelfe cloſe bedde daye ne roſe hope onely better endure whan reſtored vnto cure men toke patroclus armes paſſyngly famous diſcent come great kynrede alſo hym reade hoboundaunt golde rycheſſe ferre commēded gentilneſſe name hygh dyſcrecion ¶now aye ſuche affection entyre loue trouthe faythfulneſſe great deſyre inwarde kyndeneſſe buſy thynkyng ſo great feruence much frendſhip wt thoughtful aduertēce huge brennyng ſo paſſyng amerous betwyxt achilles patroclus theyr hertes locked cheyne ſoeuer ſhall fayne tone hath wrought brother vnto brother herte confermed wyll goodes commune death euer ſo contune without chaunge theyr loue ſo abode ¶and patroclus forth anone rode fyelde myrmydones tente abydeth achilles ¶the ſecounde warde kinge menon aſſygned agamenon ¶and worthy kinge ydumenee duke called meneſtee thre thouſand knightes ſtele armed clene wyth folke comen athene aſſygned wyth theim go ¶the thyrde warde king aſcalapho ſone hyght phylomene knightes came cumane ¶the fourth warde without lettynge archelaus noble worthy kynge prothenor securydan whych dayes ſo ſtronge man aſſygned holly theſe three knyghtes theim boece myghty lande famous ¶the fyfth warde kinge menelaus folke regyowne called spertence full high renowne yles adiacent theſe baner wente ¶of menelay freſhe couragyous vi warde kynge epyſtrophus aſſygned kinge gelyde many worthy rydyng ſyde prouynce famous yle called guydo fordeſyle ¶the ſeuenth warde thelamonius called ayax great kynge famous aſſygned ſhortly termyne folkes salomyne brought many another mo foure earles hym went alſo ¶theſeus eke amphymacus thyrde called doxus fourth named polyxarye viii warde ſhall tarye good aduyſe daye aſſygned vnto kinge called thoas ¶ayax cileus ix warde tho ladde tenth king philoctetes hadde ¶and kinge xi aſſigne ſothly byrth lyne renowmed ſo great encreaſe mighty kynge called pallamides kinge naulus ſon higheſt borne blode duke neſtor full famous knighthod xii warde ladde grekes ſyde melancolyke ſurquedous pryde kinge honux ſon one maberte fyelde hym ſelfe aparte ordre hadde wardes thyrtene proudly muſterynge endlonge grene agayne troians redy fyght ¶and eke kinge vlyxes hight ladde fourtene rede ¶and eke humelius kinge lede fiftenth mine auctour writeth thus ¶and duke called curibulus ſixtenth gouernaunce daye knightes king protheſylay aſſygned great ordinaunce enforce theim vengeaunce vpon death worthy kinge hector ſlayne grekes ariuinge ¶and kinge rodus ladde ſeuentene kinge occymene ¶the eyghtenth warde ledinge zantipus lyde kinge kepe committed garde grekes ſyde xix warde ¶and twenty mine auctour lerneth v kinge called amphimacus like kinge guyde theim wyſſe philoctetes kinge laryſſe one twenty ladde eke reade two twenty hadde king diomede ¶and eneus kinge cyparye whylom ſo noble ſo worthy thre twenty gouernayle troians proudly taſſayle xxiiii ſwerde ſpere ſhelde ¶king prothecatus lad felde ¶and carpenor carpedye kinge werre expert right wiſe workynge fiue twenty riche well beſayne grekes ſyde brought playne ¶the ſyxe twenty ſothly laſte could ſe afore caſte euerye thinge good inſpection wiſe kinge great agamenon prudent werriour ordayned emperour grekes hooſt wyſeſt echone ¶and wiſe forth grekes gone felde pompe full royall thenſignes token marcyall haue take grounde paſſingly araied theyr ſtanderdes richly tho diſplayed brode baners many freſhe penowne againe winde ye made hidous ſowne right dredfull playnly heare men ſawe many criſtes cleare many tufte golde ſyluer ſhene meynt fethers red whyte grene deuiſes wonder meruaylous ſuch folkes amerous token borne ſhewe openly loue brent inwardly high empryſe daye fulfylle herde loude noyſes ſhryle ferre felde dreadfull ſownes trumpettes claryownes kalendes bin ſheding blode noiſe almoſte rage wood fomy bridelles mouthes blede furious neyhing many baſtarde ſtede ¶praunſyng horſe vpon eyther ſyde enſygnes might pryde grekes partye troye alſo knightly wiſe haue ado euery warde ſtanding place ¶the firſt aſunder lytell ſpace began approche ful entent hector tho ful vnpacient formeſt ſyde troye yre man might accoye lyke lion hungry rage yſſued furyous vyſage towarde grekes mighty ſtede ſporres made ſides blede knightly herte ſo inly toforne mortall yre rode forne brenning full hote melancolye whych thinge whan grekes gan eſpye ¶patroclus withouten abode ſurquedrye afore wardes rode toforne hooſtes ſyght encountre playnly might worthy hector whan ſawe fer lyne right dyameterre rode vnto hatefull tene ſpere ſharpe grounde kene throughout ſhelde tho enuyous rage ſmote hector without domage except onely head ſtele afore whet forged wele plate mayle mightly gan glace ſkinne nothing might race albe came wt paſſing violence yet hector done hath none offence ſaddell one flytte though ſturdely hitte might backward bēd bow chine partye make encline ¶but fatally confuſyon mighty man troian champion ire aye brenning vpon hate aye fret ſo ſore left ſpere mine auctour wryteth thus ſworde rode patroclus auyſed fully ſhall dead furiouſly gan aymen head roue downe maner let breſt baſſenet ſayth guydo ſo great payne ſtroke parted ī twayne mortall ſwerde whetted ſo kene patroclus myght ſuſtene vpon horſe fell downe grounde caught laſt fatall wounde ¶beyng preſent knyghtes euerychon delyuerly vpon anone worthy hector ſtede adowne deſcended like wood lyowne hatefull yre brenning fyre hauing hert inly great deſyre ſpoyle armure anone full many riche ſtone ruby saphyres ynde dayes playnly finde kinges lordes knightes naye battayle went beſt araye ſothly hector whan firſt gan ſe multitude ſtones perre patroclus ſo oryent ſheyne vpon arme hinge horſe reyne meane hole entente catche praye ſo diligent couetiſe theyr alder ſyghtes ¶tyll king menō wt thre thouſād knighꝭ armed ſtele rounde ſodaynly vpon hector fall dead corp patroclus ſaue purpoſe hector may haue lybertye riche kinge ſpoyle cauſed hym angre boyle king called menon irous wood ſayde amonge echon oh gredy liowne oh wolfe moſt rauinous oh hatefull tygre paſſing enuyous aueryce oh beaſt inſaturable deſyre ſothly vnſtaunchable ¶vpon praye thou ſhalt ye fede go elles ſewen thy mede truſteth well concluſyon fyfty thouſande thy deſtruction one entent playnly fayle thine hatefull pryde attones aſſayle ſodeynly ſperes ſharpe whet euery halfe gan beſette maugre force might manhode enforſyng theim reue ſtede ſothfaſtly great violence conſtrayned ſtrong defēce ſayth guydo fall vpon kne might magnanimite manhode hath horſe recured maugre grekes ſo ferre aſſured ſtrengthe great might recured like worthy knight ſtede agayne amiddes foen right lyne rode kinge menon full deſyrous auenged furye haſty cruelte therupon ſet hole delyte mortall cruell appetite ſothe ſlayne anone saue kinge called glacō came reſcue kinge theſeus ſone hight archilogus haue tolde menon reſkewe thre thouſande knightes gan ſewe full aſſented attones battayle life death hector aſſayle awayte vnware ſet al whyle whō euer met ſworde killed bare downe fynally gayneth raunſowne greke durſte mete went felt full vnſwete ¶he made waye aboute euery fledde death feare rode made patth ful plaine reade patroclus agayne repeyred ſpoyle might amid felde grekes ſyght would praye lightly lete till idume mighty king crete two thouſande cladde plate mayle worthy knightes hector aſſayle while ſo inly deſyrous haue tolde ſpoyle patroclus newe agayne confuſion like finde came king merion hector might theim take hede force reft hys ſtede ſothly none boote compelled fight foote knighthod herte reſumeth wt ſwerde conſumeth withſtande horſe man furyouſly troian knight began armes legges ſhoulders bone hewe amid mortall fone grekes might afore ſuſtene reade ſlewe fiftene theim buſy take ſuch ſlaught gan among thē make ne durſt abyde afore face ¶and merion ſelfe place meane toke vp patroclus heuy cheare face full piteous ſtede layd beforne tente anone hath borne alway grekes cruell mode hector furyous wode felly abode fyghting vpon fote ſome felt full vnſote preſumed vpon preſſe manhode ne woulden ceſſe beſet rounde euery ſide hauing truſt great pride fynally miſchiefe take dempt might eſcape handes ſhortly none aduenture ſtede lyklyhede recure force caſten let attones gan ſet ſpecially amonge theim euerichone finde ſothe one grekiſhe knight right worthy fame ¶and carion playnly name enforced hector oppreſſe whan moſt miſchiefe diſtreſſe beſet grekes enuyroning tyll fortune aye awaytinge longe daye fell fight reſcuſe came troian knighte midde grekes whan beſet hent two dartes ſharpe kene whet furiouſly fyrſt ſhoke toen ye herte ſmote carion darte felde gan glide playte mayle throughout outher ſide fatally deadly wounde caryon glode anone togrounde amonge hundred knightes ferys afore conſpyred fell chearis haue ſlayne hector ſome maner waye eft agayne yonge knight troye full delyuer raughte another ſpere caſt one ſawe yfere auaunce ſelfe hector felde plate playnly ſhelde line right ne ſhould aſterte might roue herte ¶and haſt coude vpon troians gan crye aloude enhaſte theim knightly ſuccoure worthy hector ſtode aduenture amonge grekes hauing refute sole ſelfe helpe deſtitute whych crye grekes vnware ¶fyrſt came worthy cincibare brother hector borne baſte ridinge ſelfe tofore haſte ye knightes tho guyde wonder proudly pricking ſyde sodaynly together one froſhe grekes fall hector rounde beſet aboute manhode great route enbuſhed theim backe thre hondred knightes yt ſpacke aſtoned gan theim withdrawe thurty firſt cruelly ſlawe maugre theim hector manhede amid felde taken hath ſtede entred amonge prees daye knighthode pereles helde blody ſworde hande tho felde agayne ſtande helpe playnly rede brake karfe two threde knotte cruell attropos onely let purpoſe leyſer ſpoylen patroclus therfore ire wood furious full cruelly grekes quytte mede whiche face faſte gan ſpede whoſe ſharpe ſworde bathed theyr bloud dyed red dyd hym good vpon tho auenged daye lyon played vpon grekes manhode haunte pryde ſo mortally gan daunte hym fledde ſo rode makyng hote ſtreintes bloud endlonge renne ſhede vpon ye grene ¶tyll tyme duke great athene called whylom meneſteus thre thouſande knyghtes full famous lorde guyde fyelde hath take vpon lefte ſyde deceyte full ſecrete wyſe ¶where troylus ye folke friſe whiche hath daye ſo lyſte ſeke knighthode kylled many greke lyke tygre gredy praye troylus bare hym longe daye sleynge grekes many worthy knyght whyle buſyeſt fyght ¶agayne foen kyng antipus kynge hyght alchanus vpon grekes ylyche freſhe newe making ſides blody hewe one aſſent theſe thre māhed ſpecially vpon bay ſtede ſo euer troylus rode euery greke ſworde abode sodaynly made ſterue plate gan ſo depe kerue ¶and continued tyll duke meneſte troylus ſawe great cruelte ſlaughter grekes made haſty yre face pale fade ¶hent ſpere threwe reſt troylus ſmytte euen amydde breſt ſternely maugre renowne earth anone bare downe myddes mortall foen cruelly hym beſette anone hym treyne layde hoke laſe rounde maner compaſe ſpere darte ſwordes forged bright hym ſelfe deffendeth lyke knight great manhode honour auaunce albe lyfe hanged balaunce ſtode felte full vnſwete poynt deth amonge horſe fete great awayte duke meneſte howe troylus myght haue take mortall hate caſtynge thought myſchyefe take eſcape nought euery halfe ſo beſette ſworde ſpere kene grounde whette alone ala mortally beſtadde ſeaſed hym forth haue ladde tyll meſers worthy knight troye gan crye ſtode waye sore abaſhed ryght furyous wyſe oh ye noble worthy men fryſe manly knightes aye preued fyelde moſte renowmed ſpere ſhielde conſyder vnto hyghe fame aduert glorye name daye throughe neclygence power myghty vyolence grekes troylus ytake sool fyelde ye haue hym forſake ſhall rebounde alder ſhame ye ſoth greatly blame worthyneſſe floure betake grekes lacke ſuccoure yf ye taken haſty wreche shameful reporte honour ſhall apeche perpetually ſaye therof amys defaute troylus taken whiche named ſo worthy famous worde kyng alcamus melancolye felte herte ryue yre hente ſpere blyue pryckyng enchaſteth might tyll playnly ſyght buſy troylus lede full knyghtly ſyttyng ſtede ran one fell downe dead efte agayne pale nothyng redde rancour longer wolde lette greke fyrſte mette body ſmet ſpere men myght ſe therof poynt fere breſt plate ſhulder bone ground fel downe dead anone tho forthwith worthy fryſes came flokmele downe grekes fal myghtely maugre diffence ſette vpon ſo great vyolence troylus daunger free knightly magnanimyte maden hym recure ſtede ſpecially helpyng nede zantipus ſtronge manly kyng whiche diſdaine commyng meneſte gan ſpere grate ſhielde mayle thicke plate ſore ſmote meneſte dead ne armour whiche ire gan tremble tho ſhake troylus handes take eſcaped pryſoner diſpyte berde maugre power wherfore gan haſty hote enuye knyghtes furyouſly crye ſo mighty renowmed ſtronge payne venge wronge vpon troyans mete face ¶and haſt gan mightely enbrace ſharpe ſperes grounde byte felly foyne together ſmytte ¶for tho began great mortall werre fyre braſt ſhene ſterre baſenettes plate bryght ye fielde flaumeth ye fereful light lyfe death toke tho hede downe plaine length bredth wardes gan proudly auale lokes ryght enuyouſly pale aproche aſſemble yfere hate brennyng man may ſtere gan hurte ſpere ſworde darte mortally vpon euery parte ſlaughter gan greatly rewe ylyche alwaye newe newe hector grekes worthyneſſe rode manly dyd oppreſſe mercyleſſe ſlowe bare downe without excepciowne furyouſly routhe ſee ¶and new duke meneſte repayred full enuyous herte hondes troylus ſo ſterte ſlaughter eke meyne rode buſy ſlee troian people whan myght mete tauenge nothyng wolde lete tyll caſually amonges preſe ¶a knight mette hyght myſeres whyche diſpyte meneſte reſcuſe worthy troylus maugre put hym praye ſo befell ſelfe daye mete agayne aduenture meneſte cote armure marked hym armes bare ſodeynly ware might taken hede furiouſly mightye ſtede ſpere amyd renges bare hym ouer made hym fall mauger might earth adowne ¶and fynde howe kynge hupon deſcended ſtorye lyſte lye two thouſande knyghtes companye whiche grekes felly gan ſette ye berde kynge prothenor mette archelaus noble werryour boece lorde gouernour helpe onely prothenor lyke tygre wood bore gan troyans aſſaylen deth many one ſelfe daye ſleeth kyng hupon chyualrye full fell tyme melancolye full many greke gaue dethes wounde thus gan eche confounde mortall hate amonges tyll fortune knyght pollydamas ¶on troye ſyde ſonne anthenor knightes hym ſelfe tofore grekes right enuious pryde amyd wardes fallen ſyde gan breke knightly diſſeuer againe whoſe ſword might perſeuer ſo inly furyous ¶and helpe came kyng remus wynge parte breakyng many ſpere darte agayne grekes thre thouſand knightes beholde felly fyghtes ſothe vnto troye luſte heauenly aioye ſee grekes brake aſondre noyſe loude thonder fyelde ſtrokes gan aryſe ¶and remus ye haue herde deuiſe vpon grekes ſo enuyous fyelde came menelaus worthy knightes spartenſe agayne remus maken reſyſtence full proudely makyng delaye worthy remus kynge menelaye horſe backe ſharpe ſperes whette amydde fielde byn together mette manly proweſſe renown horſebacke eche bare downe none ſtroke tho might ſhone whyle anthenor ſonne pollydamas luſty freſhe lyght delyuer myght deſyrous honour attayne mette fielde neuewe heleyne mighty duke called mereus flouringe youthe ryght vertuous freſhe armed newe luſty courage ſothe twenty yere age whyche ſo yonge noble knight right renoumed bothe herte might fortune befell ala troian knight dan pollidamas ſpere throughe ſhelde maile plate hytte hym ſo cruell fate amonge grekes fallen downe dead whiche thyng menelaye toke hede ſawe hym lye ſlayne grene herte remembrynge quene quene heleine neuewe dole full delyuer pa remus rode cruelte alſo ferre might ſe full knightly mette berde ſmytte ſharpe ſwerde vpon head hatefull tene ſtede might ſuſtene wounde ſo paſſingly mortall ſtroke perillous fall knightes wende dead ¶and hent vp began fle troye warde great paſe ¶but befell pollidamas maner theim behelde made theim repayre knightly felde except ſome bidding hadde worthy remus home troye ladde pale dead woundes wide tho came grekes ſyde ¶celydys luſty freſhe kinge dare ſayeth wrytinge ſothe boke lyſt tell celydys excell beaute ſemelyheade ſhape porte goodlyheade surmounting dare liſt deſcriue fayrneſſe tho time alyue limmes compact ſo clene rede yonge freſhe quene feminye beaute floure kinge celidys loued paramoure vpon hooly pleſaunce ſo printed remembraunce chiefe reſorte ſothly herte vpon eche houre aduerte fynally departed nought day night houre thoughte fully owne knight ¶but fortune luſty freſhe light smote ſtede ſharply ſyde ſurquedrye proudly gan ryde mortall hate full furyous paſe right lyne pollidamas ſpere made flytte ſadell tho ſytte marked ſo great might eft ayene noble troian knight pollydamas deſpitous face celidys departed fro place ſwerde ſo ſmyt heade ſtede fell downe deade grekes great confuſion tune fierſer lyon hector grekes knightly gan enchaſe oft made theim leſe place euer rode neceſſyte afore ſwerde made theim ſo fle suche vengeaunce hath theim take felde fayne forſake purſewe would neuer fyne till amonge people salomine hector met worthy kinge famous lorde hight theſalus many troian daye yſlawe hector towardes gan drawe kynge tenter eke grece alſo manly knight prudent two raught ſpere haſte vnwares hector ran ſhelde plate mayle ſtele ſpeare head forged ſo wele ſharpe ſquare ſo kene ygrounde hector gaue perillous wounde hector tournen gan ſtede proude center aquite mede full wyſely haſte myght ryght ferre ſeuered ſyght wherof hector melancoleous herte wood furyous akynge wounde grene haſte tauenge conſtraynte tene greke ſhortly mette ſo bolde waye ſette without mercy death anone read encountred one whiche pryde purpoſe wolde diuerte ſworde roue herte herneys melancolye whiche ſtroke whan grekes gan eſpye aſtoned one entencyon peryllouſly ſette hym enuyron ſuche aſſaute gan aboute hym make though manhod might take accorde great multitude cruelly gan include lykelyhode mortall ſtryfe myght eſcapen lyfe hym ſo fell enuyous tyll kynge whiche hyght theſeus grekes ſyde onely gentylneſſe suche routhe caught vpon dyſtreſſe ſe hym ſtande ſo nye vpon wrake thus vnto hym manly pety ſpake oh flour knyghthode rote hardynes welle manhode ſtoke worthynes whylyſt ye haue none aduertence thy lyfe ſaue knyghtly prouydence wylfully moſt drede thy lyfe iupardeſt take lyſte hede mortall peryll howe thou art beſette amonge ſo many cloſed yſhette alone ala deuoyde ſocoure thy ſelfe wylte fauoure fortune lyketh ordayne euery wyght ought complayne beholde ſuche worthy knyght whiche world caſt ſo clere lyght worthineſſe wyll withdrawe rekleſly day thus ſlawe pyteouſly thy perſone leſe withdrawe thy hande yet ſyth yu mayſt cheſe thy hygh proweſſe compelleth preye ſuche myſchefe thou ne deye ¶and whan hector hym gan take hede thanked hym goodly hede maugre ſothly power myght grekes lyke worthy knight eft ſcaped mydde foen went way euerichone blody ſworde alway honde waye pollydamas fonde full lyke man buſy payne defende ſelfe agayne kinges twaine menelay thelamonius vpon full furyous wt ſpere greke thelamowne pollydamas ſmote earthe adowne compellyng none bote agayne theim two fyght eu fote aſſented fully wroke fyrſt haue hewen broke mighty charnelle baſſenet whan vyſer ſmet face naked bare fell hym mortall ſnare haue take ſtorye deuyſe ſent forth full cruell wyſe towarde grekes many worthy knyght whan hector therof ſyght ſawe myſchefe pollydamas caſte fully ſocoure caſe prycked wooder lyon rode aboute hym enuyron ſwerde made large ſpace tyll came ſelfe place amonges grekes furyous wood pollydamas ſelfe tyme ſtode socourles deuoyde remedye tyll hector caſte eye grekes made haſtely withdrawe thirty fyrſt hath ſlawe ſeuered maugre pryde tofore ſworde durſte abyde agaynſt hym make none obſtacle knighthode hyghe myracle pollydamas myſchyefe fyrſte awhaped grekeſhe hande frely eſcaped ¶but freſhly tho kynge epyſtrophus menelay thelamonyus knyghtes togyther hole cloſe agayne troyans getten aloſe new entred battayle great ſtrength paſſynge apparayle mightely troyans compell waye dare dwelle notwithſtandyng great worthyneſſe hector knightly hygh proweſſe fought ſo manly tyme read cowardly haue ſlayne ſtede conſtrayned fyght fote many greke felte full vnſote none aboute hym ſtode ſwerde ne ſhadde bloud though ſo thycke layne voyded made ſpace playne compaſſe rounde behynde eke afore fete ſo well hath hym bore day greke none certayne hardy hande hym layne ſo ſtronge ſturdy wall whan brothern called naturall sawe hym fote amyd foen fruſhe fell euerychon founden hym ſtory maketh mynde deffende ſelfe tygre doth inde helpe high renown fallen fyrſt kyng thelamowne hector ſo cruell founde gaue hym many blouddy wounde tyll one named dyndaron hath ſo ferre amonge renges gone bore hym ſo manhead hath wonne paſſyng myghty ſtede ¶and brought hector ſothly ſtode amonge grekes bathed bloud whiche haſte ful knightly ſtrode thē amonge lyke mar himſelfe rode full many greke makyng ſterue ſworde whetted karue daunted hath enuious pryde tyll deyphobus entred ſyde fyelde knightly chere hym brought many good archer boeme whiche arrowes kene fethers pecock freſhe ſhene vpon grekes haue fyelde recured ſhotte ſo muche aſſured mayle thicke plate ſtele perced haue harneys euery dele ¶and deiphobus full lyke manly man kynge tentran horſe backe tho ran furyouſly gan ſwerde enbrace wounded hym euen amyd face vyſer felle tene horſe backe myght ſuſtene thus grekes troyans yron agayne hath fielde ywonne ſo yrons ſo wood theſeus full knightly withſtode knightes ladde ¶and read hector brother hadde ſtory ſayth hyght quintilene yonge freſhe luſty armed bryght ſhene whiche kinge called modernus proudely falle vpon theſeus theſe twayne togither aſſent falle hym great aduiſement fynally vnhappy chaunce knyghthode broughte hym outtraunce caſt ſhortly ſhalbe dead whoſe purpoſe hector gan take hede vnto gentery myght loude gan crye beſechyng nothyng deye lowely byddyng dyd obeye withdrewe vengeaunce hector fully remembraunce theſeus ſame daye tofore towarde hym ſo goodly hym bore whan hym ſawe miſchyefe dyſtreſſe knightly thought quyte gentilneſſe lyke longeth euery gentylman ¶and theſeus full lowly tho began thanke hector eſcaped ¶but kyng thoas tho hath faſte yraped fyelde knightes many ſpecyally calydony ¶came phyloctetes myghty kinge alſo agayne troyans haue ado fyrſt thoas ſpere ran ¶furyouſly caſſybellan one ſonnes kynge pryamus gaue hym tho wounde ſo greuous without recure fell downe dead whiche ſtroke hector gan take hede herte gan death complayne haſte dyd buſy payne brother auenge myght many one made lyght knighthod horſe backe ſothfaſtly went wrake grekes ſyde came waye worthely bare hym daye ¶tyll duke neſtor entred fyght fyue thouſande ſtele armed bryght agayne troyans grekes ſocoure hym mette auenture ¶the kynge eſdras ſo mighty ſo bolde kyng phylon chare golde worthy noble chyualrye agreſta came iaconye kynges ſonne ſame lande full renowmed worthy hande ſemble together ran ſame tyme many worthy man hath loſte lyfe vpon eyther ſyde ſlaught large woundes wyde ſoyle bodyes laye dead lyke ryuer ran ſtreames red cheres gryſely pale fade bloud men might go wade ancle ſlaughter ſo huge ¶and kyng phylon ſocour refuge vnto troyans ſo bare hym ſtryfe many greke made leſe lyfe ſame day ſo well ſworde whette vnwarely ſo ſore beſette multytude grekes rounde aboute lyfe playnly ſtode doubte lykely myght eſcape grekes ſhulde anone take ne helpe worthy iaconye eſdras loude gan crye ala quod routhe pyte ¶worthy phylon kyng ſhall taken amonge grekes necligence haſte ye diligence reſcue noble worthy kynge attones without taryinge maugre tho maden reſyſtence grekes ſwerde myghty vyolence haue reſcued noble kyng phylon large gone eſcape wonder gladde lyght ¶and hector many luſty knight retourned deiphobus alſo pollydamas many mo troyan knightes deſyre newe cauſen grekes ſore rewe aſſent fully purpoſe ſuche miſchiefe grekes encloſe might fewe ſhulde eſcape therupon knightly ſhape began freſhely aſſayle fielde grekes gan faile power leſe lande fynally mighty hande force troyan knightes grekes maugre mightes brought day confuſyowne ¶but menelay kyng thelamowne ſawe febly apeyre knyghthode made repeyre ſo lyke men haue thē ſelfe deffended tyll eneas troye deſcended ewfremus duke manly man knightes newe began efte agayne grekes oppreſſe hector aye worthyneſſe lyke lyon ſterne face euer one ſo gan enchace compelled great neceſſytye echone afore ſworde fle conſtrayned ryght nede whiche thynge ayax gan take hede herte great compaſſyon ſe ſlaughter confuſyon grekes ſyde guydo maketh mynde gan loke backe behynde ſawe many warde ſtode abrode many baner penowne abode amyd fielde hole broke redy attones wroke nede troye towne whiche wardes without excepciowne hole floure grekes chyualrye ¶to anone ayax gan hye herte ſore agreued crye hath thē ſo commened haſte theim comen reſkuſe amonges reffuſe faſt gan aſſemble noyſe horſe earthe gan tremble furyouſly together flynge might men ſtrokes heren ringe ſperes ſharpe harneys borne ſheldes wrought ſtele horn breſt ſturdy ſquare brode ¶and fynde ayax rode ¶to eneas alſo great enuye atwyxe theim two death might ire apeaſe herte nother might haue eaſe tyll ſperes ſharpe ground whette horſe backe togyther mette copyng ſo ſore haue hytte eueryche earth ſmytte beholde knightly ſyght bothe foote fyght lyklyhead tho theyr wood rage fall full great domage amonge horſe bycauſe ſtode vpon ſoyle ouer ſpredde blode ¶but phyloctetes ayax come hath vp amonge horſe ynome knightly fought made memorye ſothly elles troians victorye fyelde playnly ſayne tyll philoctetes wardes twayne euen face manly theim withſtode ſpere fyrſt hector rode vpon ſhafte fynde brake ſothly vpon horſe bake kept ſo well fell ſtroke remeuinge ſturdy oke sat ſadell vpryght chine wyth ſpere ryght lyne body depe ſhyelde philoctetes ſmote fielde lyfe hys knightes doubt ¶but tho came ſo great route ¶kynge humerus vlixes eke brought many worthy greke ten thouſād knightes manly men echone gan troians aſſayle anone cruelly euery halfe certayne multytude haue theim ſo belayne diſpayred diſconſolate longe fyght waped mate gan withdrawe faynted battayle eke theyr horſe ſothly gan fayle theyr ſyde went vp ſo downe ¶but parys tho troy towne entred ful manly wyſe fyrſt mette kynge fryſe vlyxes nye allye parys ſmote ſo great enuye hym ſlewe wherof grekes sore abaſhed wyth ſpere ¶vlyxes rode auenge might fyrſt parys ſyght breſt gan ſpere throwe fynally bare lowe fayling parys ſothely reade vnder ſlewe mighty ſtede maugre grounde gone would haue fall anone ¶but troilus tho mette berde furyouſly ſharpe ſwerde ſmote vlyxes throughout viſer lyke condyte ſmall ryuer downe face bloud ſtreames ran vlyxes tho lyke manly man ſtroke aſtoned ſtede ſtiffe wall ſwerde ſo mightely gan race vmber troylus face gaue large mortall wounde ſtroke paſſingly ioycounde grekes ſuppoſing theyr thought troians fynally brought vnto outtraunce ſothly ſo hadde saue hector wt knightes lad parys deiphobus al brethern ī knighthod moſt famous troylus alſo laſte wounde alway ſo noble knight yfounde one ioyned one vpon grekes ſodaynly gone ¶and worthy hector alder fyrſt began grekes enchaſe afore ran like beaſtes fledde fro death euer one thus killeth ſleyeth mette durſt ſtroke abyde foen freſhe woundes wyde ſlaught made alway renewe thylke daye blody roſen hewe hath theyr plate harneys ſteined thought bloud heauē rained ſoyle redder might tho ben aye ylyche ſwarme grekes flockmele fledde way guydo ſayth ylke daye hector formeſt playne frounter grekes layne behynde knyghtes garde lacke hym warde wherfore ſought full longe grekes ſawe new wexen ſtronge knyghtes agayne repeyred whych theim ſelfe greatly diſpayred abſence tho ſe full inwardly recomforted glad hert haue theyr lorde receiued theyr gladneſſe hath perceyued ¶spake vnto theim full affectiouſly lykewyſe prayed theim full beningly remembre knyghtly herte conſyder wyſely aduerte firſt wronges grekes haue yore ago ouermore alſo grekes daye victorye farewell aye honour glorye troyan bloud concluſyowne fynally eke towne shall mortally tournen ruyne honour wont ſhyne throughout world worthineſſe eclipſe ſhall tournen derckneſſe ye daye lyke men quyte wherfore praye man ne atwyte hygh renowne cowardiſe ſette vpon full manly wiſe ſpare dread death praye ¶and echone full lowly gan obeye deſyre withouten longer tale entryng certayne vale vpon grekes theſe worthy knyghtes folowing hector ſodaynly fall full mortally ware hector tho greke would ſpare euery theyr confuſyon killed ſlewe aboute enuyron knyghtes riding ſide made theyr foen maugre pryde leſe lande flewe ſighte ¶tyll kinge ye thoas hight grekes ſyde inwarde gan dreſſe newe fulll knyghtly gan oppreſſe troye knight manly mā ¶that afore ſlayn caſſybellan one ſonnes king pryamus rode fortune fell thus brother fruſhe mette aſſent enuyron beſette ſadell many greke beheld amonge horſe ſmyt felde rente firſt baſenet cruelly head ſmet vnarmed myſchief ſtode ¶saue duke furyous wood athene riding tho great paſe reſkued mortall caſe knightes rode helpe without abode ſpere ſharpe whet kene ¶fyrſt fell quintiline buſy thoas haue ſlawe bretherene made alſo withdrawe whan quintiline horſe throwe ¶but parys thē drewe vp mighty bow duke let arowe glyde plate hit ſide vpon rybbe made ſore blede whych ſtroke ne toke hede bycauſe onely ſo feruent amid foen helpe thus kinge thoas amonge horſe bore grounde poynt death many mortall woūd onely naked head duke fully deuoyde dread knighthod perillous caſe amid foen hath holpe king thoas lyfe made ſcapen fre hector aye cruell enmitee iliche freſhe nothing would leue vpon grekes manhode preue enforſing deſtructiowne ¶and rode amonge theim vp ¶kinge humerus hath bowe take ſhote gan redy make hatefully therin ſet arowe hector marked hath ſo narowe ſmote euen amid face might ferther pace hector ſmyt ſo great payne wt ſwerd roue head atwayn ¶the death whō grekes know mine auctour ſaith haue horn yblow vnwarely dreadfull ſowne seuē thouſād knightꝭ came one adowne hector without abode force theim rode maugre theyr might tho withſette ſlowe tho way lette would ſtynt playnly tyll came father worthy kinge pryam many worthy full famous renowne wyth knyghtes faſt towne laye daye men horſe foote knighthod crop roote kept cloſe full high prudence tyll hector came vnto preſence beſought great nede thre thouſand would ſpede vpon grekes theyr full rage fall theim moſt auauntage thē haſte worthy priamus knightes freſhe deſyrous towarde grekes hath waye ytake ſuch mordre gan vpon theim make many grekes laye dead playne pryamus hath theim ſo ſore belayne euery halfe great might full faſt fledde ſyght ſore newe vpon theim ſette ¶and fynde tohether mette ¶hector ayax cruell auenture ſtedes ſtronge wonder ſure ſtorye ſayth haſte konne lyke wood lyon together ronne ſo great might yt lefe lothe vpon playne vnhorſed bothe ¶and whyle menelay kinge sodaynly camen ridinge ſlewe troye worthy admyrall thus ſlaughter paſſingly mortall renewed aye celidonas neuewe ſlewe kinge thoas madā met mine auctour writeth thus grekyſhe kinge called cedeus wt ſwerde ſuch ſtroke ſette ye vmber eye ſmette ¶and sardellus troye eke ſame whyle ſlewe worthy greke lorde name high proweſſe although guido name doth expreſſe ¶and alſo came margaryton troye ſide agayne thelamon two inly ſet fyre high diſdayne hatefull yre met horſe backe yfere kinge thelamon ſothly lere gaue vnto deadly wounde cruell ¶but tho came troian phanuell prothenor ſmote downe ſtede thus ſones playnly reade pryamus nothing nat diſmayde grekes haue euery parte outrayed ſo knightly daye theim borne many greke fatally hath lorne life ſothe hate enmyte kinge anglas fall meneſte athene duke gouernoure ſpere yre olde rancoure ran ſmet tho amyd ſhyelde al ſadell yet helde ¶and duke ſpere none ſwerde anglas rode anone yt owmber roue nigh naſe aſtoned ſtode maſe ſawe condyte blode ſtreame rode aſyde fully deuoyde feare vnto time ſtaunched ¶but deamor owne brother deare behelde mortall blody cheare ¶of high diſdayne rode meneſte vnhorſeth vp anone ſterte might fully vp aryſe another brother full creuell wyſe fall ſo thre attones weten vpon meneſte fully purpoſe ſhall leſe lyfe ſo knightly bare ſtryfe
