agaynſt theim wonder ſe vpon moſt cruell theim thre one thoas eldeſt echone ſleye buſy euer one broke haue baſenet ¶but tenter ſawe ſo beſet grekiſhe kinge made mencion herte great compaſſyon thought playnly manhode releue might fomen greue nought buſy payne hector tho fallen twayne ¶vpon tenter meneſte ¶and theim ſlayne ne ayax vnto hector faſte gan hye thouſande knightes companye withſtande meneſte ſaue handes might haue ¶but parys tho king perce fiue thouſande reherſe worthy knightes many troian mo vnto hector one ygo thryfty wiſe cydyng rowe parys made trumpet blowe whych came knightly enbattayled many troian full well apparayled whych fielde hector conueyed one herte fully haue obeyed vnto bydding troian knight freſhe newe begyn fyght vpon grekes ferre forth ſlayne many manly man aye ſlaughter pyteouſly reneweth many greke ſore herte reweth theyr great loſſe deſtructiowne wrought vpon thē theim troye towne ſpecially hector finde whych day dare maketh minde hande thouſande knightes ſlowe neuer adawed ſowe greke none dare waye dwell wt ſwerde coud theim ſo compell leſe theyr grounde neceſſyte lyke ſhepe afore wolfe fle ¶and reade amiddes victorye hector hath met vnder tentoree ¶amonges grekes mereon kinge ſpake without tarying oh thou tratoure thy houre aprocheth faſte thou art come ſothly thy laſte thy fatall daye hath courſe yronne truſte well weſtrynge ſonne caſte platly quyten thy mede ſwerd haſte thy bloud ſhed thou ſo bolde daye diſturben ryche praye ſpoylyng kinge patroclus cauſe thou preſumptious diſturbe thou ſhalt anone deade downe ſterte ſmote firſt head ¶and ſpoyle alſo gan haſte ¶but meneſte came faſte whan behelde trauerſe backe wt ſpere lacke smote ſo great violence without ſyght aduertence worthy hector takyng hede wound ſore gan blede went made faſte bynde ¶and meneſte ſtale away behinde purpoſe ſothly maye mete hector ylke daye ¶but ybounde ſore wound ſtaunche blede furyous erſt tofore repeyred angre al tore aye yre herte fret bare downe euer met slayth kylleth ſo mercyles tho put theim ſelfe preaſe hardy wyth hym mete boke lyke wryte darete ſothe ſtorye ſayth ſo men may gyuen fayth full credence poſſybylyte guydo clearly ye may ſe caught latter wounde fynally grekes confounde affermed certayne thouſand knightꝭ wt hande ſlayn without theim tho ſpake rathe newe alway gan ſwerde bathe grekes bloud ſodaynly ouerlayne cruelte greke none high low eſtate ne awhaped amate knighthod manly excellence none maken reſyſtence vtterly durſte take hande daye hector wythſtande ¶and made alſo mencion thylke daye kyng agamenon ſayth guydo came felde cauſes great preſence withhelde grekes ſyde al goeth vp ſo downe hector ſo playeth wood liowne theyr tentes fledde ſocours troye proudly victours sewed theim trace theyr bloud wan treaſour great good ſpoyled theim full great dyſtreſſe armure theyr richeſſe fell theim ware home troye good bare fynally daye wyth myſchaunce grekes brought vnto outraunce without recure ſothe euermore euery parte belayde ſo ſore manhode hector ye mighte helpe many worthy knyght ſo felly agayne grekes wrought ſuch miſchief playnly thē brought ne theyr owne pyteous ſlouthe pryde onely folye routhe theim theyr volunte daye euer ſoneraynte recured theyr hygh renowne lordſhyppe theim dominacyowne whych ſhoulde haue laſte continuall victoryouſly perpetuall haue endured ſaue cruell fate redy aye fortune debate agayne thynges gynne wilfulneſſe make theim fine aye wretchedneſſe theyr enuyous diſpoſytion ſodayne chaunce reuolucion vnware tourning falſe whele wyll byde thinge wele ala freyle deuoyde ſykerneſſe cauſe dimmed ſo derckneſſe hath troians falſe opynyon yblinded ſo theyr diſcreſcion ſpecially fordercked ſo ſyght worthy hector prudēt manly knyght ſe afore ſhulde ſewe good aduyſe miſchyefe eſchewe folowed theim backe behinde ala wilfully made blynde ſame daye ſytten ſofte victorye hill alofte ne could neclygence ſe fall theyr felycite put abacke theyr aduertence lacke reaſon high prudence hap haue voided theyr grace preſently ſet afore theyr face man commendable fortune fauorable blandeſhing forhead cleare ſmyle pleſaunt cheare onely fauoure helpe oute myſchyefe beſet aboute refuſe hap wylfulneſſe fortune auoyding vnkindneſſe whan ſhe miniſtreth grace another tyme ſhall embrace whan hath nede helpe ſuccour catche fall rather ingratitude frowardly mowes delude whan beſt weneth ſtande ſikerneſſe fortune aye ſo full brotilneſſe remouable ready flytte ¶her welfull houre yt lyſt admytte fauour allyed another time ſhall denied leueſt finde fauorable ſome houre ſothly fable vnto ſome man ſhe graunteth deſyres thouſande yeares peraunter one condeſcende vnto luſt ſende ¶as hath fall daye vnhappely worthy hector ſo wilfully wrought head grekes ſpare fatally ſnare theim lyke conquerour victorye tryumphe honour might haue brought thrugh hye renown palme conqueſt troye towne daye refuſed folylye ¶for rode hector cruelly amonges grekes ſlowe bare downe caſually mette thelamowne meane ayax nygh allye hate cruel hote enuye hector rode lyke wood albe full nygh bloud yet yonge luſty knight dyd power full myght without fayning haue borne hym downe whoſe father hyght alſo thelamowne hym begat ſtorye telleth v eryon ſyſter pryamus ayax flourynge yonge age freſhe delyuer great courage sette hector knyghtly hygh proweſſe met theyr woodneſſe theyr ſtedes theſe manly champyons eueryche lyke tygres lion began fall proudly aſſayle furyouſly ſeuere plate mayle firſt ſperes longe large rounde afterwarde ſwerdes kene ygroūde fyghtyng thus longe contune tyll befell caſe fortune token ſygne ſome apparence nature kyndly influence whych hertes doth full depe myne namely theym borne one lyne whych cauſe peraunter theſe twane naturally theyr rancour reſtrayne theyr yre modefye onely ſo nygh allye vnwyſt therof vnſure tyll taught onely nature naturally bloud wyll aye kynde drawe vnto bloud may fynde whych made hector kyndely aduerte meued ſtered herte knyghthod gentilneſſe whan ayax ſawe worthyneſſe ¶spake vnto full beningnely ſayd coſyn ſaye trewly thou lyſt grekes forſake come troye dare vndertake thyne allyes thy kynrede thou ſhalt withouten dreade full well receyued partye theim blode royall sothly decended hygheſt degre ryght ſhall ſuffyſe vnto kyndely great pleſaunce repayre vnto thyne allyaunce gentyll herte ſythe nothyng ſo good confedered owne bloud conceyue thy worthyneſſe whych nature doth kyndly impreſſe troian bloud thou art deſcended whych grekes longe hath offended wherfore reade leue theim vtterly aunſwered agayne full humbly ſythen byrthe greke youthe among foſtred eke tyme natiuitye taken ordre degre knighthod eke amonges theim aforne ouer bounde ſworne trewe theyr nacion making bloud none excepcion ſwore would conſerue beheſte hector made requeſte manfull gentilneſſe would knyghthod worthineſſe shewe vnto hym ſo great affectiowne make theim troye towne onely withdrawe grekes purſewe theyr tentes make theim remewe reſorte agayne vnto towne knighthode routhe compaſſyowne without aſſaylynge anye affraye made grekes ilke day sythe vnto theim ought ynoughe ſuffyſe fielde ſo knightly wyſe manhead fully poſſeſſours theyr fomen fynally victours like tofore fully defyned whoſe requeſt hector enclyned ala haſty wilfulneſſe made anone without auyſeneſſe amydde fielde trumpet blowe wherby troians fully mighten knowe wil ſhulde thē withdrawe cuſtome playnely lawe vſaunce nyghe ferre amonges experte werre whan moſte feruent fyght vpon grekes preue might chaced lowe ſtronde weake power withſtāde troye one deſyre gan ſette ſhotte wylde fyre brenne ſhyppes high miſchaūce fynally put outtraunce ¶and ſo trouth ne hector vpon routh makyng troyans repayre ayene towne vngraciouſly confuſyowne ſtory ſhall ſpecifye tho put ala iupardye lyfe death whiche elles might haue ſure whiche againe ſhall neuer recure ¶how grekes ſuite opteyned kyng pryam trewce eyght wekes battayles trewce ended capitulo xxiii haue matter complaynen ſore fro daye farewell euermore laude victory fro towne denyed diſpoſyowne mortall fate whiche contrarye matter lyſte lenger tarye troye entred citie ſhet gate ſuretie daye lyke made mynde thus ende guydo fynde wende haue done peraunter beſt ¶and ſonne ygo reſt toke eaſe ylke night tyll morowe tytan clere bryght shadde beames hemiſpherye makyng daye ſhewe merye whiche tyme troyans anone right hole luſty fyght gan arme theim purpoſe full daye foen mete platly maye hole wyll playne entent eke commaundement tofore hector redy make ſlepe morowe whan wake whiche thynge neclygent pryam grekes haue yſent meſſangers ſame day pryme take trewce onely tyme eyght wekes whiche pryamus hector wyll ſtory telleth thus hath graunted auctoritye wyſe citie whiche tyme whyle leyſer haue grekes gan burye graue bodyes afore ſlawe lyke rytes paynem lawe might buſy cure ſome brent ſome ſepulture encloſed lyke eſtate thus helde feaſt funerall fro day day duryng aye peace ¶in whiche ſpace fynde achelles patroclus death hath ſore playned teares rayned inwardly loued hym herte anguyſhe cruell ſmerte longe abode lamentacion dyd make great affection large toumbe remembraunce myd fielde tho vſaunce amonge grekes great reuerence lyke honour excellence ¶of royall burying ſo patroclus ygraue protheſelaus toumbes korue marbyll graye nye together playne laye werke rychly ywrought earth together brought solempnely lyke obſeruaunces rytes circumſtaunces grekes vſed ſothly tho dayes fro poynt poynt longeth layes ſuche eſtate royall holden feaſt funerall theſe two whyles trewſe doth laſte ¶and troye buſyed full faſte might bufy eure grene hurtes woundes cure aduyſe ſurgerye full well experte ſhapen remedye ſwolle ſores ſoften payne ſpace theſe monthes twayne reſtored helth euery thynge whiche time priamus kinge ¶suche ſorowe made caſſybellan herte wyght ne hym recomforte heuineſſe day day inwarde tenderneſſe full pyteouſly gan ſobbe wepe ¶and body made kepe aboue earth certayne ſpace tyll choſen ſome worthy place burying ſepulture guydo v fully doth aſſure ¶in venus temple ryche ſhryne made men toumbe myne marbell greye metall rychely whiche put full ſolempnely dead corp caſſybellan beinge preſent full many manly man phane cytherea whiche thynge caſſandra within ſelfe conſydered behelde ſawe vp offred helme eke ſhelde ſworde alſo vnto mar ſtede inwarde wo ſhe felte herte blede heryng noyſe pyteous crye tender wepynge ſorowyng vtterly troye lamentaciowne frendꝭ throughout al ye towne gan make ſlawe afore ſodeyne rage herte tore inwardely ſhe might reſtrayne furyouſly crye complayne ſayde ala full ofte welawaye ¶oh wofull wretch ye daye vnhappy eke graceles alſo infortunate inly wo bego ye may ſuffre great harmes kene whiche ye lykely hereafter ſuſtene duryng ſyege towne belocke seynge foen redy wroke aboute beſet euery ſyde venged great pryde wote ryght well ye may eſchewe ne ſhall vnto death purſewe euerychone beſyeged place without mercy rewth grace ala ala wyll ye beſy ye wofull wretch ſhet cite grekes ſeken peace ſworde vengeaunce mercyles hygh lowe execuciowne noble worthy royall towne euerſed ybrought nought lyſt ye conſyder thought modres child ſmale ſtretes ſhall face dead pale lye murdred grekes cruelte yonge maydens captiuite wepe ſhall myſerye wo ſeruitute towne alſo famous ryche ala pyte grekes fyre ſhall deſtroyed ſhorte tyme ſothly heleyne v ala bought dere syth ſake ſhall euerychone poore ryche exceptyng neuer one ende make wofull pyteous yre ſhalbe ſo furious vpon v none meane saue onely death v go betwene ¶this noiſe pyteons crye caſſandra ſo dredefully gan make aboute euery ſtrete ye towne euer ſhe might mete lyke ſhe mynde tyll pryamus faſte made bynde ſhytte vp routhe harde albe ſhe ſayd trouth ¶for neyther wyſedome diſcrecion counſayle wyt prudence reaſon trouth rede withouten lye ſpirite trewe prophecye auayleth ſuche ſapyence place audyence man inly neuer ſo wyſe counſaylyng hyghe deuyſe workyng outher eloquence eche thynge ſe aduertence falle afore reaſon amyd eye diſcrecion yet dole without fauour holden fole vnfauoured wiſedome vayleth nought neyther trouth dere bought caſſandra wyſe rede diſpyſed taken hede troye confuſyon cruelly ythrowen pryſon whyle wyll lette dwelle grekes forth wyll telle fyrſt pallamydes gan grutche agaynſt yt cheſe beyng abſent kyng agamenon haue lordſhyp domynacyon namely ſyth worthy ſuche dignite gouerne ſo great myghty hoſte throughout world come euery coſt kynges prynces ſo worthy renowne therof indignaciowne ¶and ſayd himſelfe pouſtee amonge grekes greater degree concludyng maner weye power ne wolde obeye peace werre ſubiection syth ne election platly affyrmyng thre whan choſe kynges degre thurty tyme abſent whiche ſwore entent accordyng opynyon ¶in wyſe agamenon grekes ſhulde haue ſuche gouernaunce ¶lo myſchyefe lyeth varyaunce amonge lordes whan accorde drawe fully one corde enuye cauſe ſuche dyuyſyon couetyſe domynacyon eueryche wolde ſurmounten felowe curſed vyſe often hath withdrawe hap grace many regyon whan diſcorde falſe diſcencion allyed ben hertes ſtryue among lordes kingdom may thriue tyll reformed agayne peace amonge ſelfe playnely leaſe whyche thinge grekes token hede thought good ferther procede matter pallamydes ymeued amonges preſe wyt ſet quyete made rancour lete accorde fully herte nowe muſt ſtyle agayne dyuerte vnto werre telle maner trewes mette yfeare lyke ſtorye maketh mencion worthy kyng great agamenon trewes paſſed ygone haſte gan ordeyne anone myght waker dylygence deuoyde ſlouthe neclygence ſette wardes full auyſely ¶and achylle full prudently fyrſte warde cōmytteth lede ſeconde vnto diomede thyrde alſo kyng menelay fourth ſame daye ¶he meneſte duke athene lodyng ſtele armed clene wardes folowyng agamenon kyng full manfully ordeyned hath ſhall procede worke dede full circumſpect werre peace ¶and worthy hector reckles ſette wardes towne knightly wyſe diſcreciowne troylus ſo yonge freſhe lyght fyrſt warde many luſty knyght hath aſſygned wardes ſet prudently ne myght bet forth haſt hym lyſte longer byde many worthy rydyng ſyde gate went towne towarde grekes troyan champiowne fyrſt whan ſawe fyerſe achylle ne coulde lenger kepe hym ſtyll ſmote horſe felly ſyde towarde hym cruelly gan ryde whiche thynge diſpyteous eye whan achylles ſothly gan eſpye agayne hector manfull hardyneſſe herte enuyous gan ſtede dreſſe fyelde together mette rounde ſperes poyntes kene whette encountryng knightly excellence eueryche great vyolence force bare vnto grounde full ofte happeth founde whan ſtronge doth mete peregall eueryche fall hector fyrſt ſtrength moſt aſſured ſtede agayne hath anone recured lefte achylle tho gentilneſſe great haſt forth gan hym dreſſe amonge grekes ſo rode kylled ſlewe hym ſtode wt ſworde made woūdes wide breſt ſome ſide perced hath waged euer ſheltroūs brake made diſſeuer herte thought good hath ſworde grekes bloud continued tyll achylles caught ſtede agayne amonge preſe entred amonges troye ſwerde made large weye sleeth bare downe yt euer met none hardy hym lette tyll befell melancolye ¶hector mette rydyng ſodainly ſawe eche come ferre without abode eueryche caught ſpere ran together reſte ¶but hector fyrſt ſmette breſt ſpere playnely tale ſhyuered peces ſmale achilles neceſſyte grounde goth wolde none vnhorſed earth laye hector haſte may enforced hym catche ſtede many greke great nede came reſcues achylles loue put ſelfe preſe thrugh help whō horſe doth attaine enhaſtyng al might payne auenged great iniurye ſodeynly wood furye ſworde ful ſharpe ground whette ¶he ſmote hector vpon baſenet ſadell made hym remewe whiche ſtroke might eſchewe noble worthy knight force great myght maugre foen ſadell hath recured manhode moſt aſſured ſodeynly herte wexed ſo wroth arage achylles goth ſworde ſo ſmyt head baſenet bloud red face gan ronnen downe lyke ryuer chekes enuyrowne hym ſelfe deffendeth knyght tho newe began cruell fyght atwene two ſe wonder euery ſtroke great dent thonder range eyre none wolde ſpare ſoth fyght fare lyke wood tygres bore rage ſterne bulles whan ſauage ſemyd ſothfaſtneſſe theſe two ſo full worthyneſſe contune longe fyghtynge endure tone cruell aduenture muſt haue dead neceſſyte whiche thyng great petye bycauſe worthy knyghtes bothe whyle fyghtyng fell wroth moſt buſy grekes tho begyn wardes entre troye ſtorye maketh mynde partye lefte behynde fyelde enhaſte euerychone knightly wyſe mete fone preaſe alſo yonder knyghtes two ſeuered ſonder ¶and tho came ſterne dyomede knyghtes whiche dyd lede full luſtly ſelue place hath mette proudly face worthy troylus horſebacke neuer yet manhode lacke countre ſtorye doth v lere eueryche vnhorſed knightly hath feare ¶but fyrſt horſe recureth dyomede haſte gan ſpede taſſayle troylus ſtondyng vpon foote ſawe none bote knightly yet dyd erſt man agaynſt hym deffende tho began dyomede hote fyre wonder enuyous hatefull deſyre ſworde rancour none ryche cercle full inde ſtones tyme troylus baſenet full cruelly hath raced ſmet troilus nolde wtdrawe hym deffendynge hath ſtede ſlawe whiche ſat tyme dyomede mauger muſt alyght nede whan fote twayne dyd myght cruell payne eueryche aſſayle ſwordes ſharpe ſo plate mayle gan ſeuere ſonder race wood lyon mortall chere face tyll grekes ſtronge ſtoute felle myne auctour boke telle haue might cauſed dyomede ſodeynly recure ſtede troyan knightes tother ſyde haue troylus brought ſtede ryde ¶and horſed two without efte togyther go ſtronge foynes yfeare ran eche felly tyll laſte cruell dyomede lyke ye may myne auctour rede caſe hap aduenture whiche man fully may aſſure fortune falſe vyſage tyme troylous avauntage hym fallen myſchyefe whiche thynge hym reprefe though toke amonge ſo great aroute euery halfe grekes ſet aboute syth doubtous euer fyne fyght vp derk bright wyght may aye vyctoryous peace werre ylyche eurous let euery man ſyth hap ſette doute take tourne commeth aboute though troylus take diomede tyme ſhall quite mede ſtorye telleth place dyomede lyttell ſpace troylus ladde forth pryſoner reſkewes ſtele armed clere many troyan came pryckynge nede maugre myght dyomede troylus haue handes take tho began ſlaughter ſake euery halfe wonder telle troyans grekes felle ¶than fyelde entred menelay whiche troyans ylke daye full buſy auenged ſo cruell enmyte ¶and whan parys ſawe hym fyelde towardes hym ryght waye helde purpoſe wardes ſette eche tyll together mette tho ſkyrmyſhe ſlaughter gan outher parte many manly man ¶and whyle hector ne wolde ceaſe amonge grekes cruelly preaſe new new hym read alyke freſhe bloud ſhede ſworde trace yſene grekes ne myghten ſuſtene reſyſte ſtande afore face rode aye gaue place ¶tyll knyght whiche boetes hyghte yonge age whan ſyght hector ſlewe grekes mortally euery ſyde hauynge mercy preaſed encreaſe name perpetually purchaſe fame furiouſly herte aferde caſte platly mete berde whiche thynge hector gan aduert hyghe rancour enbraced hath herte ſworde indignaciowne rofe hym euen nauell downe fro crowne ſo great payne fyelde parted laye twayne hector tho aſſygned hath ſtede ſquyer bad ſhulde lede troye towne without abode furyouſly rode amonge grekes euer mercileſe ſlewe tho put ſelfe preſe ſhedde bloud herte deſpiteous whiche thynge kyng archylogus rydyng beſyde ſawe gan eſpye boetes coſyn allye cruelly hector ſlawe towardes haſt gan drawe vpon death auenged rode great cruelte fully purpoſe hector quyte ſodeynly gan hym ſmyte hector vnwarely hyt head myghtly fell downe dead parted two cruell aduenture notwithſtanding mighty ſtronge armure agayne ſtroke deffence geuen ſuche violence holpe hym maner thynge ¶and anone prothenor kynge hatefull yre fole hardyneſſe ſurquedye haſtineſſe melancolye indignacion caught herte preſumpcion aſſayle hector warde folyſhe pryde goth attrauerſe ſyde furyouſly diſpiteous herte commonge might aduerte onely came backe behynde vnwarely guydo fynde hector ſmote horſe grounde ſo muche manhod foūde anone knightly herte without abode ſadell ſterte ryght fyerſely prothenor purſeweth fynally hande eſcheweth ſworde marked hym ſo wele baſenet breſte ſtele twayne without fayle roue downe paunce mayle fell downe full pyteous wiſe whych ſtroke grekes ſore agryſe ¶and ſpecially hardy fierſe achille behelde lyked full yll ¶for prothenor nygh coſyne deſcended ſame lyne death hath ſuch heuyneſſe inwarde thought ſo great diſtreſſe worlde ne wyſt ſo much payne wo death archilogus auenge full deſyrous herte many waye caſte wardes gan ſeke faſte many greke hector haue fall conſpyred fully ſothe amonge theim one entente hector aſſayle nought would auayle daye ſo cruell rage might haue none auauntage troian knightes fauour fortune vpon grekes ſo mightely contune thrugh conueyeng hector might anone haue put theim flyght theyr tentes maugre ſtryue purſuite forwoūded driue laye ſwowe many greke merciles ſlowe longe daye till drewe nyght ſothly lacke lyght theſe troians knightꝭ ful worthy renowne aboute hector repayren towne entre honour glorye daye grekes hauing victorye thus leue theim towne within forth grekes tel begyn vvhan heſperus faire bright ſterre agaynſt eue hath caſte ſtreames fer weſt ratheſt gan appeare whan twylight pale cheare maner morneth thabſence ſonne night aprocheth coopes dunne ſame time titan toke leue clerkes call crepuſculum eue whych elles meane lyght phebus abſence dercke night twylight hatte meane daye night departing theim betwene fully nother ymeynt heauen cluſtered depeynt bryght ſterres eueninge whyche tyme agamenon kinge lordes ſodaynly hath ſente come echone anone tente aſſembled yfeare tryſt heuy ruthfull cheare gan ye ſlaught hector complayne affirming playnly ne maye attayne vnto victorye alyue wherfore gan conſpyre blyue death many ſondry weye echone concludynge whyle troy lykely grekes wynne alone within chiefe deffence protectiowne ſoueraynly vpholder towne mighty caſtell ſtronge wall vnto grekes deadly foe mortall ne myght great force endure neuer aryght agayne foe ſure ſtandyng hole ſayde degre whyle floureth felycitye wherfore echone one entencion condiſcende concluſyon ſome ſlyght awayte lyinge whan moſte buſy fyghtynge amonge myſchyfe diſtreſſe achylles buſyneſſe might vnwarely hym aſſayle hym ſlea nothynge fayle ¶and grekes gan prayer make achilles vndertake empreſſe fynally ſuite manhode execute haſty deth mortall foe achylles without wordes mo requeſt aſſenteth perfourme luſte gan hooly hym confourme tyme lett hym beware reade haſty iourney ſpede vpon hector power kythe leſt fortune awronge face wrythe loke wyth frowarde cheare brynge vnto handes nere ſorte hap hector folylye put lyfe death ieopartye leſt vnto happe euen lyche fall ſelfe ſame dyche hector compaſſed hath ſhape wonder eſcape sith hector without dreade brennyng yre great hatrede achilles death puruey hym founde place ſaye conuenyent execucion trowe ſhould gayne raunſon mede herte quyete onely death ſo mete ende fyne mattere boke ye ſhall heare thus grekes made haue ende theyr counſayle anone wende eueryche theim home theyr lodgynge toke theyr reſten till morninge ¶howe troians toke kinge thoas pryſoner led captiue troie ca xxiiii vvhan aurora ſyluer droppes ſhene teares ſhad vpon freſhe grene complayning aye weping ſorow chyldrens death euery ſomer morowe ſaye dewe ſo ſoote enbawmed hath floure eke roote luſty lycoure aprill maye larke meſſenger daye cuſtome aye aurora doth ſalue ſundrye notys ſorow tranſmewe phebus ryſe ioye gladneſſe hermonye leue heuyneſſe taking leue ſainct iohn borow ſame time grekes morowe luſty herte early aryſe armed theim theyr beſt wiſe theim caſte daye gone felde mete fone ¶and hector hath ſame morowe alſo caſt fully grekes haue ado yſſued knightly troye herte hath ſo great deſyre ioye ſame daye grekes fyght wyth ladde many luſty knyght ſuch cyte borne forthe rode ſelfe aforne ¶and eneas many worthy folowed wonder faſt ¶and paris thē next deiphobus ¶and ſyth troylus coragious wardes made troye towne dare maketh menciowne within boke troye ſyde fighting men yt went ryde hundred thouſande armed go felde fyfty thouſande mo haue theim caſt daye eue one entent grekes greue ¶and ſo mette ſtrongly ſyde gan aſſemble together ryde full cruelly great hatrede theim tho paris lede entred full mighty ſtronge archeres perce lande many arbalaſters theyr arowes filed ſharp roūde wt quarelles ſquare whette ground full many greke hath reued lyfe amiddes mortall ſtryfe ¶agamenon felde come towardes hector hath ynome right way threwe ſtede amonge knightes lede ſpared nought great preſe ¶and therwithall anone came achilles awayte hector tho layne ſodaynly might payne ¶hector ſmote head ſo ſore wt ye ſtroke mine auctour ſayth baſenet bowed ycraſed ¶of ſtroke hector amaſed achilles ſhuld anone yfall ne eneas knightes worthy troylus come go betwene twayne ſwerdes kene gan achilles felly aſſale hewe playtes perſe mayle tho began ſlaught euery ſyde men foote theim ryde ¶like condyte woundes gā blede whyle cruell dyomede hap aduenture caſe rode mette wyth eneas ryght anone founde ſmet hym gaue ſuch wound lykly ſhould recure therto better cure ¶and therupon full deſpyteouſly thys diomede melancolye repreued hath troian knight enee ſayd hayle thou art whylom gaue pryamus kinge fell counſayle haſty bytynge haue ſlayne ſodayne violence laſt troye preſence truſt wel haue well minde amyd fyelde eft fynde thou ſhalt thy counſayle mortally repente fortune hereafter aſſent brynge aryght vnto hande good leyſer thine owne londe ¶i full ſette thy laboure quyte trouth ſwerde ſhal kerue bite kenely thy troian bloud ſhede fynally death ſhall thy mede beare atwene hādꝭ twayne wt word might reſtrayn diomede rode ſodaynly vpon enee tho ſo furyouſly ſmote hardy cruell knight ſuch payne ſo great myght horſe made fall maugre myght knightes ſtroke lyked full yll ¶and hector hath achylle aſſayled ſo baſenet perced hath ſwerde ſmet hath ſo narowe brought ye poynt hye mychefe ſuche diſioynt conſtrayned hym neceſſite hym take ne sodayne reſcues thys chyualrous ¶that called ſonne tydyus meane fell fyrſe dyomede achilles hath holpen nede force armes twayne smote hector tho ſo great payne gaue wounde full greuous nothyng mine auctour wryteth thus aſtoned knight manly man ſwerde haſte smote diomede ſo furyous wrothe horſe earth gothe pryde ſurquidrye ¶the anone troylus eſpye without abode downe ſtede alyght dyomede foote fyght eche theim ſothfaſtneſſe aquyte ſelfe lyke manly man nother muche lyte degre manhode wyte ¶and fought hector achilles togyther mette agayne amonge prees ran yfeare fyerſly theyr rage wood lyon ramage right ſo ſothe faired fighting tyme menelay kinge full proudly ſhope troians mete ¶vlyxes eke alſo pollymete came neptolonyus ¶pallamides eke scelemus ¶duke meneſte neſtor thoas ¶currynulus phyloctheas ¶and theſeus made mynde knyghtes proudly came behinde ¶and partye theim towne came kinges without excepciowne aſſembled • ffence agayne grekes maken reſyſtence except knightes yt hector ladde wardes made hadde ſame daye ſayeth latin boke knightly wyſe fyelde yt toke tho began fell mortall fyght daye ful many worthy knight fate handes fynally fall fortune amonge wardes ¶agamenon noble mighty kynge ſodaynly came rydynge ¶pantyſylaus waye mette agaynſt anone horſe ſette full knyghtly rode agayne mette ſayne horſe backe while wrothe violence vnhorſed bothe ¶and menelay parys mette newe whych two well togyther knewe full deſyrous eche dere ¶but menelay caught fyrſt ſpere hytte parys wyth buſy cure ſureneſſe ſtronge armure mighty plate woūde ſmall effect greued ſtroke vnto grounde gothe whych fall parys wexed wrothe wonder confuſe alſo red ſhame leſt reporte hinderyng name came eares quene heleyne daye might atteyne menelay holde chaumpartye lykly ſowne vnto vilanye whych herte greued full ſore adraſtus kinge withouten rode kinge vlyxes fonde knightly fought hōde hōde fought downe earth lowe horſe vlyxes hath throwe ful proudly ſygne victorye ſente horſe home tentorye ¶and tyme amonges preſe ¶full ſodaynly kynge pallamydes fall hupon locke hore yre wounden ſo ſore fell dead grouelyng ye groūd mortall ſwerde ſo kene ygrounde beſyde neptolonius aſſayled hath kinge archylogus whych ſelfe manly gan defende faught many ſtrokes ſpēde diffence would none eueryche theim hath vnhorſed ¶and tho came riding ſtede ¶pollidamas gan taken hede amonge renges lytell beſyde kinge pollamides doth ryde fierſely tho full lyke manly man ſmote ſtede ran maugre might worthineſſe ſtorye playnly beareth wytneſſe onely venge death kinge hupowne ſtede proudly bare downe rancoure cruell hete deſpyte gan rehete ¶and tho beſyde kynge scelenus deadly hate herte full yrous kinge carras aduenture hath met furyouſly ſtede hym ſmet ¶and alſo kinge philomene duke fall athene maugre manhode might hath horſe berafte fyght lad proudly ſyde lyſt ſhoulde abyde ¶and philoctetes worthy kinge alſo ſelfe tyme remus ado euery ſothly reade felowe made voiden ſtede ¶and theſeus king ſo ſtrong amid fyelde ſo rode amonge great preſe hathe met curyalus worthy king knighthod moſt famous two armes wonder ſtronge theim ſelfe fought leyſer longe til eche woundes freſhe grene felowe threwe horſback ye grene afterwarde fynde two vpon foote knightly ado armes ſo inly deſyrous manhode paſſyngly famous ¶and whyle ſonnes naturell pryamus bare theim wonder well amonge grekes vp downe ryding prudently together abydynge made ſlaught grekes full pyteous kinges duke lordes right famous reade worthy thelamowne tyme mette kynge sarpedowne theyr ſperes ſquared full ſharply eueryche hath wounded mortally ſhelde plate haberion mayle ſtorye maketh reherſayle harneys wexed bloud red fell almoſt bothe dead great myſchyefe amonge horſe fete whoſe bleding ſoyle gan wexe wete theyr harneys gan deſtylle while kinge thoas fyerſe achille kynne allyed ¶amyd fyelde hector haue eſpyed faught beſet amyd foen vpon one accorde gone mortally would auayle euery halfe gan newe aſſayle hate herte borne yore haue beſet troian knight ſo ſore ala head hath ſmet violence ryche baſenet wounded felly head ne toke none hede worthy man floure chyualrye defending tho ſo myghtely ¶kynge thoas ſmet face ſo wyth ſtroke rafte noſe two ſhorted halfe dele whych ſtroke brother naturele manly hector faſt gan theym hye ſuccoure firſt eſpye great myſchyefe theyr coming ſo manly bare theim fightyng ¶agayne grekes ye thoas haue take thelamon ſo made wake newe aſſaute ſharpe woundes kene take lefte vpon grene men borne home tente ¶and kinge thoas home troye wēt maugre grekes may hī helpe deiphobus alſo anthenore haue ſent forth troye cyte ¶and menelay tho began ſe ¶so rode parys ſtande aſyde ſhope ſhorty hate cruell pryde would fallon chaunce sodainly giuen miſchaunce ¶but ware kept ſelf ſo narow ¶that menelay marked arowe head wt venym enoint intoxycate ſquare poynt king dreadfull wounde diſpayred men founde whych great haſte bare tent anone ſurgyens hath ſente fyrſt head toke wounde albe yperced full profounde harneys depe bone cunningly theyr craft echone drawe inſtrumentes ſubtylly certayne oyntmentes ſerched haue wounde enuyron make cleane corrupcion prudently firſt token hede venum nat procede rounde compaſſe clenſed aboute bounde ſure without defenſyues made euery ſyde menelay longer would abyde bad haſte bryngen forth ſtede ¶in purpoſe full parys quite mede finde ſelfe ſame daye lyſt longer put delaye euer fall grene wounde forth rode tyll hath founde aduenture vnarmed fyelde without ſwerde pollax ſpere ſhelde bowe hande recklyſneſſe refreſhe weryneſſe ¶and menelay ſpere anone hath take yre felly gan ſhake towarde parys great auyſeneſſe ſhoulde haue ſlayne lyklineſſe ne eneas whych thinge beheld bore ſtocke ſtronge ſhelde defende auenture deſtytute naked armure ¶parys tyme ſuche peryll wherfore haſte hath eneas ordayned knightes armed bryght ſtele ¶aboute parys kepe wele myſchyefe confuſyowne hym conueye vnto troye towne right deſpyte kinge menelay awayte ſo parys laye ¶whom hector ytaken ſodaynly vnto troye ladde hym vtterly ne grekes come defence agaynſt maken reſyſtence ¶of hector came weye full many greke made deye remnaunt put vnto flyght māhode yt day might troians made grekes fle vnto tentes neceſſytee theim ſewe ne would neuer leue ſlee kill tyll drewe eue phebus gan faſte weſte drawe thē home thought beſt tytan goyng downe whan gan entre troye towne gatꝭ ſhet lodging wende daye thus made ende tyll morowe rowes red phebus carte gan ouer ſprede afore vpryſte oryent tyme king pryamus hath ſent ſuch wyth moſt pryue counſayle inwardly ſecre ¶and ſpecially ſent name ¶for worthy hector ye greateſt fame ¶for parys eke deiphobus ¶and troylus freſhe deſyrous ¶for anthenor pollidamas ¶and troian called eneas daye caſt gone felde mete foen paleys come theſe lordes haue right waye ynome vnto kinge within cloſet vſſher dores ſhet eueryche lyke degre place take dewe ſee worthy kinge made mencion gan declare hertes mocion meninge afore theim ſpecifye ſayd ſyres moſt affye ¶to knowē ye king thoas cite taken priſonere yet belocked priſowne whych euer hath vnto troye towne enemye great vnto power v offended aye ferre nere many wiſe albe lytell retche ferre force might ſtretche wt grekꝭ came beſiege town willeth deſtructiowne therupon hath buſyneſſe wherfore dome rightwyſneſſe reaſon equite ſaye playnly ſemeth vnto acceptable ye thynke counſayle cōmēdable like hath caſt death ſhape holde rightfull eſcape death receyue guerdon ryght requireth alſo good reaſon death death ſkilful guerdonning vnto witte right well ſyttyng ¶say aduiſe playnly caſe ¶and fyrſt tho ſpake eneas ſayd lorde ſo none offence highneſſe gyue audyence thrugh ſupport thē full wyſe ſhall reherſe playnly deuiſe worke mattere ſemeth fyrſt lyege lorde ſo deare noble royall excellence conſydre ſhoulde full high prudence euery worke operacion caſte afore concluſyon fynall ende may ſewe wyſe man onely dewe ſe gynning ende nought attones peyſen thought weye theim ſo iuſtly balaunce fine enſewe repentaunce ſaye platly meane ye ought ſene kinge thoas one pryncipall amonge grekes yt bloud royall ye conſydre deſcended lyne wherfore haue thus foule fyne ſlayne whyle pryſon happen might concluſyon ye therto aſſente afterwarde ſhoulde ſore repent ¶i preue thus aduenture fortune rule man may aſſure lordes another daye grekes take happe maye ſonnes full worthy renowne kinges towne truſteth well ſuche lyke gentylneſſe ye theim ſhewen diſtreſſe quyte caſe ſemblable fortune theim fynde fauorable man conſtrayne may binde wherfore lord haueth thing mind ¶for yf thoas ſhorte auyſemente shall dead haſty iudgemēt another daye grekes wyll v acquyte rygour make malyce byte ſome euer nother ſpare high lowe degre though peraunter bloud thinge worldes good might fall ye ne would ſe wherfore reade let kinge thoas honeſtly kept preſowne like eſtate ſtill towne leſt ſayd another daye lorde happe maye caſuelly take auenture eſchaunge ye might beſt recure without ſtryfe owne man agayne matter ſayne fynally full rede ¶to counſayl hector toke good hede according reaſon commendeth opynion ¶but pryam euer one entencion stode alway fixe concluſion playnly affirminge greks may eſpye kinge ſpare gentrye arrecte cowardyſe anone dare venge v foen dread hauynge none hardyneſſe herte nother rightwiſeneſſe yet neuertheleſſe aſſente ſhall lyue wyll myne entente deſyre fully condeſcende ¶and counſayle ſo made end without ſaue eneas ygo ¶and troylus eke anthenor alſo hall excelling beaute quene heleyne purpoſe ſe eke hecuba quene ladyes goodly ſene many mayde yonge luſty worthy troylus eneas labour buſy payne comforte fayre quene heleyne ſhe ſtode werre dreade womanheade thilke time herte entere ſhe well could made theim good chere hauinge conninge iuly ſuffyſannce cheare dalyaunce hecuba beyng hall example vnto woman bounte hauinge ſoueraygne excellence wiſedome eke eloquence beſought theim tho wonder womanly counſayled eke full prudently haſte nigh ferre auyſely kepe theim werre ieoparte theyr body folyly aduerte caſte prudently diffence knightlyy towne theim gouerne diſcreſciowne ſpake fayth could nothing feyne heleyne toke leue longer dwell went waye forth tell ¶how grekes ſame morowe amonge thē ſelfe complayne makē ſorowe harmes great murmur rage loſſe coſtes great domage haue endured folylye laſtynge werre wiſten neuer whye death ſlaught many worthy man dead ſith yt werre began hunger thurſt watche colde alſo full great vnreſte ſorowe thought wo together thinge nought ſothfaſtneſſe grounde ſought noyſe rumour eke ran throughout ye hooſt yt day man mā moſt amonge pore ſouldiours bare bronte euer ſuch ſhoures miſchiefe werre comonly though plain haue remedy ſondry thinges ſit theim full vnſoft thus grekes complayned haue full ofte many miſchief hath theim fall might haue eſchewed ne foly gonne werre grece nat come halfe ſo ferre miſchief confuſyon daye lamentacion ¶which encreaſe ſame nexte night derked without ſterre light cloudy blacke ſo thicke ayre dimmed ſkyes foule nothing fair windy eke tempeſt belayne almoſt drenched ſmoky rayne felde aſtoned yonder ſodayne ſtroke dreadfull thonder opening hidous leuene ſemed high heauen cataractes hadden vndo cloudes ſkyes two sodainly wexen ſo blake like goddes would haue takē wrake newe aſſented one lande drenche deucalyon world without refuge ouerflowe freſhe deluge winde alſo ſo ſternly gan blowe tentes ſtanding rowe forpoſſid ybeten downe furyouſly confuſyowne flodꝭ raught thē ſtāding place bare theim forth frō then large ſpace wherof myſchyefe great diſtreſſe great laboure hertye heauyneſſe grekes bydde ſame nyght tempeſt lacke lyghte tyll floude gan agayne withdrawe wynde appeaſe day gan dawe heauen gan agayne clere without cloudes freſhly appere phebus eke feruent hete ſoyle dryed vp wete moyſture enuyrowne playne grekes tentes ſette agayne adawed nyghtes ſorowe apering glade morowe arayed nothynge peace fyelde fyrſt went achylles ye ſhall entencyowne daye fyght wt troye towne vvhan dryed luſty large playne wt phebꝰ bemes ye haue hard ſain troian knightes full worthy renowne deſcended ycomen downe fyelde toke fyghtyng place achylles mete face tofore went lyke tolde lordes knightes bolde fyrſt fynde without abode vnto hupon furyouſly rode meane hupon ſtature lyke gyaunt bokes v aſſure achylles ſharpe ſpere body perced ſo fere fylle dead wounde ſo kene kynge octamene fyerſly hector wolde haue gone without abode hector hath ſlaine anone cruelly quytte fatall mede ſodaynely agaynſt diomede ¶as zantipus worthy kyng gan drawe full pyteouſly hym ſlawe ryght anone kyng epyſtrophus eke kyng hyght cedius one aſſent proudly battayle begonne hector mortally taſſayle ſpere fyrſt epyſtrophus ran hym herte deſpyteous guydo alſo doth deuyſe rebuked vngoodly wyſe hym ſo ſore herte meued wherof hector furyouſly agreued hath mortally wounde made ſo large hym ne geyneth plate ſhelde targe fell dead amonge men echone hector bad ſhulde gone furyes depe downe helle suche proude wordes amonges tell quod men take hede thus whan waged mede ¶anone brother called cedyus suche ſorowe made epyſtrophus hertye dole ſo wofull chere pytie ſe inwardely death thought thouſande knightꝭ yt brought auenged manhode deſpyteouſly hector fall hym founde fyghtyng wt foen force th • euerycone ſore enuyrowne haue beſet frō ſtede downe haue ſmit ¶whom cedyus aye cruell rage whan ſawe ouauntage hector vnhorſed ſtede ſworde lefte inwardly hatred markynge hym ſo great payne force armes twayne fully purpoſe withouten delaye ſlea hector playnly maye ſtroke deſcende myght downe hector hate indignaciowne ſworde full ſharpe whet ſhoulder hath arme ſmet reuyd hym lyfe eneas amyddes ſtryfe came rydyng ryght wood furious mette kyng amphymacus fell ſlewe hym rage grekes holdyng paſſage ¶there diſcended fyrſt menelaus ¶and kynge thelamonius ¶the great duke alſo athene ſo moche manhode ſene vlixes eke cruell diomede eke alſo helpe nede came kyng machaon alderlaſt great agamenon wardes fell ſodeynly vpon troyans full manfully diffende ſelfe agayne grekes proude put full knightly coude eche ſothly mette ſpere ſworde enuyouſly ſette mortall hate betwene whan ſonne merydyen mydday angell paſſyng hote ſhene grekes gan felly tene myghtely falle troye made geuen weye force neceſſytye ¶and achylles ſo full cruelte amonge renges gan hym drawe kyng phylem enuyouſly hath ſlawe ¶and amyd grekes ſame time hector maugre ſlewe kyng alphenor ¶and eke kynge called dorius ſo cruell irous vertue knyghtly honde troyans wonne haue agayne londe vpon grekes made flee ¶and thylke houre troye cite epyſtrophus full manlyneſſe felde haue take worthineſſe grekes proudely none knightes fauleth attones ſeuered made twinne gan fyelde faſt vpon wynne ¶hauyng tyme companye amonges tho dyd guye ¶a certayne archer whiche fynde monſtruous wonderfull kynde myddell vp vnto crowne man remnaunt downe bare horſe lykeneſſe fygure horſes heire monſtre nature ſkynne growyng enuyrowne full rough thycke voice ye ſowne lyke neyhynge horſe reade though face length brede ſhape mannyſhe yet ſothfaſtneſſe colour ſemblable lykeneſſe vnto fyry hoote brennyng glede whoſe cyen eke flawmyng alſo reade blaſe ouen mouthe ſyghte ſo vnkouth ſoeuer met berde man horſe ſore ferde face ſo hatefull ſo odyble loke ſo hydous horrible aye cuſtome vſaunce bokes made remembraunce go vnarmed fyelde without ſworde ſpere axe ſhielde nothyng coulde myſter fynde good archer bare bowe ſtyffe wonder ſtronge alſo tyller longe arrowes lyke tyller buſhment truſſed wonder ner ſyde aye ready hande ſo outher ſea lande fynde none armure agayne ſhot playnly myght endure horſe ſtede couſer durſt abyde nouther fer ner fledde anone full myght faſt hym ſyght ſo paſſynge odyous lyke deuyll ſo monſtruous founde none ſo hardy knight horſebacke force might holde horſe whan myght hym ſe anone backe wolde flee archer fynde wryten eke day ſlewe full many greke wounded arrowes kene throughout ye plate forged bryght ſhene none afore hym abode tentes faſte away rode myght hydous loke endure tyll befell wonder aduerture whyle troye helpe archer sewe chaſe lodgyng ner ſlewe miſchiefe dreade ¶beſyde tent mette hym dyomede archer neceſſyte ſtode ſo ne myght hym flee maner way backe remewe lyfe deth myght hym eſchewe many troyan tho backe flyinge go wracke ¶wherfore anone worthy dyomede cruell herte faſte gan hym ſpede towarde proudely dreffe archer great aduyſeneſſe fyrſt arrowe ſmytte dyomede thrugh harneys made blede whiche ſtroke wexed ſo wood wroth monſtre ſo hydous ſo loth went paſe hym vnarmed fonde yt ſworde helde honde gaue hym laſte fattall wounde fell dead grouelynge vnto ye ground death grekes reioyſynge haſte hertes reſumynge began ſelfe recomforte fyelde proudely reſorte ¶by conueyinge policenare worthy duke ſo well hym bare vpon troyans day fyelde whan hector ſlaught behelde vpon duke anone gan ſette ſtedes fyerſly mette ¶hector hym ſlewe full great hatrede gallathe ſtede rode forth amonge preſe ware mette achylles ſperes longe large round purpoſe fully eche confounde ran yfeare yrous right wrothe ſtroke vnhorſed ¶but achylles diſpyteous herte fyrſt reade ſadell ſterte buſy inwarde peyne gallathe taken reyne therof euer hector depryue bad men lede home blyue hector none bote full lyke man faught ſtandyng fote amonges grekes fomen knightes loude gan call ſtede ſhulden ſewe haſte horſe reſcue ben attones fallen vpon achylle ¶and maugre force agayne haue hym berafte plaine vnto hector reſtored agayne knighthod ſo moche ſelf aſſureth diſpyte ſadell recureth whiche afterwarde full dere aboughte lyke lyon day wrought amonges rydyng death fled ſword fere whoſe manhod troians efte begyn vpon grekes fielde agayne wyn ¶but befell amyd great fyght anthenor certayne troyan knight amonge preſe ſo fer ygone grekes take anone tentes ſent haſte albe ſonne called pollydamas reſcue hym dyd dylygence manfully neclygence founde hym ſo lyſte ſeke full dere bought many greke ſame day worthyneſſe cauſe onely derckeneſſe gan drawe towarde nyght made ende onely lacke lyghte grekes went home lodgyng eke troyans tyll mornyng ¶that phebꝰ gan bryght beames ſhew aurora newe gan dewe herbes ſote grene leues hayes freſhe greues syluer bryght rounde perles fyne ſo clerely agayne ſonne ſhyne ſhewe ſelfe ſo oryent ſhene hylle vale euery grene rody morowe tyll hote beames bryght phebus fyry ſtemes vapoureth vp moyſture ayre wether cleare agreable fayre attempre alſo hete whan troians caſte mete fomen platly maye went beſte arraye wardes fyelde rowe ¶agaynſt grekes ſlowe ſhope forth without longer lette tyll togyther manfully haue mette ſperes ſwordes clere ran together diſpyteous chere tyll ſhyuered ſonder many ſpere ſheldes ſtronge ſelfe ryuen peces many targe ax rounde brode large baſenettes tho ſmyte ſhrede full many knyght mortally gan blede ſothfaſtneſſe tell ſame day ſlayne many man outher parte moſt troye towne albe guydo maketh mencyowne perſon ſpecyall nouther ſyde generall saue concludeth playnely fyght laſted fro morowe tyl nyght troyans haue ful dere abought day fortune holpe nought tourned hole confuſyowne ſo repeyred towne tentes grekes faſt ſpede ¶till morowe ſenten dyomede vlixes troye cytie trewes onely monthes thre kyng pryam therto wolde aſſente two meſſage wente certayne knyght borne troye towne hyght dolon great diſcreciowne alſo ryght famous rycheſſe curteſy gentylneſſe deuer dyd diligence conueye vnto preſence ¶of pryamus paleys royall ſea moſt chyefe pryncipall ſatte lordes enuirowne many knyght full worthy renowne gan hym fyrſt ſpecyfye hooly ſubſtaunce embaſſadrye trewes theyr entent tolde ſo aſſent wolde kyng benyngnely herde aduyſe prudently anſwerde thervpon honour ſaue good leyſer wolde counſayle haue lordes fully hym gouerne matter lyke diſcerne ¶and conclude ſhortly euerychone aſſented except hector alone vnto trewes wolde denye hector ſayde trecherye onely ſlaughter falſe treaſon axynge vnder occaſyon fyrſte burye grekes dead vnder coloure therof dread afterwarde ſelfe vyttayle well knewe ſtuffe gan fayle enfamyned leſte ſhulden dye ſought ſpace ſelfe purueye outwarde ſygnes dyd eſpye wherfore quod lyketh lye apparaunce dare preſume whyles waſte thus conſume oure ſtuffe within dreade wyll prouyde yt haue nede auauntage myght v hyndryng damage whyles encreaſen amende ſhall ſtore diſcreaſe diſpende yet neuertheleſſe euer touchyng trewes monthes thre sythen ye aſſent accorde ſentence diſcorde wyſe varyaunt thus trewes confirmed graūt outher ſyde thought beſte bycauſe ſhulde quyet reſte meane whyle eaſe releue felte woundes ſore greue myght leyſer haue ſores recure yt meane trewes thus endure fell treatee communyng ¶of anthenor thoas kyng anthenor delyuered ſhulde kyng thoas troye cyte ¶and thoas ſhuld grekes home againe enchaunge ye haue herd ſaine one accorded ¶and ye troian byſhop calchas remembred hym vpon doughter dere called cryſeyde eyen clere troye lefte behynde whē went thenſe bokes maken mynde felte paſſyngly great ſmerte tenderly ſhe ſette herte enprented eue morowe chiefe cauſe grounde al ſorowe ſhe lefte behynde towne without comforte conſolaciowne caſte ſothly abſence ſpecially great offence hath wrought agaynſt thē troye hym thought ſhuld neuer haue ioye tyll doughter recured hath agayne ¶wherfore calchas ſtory ſayth certaine wyttes many wayes caſte beſt might trewes doth laſt recure doughter ſome maner waye fynde vpon certayne daye porte wonder humbly wepyng eye wente full pyteouſly complaynyng teares albe reyned whoſe inwarde wo ſothly feyned knee anone falleth downe tofore great kyng agamenowne beſechynge hym humilite mercy hyghe pyte kynges ſyttyng place haue routhe hym grace wo haue compaſſyon maye haue reſtitucion doughter loued ſo praying deuer prudent mediacyon anthenor pryſon kyng thoas ſhe myght eſchaunged lyſte benignite requeſte goodly aſſent graunt forth anone ſent kyng pryam haue creſeyde calchas ſake therwith al leyde charge wonder ſpecially went embaſſadrye ¶to troye towne kynge pryamus calchas ſo odyus hatefull eke throughout towne reporte vp downe treatour alſo falſe worthy enhonged halſe treaſon doubleneſſe euermore ſayd eke expreſſe deſerued hath ryght lawe shamefully fyrſte drawe afterwarde moſte horryble death may haue yelden vp breth lyke treatour dyſpyteous wyſe herte thyncke deuyſe eueryche affyrmyng iudgement death none fully equypollent deſerte falſeneſſe yonge olde playnely bare wytneſſe concludyng eke iniquyte wolde aſſent degree vnto nothyng myght herte pleaſe creſeyde hym eaſe caſte make delyueraunce leuer gyuen hym miſchaunce hym myght haue good large ¶but fynally effect charge ſo ferforth dryuen ende priamus hath graūted ſhe ſhal wende kyng thoas ſhortly vnto father dan anthenore euer grutche kyng parlement hath thervpon geuen iudgement vtterly may repealed worde ſentence aſſealed ſhe muſt parte eyen glade ſorowe playnely ſhe made departynge hereafter ye ſhall whan agayne cometh matere ¶how duryng trewes iii monthes hoctor walked grekes hooſte talke hadde betwyxte achylles hym capitulo xxv truſe affyrmed ye haue herd deuiſe outher ſyde yt full wiſe full aſſented euerychone tyll three monthes comen gone lyke reade certayne daye whan agreable morowe graye blandyſhyng pleaſaunt delyte hector harte caught appetyte lyke guydo lyketh wryte ſame daye wolde grekes vyſyte full well beſene wonder rychely many worthy companye ſuche none cheſe tent fyrſt achylles fynde ſoth troyan knyght vpon ſtede hath take weye ryght full lyke man made mencion ¶nowe achylles great affection herte daye nyght worthy hector haue ſyght neuer yet none occaſyon myght hym haue full inſpection hym beholde good lyberte vnarmed myght hym neuer ſe wonder knightly aſwell porte chere mette yfere ryght manly countenaunce laſte fell dalyaunce ¶but achylles fyrſt began abreyde vnto hym euen thus ſayde hector quod full pleaſynge leyſer naked may ſe syth neuer myght haue ſyght whan thou armed knyght ſhalbe full greuous whiche ſo inly enuyous thou ſayne ſlayne anone handes twayne ſoth hooly pleaſaunce cruell death take vengeaunce full ofte werre eke fyght haue felte vertue great myght thy force many woundes kene vpon full freſhe byn grene many place ſhedyng bloud thou ſo furyous wood aye compaſſynge deſtructiowne many mayle myne haberiowne thy ſharpe ſwerde racyd hath ſonder cruelly ſeuered yonder mortally ſygnes ſhewe plate ſtronge perſed yhewe harneys forged bryght ſtele myght neuer yet aſſured ſo wele thyne yre whan thou lyſte ſmyte thy ſworde ne wolde kerne byte fleſhe full depe full profounde ſheweth yet many mortall wounde body large longe wyde yet appere vpon euery ſyde day day full ſore ake ſmerte whiche thynge ſemeth herte enbolleneth newe nowe whan ſee hyghe deſpyte auenged fret olde enuious rage may neuer breſt aſwage tyll vengeaunce fatall ſute cruell death execute ¶and one thyng moſt greuaunce whan haue fully remembraunce mynde conſyder vp downe howe thou haſt made fynall deuyſyowne ¶of ala hym patroclus yonge ſo manly ſo vertuous loued ſkylle ryght euen ſelfe full myght hoole herte inly kyndneſſe tongue may telle expreſſe haſt thou made departiſyon v hole affection yknyt one hertie allyaunce without partyng diſſeueraunce entyerly faythfull hertes twayne ylaced locked chayne whiche myght none aduerſyte lyfe death ſonder twynned tyll cruelly thou madeſt v departe thrugh hert ſo inwardly doth darte wyll neuer ſoth thought truſteth well ful dere ſhalbe bought death hym nothyng perauenture ended yere vpon onely ſake cruell deth vengeaunce ſhalbe take enſure without bonde may lyue myne owne hande ſhall death execucyon without abode longe delacyon ryght requireth without dreade death death fynall mede ſelfe theron ſhall wroke ye world hereafter ſhalbe ſpoke achylles venged ſoe ¶for patroclus loued ſo though enuyous thy death inly deſyrous ne wete put blame well wotte thou arte ſame haſt death many day deſyred thervpon inwardly conſpyred thus ſhortely atwene v two death without wordes mo whan fortune lyſt tyme thereto ſhape hope fully thou ſhalte eſcape truſte none ſaye vtterly ¶to hector haſtely anſwerde againe ſober countenaunce auyſed well dalyaunce nothyng rekles ¶and euen thus ſpake achylles syr achylles without fayle thou ne oughteſt greatly meruayle though power full myghte herte dewe ryght day day thy death conſpyre euer one compaſſe deſyre laboure early eke late purſue full cruell hate thou oughteſt wonder wyſe fully knowe ſentence wyſe maner ſo taketh hede ryghtwyſeneſſe may procede wyght loue al myght death purſeweth deſtruction ouer confuſyon hath layde ſyege aboute cyte kinrede alſo vpon thervpon felly doth preſume mortall hate werre conſume v euerychone ywyſſe fynde herte lawe kynde suche one loue ryght equyte haue chere ſothly degre werre may frendlyhead debate loue aryght procede ¶for ſothly loue moſt ſpeciall faythfulneſſe hath orygenall hertes ioyned conuenyence one accorde difference doubylneſſe may degre nother ioye aduerſyte lyfe death aſunder diſſeuer loue contuneth euer ¶but hate contrarye whych ſothly hertꝭ varye procedeth rancoure eye men maye ſe debate enuye ſtryfe enmyte mortall ſlaughter nygh ferre mother whyche ſothfaſtnes werre fyne wherof longe seuereth hertes frendſhip cutte atwo cauſeth loue leyde full lowe ¶but wil thou knowe thy proude wordes herte thoughte ſothe agaſten ryght nought ſhall furthermore breake without auaunt trouthe ſpeake ſaye playnly henſe two yeare maye lyue werres ſwerde knighthod forthe acheue hope ſothe ſo mortally greue grekes thē maye mete thou ſhall fele full vnſwete ye contynue werres haunte ſhal pryde ſurquedrye adaunte ſuche wiſe handes two werre fully ado well many greke full ſore ſhall rewe well wote olde newe grekes gathered one ſurquedrye founde euerychone onely lacke diſcreſcion vndertake preſumpcion highe thinge ſyege layne ſelfe ouer charge vayne empryſes withouten fable byn weyght importable peys ſo great heuyneſſe fynally oppreſſe pride auale lowe enclyne burthē ſhall enbowe backe chyne vnwarely cauſen fall ye haue done ſaye one ¶and ouer full ſuerte ¶thou achilles ſpeake vnto fatall deathe firſt ſhall aſſayle tofore thy ſwerde thynge auayle agaynſt thy worthyneſſe ¶and ſo ſo great hardyneſſe courage wyll vygour force myght meue thy herte manhode knyght take derryng darreyne betwene v two thilke quarell ſo befall whych ſtryue wyll aſſent playnly ieoparde tyll death one v departe theſe lordes kinges prynces wyll accorde yfere fully one aſſent holde ſtable herte entente felde onely v tweyne haue ſayde quarell may darreyne ended condiciowne happe thy highe renowue venquiſhe dryue outtraunce make fully aſſuraunce fyrſt lorde priamus kinge shall vnto grekes maner thinge crowne ſceptre holy ſubmitte poynt varye nother flytte fully yelde ſubiectiowne lordſhip within troye towne ¶and lyeges captyuytye shall go theyr waye cyte leue quyte gouernaunce without ſtryfe varyaunce thervpon make ſecuryte deuoyde ambyguyte tofore goddes othe ſacrament ſhall ſwore full good entente ouermore fayth alſo ſaue aſſure pledge ye ſhall haue meane whyle kepe thē ſide choyſe hoſtages abyde troye towne worthieſt ye lyſt cheſe alſo beſte ye ſhall nothyng euer ſaye ¶and achilles without wordes mo lyſte accorde therunto haue ſayd thy honour encreaſe make werre ſodaynly ceaſe lykly laſte longe betwene troians grekes ſtronge thou ſhalt onely wt honour fame throughout worlde winnen name therwithall lyte thrugh thy knighthod many man profite fro death ſhall eſcape alyue countre hole ſounde aryue lykly cruell aduenture dead werre endure come therfore let prolonged let daye atwene v two ioyned haue ſayd condiciowne diffence onely towne haue victorye fortune ouer axe elles anone ye breake vp ſiege werre lete ſuffer v lyuen quyete grece home ye gone thinge achilles anone hote yre furyous alſo brenning full hote anger wo aſſented deſpytous cheare ¶and gan anone hector dreſſe nere ſayd would delyuer vtterly fro poynt poynt axynge therin made none excepciowne hole herte entencion requeſte accepted euery dell ſemed leked right well parte caſte gloue adowne ſygne token confirmaciowne lyfe death holde daye agayne hector happe happe maye vnto hector lyfely ſterte toke vp glad herte euer yet man knyght quarell toke foe fight man ſothe ryght deuyſe glad high empryſe ¶of whych noyſe great ſowne ran eares kinge agamenowne anone ſelfe came tente lordes parliament ¶where achilles hector yfere wytte mattere would aſſenten fynally put quarell full ieopardy parte atwene theſe knightes tweyn ye haue herde fully dareyne ¶and one voyce grekes denye ſayde nolde ſuche companye kinges duke lordes eke alſo bothe life death ieoparte atwene two courſe fortune theim ſubmitte daye face chaunge flytte ſome troye concluſyowne ieoparde ne wold liues towne handes onely knight put auenture fyght ¶pryam except whyche ſothly caſe within ſelfe fully aſſented playnly put ſette ieopardye hooly honour regallye suppoſynge aye made memorye hector ſhoulde haue victorye empryſe toke hande ¶but priam might tho withſtande agayne ſo many one entencion contrarye opynion bothe grekes troye ſyde helde peace let ouer ſlyde ſo grekes parted echone ¶and hector achilles gone home troye leue whyle while dyrecten ſhall ſtile tell troylus lamentable wo made parte lady fro ala fortune gery vnſtable redy aye chaungeable whē folke moſt truſt thy ſtormye face like deſyre fully embrace thy ioye away tourne writhe wpon wretch thy power kythe record troylus yt whele ſo lowe falſe enuye thou haſt ouerthrowe ioye whych lady make hym twynne beſt wende haue ſured woe hath endured muſte nedely helpe hym complayne whych herte felte ſo great payne inwarde wo ſo great diſtreſſe haue cunning expreſſe knewe partynge creſeyd almoſt wo payne deyed fully wiſte ſhe departe ſhal ſentence iudgement fynall father gyuen parlyamente wo tourment al rente poynt haue fallen rage man might appeaſe aſwage hidde paynes breſt gā dare lyke man furye gan fare ſuch ſorowe daye nyght make complayninge onely ſake ſawe ſhe ſhould aweye leuer playnly deye lyue behinde abſence thought without preſence dead ſayne teares gan berayne eyen gan bollen breſt ſighes tho vppe ſwollen ſobbynge ſorowes depe ne rore wepe ſore loue herte gan conſtrayne ſhe ne felte litle payne wepte alſo piteouſly gan crye deſyringe aye ſhe might dye rather parte fro troye owne knyght luſt lyues ioye chekes teares downe deſtyll fro eyen teares round drop tryl fordewed haue blacke wede eke vntruſſed heyre abrode gā ſprede lyke golde wyre forrent torne yplucked ſheres ſhorne ouer freſhe roſen hewe whilom ymeynt whyte lylyes newe wofull wepynge pyteouſly diſteyned like herbes april bereyned floures freſhe dewes ſwete right ſo chekes moyſte wete criſtall water vp aſcendinge hye breſt heauenly eye aye amonge lamentaciowne full ofte ſythe ſhe fell ſwowne adowne deadly pale fordimmed ſyghte ofte ſayde ala myne owne knight mine owne troilus ala ſhal parte rather let death ſpere darte herte vaynes kerue rage ſterue rather ala fro knight twinne ¶and wo oh death nilt thou come helpe make ende ſhulde troye wende abyde grekes gone dwell amonge cruell fone ala ala wofull creature ſhoulde werre endure wretched woman ſelfe alone amonge men armes euerychone thus gan ſhe crye longe daye playnte full great affray pyteous noyſe till drewe night vnto owne trewe knight full tryſt heauy came agaynes eue might ought comforte releue ¶but ſothe hath creſeyde founde ſwowne liyng grounde pyteouſly vnto wente wofull cheare armes hente toke vp atwene theim two began newe ſuche deadly wo routhe pyte ſene ſhe cheare pale grene coloure like aſhes deade fro face gone red chekes deuoyded bloude wofully atwene theim two ſtode ſhe ne might worde yſpeake redy deathe wreke vpon ſelfe naked ſwerde beſyde ſhe full ofte gan grounde glyde armes ſhe fell ſwowne ſelfe gan teares drowne ſtille dombe ſtone mouthe wordes none wery ſpyryte flykered breſt death ſtode tho vnder reſte without maynpryſe ſothly lyfe thus ſemed ſtryfe whiche theim two ſhulde fyrſte ypaſſe death portrayed herte face coloure ſuch men go theyr graue thus wo gan togyther raue diſconſolate longe nyght good fayth yf ſhould aryght proceſſe hole theyr bothe ſorowe made till next morowe poynt poynt ſpecifye longe would occupye euery thynge make mencion tarye tranſlacion ſo ſhoulde wo procede ſemeth nede ¶syth maiſter chaucer afore matter hath ſo well bore boke troylus creſeyde whych mayde longe deyed reherſyng firſt troilus cōtrayre aſcende vp loues ſtayre ſurquedrye became one compaynye loues folke olde game whan cupide ſubdued full tame brought lowe ſubiectiowne temple walked vp downe gynne hooke leyde amid eyen cercled creſeyde whych daye might aſterte breſt perced hath herte went home pale dead wan wiſe troylus firſt began ſeruaunt mayſter telleth thus till holpe pandarus whoſe comforte mediacion boke made relacion great laboure fyrſt came grace ſo continueth many yeares ſpace till gery fortune gan vpon frowne ſhe fro muſt go towne ſodaynly ſythe ſe lo ende falſe felycite lo ende worldly brotilneſſe fleſhly luſt lo thunſtableneſſe lo double variacion wordly bliſſe tranſmutacion daye myrthe wo morowe aye fine ala ioye ſorowe creſeyde kinge thoas anthenor ſhall forth gon ala vnto grekes euer theim dwell ¶the hole ſtorye chaucer tell ye lyſt man better alyue proceſſe halfe ſo well diſcriue englyſhe gilt ſayes rude boyſtous firſte olde dayes full fer parfection lytell reputacion till came poetrye gan tunge firſt magnifye adourne eloquence honour laude reuerence throughout lande giuen ſonge laurer engliſhe tonge giuen excellence right whilom ful high ſentence perpetually memoriall ¶of columpna cardinall petrack fraūceis giuen italye reporte neuer fayle honour dirked name regiſtred houſe fame amonge higheſt ſete mayſter galfride chiefe poete euer yet language name ſhall pallen none age euer yliche without eclipſing ſhine parte neuer fine magnifye writinge plianly till dye god praye ſoule bringe ioye ¶and lefte wil agayne troye ſtorye tell firſt guydo within boke thus ſpeaketh troylus rebuking full vncurteyſly ſo ſette herte folyly vpon creſeyde full doubilneſſe boke guydo liſt expreſſe teares complayninge wordes white ſofte blandiſhinge meynt fayning flatterye outward farſed many falſe lye vnderhid varyaunce cured aboue fayned countenaunce woman falſly teres borowe theyr herte though ſorowe lyke would trouthe deye thynke one ſay ſerpent vnder floures fayre venym hydeth doth repayre ſugre afore galle hydde behinde propered aye vnto theyr kynde dyuerſe double nature ratheſt deceyuing men moſt aſſure vnder coloure euery thynge werke fayre aboue foule dercke hydde ſo man may eſpye though ſo wyth wofull eye outwarde wepe pyteouſly tother eye laugh couertly whoſe ſorowes tempred alley theyr coloure euer meynt rayes vpon chaunge mutabylyte stande hole theyr truſte theyr ſuerte ſure doubylneſſe alway double theyr ſikerneſſe seminge one beſt varye lykeſt corde contrarye thus moſt varyaunt accorde hooleſt ſeme diſcorde guido ſayth fewe none herte apayed one yet one twayne thre foure theyr ſpeche fayne lyke one mo hoole theyr loue well eke wo eneryche ſhall hym ſelfe deme next lyke doth ſeme thus hope ſtādeth eche theim treweſt aye redyeſt forto fall ſerueth beſt next appayred thus chaunge theyr loue fayred let man truſte catche maye farewell morow though ſure daye fayre chaunge laſteth yeare folye bye deare thilke treaſour whyche harde poſſede flieth away men therof moſt nede yf happe chapman ſayth guydo yet daye men maye ſe ſheweth large feneſtralles chaumbers high lowe downe halle windowes eke euery ſtrete alſo eke men maye wyth theim mete pylgramage oblacions ſpectacles cityes townes ſayth guydo ſelle telle eke ſayth ſentement fraude fully equypolent fraude ſleyghty compaſſinge woman lyke workyng ſet faithfulneſſe wening theim finde ſtableneſſe ſhall theim fynde ſtedfaſt mone poynt chaunge ſoone yonge caſte rage olde falleth dotage wherfore counſayle bothe two caſte brydell lightly let theim go ¶this teacheth guido god wote hath delite ſpeake curſedly alway woman throughout boke men maye ſe ſo lyſt loke theim hadde enuye ſpecyall good fayth right wrothe wt al theim lyſt ſo debate yre latin tranſlate inwardly hert felte blede high diſpite clauſes rede reſowned concluſiowne onely malyce accuſaſiowne thoſe woman full euyll mote thriue generally ſecte deſcryue whiche made diſcrecion good badde none excepcion blame foule mote falle cauſe one hynder dare well affyrmen rode agayne one bad ben hundred good though ſome one double newe hyndreth trewe example alſo though ſhewe ſome one whylom ſhrewe good take ſhall hede hinderinge womanheade though twaine thre double faine agayne ſothly colayne vyrgyns inly full grace leuen thouſande holy place man may fynde kalender full many mayde parfyt enter death ſtable trewe ſome theim roſen hewe marterdome blyſſe heauen wonne ſome alſo bokes telle konne lylye vyrgynyte vyolettes parfyte chaſtyte aſcenden aboue ſterres cleare ſercle nynthe ſphere ioye aye gladneſſe eterne wherfore ſothe diſcerne though ſome clerkꝭ ſhrewes haue miſſaid let good woman therof miſpayde lacke one blame eke men maye ſayde ſame trewe reprefe though ſo another thefe worſe degre though hanged tree vnto woman hinderyng none amonge hundred though yt one gouernaunce vicious agayne byn ful vertuous yf ye lyſt thouſande ye may fynde though guido write haue kinde double men ſhoulde goodly take agayn maner grutching make nature workynge hath full great powere harde courſe holde reſtreyne ſhe guyded reyne coarted dewe righte therfore eche man full might shoulde thanke god taketh paciently yf woman double naturelly ſhulde men laye theim blame though min auctour hīder ſo name writynge onely cryſeyde vpon ſuch blame leyde counſayle lyghtly ouerpaſſe myſſayth place hyndre woman eue morowe taketh hede let theim wyth ſorow paſſe ouer ye liſt rede tyll ye come diomede ſente troye towne ceryouſly made menciowne fyrſt ſhe delyuered ¶for anthenor kinge thoas troylus gan conueye many brynge weye ¶and dyomede waye gan brydell lede tyll brought father tent calchas full good entent receyued lodged laye ſpeche duryng daye maner hole euerydele reherſed ceryouſly wele troylus boke ye haue herde ſaine wryte ofte holde vayne ¶but guydo ſayth longe nyght cryſeyde hath forſake owne knight gaue herte vnto diomede tenderneſſe womanhede troylus herte colde without fyre byn theſe aſſhes olde none accuſacion onely kyndes tranſmutacyon appropryed vnto nature selde neuer ſtable endure experyence men maye ofte lere nowe tourne agayne matere muſt reſorte though ferre began wryten werre ¶of battayles trewſe deſcripcion pallaſe ilion great peſtylence grekes hoſte whereby enforced ſeke trewſe whiche vpon ſuyte obteyned thyrtye dayes capitulo xxvi tyme paſſed trewſe ytake next morow whā titā hath forſake vnder partye hemyſperye al night full merye aurora liynge ſyde bed hym lyſt longer byde ſhope vp caſte ſtreames ſhene ¶on troy wall whan hector armed clene fyelde faſte gan hym hye fyftene thouſande companye worthy knyghtes manly men fynde troylus tenne knyghtes eke baner ſewe haſt parys gan remewe towne perce londe eche thē mighty bowe honde arrowes ſharpe truſſed ſyde knyghtes aboute ryde alſo thre thouſande fynde ¶and deiphobus next came behynde thre thouſande knightes armed clene whoſe plate ſonne ſhone full ſhene ¶and nexte hym came troyan eneas reade ſothīy ſame day troye towne hundred thouſande knyghtes renown lyke recordeth dare frygyus boke guydo writeth thus ¶and grekes toforre day ſeuen thouſande goeth menelay knyghtes echone whiche tho dyd lede many went dyomede next ſeweth hardy achylles mayne called myrmydones ¶and zantipus worthy kyng eke thre thouſand knightꝭ wt hym lad fyelde agayn towne alderlaſte great agamenowne ſuche nombre grekes felle wonder heren telle whan wardes felde abrode take place without abode ¶a grekyſhe kyng phillis hight anone hector ſyght towardes hym ſyttynge ſtede ſpere gan faſte ſpede hector hath commynge ſayne hente ſpere rode hym agayne ſhyelde plate rounde gaue hym hys laſte fatall wounde vpon whoſe deth auenged full many greke gan hector flee fyrſt worthy kyng famous ¶that grekes called zantypus hye diſdayne onely phyllys ſake towarde hector hath courſe ytake ſpere ran full ryght hector fyrſt hyt ſuche might harneys ſperes head zantyhus fell grounde deade death grekes ſore cōplaine dyd myght buſy payne euery halfe furyous wood auenge troyans bloud paſſyng cruell hardyneſſe gan troyans tho ſo ſore oppreſſe many one day ne myght aſterte breſt yperced herte dead ſlayne amonge preſe amonge whiche cruell achylles slewe lychaon eutorbyus noble knyghtes ryght worthy famous ycome countre agayne grekes helpen citie troians cōſtrained ſo narow ſpere quarell darte arowe hector wounded throughout vyſer face lyke ryuer red bloud downe began rayle harneys auentayle wherof aſtoned whan ſyght full many troyan toke hym flyght cyte faſte gan drawe chaſe full many one ſlawe myght efte felde remewe euer one grekes ſewe vnto walles almoſt towne tyll hector troyan champyowne knyghthode gan taken hede albe wounde ſore gan blede yet manhode gan recomforte maugre fyelde reſorte namely whan inſpectiowne walles toures towne heleyne heccuba quene ſyſter fayre polycene many lady gan beholde hym thought anone herte gan colde ſhame knygytes ſhulden flee lyke lyon crueltee made theim tourne manly euerychone waye meteth meryon grekyſhe kinge nygh allye achilles bookes ſpecifye ſworde hector ſmote ſo bodye clouen hath two achilles ſawe deade parted atwo euen fro head hēt ſpere thought ne would fayl hyt hector ſhelde plate mayle rode tho full enuyouſly myd ſhelde ſmet cruelly ſtroke hector neuer adell remeueth ſat ſo faſte well ſwerde anone taryeth nought achylles enuyous thought knyghtly ran vpon courſere creſte ſhone ſo bright clere ſuch myght hector hath hym ſmyt perced throughe baſenet raced eke auentayle ſtroke many pece mayle achylles conſtrayned nede maugre myght ſtagre ſtede enclyne bowe backe whiche tyme hector hym ſpake ſayde achylles well aduerte great enuye thy cruell herte ſpecyally thou haſte well ware therfore counſayle thy ſelfe put ſo farre aduenture one thynge playnely enſure deſyre luſte ſome daye fyelde yf mete may truſt ryght wel gayneth ſocour ne ſhal acquyten thy labour mortally vnderſtande ſworde holde hande thy life thou ſhalt thēſ • eſcape cruelly vengeaunce ſhalbe take efte whan mette euen vpon thy head ¶of thyng whan achylles toke hede aduertynge herde ſayne ryght wolde haue anſwered agayne ¶vorthy troylus knyghtly entred made ſonder twynne manhode companye worthy knyghtes tho dyd guye hyghe proweſſe owne might hath grekes put agayne flyght ſlayne day dread syxe hundred knyghtes ſothly reade loſſe whyche grekes faſte gan flee tentes neceſſytee tyll menelay dyd buſy cure make fyelde agayne recure whoſe manhode yt day doute worthy knightes fyelde grekes recured anone ¶but tho fro troye came kyng odemon haſt poſſyble may came enbuſhed vpon menelay hym vnhorſeth ſelfe place ſuche wounde gaue hym face death wende eſcape doubtles anone hym take helpe troylus lad vnto ye towne grekes ſuche preſe came downe reſcue hym great nede ¶that odemon myght tho lede kyng menelay towarde cyte whan dyomede came meyne many worthy rydynge hym aboute troylus mette amonges al route ſodeynly hap aduenture hath vnhorſeth eure anone hent ſtede bad ſquyer ſhulde lede vnto cryſeyde onely ſake beſechynge ſhe wolde take gyfte owne man syth day loue wan amyd fyelde great myght hym whylom owne knight haſte waye went therof made vnto preſent ¶prayinge full humble wyſe lyttell gyfte ſhe deſpyſe receyue remembraunce pleaſaunce pitye womanhede ſeruaunt called dyomede remembre become knyght ſhe anone harte glad lyght full womanly bad hym repayre agayne vnto lord playnly hym ſayne ſhe ne myght kyndneſſe womanhead gentylneſſe refuſen hym platly grace ſtraunge place kynde founde ſo comfortable euery thynge ſeruyſable may lykely mynde thynke hym ſo true kinde ¶with anſwere meſſager gone vnto lorde tolde hym anone worde worde lyke ſhe hath ſayde therof full well apayde hym thought playnely herte recured paynes ſmerte forth hym armes knyght ¶but day duryng ſtronge fyght troye ſo manly haue borne grekes myght ſtande aforne tentes haue thē chaſed ne kyng agamenowne grekes driuen clene fyelde whiche thyng anon behelde came vpon many worthy man tho new ſlaught agayne began euery halfe vpon large playne grekes haue troyans ſo laine efte agayne haue fyelde ywon troyans canſtrayned tho begon leſe lande tyll pollydamas whiche knyghtes beſyde gan fall vpon endlonge grene troye full manly ſuſtene grekes gan ſo enchace whan came loſte place ſtronde euen vpon ſee thrugh knyghthod made thē fle lyfe dread whiche miſchiefe whan diomede behelde ſawe pollydamas mortally purſued chaſe horſebacke fyelde yfere cruell herte hent anone ſpere ſpryngyng rode hym full ryght agayne tacquyte lyke knyght lyſte partye fayne ſtede helde agayne reyne ¶and raught ſpere threwe reſt dyomede ſmote ſo breſte mortally lyke founde hym vnhorſeth greuous wounde ryght anone knightly herte pollydamas attones ſterte vnto horſe dyomede reyne proudely gan lede ¶vnto troylus foote ſtode forbathed grekes bloude euery halfe whiche ſhadde amonges ſo knightly ne myght endure ſuſtene ſharpe ſworde grounde ſo kene ¶and delyuer maugre foen ſadell vp ſterte anone force armed vnwarely aduenture caſe ſharpe ſwerdes none whette achylles together mette worthy troylus rancour pryde achylles ſmote fell ſyde downe horſe lowe grounde notwtſtanding grene mortal woūde roſe agayne faſt gan hym ſpede myght recure agayne ſtede nought wolde auayle ſodaynly freſhe battayle troye made mencyon compaſewyſe beſet hym enuyron eueryche armed bright clene hector tho furious tene ¶as dare telleth maner howe ſame daye thouſande knyghtes ſlowe whiche withſtode onely diffence achylles maken reſyſtence tyme death ſtandyng ieopardye certaynly yf bokes lye lyklyhode myght tho eſcape miſchyefe dead take hector hym ſo furyous ¶but read kyng thelamonyus reſcued hym great nede cauſed hym recure ſtede notwithſtandyng diſdayne duke lorde athene caſe herte hole entent helpe achylles wonder dylygent hym ladde many noble knyght ¶but bycauſe drewe nyght ſtorye maketh reherſayle made ende battayle troye entred towne made menciowne hauyng delayes mortally foughten thirtye dayes without lette interrupcyon outher parte great deſtruction aldermoſt nathles great pryde loſt moſt grekes ſyde ¶saue pryamus loſt ſpecyall syxe ſonnes called naturall made great dole heuineſſe ſtorye lyketh expreſſe mene whyle hector certayne face wounded agayne thus haue cruell rage euery parte receyued great domage tyll pryam hath troye ſent downe trewes vnto agamenowne ſix monthes aſſente wolde therupon hath counſayle holde lordes beſte echone accorded therto graunte axynge concluſyon ¶and whyle within ylyon durynge pea outher parte aſſured woundes fully cured ¶lay worthi hector protector towne ryche royall chefe doungeowne ilyon troye bare name whiche buildyng ſuche fame ſhuld commende vp downe dare doth diſcrypciowne wante cunnynge termes aplye boke doth ſpecifye worlde newe ſo ryche hyghe deuyſe buildyng lyche whiche ſtode delyte ſayth twelue ſtones whyte alabaſtre ſhortly conclude twenty paſe latytude grounde ypaued thrughout wt cryſtall vp hyght performed euery wall ſtones man fynde dyamountes ſaphyres inde royall rubye ſo oryent lyght derkeneſſe dymme nyght enchaced beames ſhene euer amonge emeraudes grene ſtones maner man worlde deuyſe recken pryſe value richeſſe ther wrought large gret roūdnes ſayth dare iuory pyllers thervpon ſet corner pured golde aboue hyght ymages wonder huge weight many perle many ryche ſtone euery piller halle one maſſyfe golde burned clere bryght wonderfull man ſyght worke merueylous faſſhyon lyke eſtymacyon thynge ymade founded fayrye worke wrought fantaſye wytte man lykelyneſſe bokes dare doth wytneſſe lyke recken ſyght apparaunce thynge celeſtyall seeth boke ye get wrytynge myght neuer ſe albe dyd excelle therof thinke nowe telle retourne agayne pryamus whiche whyle inly curyous myght buſy cure ordeyne ſepulture ſonnes afore dead ¶and tyme ſycke laye dyomede loues ſtripe wounded herte felte inwardly ſmerte woful ſyghes whiche breſt abreide full ofte adaye loue creſeyde ſhake feuer newe cauſed hym full pale hewe wexen megre poore lene pyteouſly gan hym abſtene meate drynke ſolace ſene deadly face ofte daye wolde complayne diſſeaſe mortall payne prayinge grace ſhe wolde ſe vpon woo haue pytye mercy taken hede ſeruaunt onely womenhead playnely elles ſeye ſake ſayde wolde deye ¶but cunnyngly full ſleyghty wyſe kepe hym lowe vnder ſeruyce delayes ſhe helde hym forth hande▪ cauſed hym ſtande full vnſure betwene hope diſpayre whan grace ſhuld haue repaire put hym heuyneſſe daunger newe brought hym diſtreſſe diſdayne encreaſe payne double ſhe brought trayne woman holde man full narowe whan hurte cupydes arowe ſette many fell aſſayes day day put hym delayes ſtande vnſure betwyxe hope dread ryght creſeyde lefte dyomede entent ſette hym fyre woman kyndly aye deſyre whan man haue brought traūce vneuenly hange hym balaunce hope dread lynke hym chayne fyne vnſure bothe twayne dryue hym forth yeres ſerue force lyue ſterue fyne loues fyry rage ſhe wolde haue hym ſeruage locked hym vnder ſuche keye wote lyue deye wherof doubte thus lette hym dwell forth wyll ſtory tell matter eke reſorte agayne myne auctour recordeth certayne trewſe wered gone twelue dayes ſuyng one grekes haue faught wt thē towne great damage confuſyowne outher partye aduerſyte whyle great mortalyte ſworde peſtylence amonge grekes fatall influence noyous hete corrupte eyre engendred tho great diſpayre theyr lyfe fyelde leye day day ſodaynly deye wherby theyr nombre faſt gan dyſcrece whan ſawe ne wolde ſece theyr aduyſe kyng agamenowne trewſe ſent vnto towne thirty dayes priamus kinge without abode graunted axynge ¶how andromecha dreame forwarned death huſbande hector day folowing entred fielde wher ſhe admonyſhed therto hauing reſpect next day ſlain achilles capitulo xxvii vvhan moreyne wofull rage peſtylence began aſwage trewſe wered gone grekes caſte meten foen vpon day plate armed clene whan phebus roſe beames ſhene full pleaſauntly gan ſhede lyghte ¶but fynde tofore ſelfe nyght andromecha faythfull trewe wyfe worthy hector hym louyng lyfe gette chyldren two wonder ſemely inly fayre alſo ¶and lamedowne called tone yonge tother ne myght gone ¶and aſtyonax read hyght fetured well paſſynge fayre ſyghte guydo lyſteth endyte moder pappes whyte yonge tyme ſuckynge arme breſtes embraſyng ſhe nyght made mencyon ſlepe wonder vyſyon note ſothe may neuene outher dreame veryly ſweuene fro aboue reuelacyon whylom kyng scypyon ſhewyng outher oracle goddes warnyng myracle ſothneſſe ſlepynge ſhe laye thought playnly nexte daye ¶hector went fomen aſſayle wonte armed battayle ne ſhulde eſcape vtterly fate hondes falle fynally ouermore attropos ſhall fyne euermore lyues threde twyne ſhewe force fell myght parodye worthy knyght proche ſhall without wordes mo fyelde playnly go aſtoned ſtrete ſhort breth ſhe laye abrayde vpon death ſyghe ſtynte ſlepe pyteouſly braſt wepe conſtraynte herty ſorowe ſpecyally wofull morowe ſhe ſawe ſtocke worthineſſe wonte manfully hym dreſſe arme hym ſtele borned bryght troian wall hector worthy knight fete fell downe lowly declaryng vyſyowne quakyng herte womanhead wherof god wote toke full lyttle hede therof hygh indignacion platly affyrmynge diſcrecion truſten ſuche fantaſyes dreames ſhewed gladly meinte lye full iapes illuſyons whiche playnely concluſyons elles folkes delude albe ſo theſe people rude therin ſome whyle haue affection iudge deame oppynion dyuerſly may pretende ofte falle happen wende foloweth lyke concluſyon dread whiche lamentacion encreaſe gan andromecha ſwone fyrſt ſhe cryed ha sayinge ala myne owne lorde ſo dere trewe wyfe ala nyll ye whyche ſo faythfull hoole affection deſyreth aye ſaluacyon vp ſhe roſe deadly vyſage lyke woman caught ſodayne rage kynge
