pryam hecuba quene haſte ſhe went ſelfe mene wyfely herte trewe ſtele ceryouſly declared euery deale pyteous dreame myracle onely deuyne oracle yſhewed goddes purueyaunce tolde eke fynall ordynaunce fortune falſe diſpociſyon fully purueyed deſtruction lorde without delaye fyelde yf go daye ¶wherfore ſhe prayeth deadly hewe vnto kynge mercy rewe vpon wo haue compaſſyon ordeyne hyghe diſcrecion lordſhyp ſoueraynte lorde may deſtroyed reckeleſhead wylfulneſſe worde kyndneſſe aye ſo moche loue founde tofore quene ſowne fell grounde ſayde ala deadly chere helpe caſe myne owne mother dere womanhead routh grace lorde fyelde ne pace deuer motherly pytee benyngnely goodly ſe knyghthode hygh proweſſe reſtrayne renowmed nobleſſe ylke day handle ſpere ſhelde go armed fylde ¶and twayne aſſent beſte condeſcende vnto requeſte fynally accordynge one whē wardes redy euerychone ¶on yſſuynge troylus fyrſt all▪ parys next grekes fall ¶and hym troyan eneas kinge sarpedan pollydamas kyng eroys kyng epyſtrophus eke kyng ycalled forcyus plate mayle eueryche armed clene alderlaſt came kyng phylomene withall kynges lordes renowne deffence come towne grekes knyghtly debate ¶and pryamus ſothly gate conueyed theyr goynge ſet wardes noble worthy king full prudently ſapyence gaue congee lycence vpon grekes proue myght agaynſt full redy fyght fomen royall apparayle amyd fyelde abydyng battayle ¶but pryamus meane whyle lyke guydo remembreth ſtyle thylke fyne ye haue herde ſayne whothy hector repayred agayne hym contermaundyng ne ſhuld gone thilke day fyght agayne foen whyche thynge hygh deſpyte brent whan ſawe lordes went gate alone abode whiche wexed furyous wood hooly cauſe arettynge wyfe cheietie ſo tender lyfe puttyng fully occaſyowne abydynge day towne preiudyce worthyneſſe diſencreaſe hygh proweſſe leeſt tongue hygh eſtate falſe reporte derogate caſte anone full knightly herte lyfe death ſhulde hym aſterte within fyelde daye founde though ſo wt many mortall wounde ſhulde peces hewen ſonder vpon playne diſmembred yonder hole manhod herte ſette anone without longer lette agayne arme hym full dyligent agayne precept commaundemente father rode waye feare whyche anone ſhe would deye wife newe crye gan ſhoute papes alſo hangynge oute lytell chylde armes twayne tofore lorde gan wepe playne beſechynge routhe pyte ſo would vnto ſorowe ſe leaſt wyfely trouthe manhode haue herte routhe vpon childe vpon alſo whych ſhe bare armes two might criynge kepe whan ſawe wofull mother wepe knelynge downe vnto ſhe ſayde ſobbynge ſhe might abrayde mine owne lorde haue mercy lytell chylde whych ye ſe pyteouſly afore wepe crye haue mercy lorde v dye haue mercy eke vpon cite myne owne lorde haue mercy cruell death paſſe ſhall echone lacke helpe ala ye gone ¶this crye andromecha eke ſyſter caſſandra ¶hecuba fayre pollycene heleyne eke luſty freſhe quene atones fell beforne heyr vntruſſed weping torne loude gan crye place beſechynge mercy grace thilke daye abyde towne hert haue compaſſyowne complaynte wofull mone sith truſte towne alone abode reſyſtence agaynſt death chiefe defēce onely affiaunce ſuerte ſuffyſaunce eche thinge theim might greue ¶and yet ne might herte meue abyde yet goodlyheade beſought womanheade would encline herded herte ſtele might lytell droppe fele onely pyte woo rewe lykly renewe fynally deſtructiowne cite lykewyſe towne death ſoth ſhulde fully ruyne yet might enclyne ne would concluſyon indurate harted lyon alwaye continuinge rage whoſe herte might aſ often aſwage nother prayer lamantacion reſtrayne opinion euery peryll layde hath aſyde waye gan anone ryde wife none bote rage kinge ſhe ran amaſed mortall wo ſhe vnneth might ſpeake diffaced rewefull ſight hewe knoweth wight loſte ſhe bothe might ſtrengthe plat ſhe fell grounde length tofore kynge routhe ſene ¶beſechinge entente full clene grace conſider wolde wo helpe hector ago ſeynge faythfull womanhead requeſt raughte anone ſtede pricked onely ſake ſo great haſte hath ouertake worthy hector within cite hent reyne great difficulte maugre made tourne agayne ſuche wiſe durſt ſayne albe full lothe therto prayer force alſo ſtede made alyghte areſte eſchewe ne myght ne would agayne father ſtriue albe felte herte ryue melancolye hertye yre diſdayne newe ſet fyre inwardly ſtered blode lyke tygre lyon wood depriued newly praye right ſo fared ylke daye lyke bore tuſkes whette whyle grekes troye mette furyouſly walkynge vp downe diffence ſothly towne troylus fyrſte baye ſtede aduenture mette diomede eche ſurquedous pryde ſharpe ſperes gan togyther ryde guydo ſayth without dreade one bothe anone deade ne menelay knightly go betwene furyous tene ſmette horſe full knyghtly wyſe ¶and mereon mighty kinge fryſe menelaus marked hath full well wyth ſwerde ful ſharp groūd ſtele vnhorſed threwe hym grene ſtroke might tho ſuſtene menelay ſo wood lykly euen ſtode lyfe ſhoulde thenſe eſkape grekes ful haſtely theim ſhape meryon ye haue herde ſayne ſette rounde vpon playne ceſſe auentayle euery parte cruelly aſſayle deſtytute wofull caſe ¶but helpe came pollydamas knightes gan nighe nere ſawe taken pryſonere maugre vpon ſette theyr handes pollydamas fette whoſe reſkues ſo great ſtrife many one therfore loſte lyfe grekes rather ſhoulde eſcape handes haſty rape caſte theym playnly ſhoulde dead fully purpoſe haue hadde head ſtode miſchyefe ſo great diſioynt ſelpe euen vpon poynt ¶came troylus moſt knightly arraye manhod made ſuche affraye amōges reſkuſe kinge maugre theim cominge deliuered mighty kinge fryſe cruell death ye haue herde deuyſe thervpon came thelamonyus proude armes euer ſurquidous thre thouſande full worthy euerychone vnhorſeth pollydamas anone among knightꝭ proudly bare hī downe ¶but troilus hath thrugh hie renowne myd foen get horſe agayne troye ſo ſore belayne euery halfe throughe grekes pryde ne might afore theim tho abyde newe newe hardy achilles aſſayled theim myrmydones compelled neceſſyte miſchyefe made flee home walles gate towne great domage confuſyowne theyr partye abacke ſo gone ¶the whych thynge margaryton behelde ſawe howe game gothe herte gan wexen wrothe paſſyngly haue diſdayne ſtorye recordeth certayne bothe hardy famous ſonne alſo kinge priamus noble knight great worthineſſe ſawe miſchyef diſtreſſe theim troye add gan fle caſte anone auenged vpon achilles great might ran full lyke manly knight horſe backe townes ſake enforſeth achilles take amyd felde amonge knightes ¶but achilles ala ſhould befall daye ſlewe cruell aduenture troians mightē endure felde holde homeward gan thē hie mortally maken noyſe crye firſt death margaryton ¶and purſuyte king thelamō made chaſe hys crueltye home gate troye cite ſlewe killed alwaye rode albe parys manly withſtode brethrene baſte borne al ground haue lorne lefte forſake vtterly felde home wēt brought ſhelde dead corp margaryton theyr gate ſhette anone whych miſchiefe hector gan beholde yre herte gan wexe colde ſayd platly without delaye would auenge death ſame daye made haſte ſtede fet vp ſterte baſenet vnwyſte kinge lefe lothe gayne forthe anone gothe tyll paſſed gate towne furyous tygre lyowne whoſe coming thick ſwarme tofore ſworde grekes gan fleen thought tyme withdrawe fyrſt finde hath ſlawe two worthy duke wyth theim met buſy waye let one ycalled eurypalus ¶and hyght halcydius ſo troians felde agayne haue newe manfully begon grekes ſewe folowe traſe yet myſchiefe dan pollydamas ſame tyme grekes take hector hath ſo borne ſake foreſt belayne thrugh knighthod reſkued hī agayne put grekes ſo great diſtreſſe manhode worthineſſe ſo euer thylke daye rode ſharpe ſwerde bathed bloud ſo cruell ſo merciles ¶but knight called leothydes shope anone hector mete moſt yrous hete ſet full preſumptuouſly hector tho deuoyde mercy anone ſlewe threwe felde whych thinge achilles behelde great ſlaughter woundes wide hector made vpon euery ſyde gan anone compaſſe herte vp downe caſte aduerte grekes neuer maye ſure agayne foen fyght endure kepe felde theim ſtryue whyle hector alyue wherfore caſte ſhope many weye engyne hector might deye auauntage might finde ¶and therto eke pollicenes inde worthy duke alſo aſſent onely herte hole entente hope ſtode ſyſter wyue loue felte herte ryue grace better ſtande caſte fully take hande high empriſe haue tolde moſt bolde hector ſlew none gayne whych anone achilles hath ſeyne yre wexed herte wood bore tygre theyr cruell moode vpon hector auenged furyouſly gan fle ¶but hector caught quarel ſharp ygroūd threwe gaue ſuch wound throughout thighe vpon ſyde felde might abyde withdrewe anone wente men home vnto tente made anone ſurgeyn binde mortall wounde fynde whan ſtaunche ceaſeth blede haſte agayne toke ſtede leeſt wounde deade afterwarde great dreade thought fyrſt auenged vpon hector might ſe happe ſorte yf would fall thought paynes hym beſte remedye hande might dye lyfe routhe mite ſo hector might acquyte deathe deathe concluſyon holy entencion deſyre fully ſuffyſaunce death vnwarely gyue miſchaunce ¶but time hector vp downe wonte playeth lyon amonges grekes many ſondry place ſwerde gan theim ſo enchaſe death might hī ſeen fledde afore like ſwarme none ſo hardy wythſette grekiſhe kinge mette hap aduenture whiche ſothe cote armure embrouded full many ryche ſtone gaue lyght ſonne▪ ſhone full bryght cleare ioye ſene perles white emerawdes grene full many one therin ſette cercle baſenette rounde enuyron auentayle veluet fret aboue mayle saphyres ynde ſtones red whoſe arraye hector taketh hede towardes faſt gan drawe fyrſt fynde hath hym ſlawe force manheade hente vp afore ſtede faſt gan wyth ryde wardes lytell ſyde good leyſer playnly maye ſpoyle ryche arraye full glad lyght newe empryſe ala falſe couetiſe whoſe gredy fret great pytee hertes may lightly ſtaunſhed etike draweth ſo great diſtreſſe defaceth high worthyneſſe full ofte ſythe theſe conqueroures theyr fame rente away floures deſyre hauynge gredy thuoght hygh nobleſſe ſothly longeth nought ſuche pylfre ſpoylynge robberye appartayne worthy chyualrye couetyſe knighthod lere one chayne maye knet yfere kouthe ofte ſuche rauyne hath cauſe roote ruyne many worthy ſo lyſt take hede lyke ye maye nowe hector reade ſodaynly brought endynge onely ſpoylynge ryche kinge deſyre hadde horſe backe whan ladde rekleſly ſtorye maketh mynde caſte ſhelde backe behynde welde ſelfe lyberte haue oportunyte ſpoyle wyght ſpare hys breſt diſarmed bare except plate diffence agayne ſtroke maken reſiſtence ala tho ſo reckles floure knighthod māhode pereles foo ylke daye alone awayte ſo laye miſchiefe hate enuye fielde might ought eſpye achilles cruell venymous hertye moſte melancolius whych couertly houing beſide ſawe hector diſarmed ryde hente ſpere ſharpe grounde kene yre hatefull tene vnwarely hector might aduerte ¶alas ſmote herte throughout ye breſt dead fel adowne vnto earthe troian champyowne neclygence onely ſhelde death odemon behelde worthy kinge might hym refrayne ¶but achilles rode payne hit ſo amyd preſe maugre might myrmydones dead guydo ſayth certayne wounde fel grofeling ye playne knightes ſhelde alofte ylayde caryed full ſofte vnto tente haſte leue deadly wounded man full ſore ſycke tyll maye releue drewe eue troye great reuerence laboure theyr diligence dead corp carye towne worthy hector whē titan went adowne temple dolefully wende daye wofull ende thus longe night heauineſſe ſkill ryght theim leue agayne retourne matter helpe theym mourne ¶the complaynte lydgate death hector ca xxviii bvt nowe ala ſhal forth procede ſtorye wo dreade fele hande bothe tremble eke quake oh worthy hector onely thy ſake thy deathe ſo lothe wryte oh ſhall helpe endite vnto ſhall clepe call certys none amonge muſes accorde ſingen euer one pernaſus beſyde helycon aungelyke theyr hermonye tunge none may ſpecifye great ſweteneſſe theyr goodly ſonge diſcorde founde theim amonge theyr minſyke entuned ſo ſytte theim nought helpe wo mater yt mourninge ſhente tragydyes tore rente camplayninge pyteouſly rage theatre dead vyſage theim ala clepe dare crye troubled penne grace guye nother clyo callyope ¶but alecto theſyphone megera euer doth complayne lyue aye wo payne eternally torment dwell cerberus depe downe hell muſt praye gratious matter ſo furyous wyght comlaplayninge drery feare ryght well ſyttinge matter meynt heuyneſſe accordeth well cheare dreryneſſe allyed vnyte ¶wherfore helpe nowe thou wofull nyobe drery teare thy piteous payne penne dolefully rayne ¶and helpe alſo thou cruelly yxione belydes dothe bokette gone thy ſtone helpe thou secyphus thy ryuer helpe eke tantalus hunger haſte ſo huge pyne wofull playute helpe fyne buſyneſſe ſtocke roote worthyneſſe knighthod groūd māhod ſoures well tofore bare away bell derrynge floure high proweſſe exaumple alſo gentilneſſe neuer could amiſſe ſeye ¶alas hector ala ſhuldeſt thou deye oh cruell parchas toke ye hede cruelly twine fatall threde ye haſty ala ye ſo namely threde ye brake two thou attropos thrugh thy gret enuye oh troye ala well mayſt thou wepe crye make wofull lamentacion whych haſte newe thy confuſyon loſte thy diffence thy ſtronge wall thy berer vp thy ſuertie royall thy honour chiefely begonne ala ala thy bryght ſonne eclipſed ſtandeſt thou deſolate comforte diſconſolate thy lyght loſte thou derckneſſe yplounged arte ſothefaſtneſſe worthy thou haſte worthyeſt daye yloſte knightlyeſt ſhall enſure euer borne whylſe worlde may dure wonder though thou wale ſore daye daye complayne euermore thy ſhelde bothe ioye wo thou wonte loue ſo tenderly thy hole herte maye lyghtly aſterte haue euer thy remembraunce ſothe fully thy ſuffyſaunce ¶for guydo maketh mencion man dwellinge towne ne hadde kindeneſſe loue lyſte expreſſe childe lefe haue dyed caſe heyre ſo well beloued goddes fate deſtyne diſpoſed might haue woman alſo euery maner age deathe fall ſuche rage cite aboute euery ſtrete ſobbinge ſalte tearꝭ wete heyre rente deadly wo furyouſly ronnen fro mortall aduerſyte beholde ala pyte yonge maydes lykewyſe matrones olde sobbe ſyghe fyſtes folde loude crye ſayde fynally ala nowe ſhall father cruelly ſyght ſlayne day day ala man ſhal ſay nay farewell helpe nowe hector ygone ſureneſſe v euerychone wonte reſte dead ala ¶of body whan caryed preſence pryamus kynge anone loſte offyce ſpeakynge gan ſelfe ſalte teares droune pyteouſly therwith fell ſwone vpon corp cold ſtone inly deſyrous deye anone without tariyng laye ¶but force rente awaye brother eke token hede tryſte pale ſorowe well nyghe dead haue ſelfe rage al torne neuer trowe ſene aforne brother yet ſuche care eche theim ſelfe gan fare would haue dyed corſe theyr life platly gaue forſe grounde many ſorowes ſore lyke wilde bulles gan crye rore routhe theyr deadly wo ſene herte ſtele myght ſuſtene ¶what ſhall ſaye hecuba quene ſyſter yonge pollycene caſſandra prudent wyſe wyfe ſorowe deuyſe whiche rent ſelfe torment wo fynally wolde ſelfe cruell deth ſo wepe wayle yf ſhulde maken reherſayle wryte ſorowes complaynges pyteous ſobbyng ſorowes wepinges wofull cryes pyteous ſownes drery plaintes lamentaciownes wo ſpecyfye large volume wolde occupye eche thynge ſhulde order tell trowe longe dwell man tedyous many day lere woman wepte afore corp lyinge ſelfe defacyng complaynynge wonder myghte endure haue ſothly nature kynde wepe playne ſyghe ſore teares rayne tyll tempeſt wofull rage may proceſſe lyt lyt aſwage thus lette ſygh ſorowe make cely woman clothes blake ſhroude face wimpled vaine matter retourne againe tell playnely kyng pryamus herte inly deſyrous caſte awaye entencion corp kepe corrupcyon whiche naturally men taken hede corrupte muſt ryght nede kyndly diſpocyſyon may made none oppoſycion aboue grounde body lye reaſon muſt putryfye yf crafte aboue nature vncurrupte may endure ¶wherfore kyng ſhope hym ordeyne preſerue hole fro thynges twayne odoure abhomynacion therwith eke craftye operacyon ſlyght founde horrible lyefly viſyble eye apparaunce lyke quycke exiſtence coſte kyng wyll ſpare nought made anone afore hym brought craftyeſt mayſters towne suche moſte diſcrecyowne perfourme axynge curyouſly obeye byddyng faythfully theyr wyll entyer dylygence temple moſt reuerence towne whylom dedicate full yore alſo conſecrate appollo olde foundaciowne beſyde gate ſtandyng towne ¶called tymbrya troyan tongue ſtorye red ſonge phane ſpeake made fyrſte hyghe aultere great deuyſe lyttell oratorye perpetually memory ſette ryche receptacle made maner tabernacle egall ſyght large ymage reyſed ryche ſtage borne eche corner pured golde vpon foure pyllers eueryche full craftely ydyght aungell ſtode golde borne bryght ceryouſly worke ſuſtene craftye archys reyſed wonder clene enbowed ouer worke cure merueylous celature rofe cloſure enuyrowne fyne golde plated vp downe knottes graue wonder curyous fret full ſtones ryche precious euery kynde man deuyſe royally ſo thryfty wyſe derckeneſſe blacke nyght beames clere lyght enchaced dyden ſhene fro grounde vpryght lyne degree men aſcende made ſo well man coulde amende worckmanſhyp euerychone performed vp cryſtall ſtone attaynyng vp table baſe ſtandynge reſtynge ryche crafty tabernacle hauynge aboue vpon eche penecle ryche rubye reyſed hye hyght stode ymage huge large weyghte maſſye golde hauyng lykeneſſe worthy hector gan face dreſſe towarde grekes tho dyd ſtonde aye thretyng ſworde honde amiddes great rycheſſe haue yſet good auiſeneſſe dead corp worthy knight ſyght man ſtandinge vp ryghte ſubtyll crafte lyuynge face cheare quicke lokinge coloure ſouthly hewe beynge freſhe roſe newe lyke ſuppoſayle liued apparayle ¶for ſtede lyke tolde thrugh ſmall pipꝭ wrought made golde meaſure enbowed downe entre made crowne great aduyſe ſubtilte eche partye extremyte body craftely porrecte nerfe ſynewe driuen directe ſecrete pore craftely extende wherby lycour might downe deſcende kepe hole fro corrupcion withouten tranſmutacion hyde hewe parte tourne head golde vrne fylde bawme naturall ran pipe artyfyciall necke head many place penetrable vaynes face thrugh vertue force licoure conſerued liuely coloure freſhe hewe quicke nothynge pale mightely bawme auale compariſoned ſemblable ſoule vegetable whych without ſenſybelyte miniſtreth life herbe floure tre ¶and ſemblably euery vayne corp vertue attayne breſte arme ſpredinge enuyron moyſture diſcencion hande foote ſouthly reade bone ioynt gan vertue ſhede diſtillinge mightely flete fete full gummes ſwete viall ſtode tempred bawne ymeynt proceſſe may waxe feynt daye daye encreaſe amende vapoure vpwarde gan aſcend cauſinge ayre enuyron delyſe reſemble paradyſe ſauour holſome ſoote odour gumme ſpice roote pure golde foure laumpes light tofore corp brenninge daye nighte oyle ſothe credyble crafte made extinguible ne might mine auctour ſayth certayne nother queint tēpeſt winde rayne proceſſe waſten yeares whiche ayre bryght bourned wire full craftely reyſed lofte whoſe ſwetenes men reioyced ofte theyr courage lyked theim full well whē worke complete eueridell rounde enuyrowne ful ryche freſhe ſe ¶they made parcloſe eban tre ſo longe laſte maye dure tree onely nature cutte ſmelleth wonder ſwete maye waſte brenne hete though layde amonge cole red midde flawme many fiery glede conſumeth though men aſſaye ful ofte water houeth alofte kyndely thenſe grounde goth ſwymme heyght ſoth loth lyke alſo teacheth plynyus tree whylom paſſyngly famous ſo hyghe pryſe reputacion large myghty regyon worthy lande ethyope inde yore agon folkes fynde tree ſo great honour gaue trybute emperour ¶as remembred antiquite golde yuor ryche tree theſe gyftes famous royall quyte theyr dette hym ſpecyall ¶and whan pryam full thryfty wyſe performed hath ye haue herde deuyſe ryche worke noble excellent herty loue beſte entent ordayned eke guydo tell certayne nombre preſtes dwell ¶in temple deuocions contynually deuoute oryſons ¶for ſoule hector preye goddes ſpyryte lyſte conuey eternally dwell yfeare ioye blyſſe aboue ſterres clere ¶to whiche preſtes ye kyng gaue manſyons abyde poſſeſſyons whiche hath mortyſed perpetually haue herde deuyſed whyles knele praye wake caſte fully ende make fynally thirde boke rude maner vndertoke whyles troye wepe morne vnto grekes wyll agayne retourne dulle ſtyle ſtory trace onely borne vp ſupporte grace thus endeth thirde boke ¶how grekes depoſyng agamenon ordayned pallamydes general armye cap xxix hector thus deade ye haue herde ſaid achylles tent ylayde woundes mortall freſſhe grene vpon morning ye ſon ſhene enchaced away derke nyght ¶agamenon wyſe worthy knyght workes paſſyngly prudent hath haſte lordes ſent aſſembled euerychone within tente ſayde anone ¶syrs quod lordes kynge prynces duke eke yfere ye aduerte clere inſpection ye ought echeone hygh deuocyon hooly herte goddes herye inwardely ryght merye ye conſydre wyſely take hede ¶how enemye hector dead whylom berer vp troye full truſte honour ioye hoole deffence protection vnto v death confuſyon vnlykely euer haue victorye whyles lyfe floured glorye againe whoſe ſworde mighten auaile ſlewe aryuayle ye remembre fyrſte day ¶the noble kyng called protheſelay nexte ſhall fayne patroclus parted euen twayne fyelde amonges v euerychone slewe eke worthy kynge menon archylogus alſo prothenor eke kyng hyghte alphynor phyllys alſo kyng epyſtrophus ¶and ende brought zantypus meryon myghty ſtronge kyng waye came rydynge ſlayne hath kynges two ¶cedyus doryus alſo polyrenes ſtronge polybete letabonis kynge phylete manly knyght kynge iſydyus ¶and eke kynge called humerus ire cruell tene worthy kynges ſlayne hath eyghtene whiche hyther came grekes lande power myghty hande ¶nowe laude honour goddes whiche cauſed haue fall dead encreaſe ioye diſcreſe foen troye ſhall fynde experyence laude alſo preſe reuerence fortune v hath holpe wele tournyng double whele hyghe comforte conſolacyowne v echone ſyttynge enuyrowne ſtonde nowe parfyt ſykerneſſe deth yt dyd v ſo oppreſſe may waite towne deth deſtructiowne haſtely ende wo truſte hector go without may longe endure wherfore may fully v aſſure purpoſe hole ſhall acheue fynally daunte ſo greue vnto ſhalbe importable one aſſent ſtande ſtable partye tourneth wrake hope fully put bake diſpeired nonſecurytye vtterly citye shall weer death depende ſoth ſhall day day amende helpe god ſea lande victorye redy hande deuoyde platly ambyguyte excluded eye ye may ſe wantruſt foreyne dread counſayle procede ferther vpon foen ryde prudently whyle abyde kepe v cloſe paſſe boundes ¶tyll achylles heled woundes echone myghtye vyolence shal thē oppreſſe haue diffence haue ſayde helpe achylles let v nowe ſende peace two monthes kyng pryamus ſo lyſte graunt v lyke playnely ſhall whyle flawme funerall conſume may deade bodyes pale lye abrode euery hyll vale whiche reporte haue repeyre day day infecten ſo eyre throughout fielde engendryng peſtilence ſtynke ſo great vyolence ¶and whyle may eaſe reſte woundes cure ſemeth beſte ¶and aſſent therto euerychone vnto troye meſſageres gone haue trewſe graunted kynge repeyred without taryinge thereof made full relacyon grekes afore agamenon ende home tent euery lorde doth wende whyle trewſe endureth peace amonge grekes kynge pallamydes cumplayneth ſore agamenon ſo domynacyon aboue hauyng enuye day melancolye hyghe deſpyte indignacyon full inly fret yrous paſſyon gan breke rancour ſhewe certayne ſygnes though ſpake fewe tyll day wyſe agamenon conceyued hath highe diſcrecyon hooly thyng thought ne wold ſpare fro poynt poynt hym ſelfe declare whan lordes together preſent tofore owne tent noble worthy kynge full circumſpect euery maner thyng nought rakell melancolyus attempraunce inly vertuous well auyſed wonderly prudent whan knewe meaning entent conceyte pallamydes haſtye rekles longe abydyng thrugh prudence reſo • within boundes diſcrecion whoſe tongue ſapyence reſtreyned neclygence haſty ſpeche ſothly rape myght make worde lyppes eſcape vnaduiſed nothyng aſterte fyrſt examyned herte aye ſpeche ſo thryfty wyſe conueyed doctryne wyſe vnder reyne wyt hyghe prudence fourme eloquence alway ſo ſayde reaſon went aforne worde tale lorne ¶and wyſe ſhewynge ſentence tofore open audyence sayde euen thus whan peace vnto kynge called pallamydes ¶sothly quod ſo ye take hede ſemeth playnly nede auyſedly lyſte aduerte muſen ſo grutchen herte hoſte haue gouernaunce wyſely conſydered euery circumſtaunce eſtate whiche man may denye wolde maner neuer occupye tytle free election interrupt medyacyon brocage roted vpon mede aye vnder meynt fauour falſhede depeinte coloure trewe entencion might ſupport ſuche falſe ambicion ¶of whiche thyng wyll quite tofore wyte wyſe ſo hyghe offence ſtande clere conſcyence without ſpot ſuche vayne glorye touchyng eſtate whiche tranſytorye ¶yet neuertheleſſe haue cure wyt helpe procure euery thyng touchyng comentie perſeuer myght proſperyte hauyng eye inwarde ſyghte vnto eſtate euery maner wyght commytted gouernaunce great laboure buſy attendaunce indifferent vnto hye lowe helpe foſtre might knowe ſtode myſchyefe neade daye nyght taken hede beſte coulde aduyſedneſſe aye dylygent none felle diſtreſſe ſothfaſtly ſo loke aryght dayes thought watche nyght herte inly aduertence without fraude ſlouthe neclygence faythfully full myght acquyte euery maner wyghte lyke eſtate without excepcion man iuſtly reaſon greke nowe lyue vnto gylte may duely aſcryue falſehede engyne trecherye loue hate fauour flaterye cauſe named ſpecyall haue lyke egall one buſye payne man hath mater complayne partie hye lowe eſtate deuoyde rancour debate amonges haue deuer generall thyng partyculer hyther toward nothing hath miſcheued god wote well ſhuld haue agreued herte ſet pryſe haue choſe diſcrete aduyſe domynacion haue ſubiection eaſe herte tranquillite lyke lordes degree wyll fully haue obeyed lyke one vtterly haue deyed quarell haue vndertake deſtyne ſo yſhape ſaye ſoth full loth fayne ouermore alſo ye playne choſen without aſſent meruayle ſyth ye ne preſent longe yf ye remembre ryght towarde troye waye dyght ye conſyder nere ye came paſſed full two yere ſo longe abyde commyng byn muche grekes hyndryng paſſyng harme full great damage huge lettynge vnto voyage yf without wene ¶on commynge taryed athene lykely ye well ſaye naye haue yet vnto daye ye thought credyble eke affyrmed impoſſyble grekes ſhulde maner wyſe dare take great empryſe abſence manly acheue wynde nothyng leue ſo none offence grekes haue without preſence thrugh force water lande full many thynge parformed wt hande acheued worthyneſſe one thyng ye geſſe ſaye degree ſhulde herte ſo reioyſe lordſhyp great eſtate pompoſe elate chere porte occupye acquyte trewely lye deuoyde ſuſpection wyll make reſygnacion tofore excuſe nowe auiſed diſcretly ſe ye lyſt haue agayne morowe prime without ſettyng longer tyme prolongyng forth delaye thus made ende daye went waye onely night tyll morowe yt tytan ſhad lyght whiche tyme counſayle generall grekes helde moſt ſpecyall lordes congregacion haue tolde election mette yfere ¶agamenon anone ye ſhall heare sayde euen thus ſadde countenaunce lo ſyres quod touching gouernaunce haue hadde dominacion haue therto hole affection clene entente buſyneſſe euery thinge might wilfulneſſe encreaſe perſeuer contune recorde take god fortune whych haue conſerued cauſe floure felycyte honour high nobleſſe stande hole ſounde yet ſykerneſſe whyle fame moſt flourynge ſemeth ryght well ſyttyng myne eſtate fully reſygne specially fortune beninge ¶for ſo many nowe preſent knowe ſelfe onely inſuffycient without helpe bere charge men muche may ouerlade barge namely tempeſt rage ſyth ye ſo diſcrete ſage burthen let releued man therwith agreued let v one entencion without ſtryfe diſcencion choſe ſuche one moſt acceptable echone moſte couenable gouerne diſcrecion echone hole affection aſſented ſpeke generall men may ſe naturall men delyte thynges newe truſte people faynt vntrewe aye vndiſcrete full doubleneſſe varyable ſykerneſſe aye awaytyng opynyon chaunge tranſmutacyon selde neuer ſtandyng hole one day loue morowe gone full ſelde ſykerneſſe onely newfangelneſſe hath embraced affection haue ſtede agamenon newe choſe onely fauour ¶pallamydes gouernour grece lyke deſyre haue sceptre hole empyre called aboute euery coſte onely emperour grekes hooſte ryght tofore agamenon fyne concluſyon day parlement euery man went lodgyng home ryght way ¶but tente wounded laye hardy knyght fyerſe achylles whan herde pallamydes poynt poynt election diſpleaſed opynyon playnly thought aduyſe agamenon paſſyngly wyſe diſcrete vnto gouernaunce tother pleaſaunce ſayde none election maner ſubrogacyon bycauſe hym ſelfe parlement cheſyng preſent arettyng paſſyng great offence choyſe made abſenee wherwith herte inly wrothe ſo lefe loth concluſion ſtrength ſtode election ¶howe kyng pryam perſonne iſſued batayle thaduēge hector death dyd ryght valyauntly cap xxx trewſe paſſed ywered wounded eke recured aboute nexte morowe pryamus herte inly deſyrous grekes manly fyght hector death tauenge myght olde pryam knightly fyelde whan troyans ſelfe behelde great hygh courage hym ſo ferre yronne age gan reioyſe plucke vp theyr herte ſpecyally whan gan aduerte great manhode worthyneſſe liuelyed hyghe proweſſe ſake euery maner man gan arme haſte pryamus day lyue deye hundred thouſand fyfty towne lyke dare maketh mencyowne worthy knyghtes euerychone without pryam gone ¶and afore went deiphobus parys nexte pryamus menon kyng worthy eneas alderlaſt came pollydamas fynde ſterne full pryde pallamydes came tother ſyde fyelde many ſtronge battayle fyrſte eche gan aſſayle kynge pryamus knyghtly way cheſe wardes pallamydes hym vnhorſeth thrugh hye renowne lyke knyght kylleth bereth downe proude grekes ſo rode none ſo hardy ſworde abode ſo narowe gan coharte wardes made ſonder parte ſo felle furyous daye dyd dedesfull meruaylous armes wrought wonder ſene maruayle may ſuſtene ſo great age fyelde tendure credible enſure ſe howe great myght grekes put proudely flyght ¶and deiphobus alſo behynde agayne foen knightly fynde acquyte ſelfe make thē go backe sarpedowne eke lacke yfallen neptolonius proudeſt greke moſte ſurquedous moſt famous ſtrength myght whiche agaynwarde rode ful lyne ryght serpedowne ſpere rounde delyuerly ſmote hym grounde ¶but sarpedowne full yrous herte without abode fete vp ſterte ¶and neptolonye yre hote thrughout thighe wt ſword ſmote ¶and anone kyng perce lande ſo worthy famous hande sarpedowne whan toke hede knyghtly hym reſtored hath ſtede ¶not withſtandyng menelaus vpon hym paſſynge deſpyteous hym eke duke athene encloſed haue amonge great preſe kynge perce ala ſhulde befall ſlewe hym amonge ¶full knyghtly fought lyke champyowne multitude encloſed enuyrowne ſelfe alone ala deſtitute mortall caſe thrugh whoſe miſchefe troy towne gan withdrawe tyll sarpedowne hath holpen recure lande full many greke kyllyng hande ¶and kyng pryam ſo manly founde ſonnes called naturall whiche vpon hym ſo rode longe daye manfully abode departynge playnely ſyde kynge togyther ryde full mortally grekes confounde pryamus many cruell wounde hath ſlayne many worthy man horſebacke amonge ran none day yonge olde troye towne ſo hardy ſo bolde none eſtate hath ſo well hym borne amonge grekes ſo well hath hym worne poynt poynt reken euery thynge hath pryam noble worthy kyng alone confuſyon grekes deſtruction outter miſchiefe diſcomfyture afore whoſe face myght endure thynges two mortall yre inwardely haue ſette hym ſo fyer harty hate bare olde vnto grekes double many folde death remembraunce worthy hector contynuaunce whiche platly worthyneſſe ſworde ſhope hym redreſſe fret hate conſtreynt peyne veryly thylke thynges twayne whiche daye ſo loke ryght force doubled myght thrugh toke ſo cruelly vengeaunce grekes brought outtraunce thrugh knyghthod put thē ye flight ¶but grekes attones dyd myght aſſent aſſemble one ſleyght ſyde gone playne large fayre ſe betwene pryam troye cytye fyne onely entenciowne hym debarre entre towne euery waye grekes haue ſet troye tho let repayre ſtorye telleth thus ne manhode priamus whiche anone lyon ſtronge ſworde gan ryde amonge ſeuered large woundes wyde ſlewe tho wolde ſword abide euery endelonge playne ¶and paris eke hath ſo belayne myghty ſhote ſtronge archer purſuite theſe arbalaſters ne might ſhote ſo kene mortall harme abide ſuſtene gan anone fle place kinge priam ſo narowe gan thē chaſe great nede neceſſite ſlaughter cruelte ſworde ſharpe whet grounde greke felde yfounde fledde awaye eueriche tente troye cite wente bycauſe drewe faſte towarde night phebus hadde bereued light ¶and ſo honour high victorye worſhip eke laude memorye perpetually palme alſo ¶priam kinge hath wonne mo daye releaſe ſorowe ¶and reade next morowe hath yſente troye towne trewſe agamenowne graunted ſelfe daye prime albe therof reherſed tyme howe longe laſte boke expreſſe ¶during theyr buſineſſe hertye laboure inwarde diligence ordayne great reuerence corp worthy kinge perce lande without taryinge kingly honour troye towne shall caryed regiowne buryed predeceſſours kinges progenitours whych thinge complete ye aduiſe aliſaunder called paris firſte corp enbawmed richely conueyed full ſolempnely write guido huge route knightes ridinge aboute triſte heauy cladde blacke echone chare right way gone towardes perce ledinge kinge dead corp towarde buryinge halowed like eſtate royall ¶and feaſte funerall holde alſo great deuociowne ¶of worthy hector within troye towne like cuſtome vſed tho dayes rite paynym layes feaſt made mencion fro yere yeare reuolucion yhalowed ſpace fourtnight many flawme many hydous light brent enuiron ſentuarye called aniuerſarye came aboute yeare yeare certayne daye theyr kalendere whych cuſtome remembraunce people ſhoulde continuaunce playne wepe alſo praye reade theyr frendes afore deade ful piteouſly theyr heyr torne mourninge black kneling aye aforne dead corp worthy knight time ſo paſſinge mighte done trewſe dure grekes truſtely might aſſure theim liſt good liberte without daunger enter cite daye daye troians might alſo vnto grekes frely come go whiche time full great delite hath achilles caught appetite entre ſe maner towne without wiſedome dtſcreſciowne beholde playnly ſe hoole maner ſolempnite forthe wente certayne daye towarde troye haſte maye vnarmed ſothly mine auctour ſayeth without aſſuraunce fayth except trewſe ſo lyefe lothe firſt temple gothe apollo halowed feaſte throughout towne downe vnto leſt cleped anyuerſarye ye haue herde ſhuld longer tarye many worthy preſent therat amid temple high lowe eſtate lordes ladyes affecciowne euery parte gathered towne ¶now corp worthy knyght freſhe colour kept vnto ſyght lyfely eke quicke hewe beholde roſe newe vertue onely gummes ſwete bawme gan aboute flete euery ioynt eche extremyte ¶and feaſt ſolempnyte hecuba yonge pollicene womanly goodly ſene many high eſtate lowe tofore corp ſyttinge rowe heyr vntruſſed cladde wedes blake euer one ſuche ſorowe make routhe pyte ſene howe playne death bimeane worthy hecor knighthod groūd well ¶but trowe ye guydo lyſt tell pollicene wofull rage ychaunged hath vpon viſage natife coloure freſhe ſighte roſe lelye white freſhenes lippes red al teares ſhe gan ſhede chekes criſtall cleare heyr alſo reſembling golde wyere whych laye abrode like vnto ſighte phebus beames ſphere bright whan v doth light auale aye ſhe rente finger ſmale golden heyre blacke wede ¶of whyche thing achilles toke good hede gan meruayle greatly thoughte god kinde euer might haue wrought theyr workes ſo fayre ceeature thought might endure beholde brightneſſe face felte herte pace perſinge ſtreames eyen two cupides darte hath marked ſo loue deſyre brente hote dothe fyre ſoonewith ſodayne ire quoke alwaye fixe loke arowe god cupide hath perced euen ſide herte gaue ſuche wounde neuer likly ſounde aye one loke caſte durſte gan preſe faſte towarde namely eye thought muſt nedes deye founde ſome grace gayne playnly yt place newe caughte loues ſnare healthe welfare deſpeyred herte ſo ne knewe beſte eche thinge well aſſure ſet nought toke cure thought mo longe daye thus wente fro tyll phebus cheyre lowe gan decline golden axetre ſo clere ſhine ſaye ſonne wente downe whan hecuba quene troye towne ¶and doughter pollycene alſo temple paleys go ¶and aye achilles ſighte might till lacke lighte maye haue leyſure oportune loke curſed fortune haſte maked hath wente knightes home vnto tente anone without taryinge bedde goeth full tryſte complayninge aye ſelfe caſtinge vp downe minde eke reaſowne head foote beaute euerydell herte felte knewe ful well fynall cauſe languyſhynge pollicene beaute moſt paſſinge loue ſo muche pay ne felte heat thought hert melt aye bedde walowinge fro conſtreynt hidde wo almoſt thought deyde ſelfe euen thus ſeyde ¶alas quod howe wo begone ſorowe knowe ende none ſuppoſe ſith worlde began ne neuer wofull man whylom ſo great myght renowmed euery maner wyght throughout worlde high lowe none ſothe could know man armes famous yet yholde victorious tofore time remembred ſtile vnto daye ala harde nother hector playnly none pollicene worthy brother power mette theyr might ouerſette felde force daunte pryuely dare auaunte ¶but nowe ala mayde tender age hath ſodaynly brought ſuche rage ſtreames eyen twayne perced hath clouen euery vayne herte maye aſterte dead thrugh conſtreynt ſmert ¶for ſhall nowe wiſhe teache ala ſhall nowe leche ala ſhall helpe ſaue death graue hope playnly none saue mercy ala gone nother prayer treaſour rycheſſe force might nother high proweſſe highnes bloud byrthe kinrede maye auayle helpen nede meue ſadde trouthe vpon wo euer haue routhe ¶what newe furye inportune rage hath brought hertin ſuche outrage agaynſt whych nowe debate ¶to loue beſte deadly doth hate ¶and good fayth wyſely lyſte aduert lytell wonder though ſhe hate herte syth come hither fro ſo ferre kinrede make werre whyche confuſyowne knightly brother moſt worthy renown haue fatally mine handes ſlawe whych worlde felowe worthyneſſe manlyheade ala ala nowe maye quake dreade lyfe fallen diſpeyre howe ſhoulde bolde haue repeyre dare ala come theyr ſyghte woful wretche vnhappy wighte howe ſhall hardy appeare preſence eyen cleare certys ſe none mene weye fynally muſt nedes deye diſpeyred ſtande euery ſyde helpe con prouyde ryght anone ſcaldinge ſighes depe achilles braſte wepe deadly cheare pale funerall face tourned wall routhe pyte ſene hertye furye paynes kene ſo oppreſſed thoughte lyfe death rought nought continued till drewe nyght titan hath withdrawe clear light euer one like wofull man ilyche like coloure pale wan without ſlepe ſo fretinge ſorowe ¶tyll lucifer next morowe tofore ſonne beemes cleare full luſtely gan appeare oryent whan achilles vnpacient wythout reſte peace quakinge aye feuer newe ſene playnly hewe tyll abrayde anguiſhe ſodaynly called one pryue counſayle truſteth well vnto telleth euerydell fro poynt poynt howe ſtode ſent forth bycauſe could good meſſage ſtreyght troye towne full aduiſe informaciowne mattere hecuba quene wiſedome mene ſo might diſcrecion finde waye ſaluacion vnto lorde loued ſo quene anone go matter wiſely gan conueye tofore grace would preye ſhe enioyeth gyue audience tale none offence ¶he foole newe lere wherfore quene goodly gan euer liketh ſayne word yloſt ſpoke vaine tale man could amende craftely gan diſcende ſubſtaunce tolde clerely oute premiſſes full well brought aboute fynally concluſyon chiefe ſayde entencion effectuelly would make peace vnyte atwene grekes folke troye whych thinge knewe better weye werre alder eaſe witte prudently appeaſe mortall ſtryfe bytter rage allyaunce onely maryage lyſt wiſe worthy quene ¶that doughter fayre pollicene maye wedded vnto achilles theyr might fynall pea hecuba diſcreſcion wytte medyacion prudence might brynge pryamus fully aſſentinge ¶that achilles might doughter wyue might parfourmed blyue lyke tofore made mencin couenaunt onely condicion grekes ſhall theyr werre lete ſuffer lyuen quyete maryage theſe ylke twayne parfourmed knyt vp chayne ¶and ye quene hath knowen entēt full ſoberly good aduyſement tofore worde aſterte full pyteouſly ſhe ſighed herte laſte ſobre cheare euen thus ſhe ſayd meſſagere frende quod ſhe touchynge thy requeſte make beheſte leſte condeſcende lyeth bringe ende thy lordes wyll herte entiere herevpon muſt fyrſt requere kinges wyll lyſt aſſente purpoſe whych thou arte ſente ouermore muſt wytte alſo parys willynge eke therto whych thynge euery circumſtaunce wyll ſelfe maken enqueraunce ¶full faythfully priam parys meane whyle theyr aduyſe without within dayes thre whiche time come againe achilles ſo ſende fynally thou ſhalt knowe ende matter aunſwere playne home goeth achilles agayne ¶with full glad cheare lorde pleaſe ſet hert better eaſe auyſedly high diſcreſcion hath ſo made relacion tolde tale ſo thrifty wyſe could wordes ſo deuyſe brynge hope lordes herte full releſe paynes ſmerte wherby made ſorowe withdrawe thus whyle hope gan adawe ¶amid breke hecuba quene ¶to priam ſpake pollycene touchinge ſonde achilles profre make peace tolde forgate nothinge wherof aſtoned priamus kynge spake worde halfe houres ſpace ſelfe gan inly compace full prudently might meane achilles would haue pollycene vnto wife aye wonderynge laſte ſyghinge wonder ſore hath diſcloſed conceyt herte ſayd ala howe ſore doth ſmerte remembre may haue peace great offence achilles towardes playnly slewe worthy hector crueltye hooly vpon euery ſide hoole aſſuraunce gouernour guyd mine platly ſayne therwithall myne eyen twayne alone ſothfaſt lyght shelde protectour thrugh great might manhode agayne mortall rage grekes werre croked age ¶but nowe ala confuſyowne ſlayne ſo worthy renowne achilles maye minde herte neuer fynde allyed mortall foo roote grounde ſorowe woo full harde herte appeaſe loue cauſeth mine vneaſe euery halfe cruel foen proude grekes harted echone agaynſt nowe fortune contrayre tourned newe quarell apayre cauſeth grekes wood furyous ala preſumptuous ¶onely hector berafte awaye ſythen choyſe maye agaynſt herte though anger ryue matter aſſaye ſhall ſtryue though lothe ſytteth full ſore yet eſchewe harmes lykly hereafter fall ſaue myne ſonnes conſente achilles moke trewe fynall peace atwene grekes alſo cite without playnly howe haue vnto wyfe doughter pollycene ¶but leſte treaſon meane firſte ſo wende beheſt make ende wythout fraude mine aduiſe ¶to whych counſayle aſſenteth eke parys rather concluſyon made none excepcioon ¶in trete quene heleyne menelaye neuer ſhoulde atteyne recure agayne vnto hys wyfe whyche parys without noyſe ſtryfe grutchynge vnto entente within ſelfe fully aſſente therby hopynge without feare dreade perpetually heleyne poſſede right luſte man ſhall ſaye nay vpon thirde daye ¶achilles hath wytte mattere hecuba ſente meſſingere ſhe tolde aunſwere kynge ceryouſly gynninge endinge aſſenteth well therto ¶and parys eke ſhe ſelfe alſo ſo playnly ſhe tolde touchinge peace purpoſe holde fyrſte heſte brynge aboute ſure therof nede doubte ſhall haue purpoſe euerydele worke prudently wele herevpon informaciowne meſſenger troye towne without abode haſte maye achilles helde ryghte waye tolde hole effect mattere alwaye feruente entiere herte brent hole glede ſawe none way ſpede onely peace ye haue herde telle ¶and aye breſt ſighes gan ſwel loue pollycene caſte alwaye amonge throe kene purpoſe waye fynde whyles buſy mynde ſhoulde purpoſe brynge aboute ſelfe caſteth many doubte ¶anone diſpayre rage vp ſterte cruelty caught hym herte whych hath throwe ſuche thoughe power beheſte fulfyll dede except hadde well leſſe dreade euery thinge put certayne wening greke would luſte fayne deſyre varyable ſelfe thus fauorable parfourme nothynge denye luſty fantaſye maner louers euerychone ſuppoſe acheue anone thinge lyſt take hand diſioynt matter ſtande though impoſſyble theyr foly aye ſo credible ſo achilles truſteth fynally fulfyll heſtes vtterly suppoſinge aye worthyneſſe manhode hygh proweſſe whych ſelfe gloryfye pryde ſurquedrye grekes ſhoulden deſpayred theyr truſte theyr might appeyred vpon troians wynnen lande ſo withdrewe hande helpe theim therwithall alſo home grece wolden go ſyege onely ſake quarell vterly forſake ¶but ſo daye fyerſe achille theym abode cite ſpylle whyche thinge lordes aſſente aſſembled heren entente amonge theim thys achilles byddinge pallamydes gathered yfere tofore theim lyke ye ſhall heare achilles hath tale begonne ſayd ſyres ſo muche konne wyſedome high prudence renowmed eke ſapyence throughout worlde diſcreciowne ſo worthy alſo renowne kynges duke whoſe royall name eaſt weſt floureth yet fame knyghthode manlyhead ſaye pray taken hede ſaye yf ye conſyder playne entent commyng hyther good auyſe entencyon grounde founded reaſon cauſe roted maner ryght ſo ye lyft vp ſyght aduerte clerely mynde full ferre backe wytte ſet behynde prudent lokyng aduyſeneſſe fyrſt whan foly haſtyneſſe toke vpon v come ſo ferre agayne troyans gynne werre ieoparte lyues euerychone loue one man alone ye wote trowe meane ¶kyng menelay defrauded quene telle trouth lyſte feyne ye well wote onely heleyne groūde gynnyng debate ſo many worthy eſtate recurleſſe remedye lyfe good haue put ieopardye landes lefte eke regyownes cyties alſo ryche townes whiche abſence ſtonden deſolate wyues chyldren eke diſconſolate woe abyde mournynge diſtreſſe whyles ſoth expreſſe day day beſet euery ryde lye felde death abyde ſorowe care labour wo ye wotte well alſo sith fyrſt tyme werre began grekes many worthy man hath loſte lyfe thrugh deathes fatal woūd hytherto haue myght lyued ſounde home grece aſſured well ioye ne comen vnto troye remembre full great pyte ¶and ouer ſaye alſo amonge troyans cruell mode haue ſo moche loſte bloude hath full ofte made pale hewe ¶this day alſo grene newe hector ſuche mortall wounde quarell ſharpe grounde aboue thygh ſo kene head ſame daye afore dede happe yſhape death vnneth might eſcape whiche yet freſhe vpon ſene large wyde yet grene ſmerte whiche yet ful ſore cōplayne ¶and good fayth ſemeth heleyne ye aduerte wyſely thought ſuche pryſe ſhulde nat haue bought lyfe good yfeare honour yput dreadfully hangen ballaunce yf ye remembraunce conceyue aryght caſten vp downe ſodayne chaunge reuoluciowne fallen hath ſyth werre began ſlaught death many worthy man ſake hath loſte lyfe yet worſte mortall ſtryfe doth moſte rebounde damage diſencreaſe eke diſauauntage lykely dayly ordenaunce made therfore remedy ſhape outher ſyde fyne onely heleyne abyde troye ſtyll towne let v caſte good inſpectiowne eaſe ſome maner waye ¶so kynge called menelay cheſe hym wyfe ſome londe lyke eſtate ſuraunce bonde vnder wedlocke confyrmed vp newe vnto hym wyll founde trewe syth without gylte ſynne may law heleine twyn dyuerſe cauſes ynowe thrughout ye world euery wight yknowe auoutry foule vyce lawe preiudice ¶though menelay iuſtly forſake whan ſo lyſte take ſhall hym better queme pleaſe ſo v ſhall full great eaſe whan werre brought ende whiche lykely many man ſhende ſo forth contune great labour ſo importune ne ſhall whyle mowe ſuſtene ſoth withouten wene troyans yet flourynge myght wt haue full many worthy knighte helpe hye lowe degre therwithall ſo ſtronge cite euery parte without eke within lykely wynne purpoſe though euer abyde wherfore wyſedome let v voyden pryde wylfulneſſe onely prudence haue eye aduertence profyt vaine glorye honour ſhineth victory wyſedome withdrawe honde sith may conſtrayne bonde fortune whele abyde ſtable wherfore rede ſhe become mutable gery goddeſſe double chere let v gyue vp ſuche thynge lyeth whyles may alder worſhyp ſaue werre laude yet haue conſyder well manhead ¶our moſt foe hector dead whyle honour floure counſayle fortune loure ſayd ere chaunge bryght face whyle beſte ſtonde grace one aſſent one oppynyon without contradiction herte wyll one honour partye pall grece home returne longer ſoiourne quarell haue longe ſewed doutles may eſchewed full great damage without fayle haue done ſhall folowe tayle wherfore beſte folye vp reſygne whyle hap welfull benynge moſt blandyſhynge face fayre tyme beſte make repayre whyle ſtande party enmyes honour perygall fer aboue playnly coulde haue eye felicite whyle aſcencion ¶but leſt ſome man wyll make obiection may ſo honour ſaue repayre playnely haue helayne agayne cauſe whiche thynge anone anſwere ſhall ¶if man fantaſye diſhonour vyllanye arrecte wolde maner kynde go home leue behynde shortely ſaye holde ſhame syth haue one great name ¶as heleyne byrthe good amonges v ycome kynges bloud ¶syſter pryam lorde troye towne ¶exiona thelamowne kepynge hath ſhall feyne troye towne parys hath heleyne ſyth nowe may none let tone ſet agayne tother ſurplus olde enmyte betwyxe v troye cite counſayle eaſe one aſſent wyſely appeaſe ſome hence wende tale ende ¶to anone kyng menelaus yre wood furyous ¶and kyng thoas duke eke athene myght longer hym ſuſtene ſuffre hym ſo reckles spake attones vnto achylles onely inpacyence courte perturbed without prouydence tumulte gonnen repreue ¶this achilles proudely cōmeue agaynſt hym opynyon ſayde ſhortely concluſyon vnto read ne wolde aſſent condeſcende nothyng mente gouerned caſe ¶for whiche thynge anone achylles full yre rancour herte ſodaynely ſee ſterte went waye rage tryſte pale wood vyſage ſhortly ſayde lyke fayne ne wolde longer payne helpe ſo ſpede agayne troyans maner nede ¶and bad anone hardy achilles knyghtes called myrmydones ſpere ſhelde helpe grekes entre fyelde kepe thē cloſe home within thetr tente thus yre gaue commaundement men ye haue herde deuyſe withdrawe euery hygh empryſe whan ſo euer go battayle whyle ſcarſeneſſe vyttayle fell hooſt fleſhe bred wyne many greke brought vnto fyne ne myght endure diſtreſſe conſtreynt hunger dyd thē ſo oppreſſe ¶tyll laſte kyng pallamydes nothynge reckeles hath therupon made purueyaunce remedye redye ordynaunce aſſent counſayle echone ¶he hath ſent wyſe agamenon worthy ſtyng meſſa beſyde lyttell ile onely prouyde grekes myght ſpede releue great nede ¶and thelephus kynge lande gentylneſſe hath put hande large wonder free renowmed muche humanite ſuccour commaundyng aye anone purueyours haſt gone euery party aboute enuyron landes regyon faythfully ſerche euery coſte take vp vytayle grekes hooſte ¶and full haſtely made ſtuffe ſhyppes playnly lade euery thynge neceſſarye grekes water carye requeſte kynge agamenon without taryinge delacyon ¶and ſo kyng plente vytayle fraughte ylade gan anone ſayle towarde ſyege meynee aye coſtynge grekyſhe ſee ¶the wynde good kyng blyue nauye troye dyd aryue fewe dayes grekes anone ryght repeyre full glad light exployt good ſpede ſo well hath borne nede ¶and pallamydes anone ſayth guydo ſhyppes gone conſyder loke aboute nede within eke without amende repare lyſte coſte ſpare euery thynge without neclygence touchynge charge dylygence tyll trewſe fully ronne werres newe agayne begonne whiche many man ſothly dere abought ceryouſly wryte howe wrought purpoſe playnly ſentence vnder ſupporte pacyence dvrynge one deadly cruell hate ſtynte may ceſſe date atwyxe grekes towne great damage deſtructiowne outher parte felynge full vnſwete tyll daye caſte mete wont proudely wt ſpere ſhelde wardes entrynge fyelde armed full bryght vpon outher ſyde ¶and enbatayled ſtoute full pryde full knyghtly haue choſe ground take large baners wynde yſhake tyll togyther ſodaynly haue mette ¶and alderfyrſt deiphobus hath ſette freſhe luſty herte yrous ¶vpon kyng called creſeus enuye ſtorye telleth horſebacke together ran ¶deiphobus fyrſte ſpere blyue throughout breſte euen dyd hym ryue vnto herte ſpake deth grekes playne ſore loue ſuche woe make aſtoned haue fyelde forſake gan anone vnto theyr tentes flee whiche ſothe troye ſee vpon chaſe faſte gan ſpede vnto tyme worthy dyomede ¶and eke kynge pallamydes hye deſpyte cruell mercyles twenty thouſande worthy knyghtes al vpon troyans ſodaynly fall mortally made leſe waye reſorte home agayne troye ¶and eke grekes felle furious ſame tyme came thelamonius hyght ayax ſtronge knightly man lyke lyon amonge ran vpon troyans ouer ſette caſually waye mette ¶cecylien luſty freſhe lyght tyme wonder manly knyght ſonne pryam rede thelemon pryckyng ſtede slewe cruelly ſworde anone raſynge arme ſhuldre bone ala fell dead fyelde deth whō whan deiphobus behelde wodder anone tygre lyon ſpere rauhe thelamon ſmette ſo plate bright force made hym lyght leſe ſadell ſet amonge preſe ¶the whiche ſtroke whan pallamydes behelde ſawe clerely gan aduerte irous wood furyous herte caſte hym anone auenge thelamowne deiphobus full worthy renowne mortally guerdon quyte ſpere grounde byte sharpe kene large rounde ſquare full cruelly ware harneys without areſte ¶deiphobus ſmote ſo breſte ſtroke brake ye ſhafte two tronchone head alſo lefte breſte waye fynally muſt deye none helpe remedye wounde ſo cruell mortall lyfe myght abyde ¶and whyle parys came beſyde auenture whyle deiphobus wounde ſo inly anguyſhous gan haſt approche nere face pale right heuy chere diſtreſſe wepte pyteouſly knightes commaunded haſtely wounded brother ſyde ſofte feare haſt ſhulde forthwt beare wardes great preſe vnto payne releſe brethe hym leyſer auente open eyre vnto hym wente maugre grekes wounded bare full eaſy paſe towarde walle faſte towne great dole lamentaciowne full ſoftely grounde hym layde tyll laſte deadly man abrayde mortall loke face funerall pyteous ſo eche ball gan tourne vp deadly eye euen thus parys gan ſeye oh brother myne loued ſo haue pyte rewe vpon wo kyndneſſe brotherheade wordes routhe take hede syth death muſte ſonder twynne ¶for attropoſe ſhal longer ſpynne lyues threde knotte breke wherfore brother praye wreke vpon deth henſe pace thou lyſte ſuche grace kyndneſſe yet deade breſte ſperes heade rent away thou auenged vpon foe truſte may wyt dead ſpyryte paſſe fynally fyrſte diſcende depe downe helle eternally pluto dwelle myd boundes derke byn lowe fynally ſo may knowe dead ſaye gyue force ſoone deye ¶to whoſe requeſt parys toke good hede▪ fyelde faſte gan hym ſpede thought woe pyteouſly wepynge whyle brother laye lanquyſhynge awaytynge onely death vpon poynt yelden vp breth ¶and knightes parys vp downe wardes ſought enuyrowne ¶tyll laſte pallamydes fonde sarpedon fyghtyng hande hande king worthi sarpedown come defence troye towne whiche hande noble knight whyle full myght ¶moſte buſy pallamydes preſſe lyke lyon whetted woodneſſe pallamydes herte ferde let flye hym ſharpe ſworde myghtely wonder thygh parted hath ſonder ſmote herde bone ¶that sarpedon fyll downe dead anone troyans whan ſlawe compelled force withdrawe purſuite kyng pallamydes whiche vpon ſo merciles cruell wood lyon ¶after death kyng sarpedon whiche ala whan parys dyd eſpye marked hym cruell eye hente bowe paſſyngly ſtrong arowe tyller longe entoxycat venym head ſmote therwith dead hytte hym ſo auentayle throughout ſtuffe thicke mayle throte gan pace fell dead ſelfe place ¶pallamydes manfull worthy knight grekꝭ toke flight made noyſe wofull crye death complaynyng wonder piteouſlye lorde myghty gouernour late choſe emperour chiefe ſocour ſoueraine refute ala ſtonde deſtitute gouernaunce broke diſarayed without guyde ryght ſhepe diſmayed diſconſolate comfortleſſe yſhent eche flyeth vnto tente troye ſued chace horſebacke wonder huge pace merciles ſlewe fle euery ſyde pyte ſe without mercy grace lyke lyon gan enchace tyll compelled neceſſyte conſtrayned cruelte tourne agayne ſelfe diffende troye downe anone diſcende horſebacke euen vpon playne attones none gayne gan grekes proudely outraye cruelly ſo diſamaye fynally gayneth diffence mortall mighty violence troyans grekes ſo diffoyle alderfyrſte leyſer diſpoyle grekes tentes golde rycheſſe whiche time troylus gan dreſſe parys eke downe nauye thirtye thouſande companye kyllyng tho playnly mette ſhyppes wylde fyre ſette wall troye cyte men myght well hydous flawme ſe ¶and gone deſtruction ne ayax ycalled thelamon manhode knyghtly excellence come anone made reſyſtence grekes many worthy knyght tho new began mortall fyght atwene troyans grekes ſtoute red bloud raylyng aboute vpon playne ſo hydouſly blede length brede dead maymed full pale ſyght vpon ſoyle full many noble knyght atwyxe ſo cruell hate fyght togyther debate wylde bore euen ſo fare none lyſte ſpare fyelde worthy thelamowne knyghthod high renowne manly bare hym grekes deffende mā might manhode amende thrugh ye world though men ſought day perſon hath wroughte meruailes armes thrugh great might ſothneſſe grekes anone ryght without hym fynally ſhent ſhyppes attones loſte brent purſuite parys day ¶and worthy troilus yt made ſuch affraye amonges hygh proweſſe fyfty ſhyypes guydo doth expreſſe loſte brent thelamowne reſkus came knightes downe vnto ſea remenaunt ſaue troyans daye haue hygher hande mortall fyght force great myght troylus hath ſo many ſlaine grekes ſoth fayne withdrawe fielde lete abydyng fonde full vnſwete wherfore gan leſe place ¶amonge kinges ſonne trace heber hyght wounded death ne myght vnneth drawe breth ſpere breſte ſtyckynge ¶to achylles came complaynyng vnto tent euen laye whiche fyelde daye ¶for ſake onely pollycene loue ſo ſharpe kene aye herte ylyke grene newe heber mortall hewe complayneth ſore arrettyng cowardyſe manhode trewandyſe day myght ſo ſhame withdrawe ſelfe hindring name fyelde hym full great reprefe grekes ſeynge miſchiefe confuſyon vpon brinke deſtruction abrode fielde ſe ſo lye deade lyſte one take hede knyghthode grekes releue ¶and whyle heber gan hym thus repreue ſpere whiche body ſodaynly drawen ala eye vp caſte rancoure yre full pyteouſly heber dyd expyre ¶in preſence achylles therwith came ſodayne re tente certayne knyght ¶of achylles axeth amonge grekes clerely ſtode anſwered full irours mode certes quod full vnhappely troye haue ſo cruelly grekes daye fyght full ſhamefully put vnto flyghte many ſlayne ala welawaye vnneth none eſcape myght awaye vnhurte maymed withouten wounde fell v troyans yfounde eke ſuche multitude ſuppoſe ſhortely conclude daye opynyowne lefte man within troye towne able ſtande battayle ſpere ſworde enmye aſſayle wene ſoth byn come v fyght ſo huge route ne myght force take hande fyelde agaynſt ſtande ¶but nowe lorde draweth vnto night faynte fyght pleaſyng worthyneſſe manhode hygh nobleſſe take encreſe fame euermore getten name withall owne glorye perpetually memorye ryſe vp arme anone ſodaynely vpon gone feble weake make reſyſtence agaynſt manly famous excellence victours e • er conquerours duryng worlde remembraunce euer brought vnto outraunce ſothfaſtneſſe haue dread ¶but achylles toke hym hede heber laye afore dead full colde ſtrake coloure lyke leade one lyſte gyue hym audience vnto hym haue aduertence may worde herte myne ſayde maken hym enclyne vtterly euen lyke ferde though maner worde ne herde eares paſſed ſowne ¶lo maner condiciowne cuſtome playne vſaunce theſe louers hangyng traunce ¶honour worſhyp manhode proweſſe strength might fame hardyneſſe encreaſe name vertue victorye knyghthode nobleſſe armes glorye theſe myghtye loueley aſyde suche myght god cupyde whiche hertes hye hoke ſeaſe loth playnly diſpleaſe outher chere countenaunce wyll dede diſobeyſaunce theyr ſouerayne lady dere loke eyen clere full well daunte pride venus ſoone ſo prouyde arrowes kene perce nerfe vayne enlace fyry chayne onely importable charge reſtrayned go large whiche cauſe day doubtles noble hardy achylles wolde withouten wene come fyelde drede polycene leſte ſhe offended herte thynge eſcaped aſterte achylles throughe myſgouernaunce whyles hengeth thus balaunce grekes faught twone tyll bryght phebus goinge downe troyans neceſſytye lacke lyght entre citye whyle homewarde repeyred laye deiphobus lyfe diſpeyred compleynyng aye deadly wounde whan parys troylus haue hym found myſchyefe gan wepe crye wolde routhe dye wofull noyſe pyteous ſowne ſalte teares gan renne downe chekes vpon outher ſyde whyles vpon hym abyde wounded man gan drawe ende whoſe ſpyryte redy wende breſt wery goſte full haſtely another coſte deadly eyen tourned vp ſo downe whan knewe relacyowne ¶that parys hath pallamydes yſlawe anone bad ſhulde drawe large tronchone ſtelen head anone fell downe dead corp gan faſte ſpede towarde towne nede dole wryte lamentaciowne made noble sarpedowne cytye namely kynge quene euer wepynge brother ſyſters dere vayne reherſe ¶but pryam hath great dylygence two towmbes royall excellence deyphobus kynge sarpedowne many ymage grauen enuyron many knotte koruen yonder buryed lyttle ſonder lyke cuſtome rytes olde whyles feſte halowe holde called feſte funerall grekes haue make ſpecyall ryche toumbe worthy kyng ¶pallamydes buryinge solempnely made ordinaunce amonges vſaunce great dole pyteous heuyneſſe haue kynge great worthyneſſe royally brought ſepulture ¶and myght longe endure without head gouernour choſen haue emperour one aſſente affection worthy kyng wyſe agamenon ¶and made lettynge troye next day enſuynge wardes fielde gone fully purpoſed fyght foen grekes manly face mette worthy troylus ſo ouer ſette greke none ſhortly telle thilke daye afore myght dwelle cruelly gan chace came rode place fledde ſworde lyfe doubte yonge knightes ridinge aboute suche vſaunt lede euer one grekes bloud ſhede whiche lyke ſtreame diſteined al playne whyle ſo huge rayne ſame day ſo huge myſte euery man hath felowe myſte specially vpon grekes ſyde ſtorme woundes wide manhode troian knight ¶worthy troilus ſo freſhe ſo yonge light coact cruelte maugre might dred death fle tentes ſuccour fynde troyans aye purſuynge behynde iull mortally wiſh ſterne paſe ſtorme ceaſe caſe home repayre eitie ſtronge tyll morowe larke ſonge troylus efte moſt manly battayle grekes newe caſte hym aſſayle ¶and guydo wryt yonge champyowne thylke daye rode vp downe amonge foen hygh renowne ne king duke erle barown ſworde ſo wende lyfe made mortall ende whyle phebus gaue lyght tyll laſte drewe nyght troye repayreth manfully ¶and ſeuen dayes ſuynge lyfe ledde knyghtes felle vpon grekes guydo telle aye newe new gan ſo confounde cruell ſworde ſo kene grounde ne myght mortall tene afore ſyght abyde ſuſtene vengeaunce toke rode weye forſoke traſe renges ſo redde ſoth fielde lay dead whiche ſlaughte confuſyowne grekes new ſent towne ¶for trewſe pryamus kyng anone graunted axynge two monthes fully aſſent lordes parlement wherof made full relacion ¶the enbaſſadours agamenon lodgyng forth wente ¶but vnto achylles ſente meane whyle meſſangers wyſe ſhall anone deuyſe agamenon guydo lyſte endyte lordes ſent achylles vyſyte certayne cauſes lyke ye ſhall whiche ſtorye reherſed vlixes worthy diomede ¶duke neſtor wente playnely reade fyne onely counſellyng herte myght brynge endure hym haue fantaſye wyllynge thorugh chyualrye ſtande hath toforne haue ſo many troye men ylorne lacke onely hygh preſence ¶and achylles dygne reuerence receyued right knightly chere whan ſet yfeare lyke theyr degree anone aduenture ¶whyle vlixes full eloquence gan tale prudently deuyſe ¶to achylles ſaying wiſe ¶syr achylles moſte renowned glorye throughout worlde memorye knyghthode ſhoures wel diſpleaſe ſhall tell noble famous excellence eares let none offence ſhall ſay goodlyhead pacyently ye wyll take hede wordes ſayd herte thought enſure fayne noughte ſaye yf ye remembre wel fyrſt cauſe purpoſe euery dell grekes yf ye haue mencyon fully ſette one entencyon well v pardye whan come fyrſt citye kynges prynces except none whiche ſoth recken euerychone ſelfe ſpeake ſpeciall one fyrſt moſte pryncypall aſſented full troye cite manhode deſtroyed ſhulde perpetually brought vnto ruyne nowe newe note doth enclyne worthyneſſe ſodeynly varye purpoſe contrarye ¶conſyder fyrſt ſo ſage wronges done great damage grekes lande towne conſpyryng aye deſtructiowne ye aduerte wyſely thought ſlayne haue ende brought full many worthy ſyth gone full yore treaſour man may reſtore diſpoyled v brought great diſtreſſe goodes raught golde rycheſſe▪ ſhyppes brent cruelte ala ye lyſte ſe whiche may delayed manhode fynally outtrayed sith ye haue ſlaine hope ſuffiſaūce ¶hector affyaunce fully truſte diffence alſo ¶and deyphobus alſo go lykely apeyred fro day day fynally diſpeyred frowardly fortune loureth honour fame flouteth worſhyp high renowne atteyned hath exaltaciowne hygheſt prycke fortune whele great wronge ye loke wele wylfulnes vnkynde ye ſo frendly fynde frowarde whyle ſhe benynge influence graciouſly aſſygne ſpoukes meue vnto pleaſaunce hap tourne wt plente chaunce whoſe helpe nedeth calle ¶wherfore ala wyll ye ſuffer palle noble fame wylfulneſſe whyle hyeſt worthyneſſe knyghtly prudence ſhulde aſterte whiche thynge euery gentyll herte shulde haue routhe compaſſyon wherfore praye • iſcrecyon ye ſhape purpoſe amende ye wolde herte condiſcende v ſtonde knyghtly werre manhode ſpoke ſo ferre renowne worlde ende reported ſo men wende perpetually freſheneſſe hewe day day encreaſe newe tryumphe hygh victorye put ſtorye eke memorye ſo enprynted foryetfulneſſe power haue malys oppreſſe fame knyghthode derke difface ſhyneth yet ſo clere many place without eclypſyng ſothly leſſe whiche conſerne ye reckeleſſe wylfulneſſe cloude ſo lyght renowne ye whylom ſhone ſo bryght myghty hande manhode wtdrawe conſyder fyrſt grekes yſlawe tofore tent wt mortal woundes wyde fyelde vpon euery ſyde haue diſdayne onely lacke routhe ala whyle lyttle ſlouthe ley honde miſchyefe whylom ſtrōge mighty wall chiefe diffence champiowne souerayne helpe protectiowne ye haue ſo ofte ſhedde bloud agayne foen whan ſtode full myghtely enmyes aſſayle without lyttell may auayle ſoth ne none v echone ye knyghthode lyſte v gone agayne troyans ye wont truſt fynall hope alſo ye ſhall helpe ſocour ¶and hereupon praye ye saye aduyce full wyll ¶and anone hardy fyerſe achylle whan vlixes concluded tale sith face anger dead pale sayde euen thus openly playne sir vlixes ſo ryght ye ſayne haue declared concluſyon purpoſe entenſyon fynally brenne deſtroye royall citie called troye holde ſoth lyketh lye entent grounded folye put v indiſcrecion reckleſhede haſty mocyon lyfe death ſuche ieopardye ſpecyally chiualrye grekes lande ſo ſmale thynge many prynce ſo many worthy kyng haue ieoparted body good yloſte lyfe yſpent bloud might haue ful well home ī peace ¶and nowe kyng pallamydes yſlawe alſo ſayth newe ſo wiſe ſo manly ſo trewe lyfe pryce alone cauſe whiche echone gathered ſo loke ryght grekes many noble knyght haue ſlayne worthyeſt worlde ſeke manlyeſt euery lande regyowne grekes partye ye towne chyualry knighthod ye ſoueraine floure wynne arme worſhippe honour aſſembled come fro ſo ferre whiche ſoth dureſſe werre full many one fyelde dead veryly without drede ſhall well mo werre laſte fro euery day numbre laſſeth faſte worthy knyghtes dede without routh dare ſaye conclude trouth rage furyous wood full lykely gentyl bloude worlde ſhall deſtroyed rural folke great pyty shall haue lordſhyp hooly gouernaunce churles eke ſorowe miſchaunce euery londe ſhall lordes alone whan gentyll men ſlayne echone ¶is hector ſo noble knight worldes ſonne light manhode floure ſlayne pyteouſly werte ſoth ſo myghty parauenture whiche may attayne nobleſſe ſhall fayne way ſhall death eſchewe myght purſewe fro day daye whyle lye therfore ſhortely requere touchynge werre outher praye veyne herken ſaye wyll purpoſe werre ſtryfe ieoparte lyfe leuer haue palled name ſlayne haue ydle fame worthineſſe death yblowe wynde laſteth throwe though renowne priſe blowe wide foryetfulneſſe leyth ofte aſyde length yeres oblyuion enuye falſe concluſyon lande knyghthode worthyneſſe wyſedome eke gentylneſſe fredam bounte vertue ſuche grace foryetfulneſſe darke defface therwithall male enuye yſered hath palme chyualrye falſe reporte wherfore ſaye wyll wyſedome ſuche folye let quyet forth lyfe nowe lede ¶and ouer three rede ſeke peace troyans ye may haſty wyſe without delaye counſayle platly myſchyefe death vpon fall well done ye toke hede ¶both vlixes thou dyomede ¶and neſtor eke ſythen ye wyſe worke playnely lyke deuyſe ſumme fyne myne entent ſo reporteth hym hath ſent anone ſhorte concluſyon ¶repeyred agamenon ſuch anſwere ye haue herde ſeine nedeth wryte newe againe ¶and herevpon kynge agamenon let make anone conuocaſyon lordes preſence fro poynt poynt ſothly ſentence hath reherſed achylles deſyrous haue peace troye platly prayer wyll degree agayne troians ſpere ſhelde helpe grekes armed felde wherfore kynge ful wiſe hereupon axed deuyſe whan thought beſt matter ſyth ſtode ſo ¶and fyrſte ſpeaketh menelay angry chere ſayde platly nay haue peace entent ne wolde therto aſſent sythen cyte concluſion stode prycke diſtruction hector deiphobꝰ dead yt whylom truſt euery nede diffence ago farewell truſte hope alſo without hole pryde maye death abyde ¶and truſte well without leſſe though ſo achylles ne helpe v towarde empryſe therof drede maner wyſe without hym haue victorye manhode owne glorye full ſure therof certayne vlixes gan replye agayne neſtor alſo ſodayne mocyon contrayre opynyon affyrmynge playnely wonder though menelay ſothly caſe vnto peace wolde aſſent openly wyſte ment ground roote al werre cauſe alſo come ſo ferre lande quene heleyne ¶and ſake onely tweyne grekes whiche man may denye lyues put ſuche ieopardye hym grounde ſoughte well wyſte rought nought menelay wo endure wyfe myght agayne recure ¶and ſayth hector dead hath heyre ſpeake manlyhead knyghthode wyll founde called hector ſeconde ¶worthy troylus whiche yt brother worlde ſuche worthyneſſe recken troye myghty wall ¶and diffence hector gone ye knowe well ſelfe euerychone ſo ye lyſte take hede whoſe ſharpe ſworde ſore doth v blede euery day furyous hete amyd fyelde whan hym mete ſtede worthy deiphobus whiche tyme wonderly famous ¶his brother parys nowe founde worthyneſſe knyghthode perygall haue none auauntage vnto houre rather great damage recken ſyth gonne ſoth lyttle wonne lykely alwaye leſe contune ſyth may cheſe holſome lyue quyet haue peace werre lete one aſſent ſyth ye wyſe yt worde calchas gan ryſe troyan treytour wt pale chere ire ſayde ye ſhall ¶a worthy prynces thynke ye done chaunge ſo lyke doth moone olde purpoſe fyrſt entent agayne wyll commaundement godder euery thynge gouerne purueyaunce ſo diſcerne ala als ne wyll ye leſte credence fayth geue theyr heſte whiche wyſe may fallyble ſoth impoſſyble vtterly troye citye ordynaunce neceſſytye myght deſtroyed henſe alyte ſlouth wyte victorye worſhyp honour fynall palme eke labour reported water lande reſerued hooly hande purpoſe yf ye forth contune hynder foly fortune ſoth dare well conclude peryllous goddes yllude neclygence ſlouth wylfully wherfore read manfully herte thought full vnyte platly deuoydyng ambyguyte ſet vpon knyghtly reſume force agayne fully conſume cruell foen let ſhet without wanhope drede diſpeyre euery doubte caſtyng parrell ſlouth cowardyſe let manhode vtterly diſpyſe dread death cauſeth hertes feynt cowardyſe atteynt fynally goddes haue hyght preſcyence eternall might victorye ye ſhall attayne lyke deſyre ſayne ¶and whan calchas concluſyowne falſe treytour vnto troye towne grekes wordes fayre touchynge werre put dyſpayre herte one caſte fulfyll hooly counſayle though ſo achylle frowarde aye helpe nede gaue force toke hede euerychone redy make ye ſhall fielde haſte take trewes paſſed ye monthes twayne ye felde grekꝭ gan theim ordayne troye agayne theim yſſue oute ¶and worthy troylus huge route grekes gan alderfirſte aſſayle ſwerde made rayle red bloud harneys bright death fled fro ſyght daye thrugh cruelte caſte platly auenged vpon death hector vtterly ¶and dare wryteth ſpecyally knightes troyan champyowne day hath ſlayne rydyng vp downe ¶as myne auctour guydo lyſt endyte saue hym ferther wryte boke geueth ſuche name manhode knyghtly fame grekes dryuen vnto flyght daye tyll drewe nyght ¶and morowe dawnynge grekes haue phebus vpryſynge yarmed great dylygence agayne troyans ſtanden diffence amonges whome daye rede ¶so well hym bare worthy dyomede many troyan cruelte ¶hath loſte lyfe tyll troylus gan ſe dyomede fyelde rydynge anone without lettynge ſpere throwen reſte troylus rode ſmote hym breſt myghtely nede downe horſe ſmote dyomede albe wounde tho domage furyouſly troylus rage hygh enuye gan abrayde whan ye loue faire creſeide deceyte falſe trecherye grekes faſte gan hye amonge horſe miſchiefe whiche lay drawe haſt yt may ſhelde broſed affrayde bare hym home ſo dyſmayde ſtroke home vnto tent ¶and menelay ſame whyle hath hente myghty ſpere tauenge dyomede towardes troylus faſt gan ſpede fully auyſed hym vnhorſe anone troylus fyrſte made ſtede gone ſwyfte courſe towardes menelay anone earth laye myghtely ye hyt hym ſpere ſhelde plate might body ne mortall wounde knightes anone hym founde preſe rent bare hym home owne tent grekes aye ſtandyng diſtreſſe knighthode ye hye proweſſe troilus whiche ſo hath belaine euery part rode plaine ¶tyll vnto tyme agamenowne fyelde valed downe many worthy banere ſhone full ſhene agayne ſonne clere wt knightꝭ hym rydyng enuyrowne ſore enchaſed troye towne woundeth ſleeth put theim ye flyght hym ſelfe acquytynge lyke manly knyght without abode amonge troyans fyerſly rode ¶this worthy kyng great agamenowne troylus ſpere hath ſmytten downe maugre grekes gameth ſocour whan ſawe lorde gouernour ſuche myſchyefe grounde lyende hente hym vp made hym aſſende manhode ſtronge ſtede wyt gan taken hede conſydered wiſely thought diſioynt troilus brought grekes great pryde tofore ſwerde myght abyde prudently hygh diſcrecyon ¶this noble knyght kyng agomenon hadde aye aduertence gouernaunce prouydence whan ſawe grekes gan fayle wexe feble ſtanden battayle lacke ſtuffe ſhulde recomfort full prudently made reſorte eueryche owne tent ¶and hath pryam ſent trewſe troye cyte ſyxe monthes myghte counſayle pryamus kynge without abode graunted axynge albe ſome guydo lyſte endyte euyll apayde ſo longe reſpyte mortall foen maner wyſe yet graunt ye haue harde deuyſe stode ſtrength fully read ¶in whiche tyme womanhead creſeyde lyſte longer tarye though father therto contrarye vyſyte haue ſyght ¶of dyomede become knyght ¶which troilus late caught woūd tent ſhe hath hym founde benygnely vpon beddes ſyde ſet downe ſelfe tyde platly caſte owne thought ¶touchynge troylus yt nought lyue hope recure thought ſhe wolde nothing vnſure purueyaunce without ſtore gaue anone without hooly herte vnto dyomede lo pytye womanhead mercy eke benynge routhe newly olde trouthe nature lette ſlyppe ouer ſlyde rather lyſten ſo abyde man myſchiefe ſake chaunge ſo redy make lumbardſtrete crowne doket poyſe good ſo prent ſet letter chaunge doth man abyde wynde redy tyde paſſage aye ſo lyſte pace man loſte lyſte ſeke grace daunger none counterfeyte diſdeyne ſea calme theſe rockes plain mercyles neuer man ne deyde ſought grace record creſeide whiche fynally hath gyuen herte dyomede releſe ſmerte prayed hym right glad lyght calleth owne man knyght hym behyghte rather deye euery thynge howe ſhe wolde obeye honeſt hym pleaſaunce leuer ſhe chaunge varyaunce founde lacke pytye ſyttynge femynyte nature vengeable fayth othe rather mercyable mannes lyfe ſtandynge diſtreſſe ¶hereof wyll dreſſe tell forth tranſlacyon ceriouſly agamenon durynge trewſe time peace hym ſelfe wente vnto achylles beſechynge ſome regarde haue knyghthode grekes ſaue preſence withdrawe ſuffer ſo mortally ſlawe enmyes pompous elate ¶but achylles alway indurate ilyche newe herte thought purpoſe platly chaungeth nought fully enclyned haue peace ¶but moche achylles entyerneſſe hyghe affection louyng vnto agamenon vnto hym graunted leſte great parcell touchynge requeſte ſaye achylles graunteth hym myrmydones full knyghtly men onely abſence grekes maken reſyſtence fyelde agayne towne whiche graunte kynge agamenowne duke neſtor thanked hym herte alwaye conteynynge ſmerte loue fayre pollycene ne knewe gayne wounde sgrene diſpeyred languyſheth euer one whan trewſe paſſed gone vpon day morowe full benynge achylles knyghtes dyd aſſygne fylde take agamenon ſtory maketh mencion gaue bandes freſhe read men may knowe manlyhead withholde ſpecyall▪ lyke man deadly mortall within tent achylles abode fyelde rode dole ſhulden twinne abſence werre begynne maugre wyll agayne towne ¶but forth went agamenowe vpon troyans ſterne full pryde mette ſyde manly knyghtes troyan bloud whiche ſo furyous wood cruelly grekes oppreſſe backe feare gan thē dreſſe ſo inly fell kene ¶tyll myghty duke athene entred grekes diffende vpon hym vnwarely wende came myghty troylus lyke wood lyown ſtede anone bare downe put hym ſo preſe tyll hath mette theſe myrmydones ſlewe daye full many one ſo fer troylus ygone grekes put vtterly flyght knyghthod til drewe night fro ſwerde raunſom might thē borow guydo wryte next morowe full mortall ſlaught outher ſyde amyd fielde togyther ryde manly knightes wonder ſene ¶and faught kyng phylymene helpe onely pollydamas taken hath worthy kyng thoas gan hym leade towarde troye ye towne myrmydones helpe came downe wonder proudly gan ſewe myght thoas reſcue hym delyuer ſo ſtronge ¶but troylus hurtled amonge furyouſly full lyke champyowne caſt threwe thē downe ſlewe ſome made blede tyll cruelly ſlewe myghty ſtede whiche ſat yet neuertheleſſe fought foote agaynſt myrmydones caſt troylus haue take ¶but parys tho gan ſo awake brothern hym rode place troylus ſtode vpon fete ſelfe alone mirmydones ſleine haue many one knighthod mālyhead vnto hym brought ſtede amyd foen made hym aſcende full knightly gan ſelfe dyffende ¶be ſet grekes felfe ſtounde neuer yet better knyght founde felte well tho foen brother called margaryton fought puttyng hym ſelfe preſe ſlayne ala amonge myrmydones death cruell yre troylus anger ſette fyer playnely purpoſeth tauenge may ſworde began make way ¶and parys aye faſt hym rydyng brethern vpon hym awaytyng whiche yfeare ſo mercyleſſe ¶and fynde theſe myrmydones force neceſſyte compelled playnly flee troylus ſo furyous vengeable eke ſo diſpyteous gaue many mortall wounde yet ſoth day founde noble knyghtes quyt wonder wele crafte knewe euerydele longyng armes reade made ſydes blede mayle plate ſhene ne myght playnly ſuſtene ſword troilus chaſing ouerall albe kepte cloſe wall hole together went ſonder troilus aye chaſeth yonder ſeuered mauger myght tyll fielde many worthy knyght came menelay kyng agamenon vlyxes eke cruell thelamon dyomede whiche woundes grene recured ſayth myne auctour clene troyans ſodaynly fall wardes knyghtes tho began fyght renewe euery halfe blouddy hewe plate bryght newe yſteyned troy ſo manly haue thē peyned agayne foen myghty ſtryfe many greke berafte lyfe moſt myghty bataile troylus came gan aſſayle euery parte many blouddy wounde knighthod gan confoūde aye fledde ſo ferde mortall ſtrokes ſharpe ſworde deadly foe deſtruction contynueth tyll kyng thelamon manhode whan behelde grekes made recure agayne fyelde gan troyans aſſayle wonder ſore tho began ſlaughter eche ſyde till troylus newe agayne grekes hath ſo fyerſly ouerlayne myrmydones euerychone afore ſworde made gone tentes fyelde forſake hande day hath take hundred knightes came weye proweſſe ſent troye euer one gan ſo enchace ¶myrmydones loſte place ¶and achylles lying tent repeyred forwounded rent herneys broke plate maile nombre fynde fayle hundred knyghtes ſlayne dead ala founde taas amyd fyeld thrugh girt wt many woūde ¶of troylus ſword hector ſecounde wherof achylles ſyght heauy nexte nyght bedde walowynge fro deuoyde ſlepe conſtreynt wo herte wounde ſo kene men fayre polycene wyttynge well dyd payne venged ſhulde attayne wiſe vnto deſyre thus brent double fyre loue yre made ſyghe ſore cauſe loue aferde agayne towne perſon offenciowne ¶leſte pryamus hecuba quene offended namely polycene thus ſtode double weer herte ſatte wonder nere many wonder dyuers fantaſye haue louers poynt dye ryght euen ſo fareth wofull man wo rede ne entryked wende deye recure knewe better weye whyle laye throwes wyte lyke guydo playnly lyſte endyte ſtory maketh mencyowne dayes ſeuen troye towne encreſe augment ſorowe grekes metten euery morowe thrugh ye force alder might outher parte ſlayne many knight ¶and whyle laye achylles grekes death ylyke reckeles loue onely toke maner hede ſo hole mortally doth blede plaineth woundꝭ large hym thought parcell charge moche hath thyng thincke ofte waketh whan ſhulde wynke▪ thoughtfull aye
