ymagynatyfe wery owne lyfe ¶tyll day kyng agamenon seynge death deſtruction grekes halfe withouten remedye troye ſent enbaſſadrye trewſe certayne dayes ſpace myght therof haue grace lenger tyme platly endure leyſer ſepulture worthy knyghtes dead aforne fyelde outher party lorne whiche taas full buſyly ſoughte plainly wrought durynge ſyege great vyolence ſhall deſcryuen pacyence ¶howe achylles ſlewe worthy troylus vnknyghtly trayled body fyelde tyed horſe cap xxxi cruell force mortall yre martyr myght alway ſet fyre newe enuye gonne olde hatrede brennyng hertes hole glede atwyxe grekes troye cytye whiche lykely ſtaunched tyll deth conſume mortall darte full many worthy vpon outher parte execute ala fynall fate eyther parte enuious deadly hate whiche ne myght deſtyne remewe ſet nedely muſt inſewe attropos wyll ſuffer none mayſtreſſe guyder rother deathes ſhyp tyll goth vnto wrake fortune gan tourne face abake highe diſdayne fro troye cytye ſtory ſhortly ye ſhall ſe whan trewſe ytake wered gan redy make proude grekes fyelde gone vpon morowe whan phebus bright ſhone armed full ſhene eueryche deuyſe ¶and menelay hath firſt met paris day ſtorye read eche ſmytte ſtede whiche tyme dan pollydamas ¶to vlixes rode ſterne paſe eche cruell enmyte ſtyffe ſwordes gan together flee nouther manhode wyte ſpere ſquared byte ¶the myghty duke called meneſte rode lyne ryght myght ſe anthenor troyan full pryde ſadell caſte hym downe aſyde furye hatefull tene tho haſte come kyng phylomene helpe towne gan aſſayle kyng agamenowne knyghthode hardineſſe hym brought great diſtreſſe vtter myſchyefe confuſyon ¶ne kyng thelamon full proudely came hym reſkewe ſore gan purſewe ſpere vpon phelomene horſe layde hym grene maugre force ſtory telleth thus hym mortally yrous yonge archylogus mortall courſe ran vnto brumius one ſonnes pryamus kynge yonge delyuer beſte lykyng hym ſmytte ſo great myght fell dead freſhe luſty knyght death whā troy eſpye made ſhoute pyteouſly gan crye wofull routhe death complayne tyll noyſe gan vtterly attayne troylus eares platly rode lenger abode place felly gan approche ſworde ſette broche without routhe grekes hatefull bloud mercyles hym withſtode ſlewe daye cruell auenture greke none yt might endure tofore ſworde gan ſo oppreſſe knyghthode hygh proweſſe put vtterly flyght ne byn manhode myght ¶of myrmydones al longe day one aſſent vpon troylus lay wherof full melancolyus courage manhode moſte famous ne lyſte longer lette attones vpon ſette furyouſly gan amonge thē ryde ſome ſmote euen ſyde body ſome ye herte wt ſworde thrugh doublet ſhert ſhelde plate thrugh haberion perccd hath lyke wood lyon ſlewe day many one maugre fledde eueryche grekes eueryche tent ¶and troy went swyftly horſe tyll haue take ſuch ſlaught grekes ther make fynally bette reſkuſe death ſo paſſyngly confuſe grekes myſchyefe deſolate troylus ſo narowe brought thē chekmate coulde tho better remedye hydouſly wayle crye death forwounded griſely chere ¶that achylles whan gan fyrſt dredefull noyſe wofull ſowne cauſed reflectiowne eyre agayne ſo coulde knowe rochys harde kauernes lowe lyke one worde ſpoke two men wont callen ecco confuſe lamentaciowne grekes ſyde whiche deadly ſowne pyteouſly achylles ronne lay agayne hote ſonne mortall woundes yeldyng vp breth roumble ſwowhe reſownyng deth noyſe grekes maden ment achylles dyd enquere cauſe clamour tolde lacke ſocour grekes eche tentorye ¶of troylus ſlayne ſo victorye goth fynally troye towne euermore concluſyowne many greke ſlayne laye tent gapynge vpwarde wt bloud yſpent conſtreynt wounde ſmert ¶and whyle achilles gan caſe aduerte full ſodaynely came hym man whiche tale euen thus began ala quod may ye thus ſuſtene ſe men hereupon grene afore face ſlayne lye deade lyſte one take hede ſtande ſtyll penſyfe tent vpon poynt ſelfe ſhent haſty houre yf ye abyde fyfty thouſande knyghtes beſyde redy armed plate mayle caſte playnly aſſayle doubte vnarmed ye ſtande ye knyghthode manly take hande reſyſte ſelfe place lyke man meten face ¶for whiche anone cruell mode achylles lyke woode hath armed hym fomyng bore farewell loue ſette ſtore haſty hete yre ſo kene ¶that forgat fayre pollycene beaute yt whylom made ſmert rage vp anone ſtarte toke ſtede lyon wroth agayne troyans fyelde goth lyke wolfe hunger gnawe ryght ſo gan agayne foen drawe rode without excepciowne woundeth ſleeth killeth bereth downe lyttle throwe troy gan ſworde knowe whiche infecte newe bloud none yet yt withſtode mortally gan aboute hym layne dead bodyes enlonge playne ¶tyll caſually troylus gan eſpye achylles caſte eye gan horſe might payne ¶but achylles hym ware alſo smette ſtede made hym go towarde troylus ſelfe tyde full courſe together ryde full lyne ryght ſperes ſharpe whette ſuche myght haue together mette hyghe dyſdayne ſayne grounde felle tway •• ¶but achylles caught hath ſuche wounde body depe ſo profounde longe lay myn auctour ſaith certain helth reſtored agayne ¶and troilus eke thrugh plate maile al wryte guydo wounde ſmall whiche vnto hym dyd greunaunce thus daye contynuaunce dayes ſyxe ſuynge proude grekes mette cruelly amyd fyelde troye towne great damage confuſyowne outher partye playnely nay many worthy ſlayne day day rancour hertye hoote enuye albe guydo doth ſpecyfye none theyr name playnely boke ye ſhall fynde yf ye lyſte loke al whyle ſodeine thinge penſyfe tryſte pryamꝰ kyng achylles tourned hath ſo clene luſte awaye yonge pollycene chaunge ſo ſodeyne ſo newe thought beheſtes trewe ¶but deceyte doubleneſſe fraude falſly newe fangelneſſe ſleyghty treaſon vncouert gyle rage loue laſteth whyle vtterly founde beheſte lyke wynde man may areſte faceth worde diſcordaunt fro dede whiche wyſe man take ſhall hede lette paſſe reckeleſſe albeit achylles whylom caught within loues ſnare hym lyſte nowe one ſpare hygh rancour lady offende lyke troye wende hecuba nouther yet pollycene angre gan abreyde ſhe truſte ſo entyerly hath leyde achylles ſo falſly mene wherfore full tryſte pollycene enclyned eyen clere counſayle mother dere ¶to haue wedded achylles fyne onely ſhulde haue peace atwene grekes troy towne falſe inconcluſyowne ¶in fyne trouthe yſene whan achylles woundes grene fully cured certayne day gan compaſſe euer may ymagine enuyous herte venged woundes ſmerte vpon troylus thot ſtacke aye mynde auauntage myght hym fynde hym bare ſo paſſyngly hatrede herte brennynge glede whiche day nyght may degree fully queynt tyll auenged hoote rancour gan ſo hym gnawe auyſed platly ſhall beſlawe handes whan ſo falle day hym gan calle myrmydones knightes euerychone vpon morowe whan grekes gone tofore towne ſtele armed bryght agayne troyans purpoſe fyght come proudely fielde oppoſyte many ryche ſhelde newly depeynt colour freſhe fyne vpon whiche full bryght gan ſhyne fyry titan golde treſſed ſphere vpryſte beames clere whan felle enuyous achylles knightes called myrmydones ¶vpon troylus gan hym complayne beſechynge theyr payne agayne troylus fielde daye catche hym myſchyefe may buſyly dylygence haue full aduertence one aſſent ryde thynge ſette aſyde nought elles take hede saufe fynally agayne hym procede ſo myght catche hym trappe within ſelfe troylus clappe encloſe ſette hym rounde abouie wyſe go oute whan beſet amonge ſiea euer fall myght manly cōſerue tyll hym ſelfe come make hym ſterue ſworde none wyght ¶lo manhode preyſe ryght vengeaunce deth rancour pryde compaſſed treaſon knighthode layde aſyde worthyneſſe falſe enuye yſlawe falſhede lofte trouthe backe ydrawe ala armes ſhulde befall trecherye bytter galle shulde world knight foūde trouth order bounde ¶alas ala achylles conſpyred hath myrmydones death one yt worthyeſt wight euer eke beſte knyght ala wo herte fele deade ſake ſtorye whan rede whan fortune hath thynge ordeyned though euer wayled compleyned gayne remedye though men galen aye crye touchynge mattere wryte forth lyke ye ſhall myrmydones haue lord behyght power full myght fulfyll commaundement fielde grekes went ¶but troylus fyrſt oppoſyte without abode manly mete ybrent ſo feruent hete hardyneſſe hyghe courage worthyneſſe vaſſelage ne lyſte longer abyde folke began ryde amonge grekes folke hyghe renowne wt ſword woūdeth bereth downe sleeth kylleth vpon euery haiue mortally may ſalue ſores ſounde death ſo rode yeldyng vp breth furyouſly gan enchaſe made leſe lyttell ſpace lande echone afore flee troylus ſworde ſuche cruelte maugre fielde hath wonne ſame tyme whan bryght ſonne hye ſouthe mydday marke ſhone euen houre drewe noone myrmydones gathred one compaſſe wyſe rounde aboute hym gone furyouſly one entenciowne made cercle enuyrowne hym ſawe helpe deſolate herte dyſconſolate vpon ſyde manlyhead lyke lyon toke theym hede famous knyghtly excellēce tygre ſtandeth diffence manfully gan encomber gan leſſe dyſcreaſe nomber ſome maymeth woūdeth ye death ſome made yelden vp breath ſome layde earthe lowe ſome made ouerthrowe wyth hys ſwerde theyr bloud wete great myſchyefe vnder horſe fete vpon ſtede ſturdy wall worthy knyght man moſt mercial pleyeth play amonge myrmydones hym ſelfe god wot alone helples ¶but tho ala might force auayle thre thouſande knightes aſſayle euery parte lengthe brede cowardly fyrſt ſlewe ſtede ſperes ſharpe ſo ſquare ygroūd whych ala ſtante ye grounde wythout reſkuſe refute ſocoure daye chyualrye floure well awaye haue ſo beſet head ſmote baſenet brake harueys hym aſſaile ſeuer ſtele myghty ſtronge mayle dyſarmed necke alſo heade ala whyle wyght toke none hede knyghtes longynge towne yet alway troyan champyowne knyghtly wyſe naked ¶hym ſelfe defendeth tyll achylles ala came rydynge furyous wood whā ſawe howe troylus ſtode longe fyghtynge awhaped mate folkes alone diſconſolate sole hym myſchyefe pyteouſly achylles wonder cruelly behynde vnwarely toke hede ſwerde ſmyteth heade caſt forthe cruell curſed herte thought ſure ſhould hym aſterte ſhewe malice wolfe vnmercyable full vnknyghtly vengeable vpon body dead laye colde ala euer ſhould knyght tolde wryte reherſed ſo foule deede boke ala men ſhall rede knyght ſtorye ſo horryble vnto eares paſſyngly odyble achilles crueltye ala dead corp toke taas vengeably bonde fynde tayle horſe behynde hatefully euery wyght behelde drewe ſelfe endlonge felde renges wardes oh ala euer ſhould fall knyght herte ſo cruell hatred ſo ſpytefull ſo fell drawe man deade oh thou homer ſhame red ye amaſe yt holdeſt thy ſelfe ſo wyſe achylles ſet ſuche great pryſe thy bokes chyualrye aboue echone doſt hym magnyfye ſo ſleyghty ſo full fraude geueſt thou ſo hye prayſe laude ¶certys homer thy excellence rethoryke ſugred eloquence thy luſty ſonges thy dytees ſwete thy hony mouth doth wyth ſugre flete yet one thynge thou greatly art blame cauſeles gyue hym ſuche name tytle ſuche tryumphe glorye paſſyngely put memorye thy bookes ſaye wryte ſo thrugh knighthod ſlain hath hector two firſt yt lyke vnto none ¶and ſithꝭ troilus yt owne brother thou arte meued affection whych thou haſt grekes nacion preyſe ſo thou cauſt endyte thou ſhouldeſt aye fauour wryte trouthe playnly indyfferent ſaye ſothe clerely entente ¶for ſlewe hector felde afore diſarmed ſhelde buſy eke ſpoylynge kynge yf beware comynge hym quyt chyualrye falſe deceyt trecherye ne ſo lyghtly gone ¶alſo troylus naked alone amyd thre thouſand cloſed yſhet ¶when achilles hath head ſmet backe full cruell herte nothing treaſon dyd aduerte ¶was dede manly knyght ſlee man forweryed fyght faynt trauayle longe daye amonge ſo many ſtandynge baye kynges ſonne ſo hye borne naked head armure torne euen death ſelfe poynt great myſchyefe playnly ioynt lyfe ſtandynge wrake ¶when achilles came falſly bake aſſaylynge hym halfe deade lyke cowarde ſmote heade tofore hurte wounded ſore ¶wherfor homer ne praiſe therfore let preaſe thy royall booke difface haſte renowne outrace name neuen veryly vp thirde heauen ſemeth infecte eyre ſowne therof ſo foule vnfayre vſed aduertence eye prouydence vnto knyghthod worthyneſſe manhode gentylleſſe renowne owne name reporte knyghtly fame wyſe haue taken hede hadde neuer done ſo foule dede vengeably haue ydrawe kynges ſonne ſlawe namely hym ſo good knight whyche tyme ſo loke aryght paſſed achylles dare well expreſſe manhode gentylneſſe nowe dead ala ¶the death pollydamas parys eke fyrſt gan eſpye fared ſothe woulden dye ſpecyally wyth face dead fade ¶parys ala ſuche inly ſorowe made conſtreynt deadly wo ſawe well troylus ago ſhall lyfe neuer ſe suche ſorowe alſo troyan dan enee hym hath made many mo one togyther go dead corp recure maye ¶but grekes ſo fell daye theyr haſte vtterly vayne wyſe corp get agayne tyll menon noble worthy kynge whych loued troylus ouer thynge caught ſuch routhe affection haſte fearſer lyon death caſt wreake fyrſt ire thus gan ſpeake achylles hye treaſowne oh thou tratoure oh thou scorpyowne oh thou serpent full trecherye whych diſhonour chyualrye falſe engyne haſt daye yſlawe onely beſt hadde felowe whylom worlde alyue ala ala maye aryght deſeryue thy venym hyd thy malice vntrouthe wythout pyte knyghtly routhe drawe knyght ſo gentyll ſo good kynges ſonne ſo worthy bloud ye feld thy horſe tale behynde euer ſhalbe mynde cruell dede vngentylneſſe ¶and wyth yt word menon gan dreſſe towarde achylles wythout areſte wyth ſpere ſmet breſt enuyouſly ſo great hatrede vnneth kepte ſtede menon pulled ſwerde caſt hym manly mete berde rode fully deuoyde dreade ſuche wound gaue head maugre many mannes ſyght earthe made alyght pryde mortall traunce wound felt ſuch greuaunce death laye huge whyle ſwowne ſpace halfe myle tyll myrmydones aſſembled one great laboure hente vp anone full deadly pale ſo gan blede ſet ſtede laſt hert caught agayne ſmet horſe hate hye diſdayne towarde menon faſt gan hye cominge gan eſpye full lyke knyght lyſt abyde hit horſe ſharply ſyde mette achilles proudly playne wyth theyr ſwordes togither layne gan hurtle horſe backe tho yfere wyth herte enuyous deſpytous chere ¶but kynge menon auauntage achylles wood rage poynt abrought confuſyowne tyll yt wardes newe comen downe parte theſe yonder whych ſodaynly ſeuered aſonder ſtory telleth playnly began ſlaughter many manly man nother party felde ne would leue pryde tyll drewe eue phebus gan aſwage hete gan bathe wawes wete bryght beames occyan fro felde home goth euery man theyr lodginge ſeuen dayes faught yfere made delayes ¶full mortall cruell aduenture whyle achylles full buſy cure woundes grene ſores ſounde newe treaſon founde venged vpon kynge menon wytte ſette thervpon ſo cruell enuyous achilles ycharged hath myrmydones worthy menon amonge theim enbrace hym founde opportune place theyr might theyr buſy thought theyr handes eſcape nought tyll hym ſelfe auenged hym ¶and ſo befell menon ſe nexte morowe lyke manly knyght agayne grekes armed fyght troye ſyde wonte auenture daye yt fell ſo achilles menon mette eche theim gan ſette horſe backe wyth full great emiye ſo longe theyr melancolye mine auctour wryt togyther fyght eche made force alyght ¶and whan menon ſtode vpon ye grounde▪ myrmydones wente aboute rounde charged fyerſe achylle ala wythout goddes wylle dyſſeuered knyghtes myſchyefe vpon fall deſtitute alone helples ſuche poynt ſlewe achylles ſtory lyke founde menon fyrſt gaue ſuch wounde tofore death fell ſtryfe dyſpeyred lyfe achylles falſe treaſon take hede homer demeth thy reaſon falſe fraude ſleyghty gyle treaſon caſte afore wyth many wyle achylles iudge ryght euer ſlewe worthy knyght yt preodycyon recorde take kynge menon tytle laude ala entriked wyth fraude fallace ¶that thou homer mayſt coloure though thou paynte gold wt aſoure thy wrytynge venym encloſe thorne hyd vnder roſe whoſe malyce aye dareth roote though floure aboue fayre ſoote men fraude vnder may ſe treaſon ye get bvt wyll tell grekes day meneſte kynge menelay dyomede thelamonyus troyans paſſyng deſpytous cruelly wyth theyr wardes theyr myſchyefe vpon fall made theim flee home vnto towne whylom troylus chyefe champyowne deade ala hath nowe forſake haue dead body take ſame daye great difficulte dolefully cyte haue tho brought cry oft ala death ſuch wo trowe man alyue whych could aryght halfe dele deſcriue theyr pyteous wo lamentacyowne certeyſe boy hath ſuche renowne drery wordes wepe crye ¶in complaynynge phyloſophye throughe boke accuſynge aye fortune ſelde nought one contune ſo full tranſmutaciowne oh ſtace thebe make boſt ſowne dreryneſſe wryte nother death feſtes funerall makynge ſorowe aduerſyte ¶let thy wepynge oh thou nyobe ¶ye ſyſter alſo ayeliager cuſtome haue flee ſo fer fro yere yere brother complayne thou wepteſt thine eyen twaine oedippus kyng thebe cyte thou wofull myrrha calyxtone ſo well rage bemene dydo eke whylome cartage quene lette dole contrycyon ¶and phyllys eke thy dymophon ¶and eke cecho newe doſt begyn crye wayle alſo thou corynne whylom ſo great affray death onely thy popyngay boke telleth v ouyde let wo layde aſyde make compariſowne vnto wo troye towne death onely worthy knyght loue euery maner wyght hygh lowe olde yonge age falle newe ſuche rage ne coulde wo none ende whoſe ſalte teares wyll eyen ſhende pyteous lamentaciowne euery ſtrete throughout towne ala coulde ſorowes telle ¶i trowe certeys pluto depe helle torment paynes kene nouther ſhe proſerpyna quene nother wery wood tycius iryon hungry tantalus ne coulde well bytter peyne furyouſly wepen complayne troyans troylus thy ſake nowe ſuche ſorowe make ¶or wepe kyng pryamus wepeth face full pyteous ſorowe maketh hecuba quene ¶who wepeth fayre pollycene wepeth nowe parys heleyne wepe teares reyne troyans deadly ſwole chere neded wepers hyer ynough owne ſtore ala nowe euermore helpe ſole comforte deſtytute ſhall nowe refute ¶nowe hector alſo deyphobus troylus eke ſo vertuous dead ala ſhall ſuccour helpe ſuſtene werre cyte concluſyon death fully deſtruction theyr towres walles ſtronge matter ſhulde playne longe vayleth alway ſo morne wherfore wyll agayne retorne matter tell forth kyng grekes hath without taryinge trewſe peace yſent certayne tyme great auyſement whyche graunted agamenowne ayene repeyred towne ¶howe parys ſlewe achylles archylogus duke neſtors ſonne temple apollo cap xxxii kynge pryamus dyd buſye cure make ryche ſepulture troylus corp full noble royall ſayth guydo ſtones metall encloſed great affection ¶and nighe beſyde kyng menon solempnely buryed laide graue day day haue lyke cuſtome feſte funerall ryghtes ceremonyall bothe dewe obſeruaunce seruyſe done aye contynuaunce temple lyke guyſe whiche longe deuyſe tedyus eke dwell purpoſe ceriouſly tell howe hecuba endyte caſte fully achylles requyte tirannye ſothly yf ſhe may vnto ſhe calleth day alexſaunder full ſecrete wyſe vnto hym ſhall deuyſe wepynge eyen full heuy chere sayde euen thus ye ſhall ¶parys quod ſhe ala ſaue goddes wyll thou knoweſt well howe fyerſe achylle ſonnes hath ſlayne well nye euerychone none lefte thy ſelfe alone hath made ala gayne full cowardly chyldren baraine hector troylus eke therto whiche euery trouble wo fully comforte pleaſaunce ſolace wherfore caſte playnely compaſe ſome engyne death ordayne lyke treaſon dyd payne trayterouſly ſworde ſmyte ryght ſo thynke treaſon quite ſyttynge ryght equyte ſyth thou woteſt platly hath ſette herte loue clene vpon doughter yonge polycene fyne onely haue vnto wyue whiche caſte hym ſende blyue come treate mattere ¶in temple appollo temple moſte chiefe cyte whiche tyme wyll thou thy ſelfe armed full pryuelye certayne knyghtes thy companye armed alſo agayne ſame daye wyſe ne ſcape maye handes dead haue ſaide therfore take good hede vnto thynge herte praye poynt poynt byddyng obeye aſſenteth hole herte behotynge ſhulde aſterte hym toke twenty mo manly men ryght well durſte temple full good aduyſe ¶they yhid biddynge parys whyle hecuba couert entente meſſager achylles hath ſent ye haue herde concluſyowne come haſte vnto troye towne effecte whiche myſſage onely treate maryage haſte commeth ſonde coulde nothyng vnderſtonde treaſon hyd playnly aduerte ſo hote marked herte loues bronde fyry glede lyfe death toke hede ſette ſyde wytte reaſon caſte afore good diſcrecion lokynge full prudent ſoth loue blent troye whan ſhulde gone lyke fareth louers euerychone whan haue caught herte fantaſye peryll though ſhulden dye haue myght power beware tyll vnwares trapped ſnare maladye aye ſo furyous ¶and thus achylles anthylogus neſtors ſonne haue waye nome towarde towne togither come temple ye haue harde telle parys tho lyſte longer dwelle vnwarely knyghtes achylles myſchyefe fall eueryche ſworde full bryght ſome bokes ſaye done night whan death longe afore deſyred ¶by hecuba parys conſpyred ¶but achylles mortall caſe amonge naked hent ſworde ſelfe ſteuen lyke knyght ſlewe ſeuen force mauger myght ¶but whan parys therof ſyght thre dartes raught kene ſquare ſodeynly ware full ſecretely hyd vnder ſhade markynge hym noyſe made caſte hym euen euer head ſhafte body ran therwithall knyghtes fewe ſharpe ſwordes gan vpon hym hewe lefte tyll lay grounde ¶full pale dead many mortall wounde ryghtfully reaſon ſyt thus fraude falſhed quyt ¶of achylles hygh treaſon deth deth ſkylfully guerdon egall mede without fable ¶to mercyles vengeable thilke daye guydo wryteth thus achylles anthylogus ¶of parys temple ſlawe afterwarde bodye outdrawe achylle fro holy boundes cruelly throwen vnto houndes deuoured brode ſtreſte canell rennynge fylthy water wete without pytye maner routhe lo ende falſhed vntrouth lo fyne ſuche trecherye falſe deceyte compaſſed enuye lo knotte concluſyon god aye quytteth ſlaughter treaſon lo guerdon fynall mede ſo delyten falſhede euery thyng platly ſayne lyke guerdon doth attayne ye may ſe achilles whiche nyght temple le lyfe aye cuſtomable fraude treaſon vengeable ¶but befell requeſt heleyne bodyes theſe ylke tweyne conſerued hungry rage beſte foule gredy ramage yet lay amyddes cytye full openly men myght ſe great gladneſſe towne ¶into tyme agamenowne kyng pryam ſent maſſageres haue licenſe fette home beares graunt haue corſes take grekes ſuche ſorowe make pytye routh eueryche ſpake thus vnto feare farewell truſte nowe achylles dede farewell hope hooly ſpede farewell ioye chiefe diffence hadde manhode ſo great excellence farewell ala ſouerayne aſſuraunce farewell knighthode ſuffyſaunce ala vnlykely shall euer wynne getten cite v ala ſo frowarde fortune myghten contune alway wo payne endure cauſed make ryche sepulture achylles ſtones precyous ¶and anthylogus ſhulde longer dwell ceryouſly rytes telle buryinge wo make wepynge clothes blake ſome loure hode ſome go mylke bloud dolefull herte fyre ſhete caſten gummes ſwete amydde great flaumes funerall playes called palleſtrall wraſtlynge wake vayne vndertake tellen wherfore lette fully purpoſe lyke ye ſhall ſe reſorte concluſyon tellen great agamenon lordes haſte hath ſent aſſembled tent full prudently kyng manly man great aduyſe thus tale began syres quod fortune varyaunce chere froward double countenance ſodeyne tourne falſe vyſage hertes hath put ſuche arage murdre god man odyble ¶of achylles death horryble compaſſynge hecuba quene ſemeth ſhall ſene manhode hertes knightly force aduerſytye endure vertue ſuffraunce tyll death ye taken may vengeaunce manly quyte outragious offence whan time cometh make full recompence ſyth ye manly prudent wolde fyrſt ſe playne entent matter ſo wyſe hereupon aduyſe one aſſent voyce comune whether ye wyll werre forth contune ſyege ygonne vpon towne tyll brought deſtructiowne grece reſorte agayne cauſe achylles ſlayne whilom ſtrong champiowne diſtence chiefe protectiowne fynally dead hereupon let ſe reade saye openly longer tarye ¶and ſome anone gonne varye grutche caſtynge fro standynge doute beſte ¶and ſome ſayde tother ſyde lyfe death wolde ende abyde ſome wytte rude partye gonnen conclude wolde efte home agayne retourne ſayd wyll ſoiourne styll ſyege happe happe may thus treate longe day euery man lyke opynyon tyll laſte concluſyon accorded fully one fro ſyege neuer gone vnto tyme haue towne knyghthode full poſſeſſyowne free wyll ſpylle elles ſaue albe achylles buryed graue truſte euery worthy knyght fynally goddes haue behyght haſte ſhall towne poſſede hope fully deuoyde drede vndiſpeyred opynyon ¶and anone ayax thelamon worthy knyght famous hande amonge tho grekes londe sayde euen thus playnly ſentence ¶syres quod preſence counſayle platly rede ſtandeth ſo achylles dead ſonne haſte ſende hyther come ſe ende ſyege helpe v nede ¶whiche nowe abyt kynge lycomede byſayle named pirrus ſome hym call neptolonyus ryght luſty freſhe lykelyneſſe able attayne great worthyneſſe reporte fame kouthe drawe hym armes youth ¶and ſothfaſtly yf bokes lye haue redde herde prophecye fynally troye cyte without hym ſhall neuer wonne thus bokes ſaye olde memorye howe grekes ſhall haue victorye tyll come ſonne achylles wherfore haſte reckeles sende hym done anone commende counſaile euerichone reade fully aſſent aduiſe full prudently ſente haſte embaſſyat wyſe kynge full famous eſtate meane prudent noble menelay forth goeth ſelfe ſame day iourney gan hym faſte ſpede ¶tyll came vnto lycomede olde kynge ye haue harde telle tyme wyll lette dwelle ¶and grekes meane whyle derecte againe ſtyle ¶howe parys thelamon ayax ſlewe eche fylde cap xxxiii tyme yere ſhene ſonne crabbe courſe yronne hygheſt aſcencyon whiche called ſomer ſtacyon whan vertue euery roote drawen vp bawme ſoote croppe freſhe floure moſt luſty hewe coloure tyll phebus chare diſcencion crabbe towarde lyon holdeth courſe fyrmament meane whan retrogradyent dryeth vp moyſture wete herbe floure feruent hete veer afore hym made grene white tourneth beames ſhene ſede grayne decoction naturally dygeſtyon fyrſt rawe fruites floures watry eke plente humoures dryeth vp rypeth full feruence men may pull eche kynde ſeaſon fro yeare yeare reuolucyon braunches freſhely ſprede whan cheryes powbly rede ¶firſt iune ſeweth maye whan hote mery ſomers daye dwery lyke gyaunt longe ſame tyme grekes ſtoute ſtronge rancour brent enuyous hete haue ſhapen foen mete bryght armed fyelde go troye towne alſo wardes ordeyned euerychone fyelde haue take meten foen gan aſſemble vpon outher ſyde ¶but thelamon foly pryde ſame daye hym reade death dread diſarmed battayle areſt mayle plate bare vpon breſt foly ſurquedons outrage bare heade bare vyſage bare alſo without baſenet naked eke vyſer palet rode daye nothynge tho aferde hauynge weapon naked ſworde wylfully lefte home ſhelde ſpere toke fyelde full lyke knight ſyttynge ſtede ¶and hym foloweth dyomede lyke mar hym ſelfe hym meyne faſte came duke meneſte kyng vlixes agamenon pryamus wt troy towne toke eke fyelde wt full heuy chere feareful great diſpeyre inly full dreade yſſue ſyth hector nowe dede ¶worthy troylus alſo deyphobus hym ſelfe demed playnely thus febled greatly myght death grekes fyght goth hap hap maye parys eke full knyghtly array ¶kyng phylomene pollydamas ¶worthy eſdre eneas one aſſent ſaye ſame daye knightly lyue deye diffence vtterly ieoparte goddes lyſte felde daye departe proudely fyrſte grekꝭ gan perce parys tho thē perce fell ſyde ſonne ſhene archer arrowes ſquare kene grekes gan ſondre diſſeuere felde myght perſenere onely ſhot ſtronge archer perce londe arbalaſters whiche made fle ryght nede ¶into tyme proude dyomede whan grekes ſawe ſodeyne flyghte releue lyke manly knyght come vpon felly tene ¶and fyrſte ſette phylomene worthy kynge came troye ſyde whyche agayne gan hym ryde dyomede hath lyttell wonne ſwordes ſtyffe togyther ronne beholde noble ſyght eche quyte hym lyke knyght togyther ran horſe backe man coulde nother ſe lacke euer one troyans ſo felle vpon grekes ne myght dwelle kepe londe ſo made blede mauger force dyomede ſlaughter ſo hydous ſo ſtronge ye fielde woful noyſe ronge mortall crye wounded folke laye slayne ſoyle endlonge waye ¶tyll meneſte ſyttynge ſtede worthy duke gan take hede myſchyefe grekes beſet hent anone ſpere ſharpe ywhet smyttynge horſe felly ſyde renges knightly gan ryde ſtynt ſo furyous ¶tyll mette pollydamas troyan knyght manly man vnwarely hym ran hytte ſo many mannes fyghte erthe made lyght ſworde grounde whan laye ſlayne ſelfe ſame daye rage cruell tene ne kynge phylomene reſkewed auenture whiche ſo frendely hym dyde cure maugre myght meneſtee handes went free hathed ſpreynt bloude whyle ayax proudely rode ſurquedy wylfulneſſe foly rage foule hardyneſſe naked body heade euerydele amyd foen armed bryght ſtele troyans ſuche ſlaughter made laye dead ſonne ſhade throughout felde thelamon amonge rode woodder lyon troian none might tho withſtāde held bloudy ſworde hand wonder naked rode without wounde ſo longe abode ¶and guydo maketh reherſayle wryteth eke great meruayle vnſlayne might ſo longe contune whan thynge ſhapen fortune myght falle euer thynge weale wo ioye aduerſyte whan one ſhall dye whan ſhall eſcape ſhe ala alder fyrſt iape brynge man vnwarely myſchaunce whan beſte weneth haue aſſuraunce ladye tranſmutacyon lyke fell worthy thelamon ſame daye whiche foly pryde amonge foen gan ſo ferre ryde ylyche freſhe ryght began ¶and ſlewe perce many manly man hym ſelfe toke maner hede knightly herte ſo deuoyde drede tyll parys ſawe great hardyneſſe howe knight dyd oppreſſe enchaſynge ſo mortally narowe without abode anone toke arowe extoxycat ſharpe venymous ire fell deſpyteous ſhot hym ſelfe tyde ſayth guydo ſmyt hym ye ſide hurte ſaye felte well muſt deye ¶and whan ſawe none remedye rode ſuppryſed enuye thrughout ye preſe ſword aye hand tyme parys fonde ¶and vnto hym pale chere ſpake ſayd anone ye ſhall ¶parys quod mortall wounde thyne arrowe ſharpe ſquare yground hath fynally lyfe put diſpeyre neuer grece haue repeyre ryght ſo ſhall ſhorte concluſyowne awaye ſhape troye towne thy lyfe thou entre ſhalte herte venym byt ſo ſore gayne none death ¶but yet tofore yelde vp breth truſte ryght well may ſocour thou ne ſhalte predeceſſour go afore depe downe hell pluto eternally dwell ryght neceſſarye thy time ſet thou maieſt tarye trouth morgage thy corſe haſt ſhall make deuorſe atwyxe quene heleyne twynne ſonder eke falſe cheyne whiche linked colour wedlocke hath ſo longe ſhet vnder locke fraude falſe engyne alſo ¶but nowe knotte ſhalbe broke two ryght hande trouth darayne cauſe onely twayne werre many worthy knyght lyfe hath loſte many wight outher ſyde ſake ſhall ende make loue foule auoutrye ¶for fynally parys thou ſhalte dye handes thy chaunce ye word ſword gan enhaunce aboue heade ſmote hym face fell dead ſelfe place heade hath parted twayne ryght forthwith ſaine ¶ayax ala mortall wounde fell dead alſo gruflynge vnto grounde full pyteouſly troye haue parys take vp weye bore hym home theyr cyte ¶but dyomede duke meneſtee many greke rydynge enuyrowne sewed chaſe euen towne cauſe tytan gan lowe downe arke dayes bowe weſt vnder rowes redde heſperus gan lyght ſhede ſaye drewe nyght grekes repeyred home aryght eueryche theim lodgynge place take theyr reſte nyghtes ſpace ¶saue reade agamenowne grekes made faſt towne ſette theyr tentes pauylyons pryde faſt wall habytacles newe manſyons troye dyſpeyred ouer refute could grekes let aſſent faſt theyr gate ſhette nyght walles wake ouer ſuche wo make cyte parys ſo dead fynally nowe reade wepe crye ſorowe euer one nowe al ye ſonnes priamꝰ gone fortune ala hath theim ſo appeyred theyr lyfe nowe dyſpeyred hope good welfare perpetually lyue care vnto death faſte bye nowe maner remedye vpon ſyde refute none theym kepe cloſe wythin wall ſe pyteous thynge ¶and ſuche wo maketh kynge ¶for parys death deadly ſmerte hym thought platly wofull herte recureles would braſt ryue tweyne teares gan dyſtylle reyne would tho ſorowe deye ¶and quene ala ſhall ſeye ¶hecuba owne mother deare crieth wepeth woful cheare ¶of pollycene ſo wo begone ſyſtren alſo euerychone haue theyr heir theyr clothes torne yf theyr owne death yſworne drery wo pyteous peyne ¶but fayre quene heleyne wayleth cryeth deadly cheare eyen whych whylom ſo cleare forderked dolefull teares ſmerte corp ſodaynly ſhe ſterte clypped yt armes twayne pyteouſly embrace reſtrayne lyke ſhe would dye anone ſtyll ſhe laye dombe ſtone marbyll colde lymmes craumpiſhing redy towarde buryinge tyll men force corp hent ſhe heyr chekes rente tho ſhe fallen rage chaunged ala vyſage natyfe coloure rody hewe whylom freſhe roſe newe nowe ſhe lyke vnto aſhes colde wyth handes aye togyther folde ſelfe ſhe ſmote pale face euer amonge corp ſhe embrace ſwownes ſhe fell grounde twenty tymes wept full wounde wyth wo ſhe awhaped amate comforte ala diſconſolate herte beynge inly deſyrous rage paſſynge furyous dye attones owne knyght towarde death encloſed ſyght ſhe lyſt lyue nowe ¶and trowe neuer man woman ſawe fall ſuche diſtreſſe ſuche diſioynt deadly heuyneſſe wo ſo pyteouſly yraue cleopatre goynge graue wofull teſbe fro kaue ſterte whan ſhe ſelfe ſmote vnto herte ¶nor faythfull trewe oreſtylle ſhe ſawe lord agayne ¶marcus prolancus vnto ſhyppe gone loue fell downe dead anone ¶nor ſorowe trewe iulia ¶nor feruence faythfull porcia whych one fell dead ſodaynly ſhe ſawe bloud ſpent ſo cruelly lordes dredfull gardment ¶and portia ſo trewe entent lorde brutus loſt lyfe bycauſe ſhe myght haue knyfe wyth rolys red ſlewe ſelfe ala alſo ſelfe caſe ¶arthemyſya quene tarſe londe mauſalus graue whan ſhe foude owne knyght whoſe bone ſmale full wofully wyth cheare pale poudre made dranke euery morowe ¶but wo furyous ſorowe theſe echone yet may atteyne ¶vnto ſorowe quene heleyne fynally wyll ſelfe fordo parys ſake ſhe loued ſo ſhe wyll lyue daye awreke playnly yf ſhe maye vpon lyfe rather dyſſeuere thus wo aye ſhe doth perſeuere herte parys ſat ſo depe ¶alas ſayth woman wepe yes doubtles haue nature though ſo wo endure yet fayne ſalte teares fynde plenty ynough thryr owne kynde ſorowles morne compleyne ¶i ſaye quene heleyne wyth wo wounded herte fro death ſhe wende ſterte deathes darte herte made ryue yet ſhe roſe agayne fro death lyue onely grace fell rage euery wo proceſſe muſt aſwage ouer gone waſted myracle eche venym made ſome tryacle euery wo hath remedye ¶for though heleyne tho fayn wold dye kynde ne would aſſent yet therto ſodaynly ſlea ſelfe wo woman man ſhulde wyte lyſte wo endyte leſt vnto tedyous heren paynes furyous cruell wo lamentacion whych would meue compaſſyon ſothe wryte euerydele herte though made ſtele ¶for kynge pryam quene alſo ſuche routhe pyteous wo ſe wepe furyouſly complayne felte much payne ¶as dyd almoſt hym parys ¶herof pryam deuyſe rage mortall wo amyd temple ſacred iuno ordayned hath full buſy cure corp ryche ſepulture haſte therin made ſhette ſotheneſſe ſhould lette tell rytes gyſe made theyr paynim wiſe coſtes buryinge ſhould longe taryinge ceryouſly theron abyde wherfore nowe let ouerſlyde paynim rite ſuperſticious ¶howe pantiſilia quene amazonis comming ayde troians ſlayne pyrrhus achylles ſonne ca xxxiiii telle wyll kyng priamus cōmaūded hath miſchyefe nede troye towne onely drede ſhytte theyr gate ſtrongly maye therupon nyght daye kepe watche ſhortly troye dyſconſolate theyr olde ioye refute wepe ſorowe make ne durſt vndertake agayne grekes felde gone ¶tyll daye kynge agamenon meſſager good auiſement pryamus troye hath ſent requyrynge manhode lyke knyghte yſſue wyth grekes fyght wonte wyth chyualrye ¶but kynge pryam axinge gan denye ſhortly ſayd ſent ne would aſſignement one paſſe gate towne owne free electiowne whan euer lyſt without compellynge ¶and yet ſothe cauſe taryinge ¶was hardy quene femynye towarde troye faſt gan hye lande lyttell regyon whych bokes make mencion ſcyte fyrmamente plage oryent ¶and called reygne amazonis cuſtome vſe onely woman therin ſhall abyde wonte armed ryde haue armes great experyence theyr laboure theyr dylygence fynally haue exercyſe fro daye daye martes hygh ſeruyce ¶and ouermore theyr cuſtome vſaunce daye made remembraunce man ſhall nygh nere yf thre monthes yeare ¶this ſaye iune apryll maye woman haue cuſtome aye vnto yle lytell beſyde men ſelfe abyde fro yere yere togyther euerychone vnto men theyr lande gone abyde regyon tyll tyme cometh concepcion wythout taryinge longer whyle anone home vnto theyr ile repeyred countre vnto tyme delyuered faſt chylde borne lacke kepynge lorne foſtred tyll thre yeres agone amonge woman ryght anone yle beſyde adiacent vnto men chylde haſte ſent kynde maſculyne yf fall femynyne woman abyde ſtyll ſhall tyll actes mercyall full well expert ſhe eke knowe ſpere haddle drawe bowe lyke ſtatutes regyon whych bookes make mencyon ſette betwene ewrope aſya ¶and lande pantaſilia whylom lady chyefe gouerneſſe full renowmed ſtrength hardineſſe thrugh ye worlde length brede yet ſothe ſpeake womanhead myght ſhe huge pryſe ſhe vertuous wyſe wonder dyſcrete honeſt name notwythſtandynge excellence fame renowne armes glorye conqueſt high victorye moſt ſurmountynge drede woman rede ſothely yet bookes bere wytneſſe womanhead gentylneſſe kepte ſo nothynge aſterte ¶the whych loued wyth hole herte worthy hector wyth myght onely ſo good knyght ioye worldly pleſaunce harty eaſe ſoueraygne ſuffyſaunce ſothe ſhe wake wyncke euer one vpon thynke fayth wythout ſlouthe vnto hym ſhe bonde trouthe confederate olde affectiowne ſhe herde troye towne beſeiged grekes fell thys hardy quene lyſt longer dwell haſteth faſt euer ſhe maye towarde troye infull good araye worthy woman lande full well experte preued hande well horſed eke armed rychely fynde companye thouſande maydens rydyng ſide worthy quene durſt well abyde wyth brought ſtele armed bryght loue hector owne trewe knyght waye faſt ſhe gan ſpede helpe hym yf ſhe ſe cauſe nede nothynge ſhe could delyte towarde faythfully quyte luſt hertes ioye ¶but ſhe come troye hath hard tell relacyowne dead moſt worthy renowne ſhe ſo louynge ſo trewe anone ſhe gan chaunge cheare hewe pyteouſly gan wepe crye fared ſothe ſhe would dye wo hertely heuyneſſe thought ſhe would thrugh wortthyneſſe auenge death platly ſhe maye grekes ſo vpon daye ¶she prayeth pryam wt great affectiowne open gate towne go grekes fyght maye knowe expert aright woman great worthyneſſe quene famous hardyneſſe ſo kynge hopynge beſte without abode graunted requeſte next morowe whē phebꝰ ſhone ful ſhene ¶and tofore goth philomene noble kinge wt pafflagonye knightes manye folowed worthy eneas troyan eke dan pollidamas quene pantaſilla gate called dardanica towarde grekes proudly yſſued oute woman rydynge aboute whych anone grekes eſpye felde gan faſt hye fyrſte worthy meneſte pantaſylla dyd ſe wyth ſporres made ſtede gone wyth ſpere rode anone ¶of quene aſtoned neuer dele kaught ſpere ſquared wele round ye ſhafte head well grounde coupe ſmet hī downe groūd maugre hym reued ſtede haſte came dyomede cruelly quene gan ryde ſhe faſt ſyde rode eke plate bryght ſhene met wyth theyr ſperes kene hytte ſo fell diomede myght manlyhead ſhe made ſadell leſe myght tho cheſe deſpyte men echone hath ſhelde berafte anone delyuereth proudly ſhe rode mayde vpon abode lyke tygre gredyneſſe lyke ſothe lioneſſe daye ſhe fared rydynge vp downe amonge grekes till thelamowne gan beholde ſlaughter ſhe made high deſpyte rancour ouerlade myght yre ſuſtene gan reyne horſe fall vpon quene ¶but ſhe comynge dyd eſpye fell melancolye mortally maugre knightes grounde ſhe made fall grekes put ſo great diſraye euer ſhe rode ylke daye ne might afore ſuſtene helpe kyng philomene myn auctour recordeth boke amyd felde thelamon ſhe toke ſent forth hie renowne pryſoner towarde troye towne ¶tyll vnto reſkuſe came dyomede cruelly gan lede fell vnwarely huge route knyghtes rydynge aboute theyr hādes maugre al might delyuereth lyke manly knyght whych tyme hardy quene anone woman aboute euerichone grekes hath afore playne wryt guydo ſo mortally belayne ſhe made neceſſytee felde wyth ſworde fle verely ſemed incredible leue maner impoſſyble ſe woman grekes ſo enchaſe might abide afore face felde wiſe ſtande dryue ſelfe ſtronde downe clyffe ſalte ſee ſlewe ſo huge great plentee fynally dyſtroyed euermore vtterly acloyed ¶ne dyomede ſtande tho diffence knighthod made theim reſiſtence daye partye grekes ſtode ſturdy wall alone helpe chefe ſuccour ¶but worſhyp honour pantaſilla made memorye repeyred conqueſt victorye wyth woman troye towne vpon houre phebus goyng downe ¶and ſyde hardy quene ¶armed ſtele rode kynge phylomene pryam hath wyth great reuerence knightly receyued diligence theim refreſhe euery maner thinge might vnto theyr lykinge theyr hertes could beſt deuyſe ¶and ful goodly wyſe thanked hath noble hardy quene goodneſſe lyſt ſene helpe great nede offred guydo reade hath treaſour rycheſſe hopynge fully worthineſſe vpon grekes auenged kepe hym ſafe cyte maugre grekes whych theim ſaye naye ¶for reade daye daye ſlinte proudly theim aſſayle agayne whoſe ſwerde myght auayl mortally ſhe made theyr ſydes blede ¶tyll menelay fro kinge lycomede repeyred neptolonyus bokes called eke pirrhus whylom ſonne cruell achillles ſe full huge preſe grekes goynge enuyron ¶and ſucceſſyon ¶borne heyre achilles hath receyued myrmydones great honour great ſolempnyte glad theyr yonge lorde ſe echone made affiaunce eke ſworne bonde aſſuraunce lyfe deathe trewe liege chaunge newe obeye luſt maner thynge ¶and agamenon kinge made knight thelamonius wyth ſwerde gyrte anone pirrhus sayinge ſelfe place yt baudrik hym enbrace ¶take hede quod mine owne coſin deare reſemble manhode chere knighthod eke worthineſſe thy father ſothfaſtneſſe tyme ſo noble knight ouermore thy full might auenge death thou thy payne ¶and thē grekes worthy duke twayne full humbly began downe knele ſet ſporre vpon eyther hele maner golde bourned bryght whyle pirrhus made knighte ye haue herde full high preſence great honour due reuerence lyke cuſtome grekes layes rytes vſed tho dayes anone hath kyng agamenon full glad chere great affection delyuered hym fully ſentence armes hole without difference achilles life bare worthy father ſhoulders ſquare nexte heyre lyne diſcente treaſour alſo tente armure deliuered anone vnto pirrhus grekes euerychone eyght dayes ſuynge hoſte full ſolempnely halowe honour yong knyght▪ til morow whē phebꝰ ſhone ful bright lyght ſhineth fro ſo fer diffaced hath ſtreames ſterre lucifer dayes meſſagere grekes gan plate bryght clere enarmed daye ſoure ſwete fulle purpoſe wyth theyr fone mete manfully theyr tentes wide agaynſt troyans began ride warde warde proudly felde pirrhus bare daye vpon ſhelde father armes lyke ſayth guydo ſame vpon alſo cote armure became hym wele forth rode armed bright ſtele caſually formeſt mette fyrſt wyth pollydamas knyght troye full manly man ¶and furyouſly pirrhus ran horſebacke myghty ſwerde gan hurtle berde myghtely hatefull ſtryfe ¶pollydamas loſt lyfe ne ben reſkued without taryinge phylomene noble worthy kinge onely knighthod worthyneſſe ¶to pirrhus haſtely gan dreſſe ſwerde ſmit ſyghte horſe made alighte ſtroke might ſuſtene ſothfaſtly worthy phylomene pirrhus ytake anone saue knightes aſſembled one pafflagonye came reſkue pirrhus aye ſo fyerſly gan purſewe vpon king myrmydones beſet myſchefe amonge great preſe many knight noble kynge yſlayne reſkuynge ſtode death ſo ſtreyght caſe ¶tyl fortune came pollydamas reſkuſe full myght delyuer quyte lyke knight ſotheneſſe ſuche reſyſtence ¶of pirrhus knightes ſtanding diffence aye miſchyef ſtode king philomene ¶tyll pantaſilla femenie quene woman great companye gan thinge auenture eſpye echone delyte theyr armure daye clad white veryly lylye floure ſnowe yt flaketh frō iubyters towre whyteneſſe freſher ſene felde hardy quene firſte amonge grekes chees proudly fall myrmydones amonges rydinge vp downe thē vnhorſeth hie renowne ſlewe vpon euery ſyde makinge theyr renges ſeuer wyde tyll thelamon furyous heate ſpere vnwarely mete rage ſmote playne ſhe anone ful lyfely roſe agayne ¶and wt ſwerd ſo marketh thelamown frō horſe ſhe made light downe plat grounde handes twayne woman theyr buſy payne make theyr quene ſtede recure ¶and ſtode auenture life worthy philomene pirrhus knightes ſo kene maugre men haue take geyneth diffence make grekes haue ſo ſtrongly beſet ¶and forth lad might bet toward theyr tentes throughout al felde thinge quene behelde woman aboute rode purſewed without abode fynally haue ſo ſewed force reſkued maugre manhode myrmidon ¶and pantaſilla ſo mercyles vpon grekes neceſſyte force crueltee afore ſwerde durſt abyde ¶but pirrhus ſawe great pryde knightes loud gan crye ſayde ſhame villanye woman ſo leſe theyr lande ſlayne ſo felly hande wherfore echone hertes doth reſume aſſent let v nowe conſume pryde none awaye eſcape ſome remedye ſhape ylke daye theyr force confounde shamefull reporte v ſhall rebounde perpetually ſlepe wake ¶and pirrhus gan ſwerde take furyouſly wyth knyghtly chere hardy quene happed heare ¶all pirrhus knightes ſpake lyſt one tourne bake thret take hede platly ſhe dreade right proudly gan drawe nere ſayde anone ye ſhall heare ¶oh thou pirrhe ſonne achilles ſlewe hector knyghthod pereles trenys trecherye malice onely falſe enuye vnware nothinge aduerte whych neuer maye herte grene ſticketh remembraunce vpon death vengeaunce ſyt well ſemeth vnto death venged vpon fyrſte thy father bloud loue ſo gentyll ſo good deth ſhuld al ye world cōplayne onely men theyr buſy payne quyte death woman eke alſo theyr myght helpe eke therto right requyreth without excepcion full execution nowe ſtande ſame plyte thou haſt v wonnen deſpite power ſhortly ſentence thou ſhalt haſte haue experyence knowe force ſothly euerydele right ſhorte tyme truſte right wele felde ſhedynge thy bloud wherfore pirrhus gan wood tygre bore wood lyon fret coloure complexion ire fell deſpytous toke ſpere pale furyous ran al myght payne agaynwarde ſhe liſt feyne encountred hym deuoyde feare pirrhus fyrſte brake ſpere albe myght remeue ſadell lyttel greue ſhe agayne ſo ſore gan hytte ſtede maye ſytte deſcendeth endlonge playne vp roſe full great diſdayne toke ſwerde hande anone made ſtede lyne ryght gone vpon quene paſſynge worthineſſe inwardly hate woodneſſe herte yfret ſmet many ſtroke euer ſhe ſat ſtyll oke force yre pale efte agayne ſhe made auale earthe maugre payne thus fyght laſteth theym twayne large whyle till myrmydones haue take theyr lorde force ye preſe made horſe recure agayne ¶and tyme ſelfe playne baner deſcended downe worthy kinge great agamenowne kinges duke endlonge grene theyr wardes wonder ſene prudently felde battayled hath troians mortally aſſayled ¶but tho haſte kynge phylomene ye haue herde reſkued quene hath thanked worthineſſe knightes gan dreſſe ¶and pantaſilla aſſembled one vpon grekes gan gone men may ſe wt ſperes ſharpe grounde eueryche beare vnto grounde men maye ſe proudly without lacke manly knightes renne horſe backe ¶and woman mortally oppreſſe fell grekes theyr hardyneſſe onely force myghty quene dead laye couerynge al grene ¶wherwith came dan pollydamas fro death reſkued eke eneas ¶kinge eſdras eke troye cyte ¶and tho wardes gan togyther fle eyther partye fell furious moſt neptolonius pirrhus hight ye grekes champiowne irous wood troye towne made ſwerde theyr fleſhe byte ¶and pantaſilla proudly quyte ne ſpareth wyth mortall woundes wide grekes ſlee vpon euery ſyde theyr confuſyon ¶and pirrhus fall glawcon halfe brother pollydamas anthenor eke father pirrhus ſo cruell yre melancolye newe ſet fyre smote glawcon ſo toke hede amonge preaſe fell downe dead ¶and pantaſillya woman ¶the ſame tyde pirrhus fall ſyghte rode eke agayne lyke manly knyght hurtle horſe backe yfere auenture ſwerdes ſtyffe clere eueryche made alyghte hatefully fote ſo fyghte longe myght wynne tyll made force twynne wardes wente atwene meane pirrhus hardy quene ¶and tyme dan pollydamas wood yre herte amyd grekes brother deathe mette loue ſleth without mercy hateful tene alone worthy quene suche ſlaughter grekes make felde vtterty forſake gan fle theyr tentes downe tyll dyomede ayax thelamowne pyrrhus eke made tourne agayne ſothe ſo ouerlayne ne myght daye releue thus faughte tyll drewe eue moſt domage grekes ſyde tyll phebus gan bryght chayre hyde lowe weſt ſhroude lyght vnder courtayne blacke nyght eyther parte thought beſt departe drawe theyr reſte toke theyr eaſe nyght may moneth ſuynge day daye without interrupcion fought yfere albe mencion made therof wryte ſpecyall perſon generall euer dyd euyll well troye boke fynde neuer dele saue quene lyke wryt guydo woman hundred hath forgo ſlayne thylke moneth daye death playnly ſhe maye shall well quyt ſo fortune fauorable frendly contune face chaunge contrarye ſhe euery daye ſo varye ala whyle ſelde one ſoiourne gan fro quene loke awaye tourne enhaſte vngoodlyhead attropoſe breake lyues threde ſtorye playnly ſhall lere beningly ye lyſt heare fatall houre harde remewe cruel deth mā may eſchewe lyfe fynally eſcape specially parchas haue ſhape approche gan may none bene ala whyle hardy quene ¶whych daye furyous wrothe felde troye goth gan grekes proudly ſette alderfyrſt pirrhus met mortall hate indignaciowne ſhe haſte renges downe rode vnto ſwyftly ſtede whoſe ſpores ſharpe made ſides blede mette ſperes reſte bare ſo euen markynge breſte theyr ſhaftes ſothly tale gan ſhyuer peces ſmale without bowynge backe chine neyther made enclyne saue head forged harde ſtele pantaſillia grounde wele pirrhus herte perced hath ſo depe plate ſoth maile might kepe ſharpneſſe ſperes head bloud party redde ſtroke grekes gan eſpye aſtoned loude gan crye attones noyſe ſowne vpon quene felde came downe compaſſe wyſe goynge enuyrowne thrugh proweſſe high renowne defendeth meruayle ala ſo ſore gan aſſayle hewe haue baſenet amyd grekes ſo thycke ſhe beſet wyth ax ſwerdes ſquare ſhelde ſothe made bare ſhoulders naked eke ala mayle hewen rere bra ¶and pirrhus like founde anguiſhe onely grene wounde doubte playnly ſhould eſkape towarde quene faſte gan rape auenged whatſoeuer fall amyd felde amonge grekes ¶and ſhe ſawe came ſo faſte force onely mete yet ſhe caſt wyth ſwerde fyrſte gan aſſayle ſtroke happed fayle amonge preſe ſo narowe ſhe beſette ¶and pirrhus ſworde ſo ſharpe whet ſodaynly arme ſmet ala none armure lette raceth al ſhoulder bone quene fel downe dead anone malice venge herte yre fret ſo ſore chere anger pale hath hewen peces ſmale whych foule cruell dede ¶but euer one pirrhus gan ſo blede nigh death mortall wounde lacke bloud fell grounde traunce full longe groflynge laye tyll knyghtes haſte may haue take vp laid ſhelde dolefully home felde haue borne wounded ¶and woman quene ala ſorowe inwarde deadly wo ſawe theyr lady ago dead ſo deſyrous haſte wood furyous rage without gouernayle grekes gan newe aſſayle auēge quene wer ſo herty kīde ſlewe ſothly fynde two thouſād grekꝭ thē ſo wood oh ala great dyſioynt ſtode onely lacke haue gouernour ſhe gon yt theyr chiefe ſuccoure whych alſo ſpeake hardyneſſe woman al lady mayſtreſſe hande rede oh ye troians ye ſtande great dread amid ye felde gouernaunce daye come vnhappy chaunce nowe haue ye leder none guyde farewell truſte euery ſyde grekes vpon ſo ſtronge ye felde maye kepe longe caſte felly quyte ſame daye dare lyſt endyte wryt homeward drawe ten thouſand troians grekꝭ ſlawe theyr wardes came attones downe mortally wythout excepciowne kylle ſlee al withſtode moſt vpon woman wood auenged playnly reade euery halfe theyr bloud ſhede without mercy remyſſyowne chaſynge troyans home towne felde ma none abode pyteouſly tho wyth ſtode ne none recure caſte kepe theyr towne ſhit gate faſte theyr hope clene agone fyght wyth theyr fone theyr truſt knyghthod away theyr worthy men ſlayne welawaye refute none theyr cyte kepe cloſe maye none theim thought might kepe longe walles ſo mighty ſo ſtronge plenty vytayle though ye worlde attones aſſayle may ſure kepe theim euermore men ſhall wyn yet neuertheleſſe earely eke late grekes made tofore euery gate full myghty watche awayte full ſtronge wyth preuy ſpyes goynge amonge theyr foen none eſcape away none engyne ferforth maye ¶and whyle wythin troye towne make deſcriptiowne quene ſo great ſorowe euery wyght eue morowe ſhe ala ſlayne mede aldermoſt ne myght haue dead corp burye graue reuerence wyth honour dewe whych gan grekes ſewe great prayer wyth great buſyneſſe vayne ydelneſſe theyr requeſt yt grekes ſo wrothe fynally wyth many ſondry othe onely malyce hote enuye dead corp theim denye ſhortly ſayde mortall enmyte houndes ſhall deuoured gayne rācour cōpeſſe ¶but pyrrhus gentylneſſe ne would aſſent ſo foule dede wood wroth cruell dyomede sayde openly ſyttynge ſhe fayle buryinge ſlaine hadde ſo many worthy man thus ſtryfe amonge grekes gan great rumoure alteraciowne tyll laſte vnder troye towne haue dead corp ytake cruelly profounde lake haue caſt let lye vnto troye agayne wyll hye tell forth lyue pyne oh cruell mar yt haſt made fyne thyne yre al ye worthy blode troye ala haſt thou ſo wood agaynſt ſlee theyr knightes haſt thou let thy bitter venim fall theim ala thou ſterre infortunate wyth worlde make debate oh hatefull ſterre hote combuſt drye fyryirous grounde enuye haſty euer ful diſcenſion coleryk thy complexion murdre death aye thy delyte takinge vengeaunce moſt thin appetite firſt meuer anger hate roote contek cauſinge debate ſtryfe murmur moſt thy deſyre fearfull loke wylde fyre gaſtfull euer thy wood ſyght leuen ſo flawminge thy lyght lyke twyncklynge ſpakes redde great fyres abrode ſo ſprede conſumynge aye melancolye hertes embraced wyth enuye thy wrathe aye ſo fretynge ſo kene cauſeth men longe lene comſumpt ſklendre browne citren hewed vnmercyable right euell thewed wonder ſleyghty engenyous compaſſynge ſuſpecyous tryſte ſolen full heuyneſſe aſſentynge curſedneſſe awaytinge death roberye murdre alſo trecherye without remors conſcyence venymous thine influence helper arte vnto falſe treaſon houſe scorpyon crowned arte caprycorne bull thy kingdome lorne therin thy deiection thy power loſte dominacion haſt alſo thy ſubiection exyle werre chaynes pryſon proſcripſyon captyuyte thy malyce troye cyte would god could chyde aryghte haſt theim kydde thy fell myghte thy rancour hooly outtraunce firſt theim vengeaunce ſperes ſharpe ſwerdes kene whette nowe pryſon encloſe ſhet vengeably dare grekes fell aye lying holde maner wyſe thy temple ſacrafyſe nother bulles wt bore wylde beaſtes euer vnmylde tygres beares wood lyon whych thou arte ſouerayne patron hold brymſtone ſmoke thyne aulters whiche art ſo felly wroke theym ala worſt thou haſt ſhad chefe thy gall amonge ſelfe bryng treaſon fayned trouthe ſymulacyon make hertes amonge ſelfe deuide lo ſerpent dyſcorde gan glyde full ſlyly tyll haue caughte place voyde awaye happe grace venym dyſcenſyon ſpred regyon common borough towne cyte amonges men high lowe degre hertes loue one farewell fortune theyr grace clene agone dyſcorde holdeth reſydence well worſe ſwerde peſtylence worſe ferre nere foe famylyere maye harme yf luſt enemye vpon men truſt deſcriue ſhortly clauſe roote trewe cauſe myſchyefe confuſyon euery lande diſcenſcion peryllous yf pryuye recorde take troye cyte founde fortune frendly aye nede tyll longe hid hate gan abrode ſprede prudence ſothly hath prouyded renge ſelfe deuyded shall recureles tourne wylde waſte dweller deſolate haſte mar enuye lorde amonge ſelfe ſowen hath diſcorde agayne whych maye ſucoure worſe werre ſothly ſemeth treaſon cured vnder fayned peace ¶and roote olde anchiſes ¶with ſonne called eneas dan anthenor pollydamas haue contriued amonge theym vtterly vnder veil conceyued ſecretly fall grekes troye haue fyrſt maye theyr owne lyues ſaue ſome engyne ſleyghtes treate ſo maye caſte maner waye would rather traytours troye pryuely ſo ſpyed couertly grekes ben allyed ſtande hole wyth towne trouthe wylfully neclygence ſlouthe suraunce othe olde made towne refuſe playnly concluſyowne allyaunce let ſlake ſlyde theyr lygaunce ſet alſo aſyde theyr aduyſe thought beſte theim caſte lyue reſte meryer eke erneſt game ſaue theyr life wandre forth ſhame wylfully dye miſchyefe trayiſh town held reprefe might eſcape ſelfe alyue lyſt nothynge towne ſtryue ſought ſothe ſoure ſwete meane waye lyue queet therupon haue theyr waye nome vnto kinge yt come preſence full couert wyſe vnder coloure began deuyſe tell theyr tayle ſo fynally ¶theyr counſayle pryam vtterly maner reckles purſewe grekes peace ſo get maye yelde againe king menelaye without ſtryfe freſhe quene heleyne ouermore diſdayne harmes done parys gon full yore citheron iuſtly reſtore bvt oh ala falſe iniquytye counſayle roſe vnder ſecrete venim ſugre vnder gall well wyſte grekes ne would accorde concluſyowne haue peace troie towne whyles ſuch miſchyefe brought treate therof ſothe nought ¶for pryamus thē hecuba quene ſonnes pollycene yet left wyth towne myght haue reygned longe ſucceſſyowne grekes full repented vnto peace hooly aſſented ¶but counſayle gyuen late sythen grekes well elder date profered fyrſt tenedowne aduyſe kynge agamenowne fynall peace ſhortly ſeyne would reſtore agayne heleyne amendes requyred reaſon damage wrought cytheron meſſangers fyrſte whan ſente pryamus wolde aſſente requeſte iuſtly brought peace meanes ſought pryde denyed wylfulneſſe ala ſo guyded lacke onely wyt prudence nowe haue wt coſt great diſpence ſlaughter men many great damage ſharpe ſhoutes cruel rage abyde fully mortall werre full ſure wyll differre tyme forth treate peace lyſte nothynge ſo reckeleſſe vnaduyſed ought trowe ye wyll ſo lyghtly go home grece without recompence wolde ſeme neglygence speake therof wyll specyally troye cyte myſchyefe ſtande vpon fynall fate remedye ſhape late grekes thought ryght truſte troye ſtode luſte holdynge ſelfe veryly victours foen fully conquerous without doubte ambyguyte counſayle ylke enee ¶of anthenor anchyſes ye haue herde treate peace ne roſe ſothe doubleneſſe onely treaſon hyghe falſeneſſe pryamus conceyueth theyr chere lyke boke ye ſhall ¶for daye whan pryamus ſonne called amphymacus counſayle helde towne three haue made ſuggeſtyowne vnto kynge touchynge treate anone diſcrete aduyſe prudently woulde aſſente gan vndergrope playnely mente onely wytte diſcrecion put execucion makynge therof maner delaye proudely ſtandyng baye anthenor without reuerence spake kynge open audyence ſhortly ſaide ſterne chere lyſt counſayle heare therafter platly thou mayſt cheſe thou wylt thou wynne leſe fyne thou getteſt worke thy counſayle kynge wonder ſoberly anſwered agayne full beningenely syr anthenor ye ought greue myne entente repreue wyſe counſayle prudent rede conclude common ſpede people ſaluacyon wyte ryght well iuſtly reaſon vnder ſuger cured gall preiudyce lyeges cauſynge myſchyefe fyne wyll vtterly declyne ryght requyreth alder eaſe ſemeth ſhould diſpleaſe thy conceyte none offence euery man holden prudence worſt leue better take wyſedome ſewe folye forſake remedye ſeke ſore worde troian anthenor ſodayne yre gan chaunge bloud abreydynge fete ſtode full felly ſayde vnto kynge ¶now ſykerly wonder thynge wyſedome auyſeneſſe blynded ſo wylfulneſſe ye maye ſyde ſe great myſchyefe aduerſytee vpon euery ſyde maye diſſimule hide diſioynt playnly ſtande foen alſo hande haue beſet wall rounde aboute feare dare yſſue oute ſo bolde vndo gate fyght v deadly hate ſo feble ſo ſtronge ſothly yet haue amonge fyfty kynges worthy renowne confederat deſtructiowne therupon platly wyll abyde whych vowed haue theyr great pryde neuer parte henſe fro towne tyll walles tourned vp ſo downe worthy ſonnes alſo dead wont helpe nede manly knyghtes ſlayne euerychone v ſaue remedye none vayne treaty dyffence wherfore read reaſon prudence ſlayne cyte leſe two harmes leaſt cheſe ſaye entente ſyttynge expedyent treate peace longer feyne herewythall reſtore agayne heleyne loue many worthy man hath loſt lyfe ſythen werre began nowe parys vnder ſtone ygraue beſt rede ſothe ye maye haue ſende home agayne menelaye profre fer forth ye maye reſtore within littell whyle harmes done parys yle whych men wont cithera call reade afore wyth word vp roſe amphimacus counſayle full contraryous ſhortly ſayde ſhall ¶as anthenor hath rade degre euer thus without reſpyte ſpake hygh deſpyte thou anthenor haue eſpyed wele may truſte neuer dele wyth v ſtande great nede trouth fayth nowe deade falſhed hath ſlayne ſtabilneſſe ſtede thy ſykerneſſe fynde ſothly varyaunce become fayth thy lygeaunce heſtes made ſtande wyth thy kinge thine othes ſo double meaninge hyd thy olde aſſuraunce become thy fayned falſe conſtaunce ſtede whych mutabylyte hath take place like ye maye ſe dewe chaunge thou art ſo remewable vpō ground thou mayſt ſtande ſtable thy trouth gone olde affectiowne yu ſhuldeſt haue ſtand ye towne fayth v lyue deye truſte hope exyled aweye thy perſone ſhortly wryte buſy arte kynge excyte diſencreaſe eſtate royall vnto grekes ſo thrall ſeke peace dread thou ſhouldeſt rather thy manlyhead haue profered citye diffende thy lyfe outraunce diſpende▪ wherfore ſothe aſſure rather ſhoulde endure twenty thouſande ſhall ſpere ſhelde vpon daye ſlayne felde thy worde holde prophecye procedeth trecherye doubilneſſe falſe treaſon vndermyninge prodycyon though thou outwarde ſhewe fayre venym hyd thy tayle doth repayre lyke ſerpent ſtyngynge vnder floures thereby fele ſuch counſayloures ¶and whyle wordes deſpytous ¶full bytingly hath amphymacus ¶all openly anthenor repreued counſayle ſo agreued seynge treaſon would mene tyll eneas gan go betwene floryſhed ſpeche full flatterye gan tale ſo modefye lyke mente trouth entente ¶but therin double attendemente ſpake one yet mente twayne ¶amphymacus onely refrayne attempre melancolye onely tyll might time eſpie like purpoſe maye procede execute fully vp dede founde ſpace vnder pretence trewe face tale gan breake oute many troyan ſtandinge aboute ſhortly ſayde concluſyowne touchynge diffence playnly towne howe henge onely balaunce hope truſt aſſuraunce cyte taken haue theyr flyght fynally manhod myght knyghthod togyther ago grekes haue ado theim ſtoutly fyght whych hath loſt many worthy knyght redy vpon v ſet dare gatꝭ vnſhet ala ſuppriſed ſo wyth dread ſemeth great nede ¶by good aduyſe ſeke meane matter ſhall v demeane ¶and parte ſothfaſtly ſaye knowe nowe none ſo redy waye prudentlye peace treate ¶but pyram ſodayne heate without abode cheare face pale rancoure gan interrupte tale attempre myght herte fretingely treaſon made ſmerte ¶and myght ſelfe reſtrayne thus ſayde vnto twayne anthenor alſo enee wonder greatly ye hardy trouthe ſhame ſo varye ye ſo rebell contrarye onely falſe colluſyon v brynge deſperacyon lyeges yf ſhall fayne falſe entente catche v trayne ala howe maye herte fynde agayne nature vnkynde whylom counſayle chefe euery thynge brought prefe ¶for ye abſente could nothynge fyne nowe ala ye caſte declyne awaye fro barayne lefte ſole remembre great dole wyght ala ſo chaunge ſhall truſte man ye founde double entente ye thynke aſſente counſayle aduyſe whylom ſente forth parys grece full yore ago ¶and anthenor thou woteſt thy ſelfe alſo thou fyrſte made imbaſſadour therupon chyefe counſaylour touchinge ſonde made exeon cauſe mocyon though ſothe parys ſhulde go grece thou woteſt well ſo ne durſte preſumpcion haue ſente parys vnto citheron without aduyce auctorytye eneas playnly vpon grekes werre haue gonne trowe ſothe neuer konne excuſe ſelfe aduyſed euerye thynge wrought deuiſed execute counſayle twayne parys went heleyne grounde roote ſpeake ſpeciall thou enee cauſe principall preſent alſo euery thing wrought grece ſhe hither brought ſothe regyowne neuer come towne thou haddeſt therto contrayre albe thou wouldeſt thy wordes fayre thy ſelfe excuſe audience thou knewe nought offence fully vnwittinge dede nowe ſonnes euerychone deade ye ſe alone deſtitute counſayle chyefe refute purſewe grekes peace foryetell reckles remembre infinite outrage mortall werre ſlaughter damage cruelte deſtructiowne haue wrought herupō towne veryly recorde dead accorde treate like ye deuiſe eſpye many ſondry wyſe entente right peryllous ſnare couertly vnder falſhed dare wyll confuſyon ye acheue entencion fynally ye haue ſhape impoſſyble eſcape shamefully myſchyefe dye without recure remedye fyne knowe doubte treate ye aboute ¶and ryght anone troian eneas yre rancoure ſo ameued agayne kynge ſwellynge herte ſodaynly dore ſterte awroke full many worde agayne kynge yſpoke wente waye anthenor alſo ¶and pyramus yre wo sodainly braſte wepe might ſelfe anguiſhe kepe anger fret vpon ſo ſore within ſelfe conceyuinge euydence diſcreſcyon couert guyle falſe treaſon cyte yſhapen haue auyſed dredynge aye theſe ylke twayne ſome engyne conſpyred trayne grekes would hym betrayet wherfore kynge caſte would ſaye shape awaye theyr malyce withſtande treaſon toke hande onely ryght dede founde vpon ſelfe myght agayne rebounde full execucyon theyr contryued conſpyracion reſorte agayne ful dewe wyſe onely theym gan fyrſte deuyſe treaſon treaſon conuenyent falſhed guerdon pertynente ſhamefull deathe fynall mede wherfore ſhape great nede ¶a remedye olde pryamus ¶calleth ſonne amphymacus pytyouſly alone twayne teares drowned gan complayne anthenor eneas ſayde ſonne take hede caſe thynke thy father deare yfere ſonnes lefte wyth alyue thou alone therfore blyue touching ye treaſon conſpyred yſworne eu • r fall let v toforne onely wyſedome away make maye fyrſt trappe theim take puruey theym euen ylyche iuſtly maye fall dyche whych haue made v ytreyned haſte let ſo ordeyned matter cloſe kept mewe fyne onely eſchewe ſlayue equite ryght place euen towarde night purpoſe playnly theyr ſake agayne houre counſayle make vnder coloure make call thou vnwarely ſhalt vpon fall knightes ſworne vnto matter ſecre right anone amphimacus aſſented vnto pryamus accompliſhe full ſecret wiſe fro poynt poynt ye haue herde deuyſe bvt ſothe ſayde full yore agone olde wiſe ye counſayle none worlde ſo pryuely ycaſte tyll platly laſte people whych rurall sayth yt ſecretes knowen earthe make mynde diſcure theim owne kinde nature vp caſt diſcloſe thinge men wont cloſe let euery man beware good counſayle go ferre abrode ſpecially lordes haue great nede men ſtande moſt dreade great awayte vpon layde happeth thinge ſayde one ſpoke lordes mouthe falleth ofte full kouthe reported yſprad full wyde many coſte theim ſtande aſyde ware ſodayne auenture ſome hap doth aſſure wyll fyrſte reporte amys therfore ſothe beſt beware kepe theyr tonge purpoſe caſte ſhould ronge ſpoke abrode amonge folkes rude gladly aye worſte conclude euery thynge newe reporte varyaunt vntrewe reaſon nothinge expowne folke towne lyke purpoſe deſyre fayre wiſpe fyre brenneth brighteſt blaſe sodaynly waſteth waſe ſuche folke platly truſte fire water holde fiſte beynge ylke indifferente hote nowe colde lyke theyr entente newe chaungeth ſo theyr courage calme foloweth ſodayne rage daye loue morowe hate truſte common laſteth date let lorde make ſecre nowe counſayle ronne enee pryam wende ful cloſe rumour winde aroſe falſe reporte ſo ferre yblowe eneas anthenor well knowe ende gynnynge euery maner thyng hole counſayle pryamus king ¶and two full one entente eke theyr aſſente conſpyred togyther ſworne couertly caſte waye aforne fynally troye cyte theyr engyne ſhall deſtroyed accorde caſte playnly thus hap kynge pryamus sende theim ſhortly conclude would come ſuch multytude armed men ſe nede ſhoulde nothing drede eneas cyte great power auctoryte bloud kynred allyed golde greatly magnyfyed cyte moſte ſpecyall myght power perygall ſayth guydo vnto kynge anthenor almoſt euery thynge▪ vnto hym egall power twayne one herte entyre conſpyred haue ſothe agayne towne fynally concluſyowne grekes myght haue ſuerte wyth theyr treaſour go lybertee theyr allyes borne troye towne brought deſtructyowne life good ſaufe without whyche tyme dan anthenor eneas pryamus hath ſente accomplyſhe fyne entente ¶and haſte ſo great route came knyghtes ſtuffed aboute therof aſtoned pryamus ¶and made ſende amphimacus commaundyng chaunge purpoſe well wyſſe counſayle cloſe ſygnes gan well vnderſtande matter whiche hande diſcured confuſyon bothe murder conſpyration apparceyuynge inwarde ſyght great power troyan knyght fauour eneas comon howe foſtred whiche proudely open audyence tofore kynge declareth ſentence fully concludyng maugre ſayth nay none meane waye refute gayne remedye ¶but onely peace ſo denye eſcapynge playnely none thervpon common euerychone one voyce gan calle crye counſayle gan greatly magnifye albe kynge therto al contrary eneas lyſte lenger tary dyfferre fyne purpoſe wonder irous ſee roſe full vngoodly ſpake vnto kynge ſhortely ſayde without taryinge ſo befall thou lefe lothe purpoſe pleaſed outher wrothe thou mayſt well truſte ſhall none fynally herken maugre thy wyll alſo myght ſame daye nyghte peace grekes ſhall trete ¶ whan kinge ſawe feruent hete bothe comon eneas gan anone diſſymule caſe prudence gan ſe tyme may none wherfore ſyth myght amende wiſely gan condeſcende purpoſe platly enee ſayde wolde goodly take gree except lyſte ordeyne ſo kynge lerned fayne agayne conceyte platly herte otherwyſe coulde aſterte coacte force vyolence ſawe aduertence myght dyuerte ſyde fraude ſowen ſo wyde without grutchynge falſely gaue aſſent anthenor ſhulde forth ſente comon choyſe treate towne whiche tofore inconcluſyowne grekes accorded fynally touchynge effecte ambaſſadrye fro poynt poynt wolde ſtonde variaunt fro toke hande afore hym full conceyued better chere receyued whyle anthenor treate grekes ſtoute ye haue harde peace fynall towne aboute euery wall troye gan aſcende blyue withe braunches many freſhe olyue token peace grekes eke agayne amyd fielde endelonge playne shewed myght ſene eke olyue luſty bowes grene ¶and confyrme fro poynt poynt nothinge ſtode diſioynte worthy kynge great agamenon commytted hath hyghe diſcrecion fully power auctorytie grekes playnely vnto three fyrſte peace treat vnto wyſe kynge crete ¶to vlixes dyomede cheſe mo thē thought nede wyll holde ſtable fynally variable ende platly make thervpon aſſuraunce take eyther parte bonde ſacrament ſo anthenor ywent aſyde worthy lordes three theyr liberte tumulte alone pryuely anthenor full trechery reſpecte falſhode doubleneſſe gan purpoſe vnto expreſſe behotynge traſhe cyte wolde make ſurety ¶that fyrſte hym ſelfe eneas shall fredom haue euery maner caſe playne power commited towne bvt kinge priam haſh aye ſuſpectiowne anthenor alſo enee ſhall deſtroye cytye ſelfe triſt hertye wo ſayde al beſt myſchyefe fall yet worſt myn aduerſytye bounde compelled neceſſytye maugre head maner raunſon lyfe make redempcyon vnto foen haue moſt herte ſe ryght well maye aſterte muſt paye gayneth ſuccoour good golde ryches treaſoure moſt foen dare denye yet ſtonde moſt ieopardye without refute hanginge balaunce ala conſtreyned wofull chaūce obeye theyr luſt mortally hate dryuen therto byrthe fate parchas haue deſtynye yſhape none engyne maye eſcape priā gan thus complayne anthenor came quene heleyne beſechynge embaſſadrye gentylneſſe ſpecyfye prudent medyacyon fynde awaye conſeruacyon eſtate fynally ſhe menelaye may reconſiled ſo fall treate holde lorde grace would reſtore vnto degre onely mercy high pytye ¶and anthenor vnto requeſt gaue audyence makynge beheſt would herte entere dilygent treate mattere therwithal hym ſhe toke leue done ſame eue anthenor pray god giue ſorowe grekes went next morowe onelye treate peace fynall whyle feaſte funerall holde troye myne auctour wryteth thus lorde called glaucus manly knight tofore lyuynge ſonne pryamus kynge ouer lyke ſayth guydo kynge pryam buſyed alſo pantaſylla body myght conſerued freſhly ſyghte loue hardy quene pured golde ſtones ſhene let make veſſell full royall fylde full wyth bawine naturall kepe corp corrupciowne tyll werre grekes towne treate yſtynted clene kynge called phylomene dead quene might affection carye home regyon aunceters buryed lyke maner olde antyquyte vayne ryme paſſe ouer vnto treatee atwene grekes troy cytee partye grekes reade fyrſte vlyxes diomede aſſygned kynge crete anthenor eneas mete yfere ſhortly ſentence conduyt firſt lycence noble wyſe agamenowne entred troye towne conueyinge eneas whoſe cōmynge ſuch ioye comunes whych thinges newe reioyce aye though rewe wenynge full well theyr opinyon good medyacyon vlyxes kinge crete diomede came eke treate theſe thre ſhoulde make faſte fynall peace euer laſte full ende theyr alder ſorowe therupon earely next morowe pryam let make conuocaciowne worthy within troye towne aſſembled al one wyſe vlyxes roſe vp anone tale gan ſuche wyſe prudently wordes deuyſe herken euery man hath ioye ſpecyally troye inwarde meanynge fraudelente full lyttell wyſt entente theyr pleaſaunce ſo could fayne fyrſte axeth thinges twayne one cytye would haue golde huge quantytye recompence harmes thynge axed alſo without abode amphymacus ſonne kynge pryamus perpetually exyled neuer entre troye cyte golde prayer raunſon done ſuggeſtyon anthenor falſe malycyous onely contraryous ſhoulde treate peace reckles ſaye trouthe amphimacus therfore ſothe ſerpent enuyous nowe hath founde time byte though would cruelly quyte trouthe onely entente ¶therfore full expedyent prudence euery man charge tunge ouer large trouthes ſayne wyſedome ſometyme fayne diſſymule aduerſytye specyally men trouble ſe theyr ſpeche maye auayle better theyr tunge fayle folyly theyr domage ſpeake men muſt amonge cure ouer reke trouthe thynges onely prudence humbly ſuffer pacyence falſe reporte folkes enuyous ſo holde hym vertuous better whyle abyde ſaye rancour pryde sylence ſothe hath oft haſty ſtryfe vyctorye prerogatyfe palme debate wonne well ſo ſuffre konne ſpeche preſumptuous tolde amphymacus notwithſtandynge trouth mente yet worde exyle wente albe god full iuſtly afterwarde hath anthenor quyt rewarde wyth ſame hyt falſeneſſe duely ſyt ſaye olde antyquytye exyle captyuytye foriudged proſcripſyowne relegate troye towne perpetually procurynge eneas loo howe ryghtfull kynge maye ſe drouydence full iuſtly make recompence doubylneſſe ſymulacyon ſuche contriued falſe treaſon auengeth falſhed parte ſhall hyt ſame darte ſkapeth haue wounde falſhed aye wyll agayne rebounde roſe fyrſte orygynall reſorte agayne ryght doth ball fraude euer doth caſte truſte ryght well wyll laſte ſupplanteth ſhall ſupplanted good example ye ſhall ſe anthenor ſtorye yf ye reade while treate procede touchynge exyle preſcripſion captyuytye relegacyon caſte amphymacus herde noyſe meruaylous great tumulte wonder ſowne lyke lamentacyowne ſondry folke playning diſtreſſe hertye wo inwarde heuyneſſe treate euen gone confuſe crye gan anone ¶wherof vlyxes eke dyomede sodaynly fel dreade suppoſynge theyr oppynyowne ſome rumour fall towne amonge people comontee haſty rancour auenged loue amphimacus cauſeles exyled thus volunte agayne trouthe ryght wherfore dradde drewe night murdred comons towne fraude conſpiracion falſly olde enmytee anthenor falſe enee ſothly yet maner man could wyt wherof began eſpye firſte aroſe paleys throughout cloſe herde well ſaye nought wherof aſtoned thought affrayde ſodayne dreade vlixes firſt alſo diomede leſt comons byſet anthenor without longer let make ſure tumulte crye grekes hath conueyed ſecretly aſſured theyr place vlixes firſte chaunged face gan pynche ſore ſelfe whyle anthenor reaſon guyle heſtes ſo fro daye daye ſleyghte put delaye semynge fully ought could eſpye deceyt fraude trecherye couenauntes hath behight ¶to anone falſe troian knight ſadde cheare ſobre countenaunce well auyſed dalyaunce aunſwered agayne playnly expreſſe iwyſſe quod take vnto wytneſſe hygh goddes euery thynge may ſe without fayninge haue buſy fro poynt poynt purpoſe acheue greue fynally ye lyſt heare one thinge perturbeth mattere whiche ſhall ſo none offence playnely remembre preſence ¶this ſaye olde antiquitee fyrſte buyldynge troye cytye whilom ycalled yllion cauſe onely foundacion kinge ylyus ſythe go full longe founder wall ſtronge made mencion called named yllyon whych great buſy charge pallas name made temple large paſſingly reuerence phane moſt excellence perfourmed maſonry full wele ſaue roſe complete euerydele myghty ſtone buyldinge well aſſured lede tymber cured agayne tempeſt obſtacle tell wonder onely myracle dare well affyrme certayne suche neuer ſeyne ſo liſt ſe conſydre meruayle ſo celeſtiall came downe ye high heauē plyades ſterres ſeuen eyre holdynge paſſage lyke fayre meruaylous ymage world though men ſought ne none halfe ſo well ywrought truely ſuppoſe pygmalyon remembred roſe tyme connynge graue paynte ſo curyous thynge wrought wyth dylygent laboure hande aungell heauenly toure thrugh goddes myght diuine ordinaūce hither ſent purueyaunce relyke onely grace abyde protection diffence ſaluacion perpetually whyle worlde maye dure agayne miſchyefe myſauenture euery trouble trybulacyon ſuſteynynge releuacion ſoueraygne helpe eke cyte whych neuer maye deſtroyed engyne men maye purchaſe goddes haue graunted ſuch grace ſuch vertue annexed eke therto troye ſothe maye neuer fordo tyll relyke ſtole awaye yet ſothe man maye place ſlere remewe preieſte dewe onely offyce touche honde mightely conſerued bonde attempteth concluſyon remewe preſumpcion fyne platly ſhall fayle force none maye auayle ſothe remeued except deutee pertayneth ye haue herde toforne ouermore man yet borne reade tell degre veryly ſtone tree howe deuiſed ywrought wight ſo ſubtill thoughte ceriouſly tell manere minerua ſo freſhe clere ſterne goddeſſe thrugh great might ſo dreadful loke ſight breſt hath criſtall ſhelde egys goddeſſe immortall ygraunted hath bokes lerne power eterne holy relike memoryall temple buildinge moſt royall conſerue aſſault dreade ſuccoure euery maner nede agayne theyr foen vnto troye towne kept deuocyowne alwaye ſucceſſyowne kinge kinge line downe iuſt tytle liuely ſuccede therto annexed take hede prudently auoyding necligence conſerue due reuerence bounde yholde ryght thē ſhall enemye power haue might domage hindering towne called palladyowne lyke clerkes wryte ſayne pallas make towne certayne relike ſente fro heauen downe conclude ſhortly reaſowne cauſe purpoſe ſo let ¶than quod vlixus ſith maye bet labour ydell vayne without recure certayne thou haſt ſayd towne degre relyke maye deſtroyed foly vndertake vnto grekes beheſte make without thou haddeſt well ſure ¶quod anthenor yet recure haue hight ye ſhall haue towne although dylacyowne maner anone ſhall tell ſo ye lyſt whyle dwell without noyſe perturbaunce ¶the prieſte whych gouernaunce relike ſhalbe ſpoke vnto good aduyſe ytreated ſo ſhall full aſſente golde treaſour ſhal blent accorde ſhall purpoſe brynge relyke kept ſo cloſe place ye lyſte aſſigne ſtyll porte goodly benygne workes tyll haue brought fully thinge nothyng doubte dare ſelfe take well hande meaninge vnderſtād toke leue went towne fyrſt voyde ſuſpecyowne theyr goynge anthenor hath hyght would go ſame nyghte priamus make ordynaunce bondes aſſuraunce peace ſhould ymaked knowe eke quantytye golde ye ſhall receyue thus ſhall beſt purpoſe apperceyue kinge knowe eueridele conſente like wonder wele euery thinge anthenor ſayde ſo parte glad well apayde went theyr waye made tarying ¶and anthenor goth vnto kinge hym counſaylinge make delay call lordes agayne nexte daye lyeges aſſemble yfere fynally engroce mattere ſyttynge expedyent kinge open perliament crowned ſat regalye anthenor gan ſpecyfye audyence men myght knowe eche eſtate high lowe grekes agre therto ſumme golde alſo peace ſhall ſtande twenty thouſande marke haue hande pured golde muſt anone payde ſyluer maye delayed muſt eke haue ſame quantytee ouer accorded certayne meaſures couenaunt alſo wheate floure theyr lyues ſaue theyr repayre large ſea ſayle home theyr countre collecte made anone good aduyſe euerychone redy certayne daye man durſt tho ſaye naye contrarye anthenor ſayde ſo well euyll payde ful aſſent concluſyowne haſte throughout towne collatours gathered vp golde lyke ſumme haue tolde poore ryche ſpared none whych tyme anthenor gone vnto prieſt called tonaunt might wiſe daunt make herte fully enclyne full craftely layde hooke lyne luſty bayte falſe couetyſe excytynge full ſecret wyſe would aſſente condeſcende vnto entente put poſſeſſion relyke called palladion without abode maye delyuered gaue golde huge quantytye blend much behyght done pryuely nyghte shortly concludinge condeſcende would ſtate amende paſſyngly euer heyres ſhoulde haue
