finde ye lyſt accounte maugre grutcheth trouth ſhal ſurmoūt dare affirme beare priſe man replye wiſe feble opynion ¶and vlixes alphenon made relacyon hatefull conſpiratyon certayne lordes enuyron countre rauiſhe would quene penolope maugre tho agayne albe ſhe euer ylyke playne trouthe ſtedfaſte wall yet haue caſte platly ſhe ſhall take force maye eſchewed ſo haſte ſhe reſkued caſte time aiourne daye nighte ſoiourne inly herte loue diſamayde wiſedome ſhe hath theim ſo belayde none ſo manly ſo ſage could get auauntage aduyſe workynge vlixes conceyueth thinge fully knewe open euydence alſo ſpecyall credence ¶sente vnto fro penolope matter hole declarynge ſecretee ¶his owne ſonne thelamonius wexe herte wood furyous would make dylacyon ¶but haſte beſoughte alphenon mighty kinge high bounte releue aduerſyte would mighty hāde gentilleſſe conueye lande graunteth ſaye one naye two ful great araye toke ſea winde good well fortuned nothinge theim withſtode ariued lettynge vlixes ye haue herde kinge ſecretly night conueyed haue ligaunce diſobeyed mercyles might awake theyr beddes haue theim take makynge prolongyng tyll morowe haſte wight durſt thē borow smet theyr heades iudgement fynall ſet theim vpon caſtell wall eueriche endlonge rowe vpon toure cocke gan crowe thus nyght kept theim ſelfe cloſe till phebus meryly aroſe orient larke ſonge tho theſe kinges wt theyr meyne ſtrōge freſhly beſene entre cetee ſo glad penolope made ioye goodly quene full deſyrous owne lorde ſene ¶but ſhould ordre ſette great myrthe made met make reherſayle complayntes olde gan theyr hertes vnfolde eche lyſt nothinge concele gladneſſe inly fele ſhulde put memorye reioyſynge hertye glorye lyeges made comynge coſte eke metynge giftes great preſentes ryche worlde trowe none ylyche longe taryinge boke newe aſſuraunce toke lordes lyeges grace fall cheare made eke alphenowne gentylneſſe high renowne doughter inly debonayre alphenon nauſica fayre vlixes medyacyon ywedded vnto thelamon borne diſcent may man ſaye nay reioyce crowne daye thus came purueyaunce two reygnes myghty allyaunce brought knotte men would deme playnly ſotte preſume opynyon delate deſcripcyon sythen guydo touchinge chyefe matter ſtile brefe ¶shortly reherſynge kinge alphenon repeyred home regyon vlixes chiefe cyte abode ſtyll penolope leue ioye ſolace till attropos liketh purchaſe fyche fynally date threde vntwine liues fate ¶how tranſlatour wryteth ſtocke pirrhus lyneall dyſcent father hight pelleus graundmother called thetydes ca xxxviii muſt full buſy directe trace ſtile diſcriuinge ſhortly entente ſtocke pirrhus lyneall diſcente myn auctour folowe compendious ¶whoſe olde father hyght pelleus graundmother called thetydes whych two came worthy achilles troye treaſon loſt lyfe dardanica called wife ¶pirrhus mother doughter reade vnto kynge called lychomede ¶hauinge father ataſtus hight whych ſothneſſe euer myght ¶bare heauy herte kinge pelleus achilles alſo pirrhus kyn playnly ſide malyce rancour pryde enuye hatefull rage ¶when pelleus fall age berafte ſceptre crowne ſee lowe alight downe exyle auayle maye ſtryfe made go thetydes wyfe high diſdayne gayne maye grace herte gan daye night cōpace death pyrrhus kepe ye therupon maliciouſly began ſhape waye awayte lyinge ſley home comynge pyrrhus treynes free many daunger eſcaped ſea many wawe many tempeſt wood great loſſe men good malaſus alderfyrſt gan londe ſtronge cyte lytell ſtronde refreſhed wonder wele knewe grounde euery dele fyrſte thexyle lyke men tolde ¶of thetides pelleus olde ataſtus bare hatrede vnto death wherof gan drede thought would yt right wiſe ſome engyne eſchewe malyce therupon buſy payne ¶now ataſtus ſonnes twayne ¶menalippus poliſtenes doughter ycalled thetydes whyle wofull pelleus caſtell olde ruynous thetydes full ſorowe care dread death daye night gan dare diſpeyred vnweldy age recure fynde mortall rage except hope yore pyrrhus ſhoulde helpe reſtore repeyre ſo fall whoſe comynge often gan call tyme curſe ſo longe abode pyrrhus vnderſtode malaſus relacyowne ful faſte gan haſte towne toke ſea faſt gan hye towarde lande called theſalye entent make ordynaunce ataſtus vengeaunce alder fyrſte pyrrhus ful prudent eſpyes twayne tofore hath ſent theſalye forth togyther gone ¶and crilippus named tone adraſtus named fere expert theim nedeth lere whoſe exployte auauntage ¶this pyrrhus hath dyrecte meſſage theſalye cytezyne called aſſandrus maner chamberlayne pelleus whilom ful ſecree flourynge felycytee pyrrhus concluſyon knewe ſothe relacyon ſea lande hym ne lyſt tarye albe founde winde contrarye ¶but eſcaped many dreadful ſtoundes theſalye approcheth boundes eolus luſt obeyed fortune wonderlye conueyed dryuen grace ariue ſame place pelleus doleful caue dread death laye ſelfe ſaue sole ſaue wife withouten feres al encloſed buſhes briares pirrhus went vp fyrſt londe sole hym ſelfe walkynge ſtronde penſife triſt waye toke ¶where pelleus caue quoke hauynge tho guyde saue ſworde hangynge ſyde vnwarely dreadful herte ¶pelleus caue ſterte diſmayde life doubte behelde knight walke aſtoned abode ſtode ful ſtyll ymagyninge ſawe achille ¶by pirrhus ſtondynge place ſygnes ſhewed face nature without varyaunce made ſo like cheare countenaūce fourme ſhape limmes euerychone difference effect none ¶and pelleus without longer ſpace gan anone pirrhus enbrace enbrayde deadly thoughte ioye ſet ſorowe nought gan declare exyle euyl fare pyteous lyfe pouerte miſchaūce fortune falſe varyaunce ataſtus feruent hoote enuye cruelte tyrannye ceriouſly tolde pirrhus full ſobre ſtode ſtill wall face pale herte wrothe specheles ſhyp agayne goth enformed doubtles menalippus poliſtenes ataſtus togither thre huge araye great meyne ſame daye ful ſurquedous pride hunte foreſt lytell beſyde pyrrhus therof toke good hede without abode chaunge gan wede ful porely rent diſmayde like man diſarayde gyrte ſworde made delaye foreſt toke right waye sole ſelfe without companye ſecretly man might eſpye drough many diuers boundes herde horne vncouplinge houndes like man liſt make mone fro ſyght folke drewe aye alone caſually diſſeuered fro preſe ¶firſte met poliſtenes ¶menalippus ridinge ſyde two pirrhus gan abyde boyſtouſly enquere fro whenſe came alſo febly cladde ſo pore eſtate walkinge deſolate lowly chere countenaunce styll humble daliaunce aunſwered agayne ſayde fordriuen myſchiefe ſea affirmed pale nothinge redde felowſhip drowned dead fiue hundred wawes ſo rage olde yonge mydell age eſcaped tempeſt ſo rife tolde vnneth life ouermore tolde platly eke touchinge birthe greke went deſtitute ioye late come fro ſiege troye beſought towerde liuinge helpe ſome refreſhinge cattell loſt good like ſawe naked ſtode prayinge alſo hope ſhould auayle releue clothinge vytayle refute ſome prouide ¶and bad ſhould abide wyll wytte playnly beſide ran full great harte downe ryuer ¶and menalippus pricked courſer ſemed dewe thinne thicke onely purſewe ſpareth alwaye rode brother pirrhus ſtil abode ¶poliſtenes toke hede haſte alight fro ſtede grene reſte beſyde wery ryde without meyne beynge ſelfe ſole liſting pirrhus ye complaynt dole ſodaynly might aduerte cruell pirrhus ran herte lefte dead lyinge playne menalippus repeyred agayne seynge brother baſkynge bloud pirrhus efte furyous wood face coloure pale wan menalippus yre ran ſlewe eke toke hede thus laye grounde blede brother two withe pirrhus ſworde yſlawe anone aſyde gan drawe metinge knight ſorte caſe ſayth ſtorye called cinaras pirrhus gan haſte enquere whoſe man maketh ſayde withouten tarying ſeruaunt myghty kinge called ataſtus lorde countre ¶and pirrhus tho deadly enmyte cruell ſworde al freſhe red bloud ran lyon wood foreſt forſoke haſte ryght waye toke ſhippe agayne pale blacke hewe gan anone arraye newe ¶all purple whych clerkes telles kinges wyght elles pirrhus freſhe well beſeyne foreſt repeyred ageyne ſodaynly hap walkynge ſhorte meteth wyth kynge ¶olde ataſtus aſked pirrhus man art thou thy ſelfe thus diſconſolate walkeſt fro ¶certes quod pirrhus full ſorowe wo inly ſuppryſed hertye complaynynge one ſonnes priamus kynge lately memorye sith troyans fal whilom glory refewteles miſchiefe brought thus walke ſole full care thoughte farre exyle troye towne cruell pirrhus liue priſon bounde vnto though full lothe hande aſſured ful many othe ſerue luſt aye captyuytye lo thus ſtandeth ataſtus tho full entencion many queſtyon enquered daliaunce ought knewe pirrhus gouernaunce could ought vnderſtande kept ſith came lande ywiſſe quod ye liſt haue kepeth cloſe lo yonder caue amonge bruſſhayle ſhrouded face makinge ſigne ſame place done ydellmaſe king thitherwarde gan gaſe haſty pirrhus gan ſworde outdrawe purpoſe fully ataſtus haue ſlawe wonderly ſtorye lere ¶quene thetides • anone appere albe reygned teares face gan ſworde pirrhus embrace prayinge deadly hande reſtrayne haſt thou killed yong brother twayn ala father hore graye merciles fro wilt take awaye put vp ſworde bloud ne ſhede haue ſome pytye vpon thy kinrede aduerte clerely fyne thou art come ſame line hatefull ſo loke aryght vnkinde bloud euery mannes ſight pyrrhus tho tygre wrothe afferme gan many ſacred othe ſo grutche agaynſt playne ſhall hym ſle handes twayne ¶for hath falſe extorſion ¶put pelleus regyon whyche lorde ye trewe wyfe fynally ſhall leſe hys lyfe anone myne handes deye matter ſeye pelleus darynge caue ye grace lyſte lyfe ſaue helpe platly nought pelleus anone forthe brought croked olde vnweldy eke ſe tofore pyrrhus fell downe hys kne beſechinge hym wyth pyteous face hys requeſt take hym hys grace ¶and wolde manly herte goodly beholde deadly wo ſmerte ¶of ataſtus mortall payne tho hadde ſonnes twaine whiche lay dead tofore hym grene slaine ſwerd yt ſo ſharpe kene ne may recure wyſe ſorow ought ynough ſuffyſe though ye hym vengeaunce well peyſed iuſtly balaunce sith hooly ſubmytted myghte taketh mercy anone ryght let ſworde age conſume requeſt dare preſume pirrhus ſhortly ſayne put vp ſword agayne seynge mercy myght moſt auayle without wordes reherſayle fyrſte tofore theim euerychone kynges made accorden one wyſedome concludynge vp dede eche theim ſhuld right poſſede ¶in theſalye parted twayne neyther matter complayne eueryche reygne dewe ſee togyther thre preſence man ¶ataſtus fyrſte thus tale began ¶syres quod vnknowe age brought ſo lowe nature kindly mocion wexed feble wyt reaſon beynge vnweldy lymmes many yeares vpon fall vnneth thinge diſcerne feble ſothe kingedome gouerne lyfe death takynge nowe hede sith ſonnes ſlayne dead ſole lefte withouten heyre worldly luſte fully diſpeyre tyme paſſed felycytye fortune tourne mutabylytye hathe taughte playnlye dare well expreſſe worldly ioye ſykerneſſe truſte abyde wyll ſelfe prouyde haſte prudent purueaunce clere diſcharge gouernaunce agayne ſorte liſt maligne ¶but ſceptre crowne frely reſigne theſalye lordſhip lande fre hole thy hande ſhall man reclayme ſaye naye interrupte make delaye touchinge thinge concluſyon put full poſſeſſion hereupon euer abyde makynge full fayth hand layde quene thetides ſyttynge preſent pelleus ſame entent vnto pirrhus purpartye reſygned eke ryght theſalye fully affermynge yore ago full deſyre ioye alſo euer one neuewe ſuccede ryghtfull heyre kingdome poſſede vtterly without repentaunce belongeth vnto lygeaunce sceptre ſworde crowne dyademe kynge lyfe death deme thy hande without longer date ſame houre holy tranſlate knot conuencion fully brought concluſon perfourmed vp hole vnyte euermore atwene theſe kinges thre ataſtus knightes diſſeuered enuyrowne foreſt deſcended downe byddynge platly theyr lorde echone ſworne accorde attones luſty companye theſalye faſt gan theim hye pirrhus folke lyinge ſea ſayled forthe ſtreyght cytye ataſtus doth ſytte parliament openly gaue commaundement liege hygh lowe eſtate wythout ſtrife debate specially gentyll bloud yborne ſame daye pirrhus ſworne like theyr degree royall hall perſeuer trewe liege durynge theyr lyfe erneſt game pelleus commaūded hath ſame partye without fraude thus ioye ſolempne laude pirrhus euery maner age gladly accepted heritage daye fortunate good glad aſpectes heuen ſtode well accordynge ſuch maner thinge worthy pirrhus ycrowned kinge theſalye riche regyon vayne make mencion theyr reuell theyr great arraye feaſt made ſame daye eke ſtory finde ſothe wyll paſſe ouer mine auctour dothe saue booke ſpecefyed kingdome fer magnefyed theſalye puyſſaunce might pyrrhus whylom ſo good knight hym leaue royall ſee ¶tournynge agayne kynge ydumee ygraue vnder ſtone ¶and hym hys ſonne meeryone ſtory ſaith crowned king crete awhyle reygninge equyte dyed alſo wolde none ¶and haſt leorica hys brother rightfull heyre ſucceſſyon crowned kinge regyon ¶in tyme ataſtus drede thaſſent pyrrhus rede full buſy make ſpecyal ryche toumbe paſſyngly royall buryed full huge preſe ¶menalyppus polyſtenes two foreſt ſlawe thorugh pirrhus ſwerde full cruell law ¶of none proceſſe make euen fully tale take bothe alſo eke yfere ¶of ataſtus theyr owne father dere whome ſothly hys locke hore troye booke rede ¶but muſt pirrhus wende wryte ſorye wofull ende whan ſat higheſt ſee made full blinde vayne proſperyte gouerning tho lande theſalye ¶there hym betydde fall fantaſye ſette hys loue hermyon quene ¶horeſtes wyfe reygnynge methene whome brent hote fyre fulfyllyng hys foule deſyre purpoſe hole thus brought aboute rauyſhyng lorde oute tho led hir home helde wyfe seminge hym blyſfull lyfe full releſe paynes ſmerte ¶of whyche horeſtes bare full heuy herte caſte hym playnely auenged whan therto hath opportunyte time though ſuſteined wrong ¶he feble pyrrhus ſtrong ¶whiche helde alſo ſtorye tolde ¶andromecha hym houſholde ¶hectors wyfe whylom ſhe lytell chylde whyche hir ſhe ladde ſege complete deſtructiowne whan ſhe brought troye towne laomedonte fende name encreaſyng full worthy fame ¶and pyrrhus ſhe ſonne alſo▪ ¶achylleydos ſo calleth hym guydo theſe woman theyr great eſtate atwene ſelfe amonge debate ¶and hermyone yre full hote complayning thus father wrote fere hygh degree andronomecha cheriſhed better thā ſhe kynge pyrrhus beſechynge menelay hym enhaſte al euer maye come hym ſelfe anone ſlea woman childe alſo naught abode faſtgan hym hye heate towardes theſalye avenged ſwerde ſtele herein fauleth neuer adele maugre hym cruelte reſkewed amyd cite ¶ thynge hath herde woman kynge draw hys ſwerde wyll thys matter dwelle maner ſhamed wryte telle done pyrrhꝰ courage delos gone pilgrimage hauinge litell route ¶to apollo knele loute ſoule praye achylle hys vowes alſo fulfylle hym thanke hyghe affeccyon good exployte hadde troye towne wreche alſo take cyte hys father ſake thinge yſpecified ¶kinge horeſtes warely hath eſpyed delos haſte full ryght ledinge many luſty knight vnwarely pirrhus mette vengeably vpon ſette fynally ſtraunge lande ¶horeſtes ſlewe owne hande fynde ſothe made diffence ſodayne mortall vyolence enuye could aſterte ſworde myght aduerte enuyron beſet thilke tyme myght bet nother ſocour declyne thus pyrrhus brought fine ¶late crowned kinge theſalye lo guerdon auoutrye lo mede rewarde ful rife miſuſe mannes wife dread folowe ſhall vengeaunce sodayne death vnware myſchaunce euery man greatly ought charge delos temple large ¶kinge pyrrhus locked vnder ſtone horeſtes furth waye gone force gat wyfe agayne wight durſt tho wtſayne methene proudly repeyred theſalye piteouſly diſpeyed deſtitute reade wiſt theyr worthy king dead heyre none ſucceſſion gouerne noble regyon saue achilleydos litell aforne pirrhus abſence grece borne fully age quarter cleane youth ſothly grene lyſt conſydre tender myght full many daye reioyce ryght gouerne sceptre hande large boundes ſo great lande ¶and yet childe likly right fayre ſothe borne heyre pirrhus trouth playne man lyſt withſaine ¶but finde came age reſygned hole herytage brother frely ryght ¶lamedowne wonder manly knight deſcended troyaniſhe bloud downe fro ſtock ſo good floure knighthod diffence frygya begat andromecha ordeyned nowe ſo grutche frowne theſalye beare crowne whan made lorde lande frely reſygned hande ¶he hath cōmaunded man dare replye kyngdome theaſlye captyuitye pryſoners troye cytye loue hate exceptyon none ſhulde large gone ¶by full aſſent achylleydos ſuche eke pryſon cloſe without raunſome ſhall delyuered ¶and reioyſe full lyberte cuſtome vſed borough towne lyeges great regyon thus folke yt came thralle fro troye reſtored ſodaynely ioye ¶by lamedowne ymade free eke reygneth royall ſea full myghtly haue made mynde troye boke hym fynde pyrrhus kynrede fro henſeforth proceſſe reade ¶but incydentes beare ſubſtaunce whiche vayne put remēbrance except myne auctour note entent impeth littell incydent ywrought done full yore agone touchynge death kyng menon whyche enuye cruell achylles ſlayne ſoth amonge myrmydones onely proudely gan purſewe vpon achylles troylus reſkue ¶whom kynge pryam made buryed beſyde troylus troye cyte temple ybylte marbell olde fyne tale tolde chapitle ſhall reherſe anone noble quene kynge menon tyme longe many day ſhe deade grauen vnder claye toumbe heuenly gan appere albe ſet bryght ſterres clere whoſe ſymylytude reken lyke thynge immortall man myght vtterly ſuſtene beholde loke ſhe ſo ſhene downe deſcendynge fro fyrmament full many man beynge preſent clade mantell ful celeſtyall porte paſſyngly royall ſweteneſſe freſhe roſe made haſte tombe vncloſe lorde taketh bone cheſt made golde ſtones couched faſt euer ſhe maye diſpeyred went anone waye tofore certayne place ſhe neuer ſayne afferminge lyklyneſſe aungell goddeſſe ſoule fate ſame kynge deme ſuche heauenly thynge therin holde none opinyon tranſcendeth ſhortly reaſon lyſt ſuche matter diffyne reſorte ryght lyne vlixes dwell ende ſurplus tell myght eſcape parodye hym ſhape parchas haue laſt terme ſette attropos meſured mette liues threde rocke ſponne diffende thy ſelfe vlixes thou konne shewe thy manhode aferde welfare thy ſonnes ſworde ſhall nowe like wonte sharpe penne rude blonte deſcriue fine thy ſoioure vpon boundes ſet laboure almoſt wery weake faynt ynough beaſtes ox plough longe daye agayne hyll wende almoſt landes ende troye booke fyche wyll ſtake saue muſt ſpende fewe lynes blake laſte chapiter ſhortly tranſlate worke ympen date daye death ſette areſte full execute loued beſt lowe knee muſt loute god maketh men route cauſeth folkes haue glad ſwenenes morowe luſty euenes morphe u ſlepy wande holdeth alwaye hande hath marked agayne nyght make men mery lyght ſome whyle haue gladneſſe ſodeynly falle heauyneſſe lyke gyueth euydence ſondry ſygnes apparence vnto lord muſt mekely preye tyme ſtyle conueye vlyxes dreame diſcryue laſte lyue declarynge hym token full notable ſygnes demonſtrable ſlepte agayne pale mone fatall day ſhulde folowe ſoone fell thus abedde laye mydnyght tofore morowe graye ¶hym thought ſawe appeare creature ſyght celeſtyall fygure none erthly thynge veryly deuyne porte chere wonder femynyne ¶and hym ſempte fantaſye lyke thynge ſent fayrye beaute goodly face recomforted playnely place moſt ſurmountynge moſt ſouerayne clereneſſe eyen twayne ſodeynly men myght aduerte perce woulde euen herte deffence none myght deuyſed ¶and vlyxes loke ſuppryſed gan beholde alwaye ſlepe ſyghe ſore perſynge aye full buſy peyne enbrace armes twayne ¶but aye gan purſue agaynewarde gan hym eſchewe aye preyſed ſe aye hym ſhe gan flee contrayre hym fortune whan ſhe ſawe importune aſked hym ſhortly wolde platte trouth tolde ¶certes quod lyues emperyſſe ye woman goddeſſe deme iudge halfe ryght ſo derked blynded ſyght ¶but dare well affyrme place lyfe deth ſtande hoolely grace mercy requyrynge ryght rewe owne knight pyte compaſſyon goodly ſe ſaluacyon deſyre maye fulfyll ſame night haue wyll recure remedye lacke routhe nedely muſt dye haue atwixe hope dread ſelfe declared womanhead ſhe kept cloſe tho full ſadly gan ſmyle put remembraunce sayde vnto ſobre countenaunce sothly quod ſhe thine affection would fully tourne confuſion v ſo perellous inly mortall contagyous vtterly gayne may reade one v muſt anone dead fyne hateful chaunce folowe ſhould pleaſaunce vlixes gan nighen nere beholdinge aye heauenly cheare ſhe ſtode vp right grdunde ſawe holde ſpere longe rounde head therof borned ſtele forged newe grounde wonder wele ¶and therupon auiſiowne ſawe baner blaſynge vp downe felde therof coloure ynde full fyſhes beaten fynde ¶and ſome bokes like tolde middes large crowne golde ¶and ſhe tourne gan face lykly anone parte place ſpake ſayd wordes playne full token partynge v twayne euermore efte ſowre ne ſwete daye neuer agayne mete diſaperinge anone leue ſhe toke ſodaynly awoke gan muſen fantaſye maner thing dreme might ſygnefy mente euill good ſecretneſſe tho vnderſtode ſurmounted ſothly reaſon therfore ſente throughout region ſuche ſubtill expoſytoures fate ſorte crafty dyuinours clerkes ſubeict crowne aſſemble one ſweuen expowne ¶and knewe informacyon maner hole auiſion byn concluded according one time aprocheth ſhall come anone one next kinrede ſpere ſhulde make herte blede ¶let ſe fate gan remewe sith harde deſtynye teſchewe ſaye tho folke theyr opinion worke truſt conſtellacion vlixes muſynge tale chaungeth coloure gan wexeen pale wonder dreadfull full fantaſyes gan ſelfe ſeke remedyes awaye voyde thinge ¶he ſtareth brode maye ſe inwarde loke cloude yblent ¶but weninge prudent ¶made call hym ſonne thelamon take ſhet vp pryſon ſuppoſynge fully witte miſchiefe therby go quite aduerteth ne toke none hede ſharpeneſſe ſpeares head fiſhes baner beate ſea wherin ſwimme flete quene called circe ſignes brought wer peace crowne token dignyte one holde ſhall royall ſee waltryng amid wawes fell woo amonge fyſhes large floud ¶and ſhall make ful diuiſion tofore remembred auiſion agayne ignoraunce execute fatall puruyaunce vp dreame ſpere ſtele whych vlixes conſydreth neuer dele ¶nor wyght hath ſuſpection ¶but ſonne called thelamon cloſed ſhet vp towre ¶and vlixes coſte great laboure fro daye daye doth buſyneſſe ſelfe make fortereſſe bilte rocke lime ſquare ſtones depe ditched none man maye enter ſyde caſteth hys lyfe abyde certayne men choſen ſpecyall ¶night daye watche vpon wall maner wyght ſhulde haue none entree ſo falle aye ſecree knowen olde counſayle ſworne ye ſtory reherſed hath forne olde foole dotarde vlixes ſonne begot cyrces freſhe luſty yonge coragious called thelagonyus ¶borne ſee amonge floddes rage alſo reken age fyue twenty yeres aboute ¶but hys father aye doute man mighte beynge therof ſecurytie tyll daye deſyrous knowe hys mother fell knee lowe beſeching goodly ſpare hys father trouthe declare ſhuld dwelle beſought ſhe woulde hym tell ¶but ſothly ſhe longe many dayes hyghe prudence put hym delayes tyll ſhe ſawe ſhe might haue reſte importune requeſte whē ſhe knew ther none bote fro poynt poynt ſhe tolde crop rote ¶of vlixes kynge anone made taryinge toke leue may none playnely ſayde wolde hys father ſe ¶wherof quene gan herte colde ſhe ſaw ſhe might wtholde hym beſought wyth chere debonayre wolde ſoone agayne repayre forthe ſayleth onwarde way without abode ſelfe ſame day many porte many fer countre tyll brought would ¶to achaya lande great renowne gan ſerche regyon place paleys pryncypall kinge helde ſee royall ſo longe countre rode tyll taught kynge abode vlixes ſhytte vp mewe place haſte gan purſewe great party releued hys ſorow monday erely morow ¶vnto brydge ryghteway toke foūde porter deynous hys loke lowely fyrſte gan praye voutſafe hym goodly conueye courte make taryinge meſſage hadde kynge ¶but proudely denyed gate ſhortly ſayd came late entre maner wyſe eke vngoodly gan deſpyſe frowarde ſpeche malycyous haſte thys thelagonyus heart ferde proude porter hente berde fyſte rofe chawe bone fell deade muet ſtone eke tho withſtode made proudely lepe flode whan mo came maken reſiſtence hente ſwerde manly vyolence furyouſly hys yrous tene ſtory ſayeth ſlewe fyftene hym ſelfe almoſte wounded death gan wery ſothly fayle breath vlixes noyſe ſowne bridge deſcendyd downe fynding men entre gate dead ſlayne full mortall hate full yrous hente anone adarte auenture ſtandinge tho aparte cruelly caſte thelagon yet ſtroke concluſyon domaged glode aſyde haſte longer would abyde hent vp darte without areſt ſmote king lowe vnder breſt ribbes ſhortly ſaye wounde muſt nedes deye hauinge tho opinion kinge ſuſpection owne father ſlawe faſt gan ende drawe wound ſo deadly ſo kene might ſelfe ſuſtene pale wan grounde gan glide men vpon euery ſyde buſy helpe hym releue ſore gan ſo ake greue well felte muſt dead ¶but abrayding lift vp head hauynge yet perfect minde reaſon remembre gan auyſyon tolde dreade one next kinrede deſcended downe owne lyne ſweuen ſhall parfourme fyne accompliſhe wyth darte ſtele could naught conceyuen wele ſhulde badde anone vnto meyne without harme vyolence ſette anone vnto preſence yonge man whych gate ſtode hath daye ſhed ſo muche bloud ¶and afore vlixes brought hath enquyred ſought fyrſte kyn next countre ¶certes quod borne ſea amonge fyſhes myd wawes grene ſayde alſo mother quene called circe name kouthe eaſt weſt eke right fer ſouth tolde alſo father kynge hym begat home comynge fro troye towne towarde countre mother circe tolde serteinly vlixes hyghte deſyrous haue ſyghte entred myghty regyon haue purſewed vnto dungeon onely hope father haue ſeyne ſe well laboure vayne ſyth ſothe loſt trauayle maye ſyde auayle folly longer dwell lo tell kynred aſke ¶with vlixes gan ſyghe ſore lacke bloud full pale ſayde anone herde tale ¶now wot well wofull deſtynye fulfylled maye none wot well late grutche ſtryue agayne piteous fate ¶for ſonne clerkes whilom tolde hath made ende dayes olde theron exſpectant paynes full greuous ¶and worde thelagonius ſo wiſt agayne nature lawe ala father ſlawe ye land longe borne crowne without abode fell anone ſwowne ¶his clothes rente yelowe heyre torne ¶alas quod euer borne curſed woful deſtynye fortune maye fle curſed ſorte curſed min auenture refuſe euery creature forwarryed eke diſpoſycyon curſed conſtellacyon curſed alſo full infortunate houre father begat would god without longer reade acquite anone dead laye life death borowe ¶and kynge ſawe great ſorow wyſt ſonne circe borne many ſygnes reherſed heretoforne vnto anone forgaue death tho might lacke want breth importable paſſyon ¶and efte ſonne called thelamon whyche hath priſon ſo many daye ſhet preſence haſte fet ſawe father ſuche poynt wpon death ſtandynge diſioynt knewe alſo trouthe hath founde laſt deadly wounde ſworde hente mortally yrous woulde tho haue ronne thelagonius hygh deſpyte auenged ¶but vlixes fatherly pytye made men holde reſtrayne amyd greuous payne prudence done anone made ſonnes one ¶and gaue charge vnto thelamon entereneſſe affection hole herte fayned neuer adele life loued brother wele parte treaſour golde good next borne bloud tho ſothe longer taryed vlixes full royally caryed achaya chyefe cyte liued dayes thre without tho gaue vp gooſt ſaye playnly coſt lyfe ſoule gone tumbe metall ſtone body cloſed yſhet made let thelamon wyth great ſolempnytye ycrowned father ſee sworde sceptre delyuered hand achaya ryche worthy lande ryght habundaunt treaſour golde thelagon wyth hym abode yeare complete well cheryſhed ſyght brother toke ordre knygt liſt longer abyde kynge wyſely gan prouyde golde treaſure plente repeyred home countre ¶and mother age wexen ſadde repeyre paſſyngly gladde ſhe ſawe ſorcerye ſcaped many ieopardye many peryll many great dyſtreſſe ſhe fell ſyckneſſe dette yelde vnto nature whych eſcape maye maner creature worlde lyuynge whoſe death ſon crowned king aulydos meruaylous countre haue tolde encloſed ſea amonge rockes many ſhippes drowne ſixtye yere bare crowne manly man thelagonins brother thelamonius reygned alſo regyon seuentye wynter made mencyon made royall ende two iubiter wende reygne amonge ſterres bryght bvt lanterne clere lyght waſted frygyus darete whylom troye wryter poete guyde haue none paſſe euen ſelfe place fytched hath boundes ſtyle ſyege preſent whyle aye one wyth abyde dites greke tother ſyde two theyr wrytynge ne varye lytell thynge touchynge matter ſpecyall notable hyſtoryall force incydentes ſmale whych ſothe lytell tale ¶saue dites maketh mencyon nombre ſlayne tofore towne laſtynge ſyege afferminge dreade eyghte hundred thouſande ſix deade grekes ſyde vp ryght fyelde dare alſo behelde troye partye werre kene six hundred thouſande ſeuentye ſyxtene ſlayne guydo ye maye ſe theym came helpe citye fro many coſte many regyowne diffence reſcues towne ¶and full ten yere ſo caſte ſixe monthes mighty ſyege laſte gette dare wryte ſelfe ouermore complete dayes twelue grekes full poſſeſſyon falſe engyne greke synon lyke tofore reherſed late haue latyn tranſlate dytes dare guydo adde therto myn auctours ſpecyfye ſayne occupacyon ſothly vayne lyke maner preſumpcyon tyme complete tranſlatyon iuſte reckenynge accountes clere thouſande foure hundred yeare twentye nere knowe dread chriſte receyued manhead empereſſe quene heauen hell mayde cleane eyghte yeare iuſte computacyon sewynge next coronacyon moſt gracyous workynge henry fyfthe noble worthy kinge protectour brute albyon called high renowne proweſſe chyualrye alſo ferre paſſeth anye cloude ſkye normandye mighty conquerour knighthod high labour maugre tho liſt withſayne conquered hath herytage agayne myghty prudent gouernaunce recured eke hys tytle vnto fraunce ¶that ſo lyſt loke doe vnfolde pee de grewe theſe cronicles olde ſercheth bokes ywryt longe toforne ſhall fynde iuſtly borne reygne fraunce lineall dyſcente ¶and onwarde nowe ordeined regent thylke lande durynge father lyfe goodneſſe voyden werre ſtryfe reioyſe without delay septre crowne kinges day clerely concluſion enrolled vp conuencyon ¶and hope tyme fortunat ¶of olde world called aureat reſorte ſhall influence grace cruell mar ſhall manace lokes furious wodde falſe aſpectes ſhede bloude atwene folkes theſe realmes twayne euery wyght iuſtly ought complayne ¶but truſte myne opynion thys worthy kynge wyſdome reaſon knighthode ſhall ſo doe hys payne make one longe hathe betwayne meane thus england fraūce may one withouten varyaunce hertes olde rancour enchace influence mighty grace called clerkes douteles ſoueraygne lord prince peace hope grace ſhall reygne ſet peace atwene theſe realmes twayne hys power ſothly ſtandeth ¶and allyaunce blode royall knet vp bonde mariage werre ſhall voyde away rage make peace bryght bemes ſhyne ¶and one called katheryne named right good fayre alſo shalbe mene atwyxt bothe two grace emprynted womanhede complayne ſhal haue nede ¶and hope gracyous aryuayle thys lande ſhall ſo much auayle ioye honour proſperytye without trouble aduerſytye repeyre ſhall hertye pleaſaunce plentye welfare fulſome habundaunce peace quyet nigh ferre without ſtrife debate werre myſchiefe pouerte nede▪ indigence full ceaſſinge death peſtylence sothly hope ye ſhall ſene come lande noble quene ſhall ſaye herte feyne nought bleſſed ſhe hath v broughte yt hath might working knighthod concluded thyng ſuch meruayles ī armꝭ done wrought purpoſe fully brought high wiſedome ſet inwarde ſyght inioyinge longeth ryght higheſt ſyt worthyneſſe glorye sceptre conqueſt victorye praye god onely bi beſte ¶when hath al ſette peace reſte full put clere poſſeſſyon longeth ſubiection ſende home triumphe honour great euer conquerour longe ioye quiete rule reygne royall ſete thus ſhall aye ſaye daye night exployte praye faythfull herte hole entente whilom gaue commaundemente yore ago father tyme ſyege troye maner rime moſt ſake ſpeake ſpecyall although boyſtous rurall gaue charge ſtorye tranſlate rude connynge called iohn lydgate monke burye profeſſion vſynge habite perfection albe lyfe accordeth therto feyne wot well ſo nedeth witneſſe call recorde take brother fayle ſo great nede ¶and ſhall noble ſtorye reade beſeche ſupporte grace offende maner place wher ſoeuer find ſhal errour gentylneſſe ſhewen fauour benyngly payne hyt correcte rather dyſdayne wel wot yt muche thyng ther wronge falſely metryd ſhorte longe ſhoulde haue diſdayne dreade labour vayne let ignoraunce rudeneſſe excuſe ye platly refuſe certayne fautes whiche ye ſhal finde doute thancke ſette behynde verſe though ignoraunce yet ſtory ye fynde may pleaſaunce touching ſubſtaunce yt mine auctour writ though ſo worde miſſe ſyt amendeth chere debonayre errour hyndre appayre ſayde purpoſe malyce worſhyp hym wyſe wight gladly demeth ſo ſoone lacke specyally behynde backe ſoth ſkylle goeth full hoole neuer fall fynde newe olde deme alway ſo bolde yblent vnconnynge blynde bayarde caſte peryll nothynge tyll ſtumblyng fall amydde lake none ſo redye vndertake ſothe bolder ſaye werſe ſkylle proſe yet verſe ſuche lyſten ſtyll lyttell forſe ſaye good yll vnto booke directe ſuche lyſte haue effecte ſymple folke full compaſſyon goodly correction amende thynge hyndre neuer adele cuſtome aye ready ſaye wele groūde well ſayinge lyfe hyndred makyng maiſter chaucer yt founde ful many ſpot hym liſt pynche grutche euery blot meue hym ſelfe perturbe reſte haue herde tolde ſayde alway beſte sufferynge goodly gentilneſſe full many thynge embraced rudeneſſe ſhall ſhortly hym diſcriue neuer none thys daye alyue reken bothe yonge olde worthy ynkehorne holde thys lande yf borough towne vyllage cite connyng hath tracy ſewe go brode ſhet mewe hym make full dyreccyon thys boke haue inſpeccion beſechinge theim theyr prudent loke race ſcrape al boke voyde adde theim ſeineth nede though ſo ne reade boke rethorikes newe yet hope ſhall finde al trewe ſtorye playne chiefly ſubſtaunce ſo lyſt ſe varyaunce worldly thinge wrought dayes olde boke maye full well beholde chaunge fortune courſe mutable selde faythfull ſtable lordes prince royalte sodaynly brought aduerſyte kinges eke plounged pouerte theyr dread daringe deſerte vnware ſlaughter compaſſed enuye murdre conſpyred conſpyracye awayte layinge falſhede treaſon kingedome ſodayne reuerſyon rauyſhinge woman delyte roote werre mortall deſpyte falſe mayntenaunce auoutrye many worthy cauſynge dye sinne aye concludinge ſo taketh hede vengeaunce vnware finall mede declare worldly luſte loke aryght litell truſte boke example ye maye finde liſt enprinte minde paſſeth halt ſoioure waſtinge awaye doth ſomer floure riche pore euery maner age life pilgramage meynt laboure muche wo men would taken hede therto eke tofore prudently aduerte litell ioye ſhould haue herte ſette theyr truſte worldly thinge nother prince lorde kynge ¶by example troye ye may ſee lyfe maye haue full ſurete ¶therfore ſtarfe vpō roode suffrynge deth alder good lyfte vp hartꝭ thinke amonge ye neuer ſo myghty ſo gronge without hym al may auaile gyue victorye battayle holde fyelde ſhortly conclude fewe agayne great multytude grace maketh prynces ſtronge worthy kynges reygne longe theſe tyrantes ſodeynely oppreſſe throwe thē downe al great richeſſe hande power reſerueth eche acquyte lyke deſerueth praye deuocyon myne herte hole affection lyſte graunt longe contynuaunce proſperytye good perſeueraunce helthe welfare victorye honour vnto noble myghty conquerour ¶henry fyfthe tofore eſpecyfyed name maye magnefyed lyfe vp ſterres clere afterwarde aboue nynth ſphere whan dead haue place praye god ſende grace whoſe byddynge tolde late fyrſte began ſyege tranſlate ¶and haue holy honoure full executed fyne laboure vnto ſhall ſtorye ſe humble herte humilyte lyttell booke lowely betake ſupporte thus ende make ¶of moſt noble excellent prynce kynge henry fyfthe moſt worthy prynce knighthode ſoures welle whoſe highe renowne worlde doth ſhyne manhode doeſt excelle egall meryt worthyes nyne borne alſo ryght diſcent lyne veray heyre tytle attayne beare ye crowne worthy realmes twain ¶and alſo fer phebus ſphere fro eaſt weſt throweth beames bright lucyna wt ſhrouded chere▪ goeth compaſſe rounde pale light thou art yreckened beſt knight regiſtred worthy name higheſt place ſet houſe fame ¶to holde palme knighthod thy hād worthineſſe hygh victorye thou arte drade ſea lande euermore wt lande honour glorye iuſt conqueſt put memorye crowne made laurer grene vpon thy head tofore famous quene ¶whilom ordeyned onely conquerours stable herte longe contynuaunce gaue vp till victoures empriſes take ſodayne chaunce whoſe name ay floureth wt newe remēbraūce fadeth yeares yore agone amonges thou mayſt ſet one ¶for world many regyon reported fame flyeth wyde naturally thy condicion thinge begonne knightly abyde tyme manly ſet aſyde reſt eaſe coſte theron ſpente til thou haue wonne fine thin entente ¶moſt circumſpect paſſinge auiſee al thy workes conueyed wt high prudēce sad demure like ioſuee agayne whoſe ſwerde gayneth reſyſtēce haſt alſo heauenly influence salamon wiſely diſcerne onely grace thy people gouerne ¶mercy eke ment thy magnificence oppreſſed haue pyte rebelles manly violence abate thou canſt great cruelte ſo dauid haſt kingly pyte highe proweſſe seſar iulyus tyme moſt victorious ¶and manly holdeſt thy handes two beholde clere inſpection ſword knighthod thy sceptre alſo tone bringe ſubiectyon hertes made proude falſe rebellyon ſceptre rule beſt thy trewe people liue reſt ¶now yu yt haſt vertue manhode grace attemperaunce fredome bounte lowly praye dreadfull face diſdayne benignely ſe vpon boke rudely made fyne onely argue thine highneſſe rewe mercy vpon ſimpleſſe ¶and thy noble kingly aduertenee conſydre ſoueraygne lord moſt deare thine innate famous ſapyence chriſt ieſu receyued good cheare two minute yeue herte entere widowe wil thought gaue good kepte ſelfe ryghte nought example ſo offende thrugh mine vnconning thy high nobleſſe let good litell gifte amende thy mercy renowmed goodneſſe take diſdayne bareyne rudeneſſe making al though haue muſe let trewe meninge ſurplus excuſe good herte hath maner wight preſent eyther god man parte ryght gyue hoole fer forth aye perſeuer fro tyme began thought thine eſtate pray conſerue thus finally ſaye ¶fyrſte almighty god ye wrathe queme maye pleſaunce thy crowne thy diademe grace good eure long continuaūce thy lyeges faythfull obeyſaunce vertue man maye ſpecifye praye god graunt vnto thy regallye explicit liber quintus et vltimus lenuoye go litell boke put grace ye moſt excellence hardye aye ſhewe thy face without ſupporte magnificence ſo euer ſhall finde offence bolde preſumpcion thy ſelfe tenarme aye pacience ſubmitte theyr correction verba tranſlatoris ad librum ſuum ye arte enlimmed wt floures rethorike wt white blacke therfore thou muſt nedely abide ſhoures liſt ſet alacke thou arte moſt likly go wracke agaynſt thine errour diffende humbly tho withdrawe go abacke requiring thy amiſſe amende finis ¶here begynneth table howe kinge
